Title: Financial Services and Markets Act 2023
Date: 2024-11-04
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2023/29

## Financial Services and Markets Act 2023

      B e it enacted  by the King’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the
advice and consent of the Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this
present Parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:—

### Regulatory framework

#### Revocation of  

##### Revocation of  

1

1.1

The legislation referred to in Schedule 1 is revoked.

1.2

In that Schedule—

1.2.a

Part 1 refers to  assimilated direct principal  legislation;

1.2.b

Part 2 refers to subordinate legislation;

1.2.c

Part 3 refers to EU tertiary legislation and subordinate legislation made
under an instrument referred to in Part 2;

1.2.d

Part 4 refers to primary legislation;

1.2.e

Part 5 refers to other EU-derived legislation not covered by Parts 1 to 3.

1.3

. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .

1.4

The revocation of any legislation in accordance with this section does not
affect the continued effect of any amendments to other legislation made by
that revoked legislation (as those amendments had effect immediately before
the revocation).

1.5

The Treasury may by regulations provide for specified subordinate legislation,
or for subordinate legislation of a specified description, otherwise falling
within Part 5 of Schedule 1, not to fall within that Part.

1.6

Regulations under subsection (5) are subject to the negative procedure.

##### Transitional amendments

2

2.1

Schedule 2 amends particular legislation referred to in Schedule 1 in relation
to the transitional period.

2.2

In this Chapter “ the transitional period ”, in relation to any legislation,
means the period ending with the revocation of that legislation.

2.3

The amendments in Schedule 2 do not restrict the power in section 3 to modify
legislation as amended by that Schedule.

##### Power to make further transitional amendments

3

3.1

The Treasury may by regulations modify legislation referred to in Schedule 1
in relation to the transitional period.

3.2

The power under subsection (1) is exercisable only by making such
modifications as the Treasury consider necessary or desirable for or in
connection with one or more of the following purposes—

3.2.a

protecting and enhancing the integrity or stability of the financial system
operating in the United Kingdom;

3.2.b

promoting the safety and soundness of persons providing financial services;

3.2.c

promoting effectiveness in the functioning of financial markets;

3.2.d

promoting effective competition in the interests of consumers in financial
services and markets or persons who use, or are likely to use, services
provided by payment systems in the course of business carried on by those
persons;

3.2.e

facilitating the international competitiveness of the economy of the United
Kingdom and its growth in the medium to long term;

3.2.f

protecting consumers and those who are, or may become, insurance
policyholders;

3.2.g

providing for efficient and effective arrangements in relation to the exercise
of functions under the Banking Act 2009 or Part 4 of this Act;

3.2.h

protecting public funds;

3.2.i

implementing, or making changes to reflect, developments in international
standards and practices relating to, or applied for the purposes of, the
provision of financial services or the operation of financial markets;

3.2.j

providing for efficient and effective regulatory, enforcement, investigatory
and supervisory arrangements in relation to the provision of financial
services or the operation of financial markets;

3.2.k

removing provisions that are yet to be commenced or changing the timing of
their commencement.

3.3

In subsection (2)—

3.3.a

the integrity of the financial system operating in the United Kingdom includes
the matters listed in section 1D(2) of FSMA 2000;

3.3.b

references to financial markets include references to financial exchanges;

3.3.c

“ consumer ” has the meaning given by section 1G(1) of FSMA 2000;

3.3.d

“ payment system ” has the same meaning as in Part 5 of the Financial Services
(Banking Reform) Act 2013 (see section 41 of that Act);

3.3.e

the reference to regulatory arrangements includes (among other things) a
reference to arrangements for the making of rules.

3.4

In modifying legislation for or in connection with a purpose mentioned in
subsection (2) regulations under this section may—

3.4.a

confer powers on the Treasury or on a regulator;

3.4.b

authorise the making of subordinate legislation by the Treasury;

3.4.c

authorise the making of rules or other instruments by a regulator;

3.4.d

provide for fees to be charged by a regulator in connection with the carrying
out of its functions;

3.4.e

apply (with or without modifications), or make equivalent or similar provision
to, provisions made by or under FSMA 2000 (including criminal offences created
by that Act).

3.5

The power under section 84(2)(c) to make supplementary, incidental,
consequential, transitional, transitory or saving provision includes, in
relation to regulations under this section, power to restate legislation in a
clearer or more accessible way.

3.6

Before making regulations under this section the Treasury must consult the
regulators.

3.7

The duty under subsection (6), so far as relating to the Bank of England or
the Payment Systems Regulator, applies only if, and to the extent that, the
Treasury think it appropriate to consult that regulator in view of the
modifications being made by the regulations.

3.8

The power under subsection (1) to modify legislation does not include power to
modify—

3.8.a

primary legislation referred to in Part 4 of Schedule 1;

3.8.b

technical standards of the kind mentioned in section 138P(2)(a) of FSMA 2000;

3.8.c

EU tertiary legislation of the kind mentioned in section 138P(2)(b) of FSMA
2000.

3.9

Regulations under this section that modify only the following kinds of
legislation referred to in Schedule 1 are subject to the negative procedure—

3.9.a

EU tertiary legislation;

3.9.b

subordinate legislation that was not subject to affirmative resolution on
being made.

3.10

Regulations under this section to which subsection (9) does not apply are
subject to the affirmative procedure.

##### Power to restate and modify saved legislation

4

4.1

The power under section 86(5) to make saving provision in connection with the
revocation of any legislation referred to in Schedule 1 includes power to
restate that legislation (as it has effect immediately before its revocation)—

4.1.a

by amending primary legislation or subordinate legislation, or

4.1.b

by making new subordinate legislation.

4.2

Regulations made by virtue of subsection (1) may make such modifications of
the legislation being restated as the Treasury consider necessary or desirable
for or in connection with—

4.2.a

the purpose of making the law clearer or more accessible, or

4.2.b

any of the purposes mentioned in section 3(2).

4.3

Legislation restated by virtue of subsection (1) is not   assimilated   law.

4.4

Where legislation is restated by virtue of subsection (1), the Treasury may by
regulations make such further modifications of that legislation as they
consider necessary or desirable for or in connection with a purpose referred
to in subsection (2)(a) or (b).

4.5

Subsection (4) of section 3 applies to regulations made under, or by virtue
of, this section as it applies to regulations made under that section.

4.6

The power conferred by virtue of subsection (1) to restate legislation may be
exercised in relation to the entirety of that legislation or in relation to
such parts of it as the Treasury consider appropriate.

4.7

The power conferred by virtue of subsection (1) to restate legislation does
not include power to restate—

4.7.a

technical standards of the kind mentioned in section 138P(2)(a) of FSMA 2000,
or

4.7.b

EU tertiary legislation of the kind mentioned in section 138P(2)(b) of FSMA
2000.

4.8

Regulations made by virtue of this section that do not amend primary
legislation and contain provision restating only the following kinds of
legislation referred to in Schedule 1 are subject to the negative procedure—

4.8.a

EU tertiary legislation;

4.8.b

subordinate legislation that was not subject to affirmative resolution on
being made;

4.8.c

any other legislation, so far as restated without any modifications made for a
purpose mentioned in section 3(2).

4.9

Regulations made by virtue of this section to which subsection (8) does not
apply are subject to the affirmative procedure.

##### Power to replace references to EU directives

5

5.1

The Treasury may by regulations modify legislation for or in connection with
the purpose of replacing any reference (however expressed) to an EU directive
referred to in Part 3 of Schedule 1 with such other provision (if any) as the
Treasury consider appropriate.

5.2

The power under subsection (1) is exercisable only if the Treasury consider it
necessary or desirable to replace the reference for or in connection with—

5.2.a

the purpose of making the law clearer or more accessible, or

5.2.b

any of the purposes mentioned in section 3(2).

5.3

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative procedure if
they amend primary legislation.

5.4

Regulations under this section to which subsection (3) does not apply are
subject to the negative procedure.

##### Restatement in rules: exemption from consultation requirements etc

6

6.1

A relevant requirement does not apply to the making of rules by a regulator if
and to the extent that—

6.1.a

the proposed rules make excluded provision in relation to provisions of
legislation referred to in Schedule 1, and

6.1.b

those provisions of legislation are specified, or fall within a description of
provisions specified, in relation to the making of rules by the regulator in
regulations made by the Treasury for the purposes of this section.

6.2

A relevant requirement does not apply to the making of rules by a regulator if
and to the extent that—

6.2.a

the proposed rules make excluded changes to provision of existing rules made
by the regulator containing   an assimilated   obligation, and

6.2.b

  the assimilated   obligation is specified, or falls within a description of
obligations specified, in relation to the making of rules by the regulator in
regulations made by the Treasury for the purposes of this section.

6.3

A relevant requirement does not apply to the revocation of rules by a
regulator if and to the extent that—

6.3.a

the rules being revoked make provision containing   an assimilated
obligation, and

6.3.b

the rules are revoked without being replaced by other rules made by the
regulator.

6.4

For the purposes of subsection (1), rules make excluded provision in relation
to provisions of legislation if, in the opinion of the regulator making the
rules, the rules reproduce those provisions—

6.4.a

without any changes that are material, or

6.4.b

with changes that are material but their effect is to reduce a regulatory
burden without having any other effects that are material.

6.5

For the purposes of subsection (2), rules make excluded changes to provision
of existing rules if, in the opinion of the regulator making the rules—

6.5.a

the effect of the changes is to reduce a regulatory burden, and

6.5.b

the changes have no other effects that are material.

6.6

In this section references to a “regulatory burden” include (among other
things) references to—

6.6.a

a financial cost;

6.6.b

an administrative inconvenience;

6.6.c

an obstacle to trade or innovation;

6.6.d

an obstacle to efficiency, productivity or profitability.

6.7

Where a relevant requirement does not apply to the making or revocation of
rules by virtue of subsection (1), (2) or (3), the requirement also does not
apply to any rules that contain incidental, supplemental, consequential or
transitional provision so far as made in connection with provision made by
virtue of that subsection.

6.8

“ Relevant requirement ” means—

6.8.a

in relation to rules made by the FCA, the requirements imposed by—

6.8.a.i

section 138I of FSMA 2000, except for subsection (1)(a), and

6.8.a.ii

section 138K of FSMA 2000;

6.8.b

in relation to rules made by the PRA, the requirements imposed by—

6.8.b.i

section 138J of FSMA 2000, except for subsection (1)(a), and

6.8.b.ii

section 138K of FSMA 2000;

6.8.c

in relation to rules made by the Bank of England, the requirements imposed by
paragraph 10(1)(i) of Schedule 17A to FSMA 2000;

6.8.d

in relation to rules made by the Payment Systems Regulator, the requirements
imposed by section 104 of the Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013,
except for subsection (2)(a).

6.9

Where a regulator makes or revokes rules without complying with a relevant
requirement by virtue of subsection (1), (2) or (3), the regulator must
publish a statement which must—

6.9.a

in a case falling within subsection (1), list the provisions of legislation
that have been restated by the rules;

6.9.b

in a case falling within subsection (2), specify or describe   the assimilated
obligations in relation to which changes have been made by the rules;

6.9.c

in a case falling within subsection (3), specify or describe   the assimilated
obligations that have been removed by the revocation of the rules.

6.10

Where the statement relates to the making of rules that include provision of a
kind mentioned in subsection (4)(b) or (5)(a) and (b), the statement must—

6.10.a

if made by the FCA, include an explanation of the FCA’s reasons for believing
that making the proposed rules is compatible with its duties under section
1B(1), (4A) and (5)(a) of FSMA 2000;

6.10.b

if made by the PRA, include an explanation of the PRA’s reasons for believing
that making the proposed rules is compatible with its duties under—

6.10.b.i

section 2B(1) or, as the case requires, section 2C(1) or 2D(3) of FSMA 2000,
and

6.10.b.ii

section 2H of FSMA 2000;

6.10.c

if made by the Bank of England, include an explanation of the Bank’s reasons
for believing that making the proposed rules is compatible with—

6.10.c.i

the Bank’s financial stability objective under section 2A of the Bank of
England Act 1998, and

6.10.c.ii

the Bank’s duties under section 30D(1)(a) of that Act;

6.10.d

if made by the Payment Systems Regulator, include an explanation of the
Regulator’s reasons for believing that making the proposed rules is compatible
with its duties under section 49 of the Financial Services (Banking Reform)
Act 2013.

6.11

The statement must be published in the way appearing to the regulator to be
best calculated to bring the statement to the attention of the public.

6.12

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative procedure.

6.13

In this section “rules”—

6.13.a

in relation to the Payment Systems Regulator, means—

6.13.a.i

generally applicable requirements within the meaning of Part 5 of the
Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013 (as amended by Schedule 7 to this
Act), or

6.13.a.ii

directions of general application imposed under any other enactment;

6.13.b

in relation to any other regulator, means rules made by that regulator under
FSMA 2000 or any other enactment.

##### Interpretation of Chapter

7

7.1

In this Chapter—

“ EU directive ” means a directive within the meaning of Article 288 of the
Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union; “ EU tertiary legislation ”
has the same meaning as in the European Union (Withdrawal) Act 2018 (see
section 20(1)); “ legislation ” means primary legislation,   assimilated
direct   legislation or subordinate legislation; “ regulator ” means— the FCA,
the PRA, the Bank of England, or the Payment Systems Regulator; “ the
transitional period ” has the meaning given in section 2(2).

7.2

For the purposes of this Chapter, references to legislation do not include
references to rules made by a regulator.

7.3

For the purposes of this Chapter, subordinate legislation was subject to
affirmative resolution on being made if it was made with approval given by a
resolution of each House of Parliament (whether before or after it was made).

7.4

References in this Chapter to the revocation of legislation are, in relation
to the legislation referred to in Part 4 of Schedule 1, to be read as
references to its repeal.

#### New regulatory powers

##### Designated activities regime

###### Designated activities

8

8.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

8.2

After Part 5 insert—

############ Designated activities

############# Designated activities

8.2.71K

8.2.71K.1

The Treasury may by regulations provide for an activity of a specified
description to be a designated activity for the purposes of this Act.

8.2.71K.2

Regulations under this section are referred to in this Act as designated
activity regulations.

8.2.71K.3

Designated activity regulations may provide for an activity to be a designated
activity only if the activity relates or is connected to—

8.2.71K.3.a

the financial markets or exchanges of the United Kingdom, or

8.2.71K.3.b

financial instruments, financial products or financial investments that are
(or are proposed to be) issued or sold to, or by, persons in the United
Kingdom.

8.2.71K.4

The description of an activity as a designated activity may be framed by
reference to—

8.2.71K.4.a

the way in which the activity is carried on, or

8.2.71K.4.b

the description of persons who carry on the activity.

8.2.71K.5

Schedule 6B contains examples of activities that may be specified as
designated activities.

8.2.71K.6

Nothing in Schedule 6B limits the powers conferred by subsection (1).

8.2.71K.7

The financial instruments, financial products and financial investments
mentioned in subsection (3)(b) may include cryptoassets.

############# Restrictions on carrying on of designated activities

8.2.71L

8.2.71L.1

A person must not carry on a designated activity if, or to the extent that,
designated activity regulations prohibit the carrying on of that activity.

8.2.71L.2

A person carrying on a designated activity that is not prohibited by virtue of
subsection (1) must comply with—

8.2.71L.2.a

designated activity rules relating to that activity, and

8.2.71L.2.b

any other requirements imposed in relation to that activity by designated
activity regulations.

8.2.71L.3

For the purposes of this Act designated activity rules are rules made under
section 71N.

############# Designated activity regulations: general

8.2.71M

8.2.71M.1

Designated activity regulations may make provision generally in relation to
the carrying on of designated activities.

8.2.71M.2

The following are examples of provision that may be made by designated
activity regulations—

8.2.71M.2.a

provision about cases in which the restrictions imposed by section 71L are to
apply to persons carrying on a designated activity outside the United Kingdom;

8.2.71M.2.b

provision supplementing, or in connection with, any requirements relating to a
designated activity under designated activity rules.

8.2.71M.3

Designated activity regulations may—

8.2.71M.3.a

provide for exemptions (including exemptions that are subject to specified
conditions);

8.2.71M.3.b

confer powers on the Treasury or the FCA.

############# Designated activities: rules

8.2.71N

8.2.71N.1

The FCA may make rules relating to designated activities.

8.2.71N.2

The power under subsection (1) is only exercisable in so far as designated
activity regulations provide for the FCA to make rules—

8.2.71N.2.a

relating to the designated activity, or

8.2.71N.2.b

relating to specified matters relating to designated activities.

8.2.71N.3

The FCA may by notice suspend any rules made under subsection (1) for such
period as it considers appropriate.

8.2.71N.4

Rules under subsection (1) may include provision enabling requirements imposed
by the rules to be dispensed with, or modified, in such cases or circumstances
as may be determined by the FCA under the rules (subject to subsection (5)).

8.2.71N.5

The powers under subsections (3) and (4) are only exercisable in such
circumstances as may be specified in designated activity regulations.

8.2.71N.6

Before suspending any rules in accordance with subsection (3), the FCA must
consult the PRA.

8.2.71N.7

A notice under subsection (3) must be published by the FCA in the way
appearing to the FCA to be best calculated to bring it to the attention of
persons likely to be affected by it.

8.2.71N.8

The reference in section 137T(a) (supplementary powers) to “ authorised
persons ” includes, in relation to rules made under this section, a reference
to any persons to whom the rules under this section apply.

############# Designated activities: directions

8.2.71O

8.2.71O.1

The FCA may by directions impose such requirements on a person, or such
description of persons, relating to the carrying on of designated activities
as the FCA considers appropriate.

8.2.71O.2

The power under subsection (1) is only exercisable in so far as designated
activity regulations provide for the FCA to make directions relating to the
designated activity.

8.2.71O.3

A requirement may, in particular, be imposed so as to require the person
concerned—

8.2.71O.3.a

to take specified action, or

8.2.71O.3.b

to refrain from taking specified action.

8.2.71O.4

A requirement may extend to activities which are not designated activities.

8.2.71O.5

A direction under this section—

8.2.71O.5.a

may specify the way in which, and the time by which, a thing is to be done;

8.2.71O.5.b

may be varied;

8.2.71O.5.c

may be expressed to have effect during a specified period or until revoked.

8.2.71O.6

The FCA may at any time revoke a direction under this section by notice.

8.2.71O.7

The revocation of a direction does not affect the validity of anything
previously done in accordance with it.

8.2.71O.8

A direction or notice under this section must be given in writing to the
person or persons to whom it applies.

8.2.71O.9

But if in the circumstances the FCA considers it appropriate, the FCA may, in
addition to, or instead of, proceeding under subsection (8), publish the
direction or notice in the way appearing to the FCA to be best calculated to
bring it to the attention of persons likely to be affected by it.

8.2.71O.10

Designated activity regulations may make provision for the exercise of the
power under subsection (1) to be subject to such conditions as may be
specified in the regulations.

8.2.71O.11

Provision under subsection (10) may (among other things) require, where the
exercise of the power relates to a PRA-authorised person, consultation with
the PRA.

8.2.71O.12

The imposition of a requirement that expires at the end of a specified period
does not affect the FCA’s power to impose a new requirement.

############# Designated activities: liability

8.2.71P

8.2.71P.1

Designated activity regulations may make provision about liability and
compensation in connection with this Part.

8.2.71P.2

A contravention of a requirement under designated activity regulations or
designated activity rules—

8.2.71P.2.a

does not, except as provided by designated activity regulations under section
71Q or by regulations under section 71R, make a person guilty of an offence;

8.2.71P.2.b

does not, except as provided by designated activity regulations—

8.2.71P.2.b.i

make any transaction void or unenforceable, or

8.2.71P.2.b.ii

give rise to any action for breach of statutory duty.

8.2.71P.3

Designated activity regulations may in particular—

8.2.71P.3.a

in cases where the regulations make provision for liability, make provision
excluding civil liability (whether generally or to such extent as may be
specified),

8.2.71P.3.b

make provision for liability to be determined in accordance with designated
activity rules,

8.2.71P.3.c

make provision so that a person being subject to a liability includes another
person being entitled as against that person to rescind or repudiate an
agreement, and

8.2.71P.3.d

make provision for the purposes of subsection (1) by applying provisions of
this Act with or without modifications.

############# Designated activities: enforcement

8.2.71Q

8.2.71Q.1

Designated activity regulations may make provision about enforcement in
connection with this Part.

8.2.71Q.2

Provision about enforcement includes (among other things) provision—

8.2.71Q.2.a

requiring the supply of information;

8.2.71Q.2.b

about investigations (including the making of reports);

8.2.71Q.2.c

conferring powers of entry;

8.2.71Q.2.d

conferring powers of inspection, search and seizure;

8.2.71Q.2.e

conferring powers of censure;

8.2.71Q.2.f

imposing monetary penalties;

8.2.71Q.2.g

about appeals;

8.2.71Q.2.h

conferring functions (including functions involving the exercise of a
discretion) on a person.

8.2.71Q.3

Designated activity regulations may in particular make provision for the
purposes of subsection (1) by applying provisions of this Act with or without
modifications, including any criminal offences created by this Act (and
modifications made by virtue of this subsection may widen the scope of any
such offences).

8.2.71Q.4

The power under this section includes power to amend or repeal provisions of
this Act.

############# Designated activities and rules: connected amendments

8.2.71R

8.2.71R.1

The Treasury may by regulations make such modifications to provision made by
or under this Act or any other enactment as the Treasury consider appropriate
for purposes of, or connected with, any designated activity regulations or
designated activity rules.

8.2.71R.2

The power under subsection (1) may in particular be exercised for the purpose
of removing or varying any requirement imposed by or under this Act so far as
applying to the carrying on of any designated activity.

8.2.71R.3

The power under subsection (1) includes power to modify any criminal offence
created by this Act (including by widening the scope of any such offence).

8.2.71R.4

In this section—

      “ enactment ” includes—         an enactment comprised in subordinate
legislation (within the meaning given by section 21 of the Interpretation Act
1978),           an enactment comprised in, or in an instrument made under, a
Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru,           an enactment comprised in, or in an
instrument made under, an Act of the Scottish Parliament, and           an
enactment comprised in, or in an instrument made under, Northern Ireland
legislation;                 “ modify ” includes amend, repeal or revoke.

############# Designated activities regulations: Parliamentary control

8.2.71S

8.2.71S.1

This section applies to regulations which contain provision made under section
71K which provides for an activity of a specified description to be a
designated activity.

8.2.71S.2

A statutory instrument containing regulations to which this section applies,
other than regulations to which subsection (3) applies, may not be made unless
a draft of the instrument has been laid before Parliament and approved by a
resolution of each House.

8.2.71S.3

This subsection applies to regulations which contain a statement made by the
Treasury that they are of the opinion that, by reason of urgency, it is
necessary to make the regulations without a draft of the statutory instrument
containing the regulations being laid and approved under subsection (2).

8.2.71S.4

Where subsection (3) applies to regulations, a statutory instrument containing
the regulations must be laid before Parliament after being made.

8.2.71S.5

Regulations contained in a statutory instrument laid before Parliament under
subsection (4) cease to have effect at the end of the period of 28 days
beginning with the day on which the instrument is made unless, during that
period, the instrument is approved by a resolution of each House of
Parliament.

8.2.71S.6

In calculating the period of 28 days, no account is to be taken of any whole
days that fall within a period during which—

8.2.71S.6.a

Parliament is dissolved or prorogued, or

8.2.71S.6.b

either House of Parliament is adjourned for more than four days.

8.2.71S.7

If regulations cease to have effect as a result of subsection (5), that does
not—

8.2.71S.7.a

affect the validity of anything previously done under the regulations, or

8.2.71S.7.b

prevent the making of new regulations.

8.3

The following amendments are related to the new Part 5A of FSMA 2000 inserted
by subsection (2).

8.4

In section 3E (memorandum of understanding), in subsection (2) after paragraph
(g) insert—

8.4.ga

directions under section 71O (designated activities: directions);

.

8.5

In section 3I (power of PRA to require the FCA to refrain from specified
action), in subsection (3) in paragraph (a)—

8.5.a

the words from “its powers in relation to the” to the end become sub-paragraph
(i), and

8.5.b

after that sub-paragraph insert

, or

8.5.b.ii

its powers in relation to designated activities under Part 5A;

.

8.6

##### Financial market infrastructure: general rules and requirements

###### Rules relating to central counterparties and central securities depositories

9

9.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

9.2

After section 300E (power to disallow excessive regulatory provision:
supplementary) insert—

############ General rule-making powers

############# Rules relating to central counterparties and central securities depositories

9.2.300F

9.2.300F.1

The Bank of England may make such rules applying to FMI entities—

9.2.300F.1.a

with respect to the carrying on by them of relevant regulated activities, or

9.2.300F.1.b

with respect to the carrying on by them of an activity which is not a relevant
regulated activity,

as appear to the Bank to be necessary or expedient for the purpose of
advancing its Financial Stability Objective.

9.2.300F.2

Each of the following is an “ FMI entity ” for the purposes of this section—

9.2.300F.2.a

a recognised central counterparty;

9.2.300F.2.b

a recognised CSD;

9.2.300F.2.c

a third country central counterparty;

9.2.300F.2.d

a third country CSD.

9.2.300F.3

The power to make rules under subsection (1), so far as applying to a third
country central counterparty or a third country CSD, is subject to section
300G.

9.2.300F.4

In this section “relevant regulated activity”—

9.2.300F.4.a

in relation to a recognised central counterparty, means a regulated activity
described in section 285(3A);

9.2.300F.4.b

in relation to a recognised CSD, means a regulated activity described in
section 285(3D);

9.2.300F.4.c

in relation to a third country central counterparty, means a regulated
activity described in section 285(3C);

9.2.300F.4.d

in relation to a third country CSD, means a regulated activity described in
section 285(3G).

9.2.300F.5

Rules under this section may include—

9.2.300F.5.a

provision applying to an FMI entity even though there is no relationship
between the entity to which the rules will apply and the persons whose
interests will be protected by the rules;

9.2.300F.5.b

requirements which take into account, in the case of an FMI entity which is a
member of a group, any activity of another member of the group.

############# Section 300F: rules in relation to overseas FMI entities

9.2.300G

9.2.300G.1

The power to make rules under section 300F, so far as applying to an FMI
entity of the kind mentioned in subsection (2)(c) or (d) of that section (an
“overseas FMI entity”), is exercisable—

9.2.300G.1.a

only by the application of corresponding rules, and

9.2.300G.1.b

except in the case of systemic third country CCPs (see subsection (6)), only
so far as authorised by regulations made by the Treasury.

9.2.300G.2

The reference in subsection (1)(a) to “corresponding rules” is—

9.2.300G.2.a

in relation to rules that would apply to a third country central counterparty,
rules under section 300F that apply to a recognised central counterparty;

9.2.300G.2.b

in relation to rules that would apply to a third country CSD, rules under
section 300F that apply to a recognised CSD.

9.2.300G.3

Rules may be applied in accordance with subsection (1)(a)—

9.2.300G.3.a

by applying all corresponding rules or only such corresponding rules as the
Bank considers appropriate;

9.2.300G.3.b

with such modifications as the Bank considers appropriate for the purpose of
ensuring the effectiveness of the rules in their application to the overseas
FMI entities concerned (having regard in particular to the establishment of
such entities in countries other than the United Kingdom).

9.2.300G.4

Regulations under subsection (1)(b) may authorise the making of rules
generally in respect of overseas FMI entities or only in respect of overseas
FMI entities which—

9.2.300G.4.a

are specified or described in the regulations, or

9.2.300G.4.b

satisfy conditions specified in the regulations.

9.2.300G.5

Regulations under subsection (1)(b) may—

9.2.300G.5.a

provide for the power to make rules under section 300F, so far as applying to
an overseas FMI entity, to be subject to such limitations or conditions as may
be specified in the regulations;

9.2.300G.5.b

make provision by reference to matters to be determined by the Bank;

9.2.300G.5.c

provide for exemptions.

9.2.300G.6

The restriction imposed by subsection (1)(b) does not apply in the case of
systemic third country CCPs (and accordingly references to overseas FMI
entities in subsections (4) and (5) do not include references to systemic
third country CCPs).

9.2.300G.7

A “ systemic third country CCP ” means any third country central counterparty
that the Bank has determined is systemically important, or is likely to become
systemically important, to the financial stability of the United Kingdom.

9.2.300G.8

The Bank must publish notice of any determination made under subsection (7).

9.2.300G.9

A determination under subsection (7) must be made in accordance with such
criteria of general application as are set out in regulations made by the
Treasury for the purposes of this section.

9.2.300G.10

In making a determination under subsection (7) the Bank must also have regard
to any statement of policy prepared and published by the Bank for the purposes
of providing further specification of the criteria of general application
mentioned in subsection (9).

9.2.300G.11

The Bank—

9.2.300G.11.a

may alter or replace a statement of policy prepared for the purposes of this
section;

9.2.300G.11.b

must publish a statement as altered or replaced.

9.2.300G.12

Publication under this section is to be made in such manner as the Bank
considers best designed to bring the publication to the attention of the
public.

9.2.300G.13

The Treasury must consult the Bank before making regulations under subsection
(9).

9.2.300G.14

The Treasury may by regulations provide for other provisions of this Act to
apply in relation to third country central counterparties, or third country
CSDs, to which rules under section 300F apply, with such modifications as may
be specified in the regulations.

9.3

In section 165 (regulators’ power to require information: authorised persons
etc) omit subsection (8A).

9.4

In section 165A (PRA’s power to require information: financial stability) omit
subsection (7A).

9.5

In section 293 (notification requirements)—

9.5.a

in subsection (7A) at the end insert  “and a third country central
counterparty” ;

9.5.b

in subsection (8) for “or an overseas clearing house” substitute  “, an
overseas clearing house or a third country central counterparty” .

9.6

In section 417(1) (definitions), at the appropriate place insert—

      “ Financial Stability Objective ” means the objective set out in section
2A of the Bank of England Act 1998;

.

###### Central counterparties and central securities depositories: other requirements

10

In Schedule 17A to FSMA 2000 (further provision in relation to exercise of
Part 18 functions by Bank of England), before paragraph 10 (and the heading
before it) insert—

########## Requirements

10.9B

10.9B.1

The powers conferred by section 55L(3) (FCA own-initiative power to impose
requirements on authorised persons) are exercisable by the Bank to impose
requirements on a relevant FMI entity.

10.9B.2

In this paragraph “ relevant FMI entity ” means—

10.9B.2.a

a recognised central counterparty,

10.9B.2.b

a recognised CSD, or

10.9B.2.c

a systemic third country CCP as defined by section 300G(7).

10.9B.3

The power under sub-paragraph (1) is exercisable only if it appears to the
Bank that either (or both) of the following conditions is met.

10.9B.4

The first condition is that it is desirable to exercise the power in order to
advance the Financial Stability Objective.

10.9B.5

The second condition is that the relevant FMI entity—

10.9B.5.a

has failed, or is likely to fail, to satisfy the recognition requirements, or

10.9B.5.b

has failed to comply with any other obligation imposed on it by or under this
Act.

10.9B.6

The power conferred by sub-paragraph (1) may not be exercised so as to
restrict or prohibit discretionary payments to employees or shareholders of a
recognised central counterparty (and for this purpose “ discretionary payment
” has the meaning given by paragraph 13(11) of Schedule 11 to the Financial
Services and Markets Act 2023 and “ employee ” has the meaning given by
paragraph 154 of that Schedule).

10.9B.7

The powers conferred by section 55L(5) (FCA power to impose requirements on
application of authorised persons with Part 4A permission) are exercisable by
the Bank to impose requirements on a relevant FMI entity on the application of
that entity.

10.9B.8

A power conferred by this paragraph is exercisable whether or not there is a
relationship between the entity in relation to which it is exercised and the
persons whose interests will be protected by its exercise.

10.9B.9

The following provisions apply in relation to requirements imposed by the Bank
under this paragraph as they apply in relation to requirements imposed by the
FCA under section 55L, with the modifications in sub-paragraph (10)—

10.9B.9.a

section 55L(6) (power to refuse application to impose etc requirements);

10.9B.9.b

section 55N (further provision in relation to requirements);

10.9B.9.c

section 55P (prohibitions and restrictions);

10.9B.9.d

section 55Q (exercise of power in support of overseas regulator);

10.9B.9.e

section 55R(1) (persons connected with applicant);

10.9B.9.f

section 55U(3) to (8) (applications for requirement to be imposed etc);

10.9B.9.g

section 55V(1) to (6) (determination of applications);

10.9B.9.h

section 55X(2) and (4)(f) (warning and decision notices on refusal of
applications);

10.9B.9.i

section 55Y (exercise of own-initiative power: procedure);

10.9B.9.j

section 55Z3(1) and (2) (right to refer matters to the Tribunal).

10.9B.10

The modifications are—

10.9B.10.a

any reference to the FCA is to be read as a reference to the Bank;

10.9B.10.b

any references to own-initiative powers are to be read as references to the
power conferred by sub-paragraph (1);

10.9B.10.c

any references to an authorised person are to be read as references to
relevant FMI entities;

10.9B.10.d

in section 55L(6), the reference to the FCA’s operational objectives is to be
read as a reference to the Bank’s Financial Stability Objective;

10.9B.10.e

section 55N has effect as if the reference to regulated activities in
subsection (2) were a reference to activities in respect of which a
recognition order is in force.

##### Financial market infrastructure: piloting powers

###### Testing of FMI technologies or practices

13

13.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision for the purposes of—

13.1.a

testing, for a limited period, the efficiency or effectiveness of the carrying
on of FMI activities in a particular way, and

13.1.b

assessing whether or how relevant enactments should apply in relation to FMI
activities carried on in that way.

13.2

The reference in subsection (1)(a) to FMI activities being carried on in a
particular way includes a reference to—

13.2.a

the use of developing technology in the carrying on of FMI activities;

13.2.b

the adoption of new or different practices in the carrying on of FMI
activities.

13.3

Provision made in regulations under subsection (1) is referred to in this
group of sections as an FMI sandbox.

13.4

An FMI sandbox must specify or otherwise provide for—

13.4.a

the FMI activities to which the FMI sandbox arrangements relate;

13.4.b

the description—

13.4.b.i

of FMI entities eligible to participate in the FMI sandbox arrangements, and

13.4.b.ii

of any other persons (including in particular the users of services provided
by FMI entities) eligible to so participate;

13.4.c

the limited period for which the FMI sandbox arrangements apply.

13.5

An FMI sandbox may confer functions on the appropriate regulator in connection
with the implementation and operation of the FMI sandbox arrangements.

13.6

An FMI sandbox may—

13.6.a

provide for a relevant enactment not to apply for the purposes of the FMI
sandbox arrangements;

13.6.b

provide for modifications in the application of a relevant enactment for those
purposes;

13.6.c

provide for the application of a relevant enactment (with or without
modifications) for those purposes;

but provision under this subsection may not amend, repeal or revoke a relevant
enactment.

13.7

In the case of a relevant enactment that is a rule or another instrument made
by an appropriate regulator, provision under subsection (6) may provide for
the powers under that subsection to be exercisable by that regulator.

13.8

Schedule 4 contains further examples of types of provision that an FMI sandbox
may make.

13.9

An FMI sandbox—

13.9.a

may be replaced by another FMI sandbox of the same or similar effect;

13.9.b

may have effect at the same time as one or more other FMI sandboxes.

13.10

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative procedure.

13.11

For the purposes of this group of sections—

13.11.a

“ FMI entity ” means—

13.11.a.i

a recognised investment exchange that is not an overseas investment exchange;

13.11.a.ii

a recognised CSD;

13.11.a.iii

the operator of a multilateral trading facility;

13.11.a.iv

the operator of an organised trading facility;

13.11.a.v

such other persons as may be specified in regulations under this section as
eligible to participate in the FMI sandbox arrangements concerned;

13.11.b

“FMI activities” are any activities carried on as part of the business of an
FMI entity;

13.11.c

“ FMI sandbox arrangements ” means any arrangements implemented as part of an
FMI sandbox.

###### Reports on FMI sandboxes

14

14.1

This section applies where the Treasury make regulations under section 13
implementing FMI sandbox arrangements.

14.2

The Treasury must prepare and publish a report on the FMI sandbox
arrangements.

14.3

The report must be prepared by a date no later than the date specified in the
regulations.

14.4

The report must contain—

14.4.a

a description of the FMI sandbox arrangements;

14.4.b

an assessment of the efficiency or effectiveness of those arrangements;

14.4.c

whether, and if so how, the Treasury propose exercising the power under
section 15 in relation to those arrangements.

14.5

The Treasury must consult the appropriate regulator in preparing the report.

14.6

The appropriate regulator must provide to the Treasury such information or
other assistance as the Treasury may require for the purposes of preparing the
report.

14.7

The Treasury must lay a copy of the report before Parliament.

###### Permanent implementation of arrangements tested under an FMI sandbox

15

15.1

This section applies where, after testing the efficiency or effectiveness of
FMI sandbox arrangements implemented under an FMI sandbox, the Treasury
determine that arrangements of the same or similar effect should have effect
after the expiry of the FMI sandbox.

15.2

The Treasury may by regulations make provision implementing the FMI sandbox
arrangements—

15.2.a

as tested under the FMI sandbox, or

15.2.b

with such variations as the Treasury consider appropriate.

15.3

Regulations under this section that implement FMI sandbox arrangements may be
made before (as well as after) the expiry of the FMI sandbox concerned.

15.4

Regulations under this section may include provision that amends, repeals or
revokes a relevant enactment.

15.5

Regulations under this section that amend, repeal or revoke any provision of
primary legislation are subject to the affirmative procedure.

15.6

Regulations under this section to which subsection (5) does not apply are
subject to the negative procedure.

###### Regulations

16

16.1

A power to make regulations under this group of sections includes power
conferring a discretion on an appropriate regulator, or another specified
person, to do anything under, or for the purposes of, the regulations.

16.2

Before making regulations under this group of sections the Treasury must
consult—

16.2.a

the appropriate regulators;

16.2.b

such other persons as the Treasury consider appropriate.

###### Interpretation

17

17.1

This section applies for the purposes of this section and sections 13 to 16.

17.2

The “ appropriate regulator ”, in relation to an FMI sandbox, means the
regulator specified in that sandbox as the appropriate regulator (and both of
the regulators may be specified); and for this purpose “ regulator ” means—

17.2.a

the FCA, or

17.2.b

the Bank of England.

17.3

“ Relevant enactment ” means any provision made by or under—

17.3.a

FSMA 2000;

17.3.b

the Companies Act 2006;

17.3.c

the Financial Markets Insolvency (Settlement Finality) Regulations 1999 ( S.I.
1999/2979 );

17.3.d

the Uncertificated Securities Regulations 2001 ( S.I. 2001/3755 );

17.3.e

the Financial Collateral Arrangements (No. 2) Regulations 2003 ( S.I.
2003/3226 );

17.3.f

Regulation (EU) No 596/2014  of the European Parliament and of the Council of
16 April 2014 on market abuse (market abuse regulation);

17.3.g

Regulation (EU) No 600/2014  of the European Parliament and of the Council of
15 May 2014 on markets in financial instruments;

17.3.h

Regulation (EU) No 909/2014  of the European Parliament and of the Council of
23 July 2014 on improving securities settlement in the European Union and on
central securities depositories;

17.3.i

Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2017/565  of 25 April 2016 supplementing
Directive 2014/65/EU  of the European Parliament and of the Council as regards
organisational requirements and operating conditions for investment firms and
defined terms for the purposes of that Directive.

17.4

The following terms are defined as follows—

      “ FMI activities ” has the meaning given by section 13(11)(b);
“ FMI entity ” has the meaning given by section 13(11)(a);           “ FMI
sandbox ” has the meaning given by section 13(3);           “ FMI sandbox
arrangements ” has the meaning given by section 13(11)(c);           “ this
group of sections ” means the sections referred to in subsection (1).

17.5

The following terms have the same meanings as in Part 18 of FSMA 2000—

      “multilateral trading facility”;           “organised trading facility”;
“overseas investment exchange”;           “recognised investment exchange”;
“recognised CSD”.

17.6

The Treasury may by regulations amend subsection (3) so as to add to the list
of relevant enactments.

17.7

Regulations under subsection (6) are subject to the affirmative procedure.

##### Powers in relation to critical third parties

###### Critical third parties: designation and powers

18

18.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

18.2

In the heading to Part 18, for “and CSDs” substitute  “, CSDs and other
parties” .

18.3

After section 312K (statement of policy: procedure) insert—

############ Critical third parties

############# Critical third parties

18.3.312L

18.3.312L.1

The Treasury may by regulations designate a person who provides services to
one or more authorised persons, relevant service providers or FMI entities as
a “critical third party”.

18.3.312L.2

The Treasury may designate a person under subsection (1) only if in the
Treasury’s opinion a failure in, or disruption to, the provision of those
services (either individually or, where more than one service is provided,
taken together) could threaten the stability of, or confidence in, the UK
financial system.

18.3.312L.3

The Treasury must have regard to the following factors when forming an opinion
for the purposes of subsection (2)—

18.3.312L.3.a

the materiality of the services provided to the delivery, by any person, of
essential activities, services or operations (wherever carried out);

18.3.312L.3.b

the number and type of authorised persons, relevant service providers or FMI
entities to which the person provides services.

18.3.312L.4

Before making regulations under subsection (1) the Treasury must—

18.3.312L.4.a

consult each of the relevant regulators and such other persons as the Treasury
consider appropriate,

18.3.312L.4.b

give notice in writing to the person to be designated specifying a reasonable
period within which that person may make representations in writing about the
proposal to the Treasury, and

18.3.312L.4.c

have regard to any representations made to them in accordance with paragraph
(b).

18.3.312L.5

The Treasury may not designate the Bank of England under subsection (1).

18.3.312L.6

Each of the following is a relevant regulator for the purposes of this
Chapter—

18.3.312L.6.a

the FCA,

18.3.312L.6.b

the PRA, and

18.3.312L.6.c

the Bank of England.

18.3.312L.7

Activities, services or operations are “ essential ” for the purposes of
subsection (3) if they are essential to—

18.3.312L.7.a

the economy of the United Kingdom, or

18.3.312L.7.b

the stability of, or confidence in, the UK financial system.

18.3.312L.8

In this Chapter—

      “ critical third party ” means a person designated under subsection (1);
“ FMI entity ” means—         a recognised clearing house;           a
recognised CSD;           a recognised investment exchange which is not an
overseas investment exchange;           a recognised payment system under
section 184 of the Banking Act 2009;           a person specified as a service
provider in relation to a recognised payment system under section 206A of the
Banking Act 2009;                 “ relevant service provider ” means—
an electronic money institution as defined by regulation 2(1) of the
Electronic Money Regulations 2011 ( S.I. 2011/99 );           an authorised
payment institution, small payment institution or registered account
information services provider as defined by regulation 2(1) of the Payment
Services Regulations 2017 ( S.I. 2017/752 );                 “ service ”
includes facility.

############# Power to make rules

18.3.312M

18.3.312M.1

A relevant regulator may make such rules imposing duties on critical third
parties in connection with the provision of services to authorised persons,
relevant service providers and FMI entities as appear to the regulator to be
necessary or expedient for the purpose of advancing any of its objectives.

18.3.312M.2

The reference in subsection (1) to a relevant regulator’s objectives is a
reference to—

18.3.312M.2.a

where the regulator is the FCA, one or more of its operational objectives;

18.3.312M.2.b

where the regulator is the PRA, one or more of its objectives;

18.3.312M.2.c

where the regulator is the Bank, the Bank’s Financial Stability Objective.

18.3.312M.3

In the application of Part 9A to rules made by the FCA or the PRA under this
section, the following provisions apply with the modifications specified in
this subsection—

18.3.312M.3.a

section 137T (general supplementary powers) applies as if—

18.3.312M.3.a.i

the reference in paragraph (a) to “authorised persons, activity or investment”
were a reference to “critical third parties or services”, and

18.3.312M.3.a.ii

in paragraph (b) for the words from “as” to the end there were substituted
“or the Bank, or standards issued by any other person, as those rules or
standards have effect from time to time,” ;

18.3.312M.3.b

section 138B (publication of directions) applies as if subsection (4) were
omitted;

18.3.312M.3.c

section 138F (notification of rules) applies as if subsections (1A) and (2)
were omitted;

18.3.312M.3.d

section 138I (consultation) applies as if the reference in subsection (1)(a)
to the “PRA” were a reference to the “ PRA and the Bank ”;

18.3.312M.3.e

section 138J (consultation) applies as if the reference in subsection (1)(a)
to the “FCA” were a reference to the “ FCA and the Bank ”.

############# Power of direction

18.3.312N

18.3.312N.1

A relevant regulator may, if it appears to the regulator to be necessary or
expedient for the purpose of advancing any of its objectives, direct a
critical third party to—

18.3.312N.1.a

do anything specified in the direction, or

18.3.312N.1.b

refrain from doing anything specified in the direction.

18.3.312N.2

A direction under this section—

18.3.312N.2.a

must be given by notice in writing,

18.3.312N.2.b

may be expressed to have effect during a specified period or until revoked,
and

18.3.312N.2.c

may specify the way in which, and the time by which, a thing is to be done.

18.3.312N.3

Subsection (4) applies if a direction is given to a critical third party for
the purpose of resolving or reducing a threat to the stability or integrity of
the UK financial system.

18.3.312N.4

The critical third party (including the critical third party’s officers and
staff) has immunity from liability in damages in respect of action or inaction
in accordance with the direction.

18.3.312N.5

A direction given for the purpose mentioned in subsection (3) must—

18.3.312N.5.a

include a statement that it is given for that purpose, and

18.3.312N.5.b

inform the critical third party of the effect of subsection (4).

18.3.312N.6

An immunity conferred by this section does not extend to action or inaction—

18.3.312N.6.a

in bad faith, or

18.3.312N.6.b

in contravention of section 6(1) of the Human Rights Act 1998.

18.3.312N.7

A relevant regulator may at any time revoke a direction under this section by
giving notice in writing to the critical third party to which the direction
relates.

18.3.312N.8

The revocation of the direction does not affect the validity of anything
previously done in accordance with it.

18.3.312N.9

For the purposes of this section the objectives of a relevant regulator are as
described in section 312M(2).

############# Directions: procedure

18.3.312O

18.3.312O.1

If a relevant regulator proposes to give a direction under section 312N, or
gives such a direction with immediate effect, it must give written notice to
the critical third party to which the direction is given (or is to be given)
(the “relevant critical third party”).

18.3.312O.2

A direction under section 312N takes effect—

18.3.312O.2.a

immediately, if the notice under subsection (1) states that this is the case,

18.3.312O.2.b

on such other date as may be specified in the notice, or

18.3.312O.2.c

if neither paragraph (a) or (b) applies, when the matter to which the notice
relates is no longer open to review.

18.3.312O.3

A direction may be expressed to take effect immediately, or on a specified
date, only if the relevant regulator reasonably considers that it is necessary
for the direction to take effect immediately or on that date.

18.3.312O.4

The notice under subsection (1) must—

18.3.312O.4.a

give details of the direction,

18.3.312O.4.b

state the relevant regulator’s reasons for the direction and for its
determination as to when the direction takes effect,

18.3.312O.4.c

inform the relevant critical third party that it may make representations to
the regulator within such period as may be specified in the notice (whether or
not the critical third party has referred the matter to the Tribunal), and

18.3.312O.4.d

inform the relevant critical third party of its right to refer the matter to
the Tribunal (including giving an indication of the procedure on such a
reference).

18.3.312O.5

The relevant regulator may extend the period allowed under the notice for
making representations.

18.3.312O.6

If, having considered any representations made by the relevant critical third
party, the regulator decides—

18.3.312O.6.a

to give the direction proposed, or

18.3.312O.6.b

if the direction has been given, not to revoke the direction,

it must give the critical third party written notice.

18.3.312O.7

If, having considered any representations made by the relevant critical third
party, the regulator decides—

18.3.312O.7.a

not to give the direction proposed,

18.3.312O.7.b

to give a different direction, or

18.3.312O.7.c

to revoke a direction which has effect,

it must give the critical third party written notice.

18.3.312O.8

A notice given under subsection (6) must inform the relevant critical third
party of its right to refer the matter to the Tribunal (including giving an
indication of the procedure on such a reference).

18.3.312O.9

A notice under subsection (7)(b) must comply with subsection (4).

18.3.312O.10

For the purposes of subsection (2)(c), whether a matter is open to review is
to be determined in accordance with section 391(8).

############# Information gathering and investigations

18.3.312P

18.3.312P.1

The provisions of Part 11 (information gathering and investigations) mentioned
in this section are to apply in relation to this Chapter in accordance with
the provision made by this section.

18.3.312P.2

In any case where subsection (1) applies—

18.3.312P.2.a

any reference in Part 11 to the FCA or PRA which is contained in, or relates
to, any of those provisions (however expressed) is to be read as a reference
to a relevant regulator, and

18.3.312P.2.b

Part 11 has effect with any other necessary modifications.

18.3.312P.3

The powers conferred by section 165(1) and (3) (power to require information)
are exercisable by a relevant regulator or (as the case may be) a relevant
regulator’s officers to impose requirements on a critical third party or a
person connected with a critical third party.

18.3.312P.4

The information or documents that a relevant regulator may require to be
produced or provided in accordance with subsection (3) are limited to
information and documents reasonably required in connection with the exercise
by the relevant regulator of functions conferred on it by or under this
Chapter (and accordingly section 165(4) does not apply).

18.3.312P.5

The power conferred by section 166 (reports by skilled person) is exercisable
by a relevant regulator in relation to a critical third party or a person
connected with a critical third party.

18.3.312P.6

The power conferred by section 166A (appointment of skilled person) is
exercisable by a relevant regulator in relation to a critical third party.

18.3.312P.7

The power conferred by section 168(5) (appointment of persons to carry out
investigations in particular cases) is exercisable by a relevant regulator if
it appears to the relevant regulator that there are circumstances suggesting
that a person may have contravened any requirement imposed by or under this
Chapter.

18.3.312P.8

In addition to the powers conferred by section 171, a person conducting an
investigation under section 168(5) as a result of subsection (7) is to have
the powers conferred by sections 172 and 173 (and for this purpose any
references in those sections to an investigator are to be read accordingly).

18.3.312P.9

The power under section 176(1) (entry of premises under warrant) is
exercisable on information on oath given by or on behalf of a relevant
regulator, or an investigator appointed by a relevant regulator, as if the
reference to the third set of conditions were omitted.

18.3.312P.10

For the purposes of this section a person is connected with a critical third
party if that person is or has at any relevant time been—

18.3.312P.10.a

a member of the critical third party’s group,

18.3.312P.10.b

a controller of the critical third party, or

18.3.312P.10.c

in relation to the critical third party, a person mentioned in Part 1 of
Schedule 15 (reading references in that Part to the authorised person as
references to the critical third party).

############# Power of censure

18.3.312Q

If a relevant regulator considers that a critical third party has contravened
a requirement imposed by or under this Chapter the regulator may publish a
statement to that effect.

############# Disciplinary measures

18.3.312R

18.3.312R.1

This section applies if a relevant regulator considers that a critical third
party has contravened a requirement imposed by or under this Chapter.

18.3.312R.2

The relevant regulator may publish a notice—

18.3.312R.2.a

prohibiting the critical third party from entering into arrangements, or
continuing, to provide services to authorised persons, relevant service
providers or FMI entities;

18.3.312R.2.b

prohibiting authorised persons, relevant service providers or FMI entities who
receive services from the critical third party from continuing to receive
those services from that party;

18.3.312R.2.c

prohibiting authorised persons, relevant service providers or FMI entities
from entering into arrangements for receipt of services from the critical
third party;

18.3.312R.2.d

providing for the provision of any services by the critical third party to be
subject to such conditions or limitations as are specified in the notice;

18.3.312R.2.e

providing for any receipt of services by authorised persons, relevant service
providers or FMI entities from the critical third party to be subject to such
conditions or limitations as are specified in the notice.

18.3.312R.3

A notice under subsection (2) may make different provision for different cases
and may in particular make different provision in respect of different
descriptions of services, authorised persons, FMI entities or relevant service
providers.

18.3.312R.4

A relevant regulator may only exercise the powers under subsection (2) if the
regulator is satisfied that—

18.3.312R.4.a

it is appropriate in the circumstances to take action against the critical
third party,

18.3.312R.4.b

the exercise of the power will not threaten the stability of, or confidence
in, the UK financial system, and

18.3.312R.4.c

it is desirable to exercise the power in order to advance one or more of the
regulator’s objectives.

18.3.312R.5

A relevant regulator may either on its own initiative or on an application by
the critical third party concerned withdraw or vary a notice given by it under
subsection (2) by publishing a further notice.

18.3.312R.6

Publication under this section is to be made in such manner as the relevant
regulator considers best designed to bring the publication to the attention of
the public.

18.3.312R.7

Where a notice includes a prohibition, condition or limitation imposed under
subsection (2), publication of a notice under this section must in particular
be made in a manner appearing to the relevant regulator to be best designed to
bring the notice to the attention of the persons to whom the prohibition,
condition or limitation applies.

18.3.312R.8

A person who breaches a prohibition, condition or limitation imposed by a
notice under this section is to be taken to have contravened a requirement
imposed on the person under this Act.

18.3.312R.9

For the purposes of this section the objectives of a relevant regulator are as
described in section 312M(2).

############# Procedure and right to refer to Tribunal

18.3.312S

18.3.312S.1

If a relevant regulator proposes to publish a statement or notice under
section 312Q or 312R, it must give the critical third party, authorised
persons, relevant service providers or FMI entities to whom the statement or
notice would relate a warning notice.

18.3.312S.2

A warning notice must set out the terms of the proposed statement or notice.

18.3.312S.3

If a relevant regulator decides to publish a statement or notice under section
312Q or 312R it must give the critical third party, authorised persons,
relevant service providers or FMI entities to whom the statement or notice
relates a decision notice.

18.3.312S.4

A decision notice must set out the terms of the statement or notice.

18.3.312S.5

If a relevant regulator decides to act under section 312N or 312Q a critical
third party who is aggrieved may refer the matter to the Tribunal.

18.3.312S.6

If a relevant regulator decides to act under section 312R a critical third
party, authorised person, relevant service provider or FMI entity who is
aggrieved may refer the matter to the Tribunal.

############# Statement of policy relating to disciplinary measures

18.3.312T

18.3.312T.1

The relevant regulators must prepare and publish a statement of policy with
respect to the exercise of powers under section 312Q and section 312R.

18.3.312T.2

The relevant regulators may alter or replace a statement published under this
section.

18.3.312T.3

The relevant regulators must publish a statement as altered or replaced under
subsection (2).

18.3.312T.4

Publication under this section is to be made in such manner as the relevant
regulators consider best designed to bring the publication to the attention of
the public.

############# Duty to ensure co-ordinated exercise of functions etc

18.3.312U

18.3.312U.1

The relevant regulators must co-ordinate the exercise of their respective
functions conferred by or under this Chapter.

18.3.312U.2

In complying with the duty in subsection (1) each relevant regulator must
obtain information and advice from any of the other relevant regulators who
may be expected to have relevant information or relevant expertise.

18.3.312U.3

The duty in subsection (1) applies only to the extent that compliance with the
duty does not impose a burden on the relevant regulators that is
disproportionate to the benefits of compliance.

18.3.312U.4

Before exercising any power conferred by or under this Chapter a relevant
regulator must consult each of the other relevant regulators (where not
otherwise required to do so).

############# Memorandum of understanding

18.3.312V

18.3.312V.1

The relevant regulators must prepare and maintain a memorandum which describes
in general terms—

18.3.312V.1.a

the role of the relevant regulators in relation to the exercise of functions
conferred by or under this Chapter, and

18.3.312V.1.b

how they intend to comply with section 312U in relation to the exercise of
such functions.

18.3.312V.2

The relevant regulators must review the memorandum at least once in each
calendar year.

18.3.312V.3

The relevant regulators may revise a memorandum under this section.

18.3.312V.4

The relevant regulators must give the Treasury a copy of the memorandum and
any revised memorandum.

18.3.312V.5

The Treasury must lay before Parliament a copy of any document received by
them under this section.

18.3.312V.6

The relevant regulators must ensure that the memorandum as in force for the
time being is published in the way appearing to them to be best calculated to
bring it to the attention of the public.

18.3.312V.7

The memorandum need not relate to any aspect of compliance with section 312U
if the relevant regulators consider—

18.3.312V.7.a

that publication of information about that aspect would be against the public
interest, or

18.3.312V.7.b

that aspect is a technical or operational matter not affecting the public.

############# Application of provisions of this Act to this Chapter

18.3.312W

The following provisions do not apply for the purposes of this Chapter—

18.3.312W.a

section 3D (duty to ensure co-ordinated exercise of functions);

18.3.312W.b

section 3E (memorandum of understanding);

18.3.312W.c

section 138D (actions for damages).
