##### Financial promotion

###### Financial promotion

20

20.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

20.2

In section 21 (restrictions on financial promotion), after subsection (2)
insert—

20.2.2A

The content of a communication may be approved for the purposes of this
section by an authorised person only if the giving of the approval—

20.2.2A.a

is permitted under section 55NA (which enables approval to be given with FCA
permission), or

20.2.2A.b

falls within an exemption conferred by regulations under section 55NB.

20.3

After section 55N insert—

############ General requirement relating to financial promotion approval

20.3.55NA

20.3.55NA.1

An authorised person must not approve the content of a communication for the
purposes of section 21 unless the person has permission to do so given by the
FCA under this section.

20.3.55NA.2

An authorised person who approves the content of a communication for the
purposes of section 21 otherwise than in accordance with permission granted
under this section is to be taken to have contravened a requirement imposed on
the person by the FCA under this Act.

20.3.55NA.3

Permission may be granted by the FCA under this section on the application of—

20.3.55NA.3.a

an authorised person, or

20.3.55NA.3.b

an applicant for Part 4A permission that has yet to be determined.

20.3.55NA.4

The FCA may grant a person permission under this section—

20.3.55NA.4.a

on the terms sought in the application (which may include the grant of
permission to give approvals generally for the purposes of section 21), or

20.3.55NA.4.b

subject to any other terms the FCA considers appropriate (which may in
particular provide for the giving of permission in a narrower description of
case than that sought in the application).

20.3.55NA.5

Where the FCA grants permission to a person under this section, the FCA may
vary or cancel the permission—

20.3.55NA.5.a

on the application of the person to whom it was given, or

20.3.55NA.5.b

of its own initiative,

and subsection (4)(b) applies to the variation of permission as it applies to
its grant.

20.3.55NA.6

If the FCA grants or varies permission under this section it must set out the
terms on which the permission is given, described in such way as it considers
appropriate.

20.3.55NA.7

The FCA may refuse to grant an application for permission under this section,
or for its variation or cancellation under subsection (5)(a), if it appears to
the FCA that it is desirable to do so in order to advance one or more of its
operational objectives.

20.3.55NA.8

The FCA may vary or cancel a person’s permission under subsection (5)(b) if it
appears to the FCA that—

20.3.55NA.8.a

the person has failed, during a period of at least 12 months, to give, or to
refuse to give, any approvals for the purposes of section 21 in accordance
with the permission, or

20.3.55NA.8.b

it is desirable to vary or cancel the permission in order to advance one or
more of its operational objectives.

20.3.55NA.9

The FCA must consult—

20.3.55NA.9.a

the PRA before giving permission under this section to, or before varying or
cancelling permission under this section given to—

20.3.55NA.9.a.i

a person who is, or will on the granting of an application for Part 4A
permission be, a PRA-authorised person, or

20.3.55NA.9.a.ii

a person who is a member of a group which includes a PRA-authorised person;

20.3.55NA.9.b

the Gibraltar regulator (within the meaning of Schedule 2A) before giving
permission under this section to, or before varying or cancelling permission
under this section given to, a Gibraltar-based person.

20.3.55NA.10

Subsection (9)(b) does not apply in a case where the FCA varies or cancels
permission of a Gibraltar-based person in exercise of its power under
subsection (5)(b), but the FCA must inform the Gibraltar regulator in writing
of the variation or cancellation.

20.3.55NA.11

Subsections (1) and (2) do not apply if the giving of approval falls within an
exemption conferred by regulations made under section 55NB.

20.3.55NA.12

Nothing in this section limits any other power under this Act to impose
requirements in relation to approvals given for the purposes of section 21 so
far as those requirements are additional to the requirement imposed by
subsection (1) of this section (but any such other requirement that is
inconsistent with the requirement imposed by that subsection is of no effect
to the extent of that inconsistency).

############ Section 55NA: power to provide for exemptions

20.3.55NB

20.3.55NB.1

The Treasury may by regulations provide for exemptions from the requirement
imposed by section 55NA(1) not to give approvals for the purposes of section
21 without permission.

20.3.55NB.2

Regulations under subsection (1) may provide for an exemption to have effect—

20.3.55NB.2.a

in respect of specified persons;

20.3.55NB.2.b

in respect of persons falling within a specified class;

20.3.55NB.2.c

in respect of approval given in relation to activities of a specified
description;

20.3.55NB.2.d

only in specified circumstances;

20.3.55NB.2.e

subject to specified conditions.

20.3.55NB.3

In this section “ specified ” means specified in regulations under this
section.

20.4

Schedule 5 contains amendments related to this section.

20.5

The amendments made by this section and Schedule 5—

20.5.a

apply to an authorised person whether the person became authorised before or
after the coming into force of this section;

20.5.b

do not affect the approval of a communication given before the coming into
force of this section.

##### Sustainability disclosure requirements

###### Sustainability disclosure requirements

21

21.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

21.2

After section 416 insert—

############ Sustainability disclosure requirements

############# SDR policy statement

21.2.416A

21.2.416A.1

The Treasury may prepare an SDR policy statement.

21.2.416A.2

An “SDR policy statement” is a statement of the policies of His Majesty’s
Government concerning disclosure requirements in connection with matters
relating to sustainability.

21.2.416A.3

In preparing an SDR policy statement, the Treasury must consult the
regulators.

21.2.416A.4

The Treasury must publish any SDR policy statement in such manner as they
consider appropriate.

21.2.416A.5

The Treasury—

21.2.416A.5.a

must keep any SDR policy statement under review;

21.2.416A.5.b

may prepare a revised statement (and subsections (3) and (4) apply in relation
to any revised statement);

21.2.416A.5.c

may withdraw any SDR policy statement.

21.2.416A.6

The Treasury may request a regulator to provide them with a report on any
matter that the Treasury require in connection with the preparation of an SDR
policy statement.

21.2.416A.7

A request for a report under subsection (6)—

21.2.416A.7.a

must be made in writing, and

21.2.416A.7.b

may require a regulator to send the report to the Treasury within such
reasonable period as may be specified in the request (or such other period as
may be agreed).

21.2.416A.8

A regulator must comply with a request under subsection (6).

21.2.416A.9

Nothing in section 348, or in regulations made under section 349, is to be
taken as preventing or restricting the ability of a regulator to disclose
information to the Treasury for the purposes of this section.

21.2.416A.10

Subsection (9) does not apply in relation to information provided to a
regulator by a regulatory authority outside the United Kingdom.

############# FCA and PRA rules etc

21.2.416B

21.2.416B.1

When making rules or issuing guidance in connection with disclosure concerning
matters relating to sustainability, a regulator must have regard to any SDR
policy statement (within the meaning of section 416A) that the Treasury have
published and not withdrawn.

21.2.416B.2

For the purposes of this section, matters relating to sustainability include
matters relating to—

21.2.416B.2.a

the environment, including climate change,

21.2.416B.2.b

social, community and human rights issues,

21.2.416B.2.c

tackling corruption and bribery, and

21.2.416B.2.d

governance, so far as relevant to matters within paragraphs (a) to (c).

21.3

In Schedule 1ZA (the Financial Conduct Authority), in paragraph 11 (annual
report), in sub-paragraph (1)—

21.3.a

after paragraph (ha) insert—

21.3.a.hc

how it has satisfied the requirement in section 138EA(2) so far as regarding
disclosure requirements in connection with matters relating to sustainability;

;

21.3.b

after paragraph (ia) insert—

21.3.b.ib

how it has satisfied the requirement in section 416B to have regard to any SDR
policy statement of the Treasury published and not withdrawn under section
416A (sustainability disclosure requirements: policy statement);

.

21.4

In Schedule 1ZB (the Prudential Regulation Authority), in paragraph 19 (annual
report), in sub-paragraph (1)—

21.4.a

after paragraph (e) insert—

21.4.a.ea

how it has satisfied the requirement in section 138EA(2) so far as regarding
disclosure requirements in connection with matters relating to sustainability;

;

21.4.b

after paragraph (fa) insert—

21.4.b.fb

how it has satisfied the requirement in section 416B to have regard to any SDR
policy statement of the Treasury under section 416A (sustainability disclosure
requirements: policy statement), and

.

##### Digital settlement assets

###### Digital settlement assets

22

In Schedule 6, which provides for the regulation of digital settlement assets—

22.a

Part 1 extends Part 5 of the Banking Act 2009 (Bank of England oversight of
payment systems) to payment systems using digital settlement assets and DSA
service providers, and makes consequential provision;

22.b

Part 2 extends Part 5 of the Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013
(regulation of payment systems) to payment systems using digital settlement
assets.

###### Digital settlement assets: power to make regulations

23

23.1

The Treasury may by regulations make such provision as they consider
appropriate for the purpose of, or in connection with—

23.1.a

the regulation of payments that include digital settlement assets,

23.1.b

the regulation of—

23.1.b.i

recognised payment systems that include arrangements using digital settlement
assets,

23.1.b.ii

recognised DSA service providers, and

23.1.b.iii

service providers connected with, or in relation to, the systems and providers
mentioned in sub-paragraphs (i) and (ii),

as those terms are for the time being defined in Part 5 of the Banking Act
2009, and

23.1.c

making insolvency arrangements (including administration, restructuring and
any similar procedure) in respect of the systems and providers mentioned in
paragraph (b).

23.2

In this section, “ digital settlement asset ” means a digital representation
of value or rights, whether or not cryptographically secured, that—

23.2.a

can be used for the settlement of payment obligations,

23.2.b

can be transferred, stored or traded electronically, and

23.2.c

uses technology supporting the recording or storage of data (which may include
distributed ledger technology).

23.3

The provision that may be made by regulations under this section includes
provision—

23.3.a

applying legislation relating to the regulation of electronic money and
payments to digital settlement assets (subject to whatever modifications the
Treasury consider appropriate);

23.3.b

applying legislation relating to insolvency arrangements and interactions
between different arrangements to the systems and providers mentioned in
subsection (1) (subject to whatever modifications the Treasury consider
appropriate);

23.3.c

conferring powers on the Treasury (including a power to legislate);

23.3.d

conferring powers, or imposing duties, on a relevant regulator (including a
power to make rules or other instruments);

23.3.e

about fees or other charges payable to a relevant regulator;

23.3.f

about recognition orders and recognition criteria in Part 5 of the Banking Act
2009;

23.3.g

about the enforcement of obligations arising under or by virtue of the
regulations;

23.3.h

about appeals in respect of decisions made under or by virtue of the
regulations;

23.3.i

about the sharing of information.

23.4

Provision under subsection (3)(g) may include provision creating offences
punishable on summary conviction—

23.4.a

in England and Wales, with imprisonment for a term not exceeding 3 months or a
fine, or both;

23.4.b

in Scotland and Northern Ireland, with imprisonment for a term not exceeding 3
months or a fine not exceeding level 5 on the standard scale, or both.

23.5

The power to make regulations under this section includes power to modify
legislation.

23.6

The power under subsection (5) includes power to modify the definition of
“digital settlement asset” in subsection (2).

23.7

Regulations under this section are—

23.7.a

subject to the affirmative procedure, or

23.7.b

if the Treasury consider it necessary for the regulations to come into force
without delay, subject to the made affirmative procedure.

23.8

Before making regulations under this section, the Treasury must consult—

23.8.a

the FCA,

23.8.b

the Bank of England, and

23.8.c

in relation to regulations that refer to the PRA or to the Payment Systems
Regulator, those bodies.

23.9

Where regulations under this section are subject to the made affirmative
procedure the statutory instrument containing them must be laid before
Parliament after being made.

23.10

Regulations contained in a statutory instrument laid before Parliament under
subsection (9) cease to have effect at the end of the period of 28 days
beginning with the day on which the instrument is made unless, during that
period, the instrument is approved by a resolution of each House of
Parliament.

23.11

In calculating the period of 28 days, no account is to be taken of any whole
days that fall within a period during which—

23.11.a

Parliament is dissolved or prorogued, or

23.11.b

either House of Parliament is adjourned for more than four days.

23.12

If regulations cease to have effect as a result of subsection (10), that does
not—

23.12.a

affect the validity of anything previously done under the regulations, or

23.12.b

prevent the making of new regulations.

23.13

In this section—

“ legislation ” means primary legislation, subordinate legislation and
assimilated direct   legislation; “ relevant regulator ” means— the FCA, the
Bank of England, or the Payment Systems Regulator.

##### Mutual recognition

###### Implementation of mutual recognition agreements

24

24.1

The Treasury may by regulations make such provision as they consider
appropriate for the purpose of, or in connection with, implementing any mutual
recognition agreement to which the United Kingdom is, or is expected to
become, a party.

24.2

The reference in subsection (1) to a “ mutual recognition agreement ” is a
reference to any international agreement so far as it provides for, or relates
to—

24.2.a

the recognition that the law and practice of a foreign country is, in respect
of relevant matters, equivalent to the law and practice of the United Kingdom,
and

24.2.b

the recognition that the law and practice of the United Kingdom is, in respect
of relevant matters, equivalent to the law and practice of that foreign
country.

24.3

Matters are “ relevant matters ” for the purposes of subsection (2) if they
relate to financial services or markets (whether generally or in particular
respects).

24.4

The provision that may be made by regulations under this section includes
provision—

24.4.a

conferring powers on the Treasury (including a power to legislate);

24.4.b

conferring powers, or imposing duties, on a relevant regulator (including a
power to make rules or other instruments);

24.4.c

about fees or other charges payable to a relevant regulator;

24.4.d

about the enforcement of obligations arising under or by virtue of the
regulations;

24.4.e

about appeals in respect of decisions made under or by virtue of the
regulations;

24.4.f

about the sharing of information.

24.5

The reference in this section to a mutual recognition agreement to which the
United Kingdom is, or is expected to become, a party includes a reference to
such an agreement as modified or supplemented from time to time.

24.6

The power to make regulations under this section includes power to modify
legislation.

24.7

Before making provision under subsection (4)(b) that imposes a duty on a
relevant regulator the Treasury must consult the regulator.

24.8

Provision under subsection (4)(b) that imposes a duty on a relevant regulator
to make rules may (among other things)—

24.8.a

specify matters that the rules must cover;

24.8.b

specify a period within which the rules must be made.

24.9

But except so far as permitted by subsection (8), such provision may not
require rules to be made in a specified form or with specified content.

24.10

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative procedure.

24.11

In this section—

“ foreign country ” means a country or territory outside the United Kingdom; “
legislation ” means primary legislation, subordinate legislation and
assimilated direct   legislation; “ relevant regulator ” means— the FCA, the
PRA, or the Bank of England; “ specified ” means specified in regulations
under this section.

#### Accountability of regulators

##### FCA and PRA objectives and regulatory principles

###### Competitiveness and growth objective

25

25.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

25.2

In section 1B (FCA’s general duties), after subsection (4) insert—

25.2.4A

When discharging its general functions in the way mentioned in subsection (1)
the FCA must, so far as reasonably possible, act in a way which, as a
secondary objective, advances the competitiveness and growth objective (see
section 1EB).

25.3

After section 1E insert—

############ Competitiveness and growth objective

25.3.1EB

The competitiveness and growth objective is: facilitating, subject to aligning
with relevant international standards—

25.3.1EB.a

the international competitiveness of the economy of the United Kingdom
(including in particular the financial services sector), and

25.3.1EB.b

its growth in the medium to long term.

25.4

In section 2H—

25.4.a

in the title, for “competition objective” substitute  “objectives” ;

25.4.b

for subsection (1) substitute—

25.4.b.1

When discharging its general functions in a way that advances its objectives
(see section 2F), the PRA must, so far as reasonably possible, act in a way
that advances the following secondary objectives—

25.4.b.1.a

the competition objective, and

25.4.b.1.b

the competitiveness and growth objective.

25.4.b.1A

The competition objective is: facilitating effective competition in the
markets for services provided by PRA-authorised persons in carrying on
regulated activities.

25.4.b.1B

The competitiveness and growth objective is: facilitating, subject to aligning
with relevant international standards—

25.4.b.1B.a

the international competitiveness of the economy of the United Kingdom
(including in particular the financial services sector through the
contribution of PRA-authorised persons), and

25.4.b.1B.b

its growth in the medium to long term.

###### Competitiveness and growth objective: reporting requirements

26

26.1

Each regulator must make two reports to the Treasury on how it has complied
with its duty to advance the competitiveness and growth objective.

26.2

The reports prepared by each regulator under subsection (1) must in particular
explain—

26.2.a

the action taken by the regulator to ensure that the competitiveness and
growth objective is embedded in its operations, processes and decision-making,
and

26.2.b

how any rules and guidance that the regulator has made advance that objective.

26.3

The first report under this section must be made before the end of 12 months
beginning with the first day on which section 25 of this Act comes into force,
and must relate to that period.

26.4

The second report under this section must be made before the end of 24 months
beginning with the first day on which section 25 of this Act comes into force,
and must relate to the period beginning with the day on which the first report
is published.

26.5

The Treasury must lay a copy of each report prepared under this section before
Parliament.

26.6

Each regulator must publish its reports prepared under this section in such
manner as it thinks fit.

26.7

In this section—

26.7.a

“ regulator ” means the FCA and the PRA;

26.7.b

references to the competitiveness and growth objective, and the duty to
advance that objective, are—

26.7.b.i

in relation to the FCA, references to its objective in section 1EB of FSMA
2000 and to its duty to advance that objective under section 1B(4A) of that
Act, and

26.7.b.ii

in relation to the PRA, references to its objective in section 2H(1B) of FSMA
2000 and to its duty to advance that objective under section 2H(1)(b) of that
Act.

###### Regulatory principles

27

In section 3B of FSMA 2000 (regulatory principles to be applied by both
regulators), in subsection (1) for paragraph (c) substitute—

27.c

the need to contribute towards achieving compliance by the Secretary of State
with section 1 of the Climate Change Act 2008 (UK net zero emissions target)
and section 5 of the Environment Act 2021 (environmental targets) where each
regulator considers the exercise of its functions to be relevant to the making
of such a contribution;

.

##### FCA and PRA powers to make rules etc

###### Review of rules

29

29.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

29.2

After section 3R (arrangements for provision of services) insert—

############ Rules

############# Duty of FCA and PRA to review rules

29.2.3RA

29.2.3RA.1

Each regulator must keep under review generally any rules made by the
regulator under this Act or any other enactment (whenever passed or made).

29.2.3RA.2

Subsection  (1)  does not apply to rules made for the purpose of complying
with a direction or recommendation of the Financial Policy Committee of the
Bank of England under—

29.2.3RA.2.a

section 9H of the Bank of England Act 1998 (directions to FCA or PRA requiring
macro-prudential measures), or

29.2.3RA.2.b

section 9Q of that Act (recommendations to FCA and PRA).

############# Statement of policy relating to review of rules

29.2.3RB

29.2.3RB.1

Each regulator must prepare and publish a statement of its policy with respect
to its review of rules under section 3RA.

29.2.3RB.2

The statement must provide information about—

29.2.3RB.2.a

how representations (including by a statutory panel) can be made to each
regulator with respect to its review of rules under section 3RA, and

29.2.3RB.2.b

the arrangements to ensure that those representations are considered.

29.2.3RB.3

In this section “ statutory panel ” has the meaning given by section 1RB(5).

29.2.3RB.4

If a statement published under this section is altered or replaced by a
regulator, the regulator must publish the altered or replaced statement.

29.2.3RB.5

A statement prepared under this section must be published by the regulator in
the way appearing to that regulator to be best designed to bring it to the
attention of the public.

############# Requirement to review specified rules

29.2.3RC

29.2.3RC.1

The Treasury may by direction require a regulator to carry out a review of
specified rules if—

29.2.3RC.1.a

the rules have been in force for at least 12 months,

29.2.3RC.1.b

the Treasury consider that it is in the public interest that the rules are
reviewed, and

29.2.3RC.1.c

it does not appear to the Treasury that—

29.2.3RC.1.c.i

the regulator is carrying out, or proposes to carry out, a review of those
rules, or

29.2.3RC.1.c.ii

if the regulator proposes to carry out a review, the proposals are appropriate
for the purposes of carrying out an effective review.

29.2.3RC.2

Subsection (1) only applies to rules falling within section 3RA(1).

29.2.3RC.3

The Treasury must consult the regulator concerned before giving a direction
under subsection (1).

29.2.3RC.4

In exercising the power under this section, the Treasury must have regard to
the desirability of minimising any adverse effect that the carrying out of the
review may have on the exercise by the regulator of any of its other
functions.

29.2.3RC.5

A direction under subsection (1) may—

29.2.3RC.5.a

specify the period within which a review must be carried out;

29.2.3RC.5.b

determine the scope and conduct of a review;

29.2.3RC.5.c

require the provision of interim reports during the carrying out of a review.

29.2.3RC.6

Provision made in a direction under subsection (5)(b) may include a
requirement—

29.2.3RC.6.a

for a review to be carried out by a person appointed by the regulator who is
independent of the regulator;

29.2.3RC.6.b

for any such appointment to be made only with the approval of the Treasury.

29.2.3RC.7

As soon as practicable after giving a direction under subsection (1) the
Treasury must—

29.2.3RC.7.a

lay before Parliament a copy of the direction, and

29.2.3RC.7.b

publish the direction in such manner as the Treasury think fit.

29.2.3RC.8

Subsection (7) does not apply where the Treasury consider that publication of
the direction would be against the public interest.

29.2.3RC.9

A direction under subsection (1) may be varied or revoked by the giving of a
further direction.

############# Report on certain reviews

29.2.3RD

29.2.3RD.1

This section applies where the Treasury have given a direction to a regulator
under section 3RC(1) to carry out a review.

29.2.3RD.2

The regulator must make a written report to the Treasury as to the opinion of
the regulator in relation to the following matters—

29.2.3RD.2.a

if the regulator is the FCA, whether the rules under review—

29.2.3RD.2.a.i

are compatible with the FCA’s strategic objective,

29.2.3RD.2.a.ii

advance one or more of the FCA’s operational objectives, and

29.2.3RD.2.a.iii

advance the competitiveness and growth objective;

29.2.3RD.2.b

if the regulator is the PRA, whether the rules under review—

29.2.3RD.2.b.i

advance one or more of the PRA’s objectives, and

29.2.3RD.2.b.ii

advance the PRA’s competition objective and the PRA’s competitiveness and
growth objective;

29.2.3RD.2.c

whether and to what extent the rules are functioning effectively and achieving
their intended purpose;

29.2.3RD.2.d

whether any amendments should be made to the rules and, if so, what those
amendments should be;

29.2.3RD.2.e

whether any rules should be revoked (with or without replacement);

29.2.3RD.2.f

whether any other action should be taken and, if so, what that action should
be.

29.2.3RD.3

As soon as practicable after receiving the report the Treasury must—

29.2.3RD.3.a

lay before Parliament a copy of the report, and

29.2.3RD.3.b

publish the report in such manner as the Treasury think fit.

29.2.3RD.4

When complying with subsection (3) the Treasury may withhold material from the
report if the Treasury consider that publication of the material would be
against the public interest.

###### Treasury power in relation to rules

30

30.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

30.2

After section 3RD (inserted by section 29) insert—

############ Power of Treasury to require making of rules by regulations

30.2.3RE

30.2.3RE.1

The Treasury may by regulations require a regulator to exercise a power under
this Act to make rules in relation to a specified activity or a specified
description of person.

30.2.3RE.2

Regulations under this section may—

30.2.3RE.2.a

specify matters that the rules must cover;

30.2.3RE.2.b

specify a period within which the rules must be made.

30.2.3RE.3

But except so far as permitted by subsection (2), regulations under this
section may not require rules to be made—

30.2.3RE.3.a

in a specified form or with specified content, or

30.2.3RE.3.b

to achieve or advance a specified outcome.

30.2.3RE.4

If no period is specified under subsection (2)(b) the rules must be made as
soon as reasonably practicable after the coming into force of the regulations.

30.3

In section 429 (Parliamentary control of statutory instruments) in subsection
(2) after “section” insert  “3RE,” .

###### Matters to consider when making rules

31

31.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

31.2

Before section 138F (under the italic heading “Procedural provisions”) insert—

############ Matters to consider when making rules

31.2.138EA

31.2.138EA.1

This section applies where either regulator proposes to make rules.

31.2.138EA.2

The regulator must have regard to any specified matters that are relevant to
the making of the rules in question.

31.2.138EA.3

“ Specified ” means specified in regulations made by the Treasury for the
purposes of this section.

31.2.138EA.4

The specification of a matter for the purposes of this section may apply
generally to the making of rules or be limited in whatever way the Treasury
consider appropriate, including by reference to—

31.2.138EA.4.a

the power under which the rules are made;

31.2.138EA.4.b

the persons to whom the rules apply;

31.2.138EA.4.c

the activities or subject-matter to which the rules relate.

31.2.138EA.5

The requirement imposed by subsection (2) does not apply in respect of any
rules if, or to the extent that, the rules are made for the purposes of—

31.2.138EA.5.a

complying with a direction given by the Financial Policy Committee of the Bank
of England under section 9H of the Bank of England Act 1998 (directions
requiring macro-prudential measures), or

31.2.138EA.5.b

acting in accordance with a recommendation made by that Committee under
section 9Q of that Act (recommendations about the exercise of the FCA and PRA
functions).

31.2.138EA.6

The requirement to have regard to specified matters under this section when
making rules is in addition to any other requirements to have regard to
matters when making such rules imposed by another provision of this Act or by
any other enactment.

31.3

In section 138I (consultation by the FCA)—

31.3.a

in subsection (2) after paragraph (b) insert—

31.3.a.ba

an explanation of the ways in which having regard to specified matters under
section 138EA(2) has affected the proposed rules,

;

31.3.b

after subsection (8) insert—

31.3.b.8A

The requirement to provide the explanation referred to in subsection (2)(ba)
does not apply in relation to any rules if—

31.3.b.8A.a

the FCA considers that the delay involved in complying with that requirement
would be prejudicial to the interests of consumers (as defined in section
425A) or other persons whose interests would be protected by the rules, or

31.3.b.8A.b

the rules change existing rules and the changes consist of, or include,
changes which, in the FCA’s opinion, are not material.

31.3.b.8B

Where an explanation is not provided by virtue of subsection (8A)(b), the
draft of the rules must be accompanied by a statement of the FCA’s opinion.

31.4

In section 138J (consultation by the PRA)—

31.4.a

in subsection (2) after paragraph (b) insert—

31.4.a.ba

an explanation of the ways in which having regard to specified matters under
section 138EA(2) has affected the proposed rules,

;

31.4.b

after subsection (8) insert—

31.4.b.8A

The requirement to provide the explanation referred to in subsection (2)(ba)
does not apply in relation to any rules if—

31.4.b.8A.a

the PRA considers that the delay involved in complying with that requirement
would—

31.4.b.8A.a.i

be prejudicial to the safety and soundness of PRA-authorised persons, or

31.4.b.8A.a.ii

in a case where section 2C applies, be prejudicial to securing the appropriate
degree of protection for policyholders, or

31.4.b.8A.b

the rules change existing rules and the changes consist of, or include,
changes which, in the PRA’s opinion, are not material.

31.4.b.8B

Where an explanation is not provided by virtue of subsection (8A)(b), the
draft of the rules must be accompanied by a statement of the PRA’s opinion.

###### Effect of rules etc on deference decisions

32

32.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

32.2

In the italic heading before section 410, after “international” insert
“powers and” .

32.3

Before section 410 insert—

############ Consultation in relation to deference decisions

32.3.409A

32.3.409A.1

This section applies where a regulator is proposing to take a relevant action.

32.3.409A.2

The regulator—

32.3.409A.2.a

must consider the effect of the relevant action on notified deference
decisions, and

32.3.409A.2.b

if having done so it appears to the regulator that there is a material risk
that the relevant action would be incompatible with a notified deference
decision, must consult the Treasury about the likely effect of the action on
the decision.

32.3.409A.3

Subsection (2) applies only if a duty to consult applies in respect of the
taking of the relevant action.

32.3.409A.4

For the purposes of subsection  (1)  a regulator proposes to take a “relevant
action” if—

32.3.409A.4.a

it proposes to make rules under this Act or any other enactment, or

32.3.409A.4.b

it proposes to make changes to its general policies and practices so far as
relating to its supervisory functions under section 1L (FCA supervisory
functions) or (as the case may be) section 2K (PRA supervisory functions).

32.3.409A.5

For the purposes of subsection  (2) —

32.3.409A.5.a

“ deference decision ” means a decision of the Treasury that the law and
practice of another country or territory is, so far as relating to financial
services and markets, equivalent to the law and practice of the United Kingdom
(either generally or as it relates to a particular matter);

32.3.409A.5.b

a deference decision is a “notified deference decision” if the Treasury have,
by notice in writing, informed the regulator that it is relevant for the
purposes of this section;

32.3.409A.5.c

a relevant action is “incompatible” with a notified deference decision if the
action would result in the law and practice of the United Kingdom ceasing to
be equivalent to the law and practice of the other country or territory to
which the deference decision relates.

32.3.409A.6

For the purposes of subsection (3) a duty to consult applies in respect of a
relevant action if—

32.3.409A.6.a

the duty imposed by section 138I or 138J to publish a draft of proposed rules
applies in respect of the action, or

32.3.409A.6.b

any other duty (whether or not imposed by a provision of this Act) to publish
the proposal to take the action in question applies.

32.3.409A.7

Section 138M(1) (consultation: exemptions for temporary product intervention
rules) is to be ignored for the purposes of subsection (6) in determining
whether a duty to consult applies in respect of a relevant action.

32.3.409A.8

The requirement imposed by subsection (2)(b) must be carried out before the
duty to consult in respect of the relevant action is carried out.

32.3.409A.9

The requirements imposed by subsection (2) do not apply to the extent that the
regulator takes a relevant action—

32.3.409A.9.a

by the making of product intervention rules under section 137D if the
condition in subsection (10) is met,

32.3.409A.9.b

by the making of rules under Part 9C (see instead section 143G(3)),

32.3.409A.9.c

by the making of rules under Part 9D (see instead section 144C(3)),

32.3.409A.9.d

by the making of rules under Part 12B (see instead section 192XB(2)),

32.3.409A.9.e

in order to comply with a direction given by the Financial Policy Committee of
the Bank of England under section 9H of the Bank of England Act 1998
(directions required macro-prudential measures), or

32.3.409A.9.f

in order to act in accordance with a recommendation made by that Committee
under section 9Q of that Act (recommendations about the exercise of
functions).

32.3.409A.10

The condition referred to in subsection (9)(a) is that the FCA considers it
necessary not to comply with the requirement imposed by subsection (2) for the
purpose of advancing—

32.3.409A.10.a

the consumer protection objective, or

32.3.409A.10.b

if an order under section 137D(1)(b) is in force, the integrity objective.

###### Effect of rules etc on international trade obligations

33

In FSMA 2000 after section 409A (inserted by section 32) insert—

########## Notification in relation to international trade obligations

33.409B

33.409B.1

This section applies where it appears to a regulator that there is a material
risk that a relevant action it proposes to take would be incompatible with an
international trade obligation.

33.409B.2

The regulator must give written notice to the Treasury of the proposed action
before proceeding to take it.

33.409B.3

Subsection (2) applies only if a duty to consult applies in respect of the
taking of the relevant action.

33.409B.4

For the purposes of subsection  (1)  a regulator proposes to take a “relevant
action” if—

33.409B.4.a

it proposes to make rules under this Act or any other enactment, or

33.409B.4.b

it proposes to make changes to its general policies and practices so far as
relating to its supervisory functions under section 1L (FCA supervisory
functions) or (as the case may be) section 2K (PRA supervisory function).

33.409B.5

For the purposes of subsection (3) a duty to consult applies in respect of a
relevant action if—

33.409B.5.a

the duty imposed by section 138I or 138J to publish a draft of proposed rules
applies in respect of the action, or

33.409B.5.b

any other duty (whether or not imposed by a provision of this Act) to publish
the proposal to take the action in question applies.

33.409B.6

Section 138M(1) (consultation: exemptions for temporary product intervention
rules) is to be ignored for the purposes of subsection (5) in determining
whether a duty to consult applies in respect of a relevant action.

33.409B.7

The requirement imposed by subsection (2) must be carried out before the duty
to consult in respect of the relevant action is carried out.

33.409B.8

The requirement imposed by subsection (2) does not apply to the extent that
the regulator takes a relevant action—

33.409B.8.a

by the making of product intervention rules under section 137D if the
condition in subsection (9) is met,

33.409B.8.b

in order to comply with a direction given by the Financial Policy Committee of
the Bank of England under section 9H of the Bank of England Act 1998
(directions requiring macro-prudential measures), or

33.409B.8.c

in order to act in accordance with a recommendation made by that Committee
under section 9Q of that Act (recommendations about the exercise of
functions).

33.409B.9

The condition referred to in subsection (8)(a) is that the FCA considers it
necessary not to comply with the requirement imposed by subsection (2) for the
purpose of advancing—

33.409B.9.a

the consumer protection objective, or

33.409B.9.b

if an order under section 137D(1)(b) is in force, the integrity objective.

33.409B.10

Subsection (11) applies in a case where a notice under subsection (2) is not
given because of subsection (3) or (8)(a).

33.409B.11

The regulator must give written notice to the Treasury of the relevant action
it has taken as soon as reasonably practicable after taking it if it appears
to the regulator that there is a material risk that the action is incompatible
with an international trade obligation.

33.409B.12

In this section “ international trade obligation ” means an obligation of the
United Kingdom that relates to financial services or markets under—

33.409B.12.a

a free trade agreement, as defined by section 5(1) of the Trade Act 2021, or

33.409B.12.b

the agreement establishing the World Trade Organisation signed at Marrakesh on
15 April 1994.

###### Power to disapply or modify rules

34

34.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

34.2

After section 138B insert—

############ Disapplication or modification of rules in individual cases

34.2.138BA

34.2.138BA.1

This section applies to rules made by a regulator if, or to the extent that,
regulations made by the Treasury provide for it to apply.

34.2.138BA.2

The regulator may, on the application or with the consent of a person who is
subject to the rules, give the person a permission that enables the person—

34.2.138BA.2.a

not to apply the rules, or

34.2.138BA.2.b

to apply the rules with the modifications specified in the permission.

34.2.138BA.3

Subsections (1) and (2) do not apply to—

34.2.138BA.3.a

rules made by either regulator under section 64A (rules of conduct);

34.2.138BA.3.b

rules made by either regulator under section 137O (threshold condition code);

34.2.138BA.3.c

rules made by the FCA under section 247 (trust scheme rules), section 248
(scheme particular rules), section 261I (contractual scheme rules) or section
261J (contractual scheme particulars rules);

34.2.138BA.3.d

rules made by the FCA under section 309Z(1) (rules of conduct).

34.2.138BA.4

The regulator may—

34.2.138BA.4.a

give permission under this section subject to conditions, and

34.2.138BA.4.b

revoke or vary permission given under this section.

34.2.138BA.5

Regulations under subsection (1) may make provision about procedural matters
in relation to the giving of permission under this section.

34.2.138BA.6

Provision under subsection (5) may (among other things) include provision
about—

34.2.138BA.6.a

the making of applications;

34.2.138BA.6.b

the determination of applications (including matters to be taken into account
in doing so);

34.2.138BA.6.c

the giving and withdrawal of consent;

34.2.138BA.6.d

requirements as to notification or publication of decisions of a regulator
under this section;

34.2.138BA.6.e

appeals in respect of decisions of a regulator under this section.

34.2.138BA.7

Before making regulations under this section in relation to rules made by a
regulator the Treasury must consult the regulator.

34.3

In section 429 (Parliamentary control of statutory instruments), in subsection
(2), in the list of sections beginning with “90B” insert at the appropriate
place  “138BA,” .

###### Responses to recommendations of the Treasury

35

35.1

Section 1JA of FSMA 2000 (recommendations by Treasury in connection with
general duties) is amended in accordance with subsections  (2)  and (3).

35.2

After subsection (2) insert—

35.2.2A

The FCA must respond to each recommendation made to it under subsection (1) by
notifying the Treasury in writing of—

35.2.2A.a

action that the FCA has taken or intends to take in accordance with the
recommendation, or

35.2.2A.b

the reasons why the FCA has not acted or does not intend to act in accordance
with the recommendation.

35.2.2B

The notice under subsection (2A) must be given before the end of 12 months
beginning with the date the notice containing the recommendation was given
under subsection (1).

35.2.2C

Where the FCA has given notice under subsection (2A) in relation to a
recommendation, the FCA must by notice in writing update the Treasury on the
matters mentioned in subsection (2A)(a) and (b) before the end of each
subsequent period of 12 months.

35.2.2D

Subsection (2C) does not apply if the Treasury have notified the FCA in
writing that no update (or further update) is required.

35.2.2E

The FCA is not required under subsection (2A) or (2C) to provide any
information whose publication would in the opinion of the FCA be against the
public interest.

35.3

In subsection (3), for “subsection (1)” substitute  “subsection (1), (2A) or
(2C)” .

to it under subsection (1) by notifying the Treasury in writing of—

35.5.2A.a

action that the Prudential Regulation Committee has taken or intends to take
in accordance with the recommendation, or

35.5.2A.b

the reasons why the Prudential Regulation Committee has not acted or does not
intend to act in accordance with the recommendation.

35.5.2B

The notice under subsection (2A) must be given before the end of 12 months
beginning with the date the notice containing the recommendation was given
under subsection (1).

35.5.2C

Where the Prudential Regulation Committee has given notice under subsection
(2A) in relation to a recommendation, it must by notice in writing update the
Treasury on the matters mentioned in subsection (2A)(a) and (b) before the end
of each subsequent period of 12 months.

35.5.2D

Subsection (2C) does not apply if the Treasury have notified the Prudential
Regulation Committee in writing that no update (or further update) is
required.

35.5.2E

The Prudential Regulation Committee is not required under subsection (2A) or
(2C) to provide any information whose publication would in the opinion of the
Committee be against the public interest.

35.6

############ Requirements for public consultation

############# Requirements in connection with public consultations

36.1.1RB

36.1.1RB.1

This section applies where the FCA issues a public consultation.

36.1.1RB.2

The FCA must include information in the consultation about any engagement by
the FCA with the statutory panels of the FCA, the PRA or the Payment Systems
Regulator in relation to the matters being consulted on.

36.1.1RB.3

The FCA is not required under subsection (2) to include any information whose
publication would in the opinion of the FCA be against the public interest.

36.1.1RB.4

For the purposes of this section, the FCA issues a public consultation if it
publishes the draft of any proposals for the purpose of bringing them to the
attention of the public (whether or not under a duty to do so imposed by an
enactment).

36.1.1RB.5

36.1.1RB.5.a

in relation to the FCA, has the meaning given by section 1RA(8),

36.1.1RB.5.b

in relation to the PRA, has the meaning given by section 2NA(8), and

36.1.1RB.5.c

in relation to the Payment Systems Regulator, means a panel established under
section 103(3) of the Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013.

###### Engagement with Parliamentary Committees

38

38.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

38.2

In Part 4 of Schedule 1ZA (miscellaneous provisions relating to Financial
Conduct Authority), after paragraph 27 insert—

############ Engagement with Parliamentary Committees

38.2.28

38.2.28.1

This paragraph applies where the FCA issues a relevant consultation.

38.2.28.2

For the purposes of this paragraph the FCA issues a relevant consultation if
it—

38.2.28.2.a

publishes a draft of proposed rules under section 138I,

38.2.28.2.b

publishes a proposal under a duty imposed by another provision of this Act or
by any other enactment, or

38.2.28.2.c

publishes other proposals about the exercise of any of its general functions.

38.2.28.3

The FCA must, as soon as reasonably practicable after issuing the
consultation, notify in writing the chair of each relevant Parliamentary
Committee that the consultation has been issued.

38.2.28.4

The notification must specify the parts of the consultation (if any) that
address the ways in which the proposals subject to consultation—

38.2.28.4.a

advance the FCA’s operational objectives,

38.2.28.4.b

are compatible with the FCA’s strategic objective,

38.2.28.4.c

demonstrate that the FCA has had regard to the regulatory principles in
section 3B when preparing the proposals, and

38.2.28.4.d

engage with matters to which the FCA must have regard under regulations made
under section 138EA.

38.2.28.5

The reference in sub-paragraph (4)(a) to the FCA’s operational objectives
includes, in its application as a secondary objective, the competitiveness and
growth objective (see section 1EB).

38.2.28.6

The notification must also specify any other part of the consultation which
the FCA considers should be drawn to the attention of the relevant
Parliamentary Committees.

38.2.28.7

References in this paragraph to the relevant Parliamentary Committees are
references to—

38.2.28.7.a

the Treasury Committee of the House of Commons,

38.2.28.7.b

the Committee of the House of Lords which—

38.2.28.7.b.i

is charged with responsibility by that House for the purposes of this
paragraph, and

38.2.28.7.b.ii

has notified the FCA that it is a relevant Parliamentary Committee for those
purposes, and

38.2.28.7.c

the Joint Committee of both Houses which—

38.2.28.7.c.i

is charged with responsibility by those Houses for the purposes of this
paragraph, and

38.2.28.7.c.ii

has notified the FCA that it is a relevant Parliamentary Committee for those
purposes.

38.2.28.8

References in this paragraph to the Treasury Committee of the House of
Commons—

38.2.28.8.a

if the name of that Committee is changed, are references to that Committee by
its new name, and

38.2.28.8.b

if the functions of that Committee (or substantially corresponding functions)
become functions of a different Committee of the House of Commons, are to be
treated as references to the Committee by which the functions are exercisable.

38.2.28.9

Any question arising under sub-paragraph (8) is to be determined by the
Speaker of the House of Commons.

38.2.29

38.2.29.1

This paragraph applies where—

38.2.29.1.a

the FCA issues a public consultation, and

38.2.29.1.b

a Committee of the House of Commons or the House of Lords, or a joint
Committee of both Houses, has provided to the FCA representations in response
to the consultation.

38.2.29.2

For the purposes of this paragraph, the FCA issues a public consultation if it
publishes the draft of any proposals for the purpose of bringing them to the
attention of the public (whether or not under a duty to do so imposed by an
enactment).

38.2.29.3

The FCA must give to the chair of the Committee concerned a written response
to the representations.

38.2.29.4

The duty to respond imposed by sub-paragraph (3) applies only so far as the
FCA would not be under a corresponding duty to do so imposed by another
enactment.

38.2.29.5

The FCA is not required under sub-paragraph (3) to provide any information
whose publication would in the opinion of the FCA be against the public
interest.

38.3

In Part 4 of Schedule 1ZB (miscellaneous provisions relating to the PRA),
after paragraph 35 insert—

############ Engagement with Parliamentary Committees

##### Reporting requirements

39

39.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

39.2

After paragraph 11 of Schedule 1ZA insert—

########### Other reports

39.2.11A

39.2.11A.1

The Treasury may (subject to this paragraph) at any time by direction require
the FCA to publish a report containing information about—

39.2.11A.1.a

any of the matters mentioned in paragraphs (a) to (ia) of paragraph 11(1);

39.2.11A.1.b

such other matters that the direction may specify.

39.2.11A.2

The Treasury may give a direction under this paragraph requiring information
to be published only if the Treasury consider that—

39.2.11A.2.a

the information is reasonably necessary for the purpose of reviewing and
scrutinising the discharge of the FCA’s functions, and

39.2.11A.2.b

other available information is not sufficient to meet that purpose.

39.2.11A.3

Subject to sub-paragraph (4), the FCA must publish a report prepared under a
direction given under this paragraph in such manner, and within such period,
as the direction may require.

39.2.11A.4

Nothing in this paragraph requires the inclusion in the report of any
information whose publication would be against the public interest.

39.2.11A.5

A direction under this paragraph may not—

39.2.11A.5.a

require a report to be published more than once in each quarter;

39.2.11A.5.b

require the publication of information that is confidential information for
the purposes of Part 23 (see section 348(2)).

39.2.11A.6

The Treasury must consult the FCA before giving a direction under this
paragraph.

39.2.11A.7

In exercising the power under this paragraph, the Treasury must have regard to
the desirability of minimising any adverse effect that the preparation of the
report required in accordance with the direction may have on the exercise by
the FCA of any of its other functions.

39.2.11A.8

The Treasury must—

39.2.11A.8.a

lay before Parliament a copy of a direction given under this paragraph, and

39.2.11A.8.b

publish the direction in such manner as the Treasury think fit.

39.2.11A.9

A direction under this paragraph may be varied or revoked by the giving of a
further direction.

##### Co-operation of FCA and others

###### Duty to co-operate and consult in exercising functions

40

40.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

40.2

In the italic heading before section 415B, at the end insert  “and co-
operation” .

40.3

After section 415B (consultation) insert—

############ Co-operation and consultation in relation to exercise of functions

40.3.415C

40.3.415C.1

In exercising its functions under this Act a relevant organisation (“ R ”)
must—

40.3.415C.1.a

take such steps as R considers appropriate to co-operate with each of the
other relevant organisations in relation to matters of interest to that
organisation, and

40.3.415C.1.b

consult such other persons as R considers appropriate in relation to any
matters that R considers to be of interest to those persons.

40.3.415C.2

A matter is of interest to another relevant organisation for the purposes of
subsection (1) if it appears to R that it has, or is likely to have,
significant implications in relation to—

40.3.415C.2.a

the exercise by that other relevant organisation of functions under this Act,
or

40.3.415C.2.b

the functioning generally of relevant markets within the meaning of section
1F.

40.3.415C.3

The relevant organisations must prepare and publish a statement of policy with
respect to compliance with the duty under subsection (1).

40.3.415C.4

The relevant organisations may alter or replace a statement published under
subsection (3).

40.3.415C.5

The relevant organisations must publish a statement as altered or replaced
under subsection (4).

40.3.415C.6

The relevant organisations—

40.3.415C.6.a

must, at least once a year, prepare and publish a report on their compliance
with the duty under subsection (1), and

40.3.415C.6.b

must put in place arrangements enabling representations to be made about their
compliance with that duty (whether by seeking representations in response to
the report or otherwise).

40.3.415C.7

Except in the case of the first report to be prepared under this section, a
report prepared under subsection (6)(a) must include a summary of
representations received in the preceding year in accordance with arrangements
made under subsection (6)(b).

40.3.415C.8

Publication under this section is to be made in such manner as the relevant
organisations consider best designed to bring the publication to the attention
of the public.

40.3.415C.9

In this section “ relevant organisation ” means—

40.3.415C.9.a

the FCA;

40.3.415C.9.b

the scheme operator of the ombudsman scheme within the meaning of section
225(2);

40.3.415C.9.c

the scheme manager of the Financial Services Compensation Scheme within the
meaning of section 212.

##### Panels and policy statements

###### Listing Authority Advisory Panel

41

In FSMA 2000, after section 1Q insert—

########## The Listing Authority Advisory Panel

41.1QA

41.1QA.1

Arrangements under section 1M must include the establishment and maintenance
of a panel of persons (to be known as “ the Listing Authority Advisory Panel
”) to represent the interests of practitioners who are likely to be affected
by the exercise by the FCA of its relevant functions.

41.1QA.2

The reference in subsection (1) to the FCA’s relevant functions is to its
functions relating to the listing, issue or trading of products on recognised
investment exchanges and other markets the operation of which is regulated by
the FCA, including in particular—

41.1QA.2.a

the issuing of transferable securities, and

41.1QA.2.b

the trading of transferable securities on regulated markets and multilateral
trading facilities.

41.1QA.3

The FCA must appoint one of the members of the Listing Authority Advisory
Panel to be the chair of the Panel.

41.1QA.4

The Treasury’s approval is required for the appointment or dismissal of the
chair.

41.1QA.5

The FCA must appoint to the Listing Authority Advisory Panel such persons to
represent the interests of issuers and investors as it considers appropriate.

41.1QA.6

The FCA may appoint to the Listing Authority Advisory Panel such other persons
as it considers appropriate.

41.1QA.7

Subsections (5) and (6) are subject to section 1MA.

41.1QA.8

In this section—

      “ multilateral trading facility ”, “ recognised investment exchange ”
and “ regulated markets ” have the same meaning as in Part 18 (see section
313(1));           “ transferable securities ” has the meaning given by
section 102A(3).

it considers appropriate.

After section 138I insert—

############ FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel

43.2.138IA

43.2.138IA.1

The FCA must establish and maintain a panel of persons (to be known as the “
FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel ”) to provide advice in relation to cost
benefit analyses for the purposes of section 138I.

43.2.138IA.2

Except as provided by subsection (3), the FCA must consult the FCA Cost
Benefit Analysis Panel about the following matters—

43.2.138IA.2.a

the preparation of a cost benefit analysis under section 138I(2)(a) or (5)(a);

43.2.138IA.2.b

the preparation of its statement of policy under section 138IB.

43.2.138IA.3

The requirement to consult under subsection (2)(a) does not apply in such
cases as may be set out in the statement of policy maintained under section
138IB.

43.2.138IA.4

Arrangements made by the FCA under subsection (1) for the establishment and
maintenance of the FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel must include arrangements
for the Panel to—

43.2.138IA.4.a

keep under review how the FCA is performing generally in carrying out its
duties under section 138I(2)(a) and (5)(a), and

43.2.138IA.4.b

provide to the FCA whatever recommendations the Panel thinks appropriate as a
result of such review.

43.2.138IA.5

The FCA must appoint one of the members of the FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel
to be the chair of the Panel.

43.2.138IA.6

The Treasury’s approval is required for the appointment or dismissal of the
chair.

43.2.138IA.7

The FCA must appoint to the FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel such persons with
knowledge or experience of the preparation of cost benefit analyses as it
considers appropriate.

43.2.138IA.8

The FCA must appoint to the FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel at least two
individuals who are employed by persons authorised for the purposes of this
Act by the FCA, with each one being employed by a different person.

43.2.138IA.9

The FCA may appoint to the FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel such other persons
as it considers appropriate.

43.2.138IA.10

Subsections (7) to (9) are subject to section 1MA.

43.2.138IA.11

The FCA must consider representations that are made to it by the FCA Cost
Benefit Analysis Panel.

43.2.138IA.12

The FCA must from time to time publish in such manner as it thinks fit
responses to the representations.

or 138IA.

subsection if regulations made by the Treasury provide for it not to apply to
that panel.

46.2.1MA.a

generally, or

46.2.1MA.b

only in relation to such descriptions of persons or cases as the regulations
may specify (but the power to make such regulations may not be exercised so as
to specify persons by name).

###### Panel reports

47

47.1

The Treasury may by regulations require specified statutory panels of the
regulator to produce an annual report on their work and provide that report to
the Treasury.

47.2

Regulations under subsection (1) may make provision about the content of the
annual report.

47.3

The Treasury must lay a copy of each report prepared by virtue of this section
before Parliament.

47.4

Each specified statutory panel of the regulator must publish its reports
prepared by virtue of this section in such manner as it thinks fit.

47.5

In this section—

47.5.a

“ statutory panels of the regulator ” means—

47.5.a.i

in relation to the FCA, the panels mentioned in section 1RA(8) of FSMA 2000,

47.5.a.ii

in relation to the PRA, the panels mentioned in section 2NA(8) of FSMA 2000,
and

47.5.a.iii

in relation to the Payment Systems Regulator, a panel established under
section 103(3) of the Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013;

47.5.b

“ specified ” means specified in regulations under this section.

47.6

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative procedure.

##### Bank of England regulatory powers

###### Exercise of FMI regulatory powers

48

After section 30C of the Bank of England Act 1998 insert—

########## Central counterparties and central securities depositories

########### Exercise of functions relating to CCPs and CSDs

48.30D

48.30D.1

In exercising its FMI functions in a way that advances the Financial Stability
Objective (and subject to that), the Bank must have regard to—

48.30D.1.a

the regulatory principles in section 30E;

48.30D.1.b

the effects generally that the exercise of FMI functions will or may have on
the financial stability of countries or territories (other than the United
Kingdom) in which FMI entities are established or provide services;

48.30D.1.c

the desirability of exercising FMI functions in a manner that is not
determined by whether the persons to whom FMI services are provided are
located in the United Kingdom or elsewhere.

48.30D.2

In exercising its FMI functions in a way that advances the Financial Stability
Objective the Bank must, so far as reasonably possible, act in a way which, as
a secondary objective, facilitates innovation in the provision of FMI services
(including in the infrastructure used for that purpose) with a view to
improving the quality, efficiency and economy of the services.

48.30D.3

For the purposes of this Part the Bank’s “FMI functions” are the following
functions so far as exercisable in relation to FMI entities—

48.30D.3.a

its function of making rules under FSMA 2000 (considered as a whole);

48.30D.3.b

its function of making technical standards in accordance with Chapter 2A of
Part 9A of FSMA 2000;

48.30D.3.c

its function of preparing and issuing codes under FSMA 2000 (considered as a
whole);

48.30D.3.d

its function of determining the general policy and principles by reference to
which it performs particular functions under FSMA 2000.

48.30D.4

In this Part—

      “ FMI entities ” means—         a recognised central counterparty within
the meaning of Part 18 of FSMA 2000 (see section 285(1)(b)(i) of that Act),
a recognised CSD as defined by section 285(1)(e) of FSMA 2000,           a
third country central counterparty as defined by section 285(1)(d) of FSMA
2000, and           a third country CSD as defined by section 285(1)(g) of
FSMA 2000;                 “ FMI services ” means services provided by FMI
entities as part of their business as FMI entities;           “ FSMA 2000 ”
means the Financial Services and Markets Act 2000.

########### Regulatory principles

48.30E

48.30E.1

These are the regulatory principles referred to in section 30D(1)(a)—

48.30E.1.a

the need to use the resources of the Bank in the most efficient and economic
way;

48.30E.1.b

the principle that a burden or restriction which is imposed on a person, or on
the carrying on of an activity, should be proportionate to the benefits,
considered in general terms, which are expected to result from the imposition
of that burden or restriction;

48.30E.1.c

the desirability of sustainable growth in the economy of the United Kingdom in
the medium or long term, including in a way consistent with contributing
towards achieving compliance by the Secretary of State with section 1 of the
Climate Change Act 2008 (UK net zero emissions target) and section 5 of the
Environment Act 2021 (environmental targets) where the Bank considers the
exercise of its FMI functions to be relevant to the making of such a
contribution;

48.30E.1.d

the general principle that consumers should take responsibility for their
decisions;

48.30E.1.e

the responsibilities of the senior management of FMI entities subject to
requirements imposed by or under FSMA 2000, including those affecting
consumers, in relation to compliance with those requirements;

48.30E.1.f

the desirability where appropriate of the Bank exercising its FMI functions in
a way that recognises differences in the nature of, and objectives of,
businesses carried on by different persons;

48.30E.1.g

the desirability in appropriate cases of the Bank publishing information
relating to persons on whom requirements are imposed as a result of the
exercise of the Bank’s FMI functions, or requiring such persons to publish
information, as a means of contributing to the advancement by the Bank of its
Financial Stability Objective and its objective under section 30D(2);

48.30E.1.h

the principle that the Bank should exercise its FMI functions as transparently
as possible;

48.30E.1.i

the desirability of facilitating fair and reasonable access to FMI services.

48.30E.2

For the purposes of subsection (1) “ consumer ” has the same meaning as in
section 3B of FSMA 2000 (and for these purposes includes in particular persons
who receive FMI services).

########### Financial Market Infrastructure Committee

48.30F

48.30F.1

There is to be a committee of the Bank known as the Financial Market
Infrastructure Committee (the “ FMI Committee ”).

48.30F.2

The FMI Committee is to consist of—

48.30F.2.a

a chair appointed by the Bank;

48.30F.2.b

at least three independent members appointed by the Bank;

48.30F.2.c

such other members as may be appointed from time to time by the Bank.

48.30F.3

The person appointed as chair under subsection (2)(a) must be the Governor, or
a Deputy Governor, of the Bank.

48.30F.4

A person is an independent member for the purposes of subsection (2)(b) if the
person is an officer, employee or agent of the Bank—

48.30F.4.a

as a result only of their membership of one or more of the Bank’s committees,
or

48.30F.4.b

is appointed as an independent member to the FMI Committee with the consent of
the Treasury.

48.30F.5

For the purposes of subsection (4)(a)—

48.30F.5.a

the Bank’s committees are—

48.30F.5.a.i

the FMI Committee,

48.30F.5.a.ii

the Financial Policy Committee,

48.30F.5.a.iii

the Monetary Policy Committee, and

48.30F.5.a.iv

the Prudential Regulation Committee;

48.30F.5.b

the reference to a person who is an officer, employee or agent of the Bank as
result of their membership of one or more of those committees includes a
reference to a person who becomes such an officer, employee or agent as a
result of their appointment to the FMI Committee under this section.

48.30F.6

Before appointing a person under subsection (2)(b) the Bank must—

48.30F.6.a

be satisfied that the person has knowledge or experience which is likely to be
relevant to the FMI Committee’s functions, and

48.30F.6.b

consider whether the person has any financial or other interests that could
substantially affect the functions as member that it would be proper for the
person to discharge.

########### Functions of the Financial Market Infrastructure Committee

48.30G

48.30G.1

The following functions of the Bank are to be exercised by the Bank acting
through the FMI Committee (and, except as authorised by this section, are not
to be exercised in any other way)—

48.30G.1.a

its FMI functions;

48.30G.1.b

such other functions of the Bank as the court of directors may specify as
functions that are to be discharged by the FMI Committee.

48.30G.2

The FMI Committee may arrange for such of its functions as it thinks fit to be
carried out only by, or after consultation with, the Governor of the Bank.

48.30G.3

Except as provided by subsection (4), the FMI Committee may delegate such of
its functions as it thinks fit to—

48.30G.3.a

a member of the FMI Committee;

48.30G.3.b

a sub-committee of the FMI Committee consisting of members of the FMI
Committee or one or more such members and one or more officers, employees or
agents of the Bank;

48.30G.3.c

an officer, employee or agent of the Bank;

48.30G.3.d

a committee consisting of officers, employees or agents of the Bank.

48.30G.4

The FMI Committee may not delegate under subsection (3) its FMI functions
under FSMA 2000 of making rules or technical standards (but this does not
prevent arrangements under subsection (2) being made in respect of such
functions).

########### Information

48.30H

48.30H.1

The Bank must publish a statement setting out the following matters in respect
of the FMI Committee—

48.30H.1.a

the number of members and whether each such member is a Bank member or an
independent member;

48.30H.1.b

if the Committee includes any Bank members, the role of each such member
within the Bank;

48.30H.1.c

arrangements for meetings and how proceedings at meetings are conducted;

48.30H.1.d

arrangements for the taking of decisions otherwise than at meetings;

48.30H.1.e

arrangements for any functions to be carried out by, or after consultation
with, the Governor of the Bank (including details of the functions to which
such arrangements relate);

48.30H.1.f

arrangements for the delegation of functions.

48.30H.2

If there is a material change in any of the matters contained in the statement
the Bank must publish an updated statement.

48.30H.3

Publication under this section is to be made in such manner as the Bank
considers best designed to bring the statement to the attention of the public.

48.30H.4

For the purposes of subsection (1)—

48.30H.4.a

a person is an independent member if they are appointed in accordance with
section 30F(2)(b) and (4);

48.30H.4.b

a person is a Bank member if they are an officer or employee of the Bank who
is not appointed as mentioned in paragraph (a).

########### Recommendations by Treasury

48.30I

48.30I.1

The Treasury may at any time by notice in writing to the FMI Committee make
recommendations about aspects of the economic policy of His Majesty’s
Government to which the Bank should have regard—

48.30I.1.a

when considering how to advance the Financial Stability Objective and the
objective under section 30D(2), and

48.30I.1.b

when considering the application of the regulatory principles set out in
section 30E.

48.30I.2

The Treasury must make recommendations under subsection (1) at least once in
each Parliament.

48.30I.3

The Treasury must—

48.30I.3.a

publish in such manner as they think fit any notice given under subsection
(1), and

48.30I.3.b

lay a copy of it before Parliament.

48.30I.4

The FMI Committee must respond to each recommendation made under subsection
(1) by notifying the Treasury in writing of—

48.30I.4.a

action that the Bank has taken or intends to take in accordance with the
recommendation, or

48.30I.4.b

the reasons why the Bank has not acted or does not intend to act in accordance
with the recommendation.

48.30I.5

The notice under subsection (4) must be given before the end of 12 months
beginning with the date the notice containing the recommendation was given
under subsection (1).

48.30I.6

Where the FMI Committee has given notice under subsection (4) in relation to a
recommendation, it must by notice in writing update the Treasury on the
matters mentioned in subsection (4)(a) and (b) before the end of each
subsequent period of 12 months.

48.30I.7

Subsection (6) does not apply if the Treasury have notified the FMI Committee
in writing that no update (or further update) is required.

48.30I.8

The FMI Committee is not required under subsection (4) or (6) to provide any
information whose publication would in the opinion of the Committee be against
the public interest.

###### Bank of England: rule-making powers

49

49.1

FSMA 2000 is amended as follows.

49.2

After section 300H (inserted by section 11) insert—

############ Bank of England rules

############# Duty of Bank of England to review rules

49.2.300I

49.2.300I.1

The Bank of England must keep under review generally any rules made by the
Bank under this Act.

49.2.300I.2

Subsection (1) does not apply to rules made for the purpose of complying with
a recommendation of the Financial Policy Committee of the Bank of England
under section 9O of the Bank of England Act 1998 (making of recommendations
within the Bank).

############# Statement of policy relating to review of rules

49.2.300J

49.2.300J.1

The Bank of England must prepare and publish a statement of policy with
respect to its review of rules under section 300I.

49.2.300J.2

The statement must provide information about—

49.2.300J.2.a

how representations (including by a statutory panel) can be made to the Bank
with respect to its review of rules under section 300I, and

49.2.300J.2.b

the arrangements to ensure that those representations are considered.

49.2.300J.3

In this section “ statutory panel ” has the meaning given by section 1RB(5).

49.2.300J.4

If a statement published under this section is altered or replaced, the Bank
must publish the altered or replaced statement.

49.2.300J.5

A statement prepared under this section must be published by the Bank in the
way appearing to the Bank to be best designed to bring it to the attention of
the public.

############# Requirement to review specified rules

49.2.300K

49.2.300K.1

The Treasury may by direction require the Bank of England to carry out a
review of specified rules made by the Bank under this Act if—

49.2.300K.1.a

the rules have been in force for at least 12 months,

49.2.300K.1.b

the Treasury consider that it is in the public interest that the rules are
reviewed, and

49.2.300K.1.c

it does not appear to the Treasury that—

49.2.300K.1.c.i

the Bank is carrying out, or plans to carry out, a review of those rules, or

49.2.300K.1.c.ii

if the Bank proposes to carry out a review, the proposals are appropriate for
the purposes of carrying out an effective review.

49.2.300K.2

Subsection (1) only applies to rules falling within section 300I(1).

49.2.300K.3

The Treasury must consult the Bank before giving a direction under subsection
(1).

49.2.300K.4

In exercising the power under this section, the Treasury must have regard to
the desirability of minimising any adverse effect that the carrying out of the
review may have on the exercise by the Bank of any of its other functions.

49.2.300K.5

A direction under subsection (1) may—

49.2.300K.5.a

specify the period within which a review must be carried out;

49.2.300K.5.b

determine the scope and conduct of a review;

49.2.300K.5.c

require the provision of interim reports during the carrying out of a review.

49.2.300K.6

Provision made in a direction under subsection (5)(b) may include a
requirement—

49.2.300K.6.a

for a review to be carried out by a person appointed by the Bank who is
independent of the Bank;

49.2.300K.6.b

for any such appointment to be made only with the approval of the Treasury.

49.2.300K.7

As soon as practicable after giving a direction under subsection (1) the
Treasury must—

49.2.300K.7.a

lay before Parliament a copy of the direction, and

49.2.300K.7.b

publish the direction in such manner as the Treasury think fit.

49.2.300K.8

Subsection (7) does not apply where the Treasury consider that publication of
the direction would be against the public interest.

49.2.300K.9

A direction under subsection (1) may be varied or revoked by the giving of a
further direction.

############# Report on certain reviews

49.2.300L

49.2.300L.1

This section applies where the Treasury have given a direction to the Bank of
England under section 300K to carry out a review.

49.2.300L.2

The Bank must make a written report to the Treasury as to the opinion of the
Bank in relation to the following matters—

49.2.300L.2.a

whether the rules under review advance—

49.2.300L.2.a.i

the Bank’s Financial Stability Objective, and

49.2.300L.2.a.ii

the Bank’s secondary innovation objective (see section 30D(2) of the Bank of
England Act 1998);

49.2.300L.2.b

whether and to what extent the rules are functioning effectively and achieving
their intended purpose;

49.2.300L.2.c

whether any amendments need to be made to the rules and, if so, what those
amendments should be;

49.2.300L.2.d

whether any rules should be revoked (with or without replacement);

49.2.300L.2.e

whether any other action should be taken and, if so, what that action should
be.

49.2.300L.3

As soon as practicable after receiving the report the Treasury must—

49.2.300L.3.a

lay before Parliament a copy of the report, and

49.2.300L.3.b

publish the report in such manner as the Treasury think fit.

49.2.300L.4

When complying with subsection (3) the Treasury may withhold material from the
report if the Treasury consider that publication of the material would be
against the public interest.

############# Power of Treasury to require making of rules by regulations

49.2.300M

49.2.300M.1

The Treasury may by regulations require the Bank of England to exercise a
power under this Act to make rules in relation to a specified activity or a
specified description of person.

49.2.300M.2

Regulations under this section may—

49.2.300M.2.a

specify matters that the rules must cover;

49.2.300M.2.b

specify a period within which the rules must be made.

49.2.300M.3

But except so far as permitted by subsection (2), regulations under this
section may not require rules to be made—

49.2.300M.3.a

in a specified form or with specified content, or

49.2.300M.3.b

to achieve or advance a specified outcome.

49.2.300M.4

If no period is specified under subsection (2)(b) the rules must be made as
soon as reasonably practicable after the coming into force of the regulations.

49.3

In section 429 (Parliamentary control of statutory instruments), in subsection
(2), in the list of sections beginning with “90B” insert at the appropriate
place  “300M,” .
