##### Consultation on rules

###### Consultation on rules

53

53.1

In section 138I of FSMA 2000 (consultation by the FCA), after subsection (4)
insert—

53.1.4A

The FCA must include, in the account mentioned in subsection (4), a list of
the respondents who made the representations, where those respondents have
consented to the publication of their names.

53.1.4B

The duty in subsection (4A) is not to be read as authorising or requiring such
processing of personal data as would contravene the data protection
legislation (but the duty is to be taken into account in determining whether
particular processing of data would contravene that legislation).

53.1.4C

For the purposes of this section, the exemption relating to functions
conferred on the FCA mentioned in paragraph 11 of Schedule 2 to the Data
Protection Act 2018 (exemption from application of listed GDPR provisions)
does not apply.

53.1.4D

Where representations are made to the FCA by a Committee of the House of
Commons or the House of Lords or a Joint Committee of both Houses in
accordance with subsection (2)(e), the FCA’s account mentioned in subsection
(4) must also describe how the FCA has considered the representations made by
that Committee in making the proposed rules.

53.2

In section 138J of FSMA 2000 (consultation by the PRA), after subsection (4)
insert—

53.2.4A

The PRA must include, in the account mentioned in subsection (4), a list of
the respondents who made the representations, where those respondents have
consented to the publication of their names.

53.2.4B

The duty in subsection (4A) is not to be read as authorising or requiring such
processing of personal data as would contravene the data protection
legislation (but the duty is to be taken into account in determining whether
particular processing of data would contravene that legislation).

53.2.4C

For the purposes of this section, the exemption relating to functions
conferred on the PRA mentioned in paragraph 9 of Schedule 2 to the Data
Protection Act 2018 (exemption from application of listed GDPR provisions)
does not apply.

53.2.4D

Where representations are made to the PRA by a Committee of the House of
Commons or the House of Lords or a Joint Committee of both Houses in
accordance with subsection (2)(e), the PRA’s account mentioned in subsection
(4) must also describe how the PRA has considered the representations made by
that Committee in making the proposed rules.

53.3

In section 104 of the Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013
(consultation requirements), after subsection (5) insert—

53.3.5A

The Payment Systems Regulator must include, in the account mentioned in
subsection (5), a list of the respondents who made the representations, where
those respondents have consented to the publication of their names.

53.3.5B

The duty in subsection (5A) is not to be read as authorising or requiring such
processing of personal data as would contravene the data protection
legislation (but the duty is to be taken into account in determining whether
particular processing of data would contravene that legislation).

53.3.5C

In this section “ data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the
Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act).

53.3.5D

Where representations are made to the Payment Systems Regulator by a Committee
of the House of Commons or the House of Lords or a Joint Committee of both
Houses in accordance with subsection (3)(d), the Payment Systems Regulator’s
account mentioned in subsection (5) must also describe how the Payment Systems
Regulator has considered the representations made by that Committee in making
the proposed requirement.

### Access to cash

#### Cash access services

54

Schedule 8 makes provision about the provision of cash deposit and withdrawal
services in the United Kingdom or a part of the United Kingdom.

#### Wholesale cash distribution

55

Schedule 9 makes provision about persons involved in wholesale cash
distribution (as that term is defined in the Schedule).

### Performance of functions relating to financial market infrastructure

#### Recognised bodies: senior managers and certification

56

Schedule 10 amends FSMA 2000 to make provision about the performance, by
senior managers and others, of functions in relation to activities carried on
by recognised bodies (within the meaning of Part 18 of that Act) of types
specified by the Treasury.

### Central counterparties in financial difficulties

#### Central counterparties in financial difficulties

57

Schedule 11 makes provision for a special resolution regime for central
counterparties where all or part of its business has encountered, or is likely
to encounter, financial difficulties.

### Insurers in financial difficulties

#### Insurers in financial difficulties

58

58.1

Schedule 12 makes provision about the powers of the court in relation to
liabilities of an insurer that is, or is likely to become, unable to pay its
debts (an order made in exercise of these powers is a “write-down order”).

58.2

Schedule 13 makes provision about the enforcement of contracts to which an
insurer is a party, where the insurer is subject to a write-down order or to
certain insolvency proceedings.

#### Bank of England levy

##### Bank of England levy

70

70.1

The Bank of England Act 1998 is amended as follows.

70.2

Omit section 6 and Schedule 2 (cash ratio deposits).

70.3

Before section 7 insert—

########### Bank of England levy

70.3.6A

Schedule 2ZA makes provision for the Bank to impose a charge on financial
institutions in connection with the pursuit of its financial stability and
monetary policy objectives.

70.4

Before Schedule 2A (financial policy committee) insert—

  Bank of England levy

Section 6A

############# “The levy”

70.4.1

70.4.1.1

The Bank may impose a charge on eligible institutions in accordance with this
Schedule.

70.4.1.2

The charge is to be known as the Bank of England levy (and is referred to in
this Schedule as “ the levy ”).

############# “Eligible institutions”

70.4.2

70.4.2.1

For the purposes of this Schedule, an “eligible institution” is a person who,
at any time during a levy year, is an authorised deposit-taker.

70.4.2.2

An “authorised deposit-taker” for these purposes is a person who has
permission under Part 4A of the Financial Services and Markets Act 2000 to
accept deposits, other than—

70.4.2.2.a

a credit union;

70.4.2.2.b

a friendly society;

70.4.2.2.c

a person who has such permission only in the course of effecting or carrying
out contracts of insurance in accordance with that permission.

70.4.2.3

In this paragraph—

      “ credit union ” has the meaning given by section 31(1) of the Credit
Unions Act 1979 or Article 2(2) of the Credit Unions (Northern Ireland) Order
1985;           “ friendly society ” means a society that is registered within
the meaning of the Friendly Societies Act 1974 or incorporated under the
Friendly Societies Act 1992;           “ levy year ” has the meaning given by
paragraph  3 .

70.4.2.4

The Treasury may by regulations—

70.4.2.4.a

amend the foregoing provisions of this paragraph;

70.4.2.4.b

amend any other provision of this Schedule in consequence of provision made
under paragraph  (a) .

############# “Levy year”

70.4.3

70.4.3.1

For the purposes of this Schedule, a “levy year” is—

70.4.3.1.a

the period of 12 months beginning on such day as the Bank may determine, and

70.4.3.1.b

each subsequent period of 12 months.

70.4.3.2

The day determined under sub-paragraph  (1)(a)  may not be before the day on
which the Financial Services and Markets Act 2023 is passed.

############# “Anticipated levy requirement”

70.4.4

70.4.4.1

The Bank must, in respect of a levy year—

70.4.4.1.a

determine which of its policy functions it intends to fund (in whole or in
part) by means of the levy;

70.4.4.1.b

determine the total amount of the levy it reasonably considers it requires in
connection with the funding of those functions (“the anticipated levy
requirement”).

70.4.4.2

The Bank may add to the anticipated levy requirement for a levy year such
amount (if any) that—

70.4.4.2.a

was required in connection with the funding of policy functions in the
previous levy year, and

70.4.4.2.b

was in excess of the total amount of the levy that it received in respect of
that previous levy year.

70.4.4.3

For the purposes of this Schedule, a function of the Bank is a “policy
function” if it is exercised in pursuit of—

70.4.4.3.a

the Financial Stability Objective (see section 2A), or

70.4.4.3.b

its objectives in relation to monetary policy (see section 11).

70.4.4.4

In making a determination in accordance with sub-paragraph  (1) , the Bank
must take account of any other amounts which are, or are likely to be,
available in the levy year to fund policy functions (for example, amounts of
the levy received in respect of a previous levy year or amounts available from
sources other than the levy).

70.4.4.5

The Bank must publish a determination made in accordance with sub-paragraph
(1) —

70.4.4.5.a

at such time before or during the levy year to which the determination relates
as the Bank considers appropriate, and

70.4.4.5.b

in such manner as the Bank considers appropriate.

70.4.4.6

The reference in sub-paragraph  (3)  to the exercise of a function includes
anything done in preparation for, to facilitate, or otherwise in connection
with, the exercise of the function.

############# Liability to pay the levy

70.4.5

70.4.5.1

The amount of the levy that an eligible institution is liable to pay in
respect of a levy year is to be determined by the Bank in accordance with
regulations made by the Treasury.

70.4.5.2

Regulations under sub-paragraph  (1)  may—

70.4.5.2.a

make provision by reference to the Bank’s anticipated levy requirement in
respect of the levy year (see paragraph  4 );

70.4.5.2.b

make provision by reference to specified liabilities of an eligible
institution;

70.4.5.2.c

make provision for cases in which no amount of the levy or a reduced amount of
the levy is payable.

70.4.5.3

Regulations made by virtue of sub-paragraph  (2)(b)  may include (among other
things) provision—

70.4.5.3.a

specifying types of liability that may or may not be taken into account for
specified purposes;

70.4.5.3.b

about how and when liabilities of a specified type are to be taken into
account for specified purposes;

70.4.5.3.c

about how the amount of a liability of a specified type is to be determined,
including specifying times, or periods of time, by reference to which the
amount is to be determined;

70.4.5.3.d

for an amount of a liability of a specified type to be treated as reduced by
the amount of assets of a specified type.

70.4.5.4

Regulations under sub-paragraph  (1)  may include provision conferring a
discretion on the Bank to determine specified matters (including matters
mentioned in sub-paragraph  (2)(b)  or  (3) ).

70.4.5.5

Regulations made by virtue of sub-paragraph  (4)  may, in particular, confer a
discretion—

70.4.5.5.a

to determine the method used to determine a matter, and

70.4.5.5.b

to determine different methods to be used in relation to different eligible
institutions.

70.4.5.6

In this section, “ specified ” means specified in the regulations.

############# Payment of the levy

70.4.6

70.4.6.1

The Bank must notify each eligible institution that is liable to pay the levy
in respect of a levy year of the following matters—

70.4.6.1.a

the levy year in respect of which the levy is payable;

70.4.6.1.b

the amount of the levy the institution is liable to pay;

70.4.6.1.c

the time by which the levy must be paid (or, if the Bank determines that the
levy may be paid in instalments, the times by which each instalment must be
paid);

70.4.6.1.d

the methods by which the levy may be paid.

70.4.6.2

A time notified in accordance with sub-paragraph  (1)(c)  (or if more than one
time is notified, the earliest of them) may not be before the end of the
period of 30 days beginning with the day on which the notification is given.

70.4.6.3

Notification may be given in such form or in such manner as the Bank considers
appropriate (and may be given in a different form or manner to different
eligible institutions or eligible institutions of a different description).

############# Recovery of the levy

70.4.7

The levy is recoverable as a civil debt due to the Bank.

See also paragraph  8  (interest on unpaid amounts of the levy).

############# Interest

70.4.8

70.4.8.1

This paragraph applies where an eligible person has been notified—

70.4.8.1.a

of an amount of the levy that is payable, and

70.4.8.1.b

the time by which the amount must be paid.

70.4.8.2

Interest is payable, at the rate mentioned in sub-paragraph  (3) , on any part
of the amount mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1)(a)  which remains unpaid after
the time mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1)(b) .

70.4.8.3

The rate mentioned in this sub-paragraph is the rate equivalent to an annual
percentage rate of 4% above the benchmark rate.

70.4.8.4

The “benchmark rate” is—

70.4.8.4.a

the percentage rate announced from time to time by the Monetary Policy
Committee of the Bank as the official dealing rate, or

70.4.8.4.b

where an order under section 19 (Treasury reserve powers) is in force, any
equivalent percentage rate determined by the Treasury under that order.

70.4.8.5

The Treasury may by regulations amend this paragraph so as to change the rate
of interest payable on an unpaid amount of the levy.

############# Power to obtain information

70.4.9

70.4.9.1

The Bank may, by written notice, require an eligible institution to provide
information or documents in connection with the levy.

70.4.9.2

The notice must specify—

70.4.9.2.a

the information required;

70.4.9.2.b

the form or manner in which the information must be provided;

70.4.9.2.c

the time at which, or period within which, the information must be provided;

70.4.9.2.d

the period to which the information must relate.

############# Regulations

70.4.10

70.4.10.1

Before making regulations under this Schedule the Treasury must consult—

70.4.10.1.a

the Bank, and

70.4.10.1.b

such other persons who appear to the Treasury to be representative of persons
who are likely to be affected by the regulations.

70.4.10.2

When making regulations under this Schedule the Treasury must have regard to
the financial needs of the Bank.

70.4.10.3

Regulations under this Schedule are to be made by statutory instrument.

70.4.10.4

Regulations under this Schedule may—

70.4.10.4.a

make different provision for different purposes;

70.4.10.4.b

make incidental, supplemental, consequential, saving or transitional
provision.

70.4.10.5

A statutory instrument containing (whether alone or with other provision)
regulations under paragraphs  2(4)  or  5(1)  may not be made unless a draft
of the instrument has been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, each
House of Parliament.

70.4.10.6

A statutory instrument containing only regulations under paragraph  8(5)  is
subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

#### Other miscellaneous provisions

##### Liability of payment service providers for fraudulent transactions

72

72.1

The Payment Systems Regulator must prepare and publish a draft of a relevant
requirement for reimbursement in such qualifying cases of payment orders as
the Regulator considers should be eligible for reimbursement.

72.2

A case is a “ qualifying case ” for the purposes of this section if—

72.2.a

the case relates to a payment order executed over the Faster Payments Scheme,
and

72.2.b

the payment order was executed subsequent to fraud or dishonesty.

72.3

The draft of the relevant requirement must—

72.3.a

be published in the way appearing to the Payment Systems Regulator to be best
calculated to bring it to the attention of the public;

72.3.b

be accompanied by notice that representations about the proposed relevant
requirement may be made to the Payment Systems Regulator within a specified
time.

72.4

The duty imposed by subsection (1) must be carried out before the end of two
months beginning with the day on which this section comes into force.

72.5

The Payment Systems Regulator must impose a relevant requirement, in whatever
way and to whatever extent it considers appropriate, for reimbursement to be
made in qualifying cases of payment orders.

72.6

In complying with the duty imposed by subsection (5) the Payment Systems
Regulator must have regard to any representations made in accordance with
subsection (3)(b).

72.7

The duty imposed by subsection (5) must be carried out before the end of 6
months beginning with the day on which this section comes into force.

72.8

The duty under subsections (1) to (3), and under section 104(2) of the
Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013 in the application of that
section to a relevant requirement imposed under subsection (5) of this
section, may be satisfied by things done before (as well as after) this
section comes into force.

72.9

Nothing in subsections (1) to (8) is to be taken as limiting the power of the
Payment Systems Regulator—

72.9.a

to vary or revoke a relevant requirement imposed under the duty imposed by
subsection (5), or

72.9.b

to impose further relevant requirements (after that duty is complied with) in
connection with reimbursement of payment orders executed subsequent to fraud
or dishonesty.

72.10

In subsections (1) to (9)—

      “ the Faster Payments Scheme ” means the payment system, known as the
Faster Payments Scheme, designated as a regulated payment system for the
purposes of Part 5 of the Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013 by
order made by the Treasury in exercise of the power conferred by section 43(1)
of that Act;           “ relevant requirement ” means a requirement imposed by
or under section 54 or 55 of the Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013
(or by or under a combination of those sections).

72.11

In regulation 90 of the Payment Services Regulations 2017 ( S.I. 2017/752 )
(liability of payment service providers for incorrect unique identifiers),
after paragraph (5) insert—

72.11.6

Nothing in this regulation affects the liability of a payment service provider
under a relevant requirement in a case where the payment order is executed
subsequent to fraud or dishonesty (and the requirements imposed by this
regulation are subject to any such relevant requirements).

72.11.7

In this regulation, a “ relevant requirement ” means a requirement imposed by
or under—

72.11.7.a

a direction given under regulation 125,

72.11.7.b

a direction given under section 54 of the Financial Services (Banking Reform)
Act 2013,

72.11.7.c

a rule made under section 55 of that Act,

72.11.7.d

an order made under section 56(3) of that Act, or

72.11.7.e

a variation of an agreement under section 57(2) of that Act.

##### Credit unions

73

Schedule 14 amends the Credit Unions Act 1979 to make provision about
additional financial activities credit unions may choose to carry on.

##### Reinsurance for acts of terrorism

74

74.1

The Reinsurance (Acts of Terrorism) Act 1993 is amended as follows.

74.2

After section 2, insert—

########### Directions

74.2.2A

74.2.2A.1

A relevant person must comply with any directions given to it by the Treasury
under this section.

74.2.2A.2

For the purposes of this section, a “ relevant person ” means—

74.2.2A.2.a

a person who—

74.2.2A.2.a.i

has entered into arrangements to which this Act applies (see section 2(1))
(whether before or after the passing of this Act), and

74.2.2A.2.a.ii

has been classified as a public sector body by the Office for National
Statistics (whether before or after the passing of this Act), or

74.2.2A.2.b

a group undertaking of a person falling within paragraph (a) (within the
meaning of section 1161 of the Companies Act 2006).

74.2.2A.3

The Treasury may direct a relevant person to appoint a person to perform the
functions of an accounting officer.

74.2.2A.4

The Treasury may give a direction to a relevant person under this subsection
if the Treasury consider it necessary for the purpose of ensuring compliance
with any requirements associated with the classification, as mentioned in
subsection (2)(a)(ii), of a person falling within subsection (2)(a).

74.2.2A.5

Directions under subsection (4) may include provision about compliance with
requirements relating to—

74.2.2A.5.a

auditing;

74.2.2A.5.b

accounting;

74.2.2A.5.c

budgeting;

74.2.2A.5.d

arm’s length bodies;

74.2.2A.5.e

public sector bodies.

74.2.2A.6

Before giving a direction under this section the Treasury must consult the
relevant person to whom the Treasury intend to give a direction.

74.2.2A.7

A direction under this section must be accompanied by a notice that—

74.2.2A.7.a

states when the direction takes effect (see subsection  (8) ), and

74.2.2A.7.b

gives the Treasury’s reasons for giving the direction.

74.2.2A.8

A direction may, if the Treasury reasonably consider it necessary, take
effect—

74.2.2A.8.a

immediately it is given to the relevant person, or

74.2.2A.8.b

on a later date specified in the direction.

74.2.2A.9

A direction may be given so as to have effect—

74.2.2A.9.a

for a specified period, or

74.2.2A.9.b

until the occurrence of a specified event.

74.2.2A.10

A direction under this section must be given in writing.

74.2.2A.11

A direction under this section must—

74.2.2A.11.a

be published in whatever manner the Treasury consider appropriate, and

74.2.2A.11.b

be laid before Parliament.

74.2.2A.12

A direction under this section may be varied or revoked by another direction
under this section.

########### Compliance

74.2.2B

74.2.2B.1

Compliance with a direction given under section 2A is enforceable—

74.2.2B.1.a

by injunction, or

74.2.2B.1.b

in Scotland, by interdict or by an order for specific performance under
section 45 of the Court of Session Act 1988.

74.2.2B.2

Proceedings under subsection (1) may be brought only by the Treasury.

##### Politically exposed persons: money laundering and terrorist financing

77

77.1

The Treasury must exercise the power conferred by section 49 of the Sanctions
and Anti-Money Laundering Act 2018 (power of appropriate Minister to make
regulations about money laundering etc) for the purpose mentioned in
subsection (2).

77.2

The purpose is to make provision amending Part 3 of the Money Laundering,
Terrorist Financing and Transfer of Funds (Information on the Payer)
Regulations 2017 ( S.I. 2017/692 ) (“ the 2017 Regulations ”) (customer due
diligence) so as to secure the result required by subsection (3).

77.3

The result required by this subsection is that, where a customer is a domestic
PEP, or a family member or a known close associate of a domestic PEP—

77.3.a

the starting point for the relevant person’s assessment under regulation 35(3)
of the 2017 Regulations is that the customer presents a lower level of risk
than a non-domestic PEP, and

77.3.b

if no enhanced risk factors are present, the extent of enhanced customer due
diligence measures to be applied in relation to that customer is less than the
extent to be applied in the case of a non-domestic PEP.

77.4

In this section—

77.4.a

“ customer ” includes a potential customer;

77.4.b

“ domestic PEP ” means a politically exposed person entrusted with prominent
public functions by the United Kingdom;

77.4.c

“ enhanced risk factors ”, in relation to a customer who is a domestic PEP or
a family member or a known close associate of that domestic PEP, mean risk
factors other than the customer’s position as a domestic PEP or as a family
member or known close associate of that domestic PEP;

77.4.d

“ non-domestic PEP ” means a politically exposed person who is not a domestic
PEP;

77.4.e

the following terms have the same meaning as in regulation 35(12) of the 2017
Regulations—

      “politically exposed person” or “PEP”;           “family member”;
“known close associate”.

77.5

Section 55 of the Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act 2018 (Parliamentary
procedure for regulations) does not apply to regulations made in compliance
with the duty imposed by subsection (1).

77.6

Regulations made in compliance with the duty imposed by subsection (1)—

77.6.a

are subject to the negative procedure, and

77.6.b

must be laid before Parliament in accordance with paragraph (a) before the end
of 12 months starting with the day on which this section comes into force.

77.7

The Treasury must, before the end of 6 months starting with the day on which
this section comes into force, lay before Parliament a statement setting out
what progress has been made towards making the regulations in compliance with
the duty imposed by subsection (1).

77.8

The duty in subsection (7) does not apply where the regulations have been laid
before Parliament in accordance with subsection (6)(a) before the end of 6
months starting with the day on which this section comes into force.

##### Politically exposed persons: review of guidance

78

78.1

The FCA must review its guidance on politically exposed persons (“PEPs”) given
under section 139A of FSMA 2000 and in compliance with the requirements under
regulation 48 of the Money Laundering, Terrorist Financing and Transfer of
Funds (Information on the Payer) Regulations 2017 ( S.I. 2017/692 ) (“ the
2017 Regulations ”).

78.2

The review required under subsection (1) must include—

78.2.a

an assessment of the extent to which the guidance is followed by those persons
to whom it is given under regulation 48 of the 2017 Regulations, and

78.2.b

in the light of that assessment, consideration as to whether the guidance
remains appropriate or whether it should be revised.

78.3

The FCA must—

78.3.a

before the end of 3 months beginning with the day on which this section comes
into force, publish an update on the FCA’s plan for the review required under
subsection (1), and

78.3.b

before the end of 12 months beginning with the day on which this section comes
into force—

78.3.b.i

publish the conclusions of the review, and

78.3.b.ii

where the FCA concludes that the guidance should be revised, publish draft
revised guidance for consultation.

78.4

Publication as required by subsection (3) must be in the way appearing to the
FCA to be best calculated to bring the publication to the attention of persons
likely to be affected by it.

78.5

The FCA is not required under this section to publish any information whose
publication would be against the public interest.

78.6

In this section—

78.6.a

“ domestic PEP ” means a politically exposed person entrusted with prominent
public functions by the United Kingdom;

78.6.b

the following terms have the same meaning as in regulation 35(12) of the 2017
Regulations—

      “politically exposed person” or “PEP”;           “family member”;
“known close associate”.

##### Forest risk commodities: review

79

79.1

The Treasury must carry out a review to assess the extent to which regulation
of the UK financial system is adequate for the purpose of eliminating the
financing of the use of prohibited forest risk commodities.

79.2

In subsection (1) the reference to “prohibited” forest risk commodities is a
reference to forest risk commodities, or products derived from forest risk
commodities, the use of which is prohibited by paragraph 2 of Schedule 17 to
the Environment Act 2021.

79.3

Having carried out a review the Treasury must lay before Parliament, and
publish, a report stating—

79.3.a

the conclusions of the review, and

79.3.b

the steps the Treasury consider it appropriate to take to improve the
effectiveness of the regulation of the UK financial system for the purpose
stated in subsection (1).

79.4

Subsection (3) must be complied with before the end of 9 months beginning with
the day on which the first regulations under paragraph 1 of Schedule 17 to the
Environment Act 2021 are made.

79.5

In this section—

      “ forest risk commodities ” has the same meaning as in Schedule 17 to
the Environment Act 2021;           “ UK financial system ” has the same
meaning as in FSMA 2000 (see section 1I of that Act).

### General

#### Interpretation

80

80.1

In this Act—

“ domestic law ” means the law of England and Wales, Scotland or Northern
Ireland; “ enactment ” means an enactment whenever passed or made and
includes— an enactment contained in any Order in Council, order, rules,
regulations, scheme, warrant, byelaw or other instrument made under an Act, an
enactment contained in, or in an instrument made under, an Act of the Scottish
Parliament, an enactment contained in, or in an instrument made under, a
Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru, an enactment contained in, or in an instrument
made under, Northern Ireland legislation, and any   assimilated direct
legislation; “ FCA ” means the Financial Conduct Authority; “ FSMA 2000 ”
means the Financial Services and Markets Act 2000; “ modify ” includes amend,
repeal or revoke (and related expressions are to be read accordingly); “
Payment Systems Regulator ” means the body established under section 40(1) of
the Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013; “ PRA ” means the Prudential
Regulation Authority; “ primary legislation ” means— an Act of Parliament, an
Act of the Scottish Parliament, an Act or Measure of Senedd Cymru, or Northern
Ireland legislation; “ subordinate legislation ” means— any Order in Council,
order, rules, regulations, scheme, warrant, byelaw or other instrument made
under any Act, or any instrument made under an Act of the Scottish Parliament,
a Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru or Northern Ireland legislation, and includes
any Order in Council, order, rules, regulations, scheme, warrant, byelaw or
other instrument made on or after IP completion day under any   assimilated
direct   legislation.

80.2

. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .

#### Pre-commencement consultation

81

81.1

Subsection (2) applies to a duty to consult, so far as applying to or in
connection with, or otherwise arising in consequence of, a provision of an
enactment as modified or made—

81.1.a

by or under this Act, or

81.1.b

by or under another Act as amended by this Act.

81.2

The duty to consult may be satisfied by things done before the commencement
date (as well as by things done on or after that date).

81.3

The “ commencement date ”, in relation to a provision of an enactment as
modified or made—

81.3.a

by or under this Act, or

81.3.b

by or under another Act as amended by this Act,

means the date on which the modification or making of that provision comes
into force.

#### Financial provision

82

There is to be paid out of money provided by Parliament any expenditure
incurred by the Treasury for any purpose in connection with this Act.

#### Power to make consequential provision

83

83.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision that is consequential on this
Act or on any provision made under it.

83.2

The power to make regulations under this section may (among other things) be
exercised by modifying any provision made by or under an enactment (including
this Act).

83.3

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative procedure if
they amend, repeal or revoke any provision of primary legislation.

83.4

Regulations under this section to which subsection (3) does not apply are
subject to the negative procedure.

#### Regulations

84

84.1

Any power to make regulations under this Act is exercisable by statutory
instrument.

84.2

Any power to make regulations under this Act includes power—

84.2.a

to make provision by reference to any rules or other instruments as they have
effect from time to time;

84.2.b

to make different provision for different purposes;

84.2.c

to make supplementary, incidental, consequential, transitional, transitory or
saving provision.

84.3

Where regulations under this Act are subject to “the affirmative procedure”,
the regulations may not be made unless a draft of the statutory instrument
containing them has been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, each
House of Parliament.

84.4

Where regulations under this Act are subject to “the negative procedure”, the
statutory instrument containing them is subject to annulment in pursuance of a
resolution of either House of Parliament.

84.5

Any provision that may be made by regulations under this Act, or under any
other enactment, subject to the negative procedure may be made in regulations,
made under or by virtue of this Act, subject to the affirmative procedure.

84.6

If an instrument, or a draft of an instrument, containing regulations under
this Act would, apart from this subsection, be treated as a hybrid instrument
for the purposes of the standing orders of either House of Parliament, it is
to proceed in that House as if it were not a hybrid instrument.

84.7

This section does not apply to regulations under section 86, except so far as
making provision by virtue of section 4(1).

#### Extent

85

85.1

This Act extends to England and Wales, Scotland and Northern Ireland except as
provided by subsection (2).

85.2

The following extend to England and Wales and Scotland only—

85.2.a

section 73;

85.2.b

section 74.

85.3

The power under section 430(3) of FSMA 2000 may be exercised so as to extend
to any of the Channel Islands or the Isle of Man any amendment or repeal made
by or under this Act of any part of that Act (with or without modifications).

#### Commencement

86

86.1

The following come into force on the day on which this Act is passed—

86.1.a

this Part;

86.1.b

Part 5 of Schedule 2, and section 2 so far as relating to that Part;

86.1.c

section 20(3), so far as conferring a power to make regulations;

86.1.d

section 24;

86.1.e

section 56 and Schedule 10, so far as conferring power to make regulations;

86.1.f

section 77;

86.1.g

section 78.

86.2

The following provisions come into force two months after Royal Assent—

86.2.a

section 22;

86.2.b

section 52;

86.2.c

section 54;

86.2.d

section 55;

86.2.e

section 58;

86.2.f

section 60;

86.2.g

section 61;

86.2.h

section 62;

86.2.i

section 72;

86.2.j

section 74.

86.3

The rest of this Act comes into force on such day as the Treasury may by
regulations appoint.

86.4

Different days may be appointed for different purposes.

86.5

The Treasury may by regulations make transitional or saving provision in
connection with the coming into force of any provision of this Act.

86.6

The power to make regulations under subsection  (5)  includes power to make
different provision for different purposes.

86.7

Regulations under this section are to be made by statutory instrument.

#### Short title

87

This Act may be cited as the Financial Services and Markets Act 2023.

##### EU tertiary legislation etc

Any provision made under any of the following EU directives— a Directive
98/26/EC  of the European Parliament and of the Council of 19 May 1998 on
settlement finality in payment and securities settlement systems; b Directive
2001/24/EC  of the European Parliament and of the Council of 4 April 2001 on
the reorganisation and winding up of credit institutions; c Directive
2001/34/EC  of the European Parliament and of the Council of 28 May 2001 on
the admission of securities to official stock exchange listing and on
information to be published on those securities; d Directive 2002/47/EC  of
the European Parliament and of the Council of 6 June 2002 on financial
collateral arrangements; e Directive 2002/65/EC  of the European Parliament
and of the Council of 23 September 2002 concerning the distance marketing of
consumer financial services; f Directive 2002/87/EC  of the European
Parliament and of the Council of 16 December 2002 on the supplementary
supervision of credit institutions, insurance undertakings and investment
firms in a financial conglomerate; g Directive 2004/109/EC  of the European
Parliament and of the Council of 15 December 2004 on the harmonisation of
transparency requirements in relation to information about issuers whose
securities are admitted to trading on a regulated market; h Directive
2008/48/EC  of the European Parliament and of the Council of 23 April 2008 on
credit agreements for consumers; i Directive 2009/65/EC  of the European
Parliament and of the Council of 13 July 2009 on the coordination of laws,
regulations and administrative provisions relating to undertakings for
collective investment in transferable securities; j Directive 2009/103/EC  of
the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 September 2009 relating to
insurance against civil liability in respect of the use of motor vehicles, and
the enforcement of the obligation to insure against such liability; k
Directive 2009/110/EC  of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16
September 2009 on the taking up, pursuit and prudential supervision of the
business of electronic money institutions; l Directive 2009/138/EC  of the
European Parliament and of the Council of 25 November 2009 on the taking-up
and pursuit of the business of Insurance and Reinsurance; m Directive
2011/61/EU  of the European Parliament and of the Council of 8 June 2011 on
Alternative Investment Fund Managers; n Directive 2011/89/EU  of the European
Parliament and of the Council of 16 November 2011 amending  Directives
98/78/EC ,  2002/87/EC ,  2006/48/EC  and  2009/138/EC  as regards the
supplementary supervision of financial entities in a financial conglomerate; o
Directive 2013/36/EU  of the European Parliament and of the Council of 26 June
2013 on access to the activity of credit institutions and the prudential
supervision of credit institutions and investment firms; p Directive
2014/17/EU  of the European Parliament and of the Council of 4 February 2014
on credit agreements for consumers relating to residential immovable property;
q Directive 2014/49/EU  of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16
April 2014 on deposit guarantee schemes; r Directive 2014/57/EU  of the
European Parliament and of the Council of 16 April 2014 on criminal sanctions
for market abuse; s Directive 2014/59/EU  of the European Parliament and of
the Council of 15 May 2014 establishing a framework for the recovery and
resolution of credit institutions and investment firms; t Directive 2014/65/EU
of the European Parliament and of the Council of 15 May 2014 on markets in
financial instruments; u Directive 2014/92/EU  of the European Parliament and

instrument as it had effect in EU law before IP completion day).

Any provision made under an instrument listed in Part 2.

Any technical standards to which Chapter 2A of Part 9A of FSMA 2000 applies.

##### Primary legislation

In FSMA 2000— a section 55J(7A) to (7C); b section 55KA; c section 137A(6) and
(7); d section 137G(6) and (7); e Chapter 2A of Part 9A; f Part 9D; g section
192XA(3) and (4); h section 300H(4) (as inserted by section 11(2) of this
Act); i section 367(3)(za); j paragraph 10(5) of Schedule 17A.

##### Other EU-derived legislation

EU-derived legislation not falling within Parts 1 to 3 so far as relating to
financial services or markets (other than instruments excluded from this Part
by regulations under section 1(5)).

For this purpose— a “ EU-derived legislation ” means— i   assimilated direct
legislation, ii subordinate legislation so far as it contains provision for
the purpose of implementing, or otherwise in relation to, an EU directive or
any other obligation that was created or arose by or under the EU Treaties
before IP completion day, iii subordinate legislation made under section 3, or
iv subordinate legislation made under the European Union (Withdrawal) Act
2018; b EU-derived legislation is to be taken as “relating” to financial
services or markets if its purpose, or one of its main purposes, is for or in
connection with the imposition of requirements on the provision of financial
services or the operation of financial markets or exchanges.

Transitional amendments

Section 2

##### Amendments to the Markets in Financial Instruments Regulation

###### Introductory

1

Regulation (EU) No 600/2014  of the European Parliament and of the Council of
15 May 2014 on markets in financial instruments is amended in accordance with
this Part of this Schedule.

###### Transparency requirements for equities

2

In Article 3 (pre-trade transparency requirements), after paragraph 3 insert—

2.4

The FCA may make technical standards to specify—

2.4.a

the range of bid and offer prices, or designated market-maker quotes, to be
made public for each class of financial instrument concerned in accordance
with paragraph 1, and

2.4.b

the depth of trading interest at those prices.

2.5

In making technical standards under paragraph 4 the FCA must take into account
the necessary calibration for the different types of trading systems referred
to in paragraph 2.

3

For Article 4 substitute—

######### Waivers for equity instruments

3.1

The FCA may by rules provide for the obligation for market operators and
investment firms operating a trading venue to make public the information
referred to in Article 3(1) to be waived in such cases as the rules may
specify.

3.2

The power to make rules under paragraph 1 is exercisable only if the FCA
considers that the rules are necessary or expedient for the purpose of
advancing one or more of its operational objectives referred to in section
1B(3) of FSMA.

3.3

Rules under paragraph 1 may impose whatever conditions on the application of
the waiver the FCA considers appropriate.

3.4

The FCA must monitor the application of waivers conferred by rules under
paragraph 1 (in particular the effect of such waivers on price formation and
compliance with any conditions imposed under paragraph 3).

3.5

The FCA may by notice given to a market operator, or an investment firm
operating a trading venue, withdraw a waiver granted by rules made under this
Article if the FCA considers that the waiver is being used—

3.5.a

in a way that deviates from its original purpose, or

3.5.b

to avoid requirements imposed by the rules.

4

After Article 4 insert—

######### Suspension of waivers

4.1

The FCA may direct that a waiver provided for by Article 4 is suspended
(whether entirely or to such an extent as may be specified in the direction)
if it considers that continued use of the waiver would unduly harm price
formation.

4.2

The suspension of a waiver by virtue of a direction under paragraph 1 may not
have effect for a period longer than six months, but this does not prevent the
giving of a further direction under that paragraph by which the suspension is
renewed for a period no longer than six months.

4.3

The FCA may give a direction under paragraph 1 only if it considers that the
direction is necessary to advance the FCA’s integrity objective under section
1D of FSMA.

4.4

In deciding whether to give a direction under paragraph 1 to suspend (or renew
the suspension of) a waiver the FCA must have regard to—

4.4.a

its consumer protection objective under section 1C of FSMA and its competition
objective under section 1E of FSMA,

4.4.b

relevant information produced under Article 3, or under equivalent pre-trading
transparency requirements in other jurisdictions, about the use of the waiver
in the United Kingdom, or under equivalent waiver arrangements in any other
country, in relation to the financial instrument concerned, and

4.4.c

any other relevant information available in relation to trading volumes in the
financial instrument concerned, whether in the United Kingdom or elsewhere.

4.5

The FCA must consult the Treasury before giving a direction under paragraph 1.

4.6

The requirement to consult under paragraph 5 does not apply if the FCA
considers it necessary by reason of urgency to give the direction before such
consultation can be carried out in order to protect—

4.6.a

the transparency of the price formation process, or

4.6.b

the interests of consumers (within the meaning of section 1G of FSMA).

5

Omit Article 5 (volume cap mechanism).

6

6.1

Article 14 (obligation for systematic internalisers to make public firm quotes
in respect of shares etc) is amended as follows.

6.2

In paragraph 6A, omit “referred to in Article 5(3A)”.

6.3

After paragraph 6C insert—

6.3.6D

The reference in paragraph 6A to the “ transitional period ” is a reference
to—

6.3.6D.a

the period of four years beginning with IP completion day; or

6.3.6D.b

the period ending on such day as the Treasury may direct, if that period ends
earlier than the period mentioned in sub-paragraph (a).

6.3.6E

In deciding whether to issue a direction under paragraph 6D(b), the Treasury
must take into account whether the FCA is able to carry out its functions
relating to transparency under this Regulation and its implementing measures.

###### Transparency requirements for fixed income instruments and derivatives etc

7

For Articles 8 to 11 substitute—

########## Pre-trade transparency requirements for fixed income instruments and derivatives etc

7.1

The FCA must by rules impose pre-trade transparency requirements on relevant
persons in respect of the trading of such relevant instruments as the FCA
determines should be subject to the requirements for the purposes of
furthering—

7.1.a

efficient price formation, and

7.1.b

the fair evaluation of financial assets.

7.2

The power to make rules under paragraph 1 is exercisable only if the FCA
considers that the rules are necessary or expedient for the purpose of
advancing one or more of its operational objectives referred to in section
1B(3) of FSMA.

7.3

In making rules under paragraph 1 the FCA must (in particular) have regard to
the impact that requirements imposed by the rules will have on market
liquidity.

7.4

The reference in paragraph 1 to “ pre-trade transparency requirements ” is a
reference to whatever kinds of requirements relating to transparency before
trading that the rules may specify, for example—

7.4.a

requirements to make public matters specified in the rules in respect of the
trading of relevant instruments;

7.4.b

requirements about the means by which, and the times at which, such matters
are to be made public;

7.4.c

requirements for the giving of access to the arrangements employed for the
making of such matters public;

7.4.d

requirements in respect of relevant instruments that are traded in a
standardised and frequent way, if not subject to disclosure requirements of
the kind mentioned in sub-paragraph (a).

7.5

Rules under paragraph 1 may—

7.5.a

impose requirements by reference to the types of trading system used;

7.5.b

impose different requirements in relation to different types of trading
system;

7.5.c

provide for the criteria by which the determination referred to in that
paragraph is to be made.

7.6

In this Article and in Article 9—

“ relevant instruments ” means bonds, structured finance products, emission
allowances, derivatives and instruments included within package orders; “
relevant persons ” means market operators and investment firms operating a
trading venue.

########## Article 8: waivers or suspensions for fixed income instruments and derivatives etc

7.1

Rules under Article 8 may include provision for any requirements imposed by
the rules to be waived in such cases, and to such extent, as may be determined
by or under the rules.

7.2

Rules that include provision under paragraph 1 may impose whatever conditions
on the application of a waiver the FCA considers appropriate.

7.3

The FCA may by notice given to a relevant person withdraw a waiver granted by
virtue of paragraph 1 if the FCA considers that the waiver is being used—

7.3.a

in a way that deviates from its original purpose, or

7.3.b

to avoid requirements provided for in the rules.

7.4

The FCA may by notice suspend requirements imposed by rules under Article 8 in
the case of such relevant instruments, or class of relevant instruments, as
may be specified in the notice.

7.5

A notice under paragraph 4 suspending requirements—

7.5.a

may be given subject to conditions;

7.5.b

must specify the period for which the suspension has effect;

7.5.c

must be published in the manner appearing to the FCA to be best calculated to
bring it to the attention of persons likely to be affected by it;

7.5.d

may be varied or withdrawn by the giving of a further notice (and sub-
paragraph (c) applies to any such notice).

7.6

The power under paragraph 4 to suspend requirements is exercisable only if the
FCA considers that it is necessary to do so to advance the FCA’s integrity
objective under section 1D of FSMA.

7.7

In deciding whether to exercise the power under paragraph 4 to suspend
requirements the FCA must also have regard to—

7.7.a

its consumer protection objective under section 1C of FSMA, and

7.7.b

its competition objective under section 1E of FSMA.

########## Post-trade transparency requirements for fixed income instruments and derivatives etc

7.1

The FCA must by rules impose post-trade transparency requirements on relevant
persons in respect of the trading of such relevant instruments as the FCA
determines should be subject to the requirements for the purposes of
furthering—

7.1.a

efficient price formation, and

7.1.b

the fair evaluation of financial assets.

7.2

The power to make rules under paragraph 1 is exercisable only if the FCA
considers that the rules are necessary or expedient for the purpose of
advancing one or more of its operational objectives referred to in section
1B(3) of FSMA.

7.3

In making rules under paragraph 1 the FCA must (in particular) have regard to
the impact that requirements imposed by the rules will have on market
liquidity.

7.4

The reference in paragraph 1 to “ post-trade transparency requirements ” is a
reference to whatever kinds of requirements relating to transparency after the
execution of trades that the rules may specify, for example—

7.4.a

requirements to make public matters specified in the rules in respect of the
trading of relevant instruments (including the price, volume and time of
transactions);

7.4.b

requirements about the means by which, and the times at which, such matters
are to be made public;

7.4.c

requirements for the giving of access to the arrangements employed for the
making of such matters public.

7.5

Rules under paragraph 1 may—

7.5.a

impose requirements by reference to the types of trading system used;

7.5.b

impose different requirements in relation to different types of trading
system;

7.5.c

provide for the criteria by which the determination referred to in that
paragraph is to be made.

7.6

In this Article and in Article 11—

“ relevant instruments ” means bonds, structured finance products, emission
allowances, derivatives and instruments included within package transactions;
“ relevant persons ” means market operators and investment firms operating a
trading venue.

########## Article 10: deferrals and suspensions for fixed income instruments and derivatives etc

7.1

Rules under Article 10 may include provision authorising relevant persons to
defer complying with requirements imposed by the rules in such cases and to
such extent as the rules may specify.

7.2

Rules made by virtue of paragraph 1 may impose whatever conditions on the
application of a deferral the FCA considers appropriate.

7.3

The FCA may by notice suspend any requirements imposed by rules under Article
10 in the case of such relevant instruments, or class of relevant instruments,
as may be specified in the notice.

7.4

A notice under paragraph 3 suspending requirements—

7.4.a

may be given subject to conditions;

7.4.b

must specify the period for which the suspension has effect;

7.4.c

must be published in the manner appearing to the FCA to be best calculated to
bring it to the attention of persons likely to be affected by it;

7.4.d

may be varied or withdrawn by the giving of a further notice (and sub-
paragraph (c) applies to any such notice).

7.5

The power under paragraph 3 to suspend requirements is exercisable only if the
FCA considers that it is necessary to do so to advance the FCA’s integrity
objective under section 1D of FSMA.

7.6

In deciding whether to exercise the power under paragraph 3 to suspend
requirements the FCA must also have regard to—

7.6.a

its consumer protection objective under section 1C of FSMA, and

7.6.b

its competition objective under section 1E of FSMA.

###### Systematic internalisers and other investment firms

8

In Article 2(1) (definitions), for points (12) and (12A) substitute—

8.12

“ systematic internaliser ” means an investment firm which deals on own
account when executing client orders outside a UK regulated market, UK MTF or
UK OTF without operating a multilateral system and which—

8.12.a

does so on an organised, frequent, systematic and substantial basis, or

8.12.b

has chosen to opt in to the systematic internaliser regime;

8.12A

for the purposes of point (12), whether dealing is taking place on a basis
that is organised, frequent, systematic and substantial is to be determined in

under paragraph 2 of this Article);

.

For Article 18 substitute—

######### Systematic internalisers: pre-trade transparency requirements for fixed income instruments and derivatives etc

10.1

The FCA may by rules impose pre-trade transparency requirements on systematic
internalisers in respect of the trading of such relevant instruments as the
FCA determines should be subject to the requirements for the purposes of
furthering—

10.1.a

efficient price formation, and

10.1.b

the fair evaluation of financial assets.

10.2

The power to make rules under paragraph 1 is exercisable only if the FCA

1B(3) of FSMA.

10.3

In making rules under paragraph 1 the FCA must (in particular) have regard to

10.4

The reference in paragraph 1 to “ pre-trade transparency requirements ” is a

10.4.a

10.4.c

instruments;

10.4.d

10.5

determine.

In this Article and in Article 18a “ relevant instruments ” means bonds,
structured finance products, emission allowances, derivatives and instruments
included within package orders.

######### Article 18: waivers and suspensions for fixed income instruments and derivatives etc

10.1

Rules under Article 18 may include provision for any requirements imposed by
those rules to be waived in such cases, and to such extent, as may be
determined by or under the rules.

10.2

Rules that include provision under paragraph 1 may impose whatever conditions
on the application of a waiver as the FCA considers appropriate.

10.3

10.3.a

10.3.b

10.5.a

10.5.b

10.5.d

may be varied or withdrawn by the giving of a further notice (and sub-
paragraph (c) applies to any such notice).

10.6

The power under paragraph 4 to suspend requirements is exercisable only if the

10.7

10.7.a

######### Notification and publication requirements

10.1

10.2

internalisers for which it has received notification under paragraph 1.

For Article 21 substitute—

######### Investment firms (including systematic internalisers): post-trade transparency requirements for fixed income instruments and derivatives etc

11.1

11.1.a

counterparties, or relevant non-financial counterparties, for the purposes of
Article 28 (see paragraph 1A of that Article)” .

16

16.1

Article 28 (obligation to trade on regulated markets, MTFs or OTFs) is amended
as follows.

16.2

In paragraph 1, for the words from the beginning to “Article 10(1)(b) of
Regulation (EU) No 648/2012 ” substitute  “Relevant financial counterparties
and relevant non-financial counterparties shall conclude transactions which
are neither intragroup transactions as defined in Article 3 of  Regulation
(EU) No 648/2012  nor transactions covered by the transitional provisions in
Article 89 of that Regulation with other relevant financial counterparties or
other relevant non-financial counterparties” .

16.3

After paragraph 1 insert—

16.3.1A

For the purposes of this Article—

16.3.1A.a

“ financial counterparty ” and “ non-financial counterparty ” have the same
meanings as in  Regulation (EU) No 648/2012  (see Article 2(8) and (9) of that
Regulation);

16.3.1A.b

a financial counterparty is a “relevant” financial counterparty if it is
subject to the clearing obligation referred to in Article 4 of  Regulation
(EU) No 648/2012 ;

16.3.1A.c

a non-financial counterparty is a “relevant” non-financial counterparty in
respect of derivative contracts pertaining to any asset classes if it is
subject to that clearing obligation in respect of derivative contracts

17

After Article 28 insert—

########## Suspension or modification of Article 28

17.1

The FCA may direct that the trading obligation imposed by Article 28(1) and
(2) (the “DTO”) is suspended or modified in accordance with the direction if
it considers that the suspension or modification—

17.1.a

is necessary for the purpose of preventing or mitigating disruption to
financial markets, and

17.1.b

advances one or more of the FCA’s operational objectives referred to in
section 1B(3) of FSMA.

17.2

A direction under this Article may provide for the DTO to be suspended or
modified—

17.2.a

in the case of all persons to whom the DTO applies or only to such persons or
descriptions of persons as are specified in the direction;

17.2.b

in the case of all derivatives to which the DTO applies or only to such
derivatives, or classes of derivatives, as are specified in the direction;

17.2.c

by reference to the venues on which derivative transactions are concluded
under the DTO;

17.2.d

subject to conditions.

17.3

In giving a direction under this Article the FCA must have regard to its
competitiveness and growth objective in section 1EB of FSMA.

17.4

Before giving a direction under this Article the FCA must consult—

17.4.a

the Bank of England, and

17.4.b

the PRA, if the PRA has an interest in the proposed direction.

The PRA has an interest in a proposed direction if the direction—

17.4.a

might affect the PRA’s discharge of its functions conferred by or under FSMA
or any other enactment, or

17.4.b

would apply to a PRA-authorised person or to a person connected with a PRA-
authorised person (and for this purpose “ PRA authorised person ” has the same
meaning as in FSMA and “ connected ” is to be read in accordance with section
165(11) of FSMA).

17.5

A direction under this Article may be given only with the consent of the
Treasury.

The Treasury must notify the FCA in writing whether or not consent is given
before the end of four weeks beginning with the day on which the proposed
direction is submitted to the Treasury for consent (and if the notice is not
given before the end of that period the Treasury are deemed to have
consented).

17.6

Where the FCA gives a direction under this Article it must also prepare a
statement setting out—

17.6.a

an explanation of the purpose of the direction, including (where relevant) the
ways in which the direction will further the purpose mentioned in paragraph
1(a) and advance one or more of the objectives mentioned in paragraph 1(b),
and

17.6.b

such guidance in connection with the direction that the FCA considers
appropriate.

17.7

The FCA must publish a direction given under this Article together with the
statement mentioned in paragraph 6.

17.8

The Treasury must lay before Parliament a copy of a direction given under this
Article and the statement mentioned in paragraph 6.

17.9

If a direction under this Article has effect for a period lasting longer than
6 months, the FCA must publish, as soon as reasonably practicable after the
end of each applicable 6 month period, a statement with an explanation as to
why the conditions in paragraph 1(a) and (b) continue to be met.

The reference to each “applicable 6 month period” is to—

17.9.a

the period of 6 months beginning with the day on which the direction is given,
and

17.9.b

each subsequent 6 month period during which the direction continues in effect.

17.10

Publication under paragraph 7 or 9 is to be in whatever way appears to the FCA
to be best calculated to bring the publication to the attention of the public.

17.11

A direction under this Article may be varied or revoked by the giving of a
further direction under this Article.

17.12

For the purposes of this Article—

17.12.a

the variation of a direction by virtue of paragraph 11 is not to be treated as
the giving of a new direction for the purposes of paragraph 9;

17.12.b

paragraphs 6(b) and 9 do not apply to the revocation of a direction by virtue
of paragraph 11.

17.13

The functions of the FCA under this Article are not “ relevant functions ” for
the purposes of section 84 of the Financial Services Act 2012 (arrangements
for the investigation of complaints relating to exercise of relevant functions
of regulators).

18

For Article 31 substitute—

########## Risk reduction services

18.1

The FCA may by rules provide for one or more relevant obligations not to
apply—

18.1.a

in relation to activities or transactions of a specified description carried
out as part of a risk reduction service, or

18.1.b

to persons of a specified description in the provision of such services.

18.2

The power to make rules under paragraph 1 is exercisable only if the FCA
considers that the rules are necessary or expedient for the purpose of
advancing one or more of its operational objectives referred to in section
1B(3) of FSMA.

18.3

The risk reduction services to which the rules relate may only be post-trade
services that do not give rise to any transactions that contribute to the
price discovery process.

18.4

The rules—

18.4.a

may describe the risk reduction services to which they relate in whatever way
the FCA considers appropriate (subject to paragraph 3);

18.4.b

may provide for whatever conditions or exceptions the FCA considers
appropriate.

18.5

Before making rules under paragraph 1 the FCA must consult the Bank of
England.

18.6

In this Article—

“ relevant obligation ” means— the best execution obligation in section 11.2A
of the Conduct of Business sourcebook; the obligation in rule 5AA.1.1 in the
Market Conduct sourcebook; the trading obligation imposed by Article 28 of
this Regulation; “ risk reduction service ” means a service provided to two or
more counterparties to derivatives transactions for the purpose of reducing
non-market risks in derivatives portfolios (including, for example, portfolio
compression); “ specified ” means specified in the rules.

######### Bank of England rules

“country or territory outside the United Kingdom” .

33

After Article 28 (third party verifying STS compliance) insert—

########## STS equivalent non-UK securitisations

########### Designation of country or territory in relation to securitisations

33.1

The Treasury may by regulations designate a country or territory in relation
to securitisations of descriptions specified in the regulations.

33.2

The power in paragraph 1 is exercisable only if the Treasury are satisfied
that the law and practice which applies in the country or territory, in
relation to securitisations of the descriptions specified, has equivalent
effect (taken as a whole) to applicable UK law.

33.3

“ Applicable UK law ” means:

33.3.a

this Regulation, as it applies to STS securitisations, and

33.3.b

the Securitisation Regulations 2018 ( S.I. 2018/2188 ), as those regulations
apply to STS securitisations.

33.4

In making regulations under paragraph 1, the Treasury must have regard, in
addition to any other matters they consider relevant, to whether the FCA (and,
where relevant, the PRA) have established effective cooperation arrangements
with the competent authorities of the country or territory.

33.5

When considering whether to make, vary or revoke regulations under paragraph
1, the Treasury may, by making a request in writing to the FCA, require the
FCA to prepare a report on the law and practice of a country or territory
outside the United Kingdom, or particular aspects of such law and practice, in
relation to securitisations of descriptions specified in the request.

33.6

If the Treasury request a report under paragraph 5, the FCA must:

33.6.a

consult the PRA when preparing the report, and

33.6.b

provide the Treasury with the report within such reasonable period as may be
specified in the request (or such other period as may be agreed with the
Treasury).

33.7

Regulations under paragraph 1 may—

33.7.a

specify matters that a person carrying out a due-diligence assessment required
by Article 5(3) must consider with regard to an STS equivalent non-UK
securitisation;

33.7.b

in relation to a matter specified, specify the extent to which the person may
rely on the matter.

33.8

Regulations under this Article are to be made by statutory instrument.

33.9

Such regulations may—

33.9.a

contain incidental, supplemental, consequential and transitional provision;
and

33.9.b

make different provision for different purposes.

33.>10.

Regulations under this Article are subject to annulment in pursuance of a
resolution of either House of Parliament.

###### Position limits for commodity derivatives

45

In Part 3 (position limits and position management controls in commodity
derivatives), before regulation 16 insert—

########## FCA rules relating to position limits

45.15A

45.15A.1

The FCA may by rules require relevant persons to establish and apply—

45.15A.1.a

position limits in respect of specified commodity derivatives, or commodity
derivatives of a specified class, that are traded on a trading venue, and

45.15A.1.b

position management controls in relation to the trading of commodity
derivatives.

45.15A.2

The power to make rules under paragraph (1) is exercisable only if the FCA
considers that the rules are necessary or expedient for the purpose of
advancing one or more of its operational objectives referred to in section
1B(3) of the Act.

45.15A.3

In making rules under paragraph (1) the FCA must have regard to its
competitiveness and growth objective in section 1EB of the Act.

45.15A.4

Rules under paragraph (1) may provide for matters that relevant persons must
have regard to when establishing position limits, or position management
controls, under requirements imposed by the rules.

45.15A.5

Rules under paragraph (1) may provide for exemptions from the requirements
imposed by the rules to such extent, and in such cases, as the rules may
specify.

45.15A.6

The reference in paragraph (1)(b) to position management controls includes
(for example) arrangements under which—

45.15A.6.a

the open interest positions of persons can be monitored;

45.15A.6.b

information and documentation can be obtained from persons about the size of
positions entered into;

45.15A.6.c

requirements can be imposed on persons to terminate or reduce positions or to
provide liquidity.

45.15A.7

The following provisions of Part 9A of the Act (rules and guidance) apply in
relation to rules made by the FCA under this regulation as they apply in
relation to rules made by the FCA under that Part of the Act, subject to the
modification in paragraph (8)—

45.15A.7.a

section 137T (general supplementary powers);

45.15A.7.b

Chapter 2 (modification, waiver, contravention and procedural provisions),
with the exception of sections 138D (actions for damages) and 138EA (matters
to consider when making rules);

45.15A.7.c

section 141A (power to make consequential amendments of references to rules
etc).

45.15A.8

Section 137T applies as if the reference to authorised persons were a
reference to relevant persons to whom rules under this regulation apply.

45.15A.9

A requirement imposed by rules under this regulation is, for the purposes of
section 296 of the Act (regulator’s power to give directions), to be treated
as an obligation imposed under the Act.

45.15A.10

In this Part “ relevant persons ” means market operators and investment firms
operating a trading venue.

  New Schedule 6B to FSMA 2000

Section 8

    SCHEDULE 6B   Designated activities     Introductory   1     The matters
with respect to which provision may be made under section 71K in respect of
activities include (but are not limited to) those described in general terms
in this Schedule.       Derivatives   2     Activities related to entering
into derivative contracts (including those contracts not cleared by a central
counterparty).       3     Holding positions in commodity derivatives.
Short selling   4     Engaging in short selling in relation to specified
financial instruments (“shorted instruments”) including where—     a     a
person enters into a transaction which creates, or relates to, another
financial instrument, and         b     the effect (or one of the effects) of
the transaction is to confer a financial advantage on that person in the event
of a decrease in the price or value of the shorted instrument.
Securitisation   5     Acting as one of the following in a securitisation—
a     an originator,         b     a sponsor,         c     an original
lender, or         d     a securitisation special purpose entity.           6
Selling a securitisation position to a retail client located in the United
Kingdom.       Financial markets   7     Offering securities to the public.
8     Applying for, securing or maintaining the admission of securities to
trading on a securities market.       Using a benchmark   9     Issuing an
instrument which references a benchmark.       10     Determining the amount
payable under an instrument or financial contract by reference to a benchmark
or otherwise being a party to a financial contract which references a
benchmark.       11     Measuring the performance of an investment fund
through a benchmark.       Contributing to a benchmark   12     Acting as a
“benchmark contributor” including persons in the United Kingdom or a third
country.       13     Contributing data to a regulated benchmark administrator
for the purpose of the administrator determining a benchmark.

  FMI Sandboxes

Section 13

##### Participation

1

1.1

Eligibility for participation in the FMI sandbox arrangements for FMI entities
and persons other than FMI entities.

1.2

The requirements mentioned in sub-paragraph (1) may be framed by reference to—

1.2.a

the description of persons who carry on activities;

1.2.b

the description of activities carried on by persons;

1.2.c

the relationship of persons with FMI entities.

1.3

Application or other procedures for participating in the FMI sandbox
arrangements.

1.4

Information to be supplied by persons wishing to participate in the FMI
sandbox arrangements for the purposes of assessing eligibility.

1.5

Information to be supplied by persons participating in the FMI sandbox
arrangements for the purposes of notifying other persons of their
participation.

##### Technology

2

The particular kinds of technology that may be used under the FMI sandbox
arrangements for the purposes of assessing their efficiency or effectiveness.

##### Practices

3

3.1

The particular kinds of practices that may be adopted under the FMI sandbox
arrangements for the purposes of assessing their efficiency or effectiveness.

3.2

The practices referred to in sub-paragraph (1) include practices adopted in
the issuance, trading or settlement of financial instruments in a way not
otherwise possible or practicable as a result of requirements imposed by
relevant enactments.

##### Financial instruments

4

4.1

Descriptions of financial instrument (“the FMI sandbox instruments”) that may
be traded under the FMI sandbox arrangements.

4.2

The forms that the FMI sandbox instruments may take for the purposes of
trading as part of the FMI sandbox arrangements.

4.3

Limitations or prohibitions on the trading of the FMI sandbox instruments, or
of other instruments that are converted from, or are otherwise linked to, the
FMI sandbox instruments.

4.4

Limitations (whether by reference to number, value or another metric) on the
amount of FMI sandbox instruments permitted for trading under the FMI sandbox
arrangements.

4.5

References in this paragraph to the trading of FMI sandbox instruments include
references to their settlement.

##### Settlement of payments

5

5.1

How payments are to be settled in respect of transactions taking place under
the FMI sandbox arrangements.

5.2

Provision under sub-paragraph (1) includes provision as to cash settlement or
whatever other forms of settlement the provision may specify.

##### Requirements

6

6.1

Requirements applicable—

6.1.a

to persons participating in the FMI sandbox arrangements, and

6.1.b

to other persons in connection with such arrangements.

6.2

Provision under this paragraph includes provision conferring powers on the
appropriate regulator to make rules or technical standards applicable for the
purposes of the FMI sandbox arrangements.

##### Cooperation

7

Duties of the appropriate regulators to cooperate with each other for the
purposes of implementing and operating the FMI sandbox arrangements.

##### Transparency and reporting

8

8.1

Publication of specified details of the FMI sandbox arrangements by the
Treasury or the appropriate regulator (or both).

8.2

Duties of appropriate regulators to provide the Treasury with information
about the operation of the FMI sandbox arrangements.

8.3

Requirements imposed by virtue of this paragraph are in addition to the
requirement imposed by section 14.

##### Enforcement

9

9.1

How requirements imposed by or under the FMI sandbox arrangements are to be
enforced.

9.2

Provision under sub-paragraph (1) may be made by—

9.2.a

conferring powers on the appropriate regulator;

9.2.b

applying provisions of FSMA 2000 in relation to enforcement;

9.2.c

imposing other means of enforcement set out in the arrangements.

9.3

9.3.a

suspend or terminate a person’s participation in the FMI sandbox arrangements;

9.3.b

impose civil penalties.

  Digital settlement assets

Section 22

##### Amendments to the Banking Act 2009

1

The Banking Act 2009 is amended as follows.

2

In the heading to Part 5 (payment systems), after “systems” insert  “and
service providers” .

3

In section 181 (overview), after “services” insert  “, including” .

4

4.1

Section 182 (interpretation of payment system) is amended as follows.

4.2

In the heading, for ““payment system”” substitute  “key terms” .

4.3

In subsection (1), after “money” insert  “or digital settlement assets” .

4.4

After subsection (4) insert—

4.4.4A

In subsection (1) “ digital settlement asset ” means a digital representation
of value or rights, whether or not cryptographically secured, that—

4.4.4A.a

can be used for the settlement of payment obligations,

4.4.4A.b

can be transferred, stored or traded electronically, and

4.4.4A.c

uses technology supporting the recording or storage of data (which may include
distributed ledger technology).

4.4.4B

In this section, “ digital settlement asset ” includes a right to, or an
interest in, a digital settlement asset.

4.5

After subsection (5) insert—

4.5.5A

In this Part, a “DSA service provider” is a person who provides one or more
services in relation to a payment system that includes arrangements using
digital settlement assets where—

4.5.5A.a

the person creates or issues the digital settlement assets involved in the
payment system,

4.5.5A.b

the person provides services to safeguard, or to safeguard and administer,
digital settlement assets including their private cryptographic keys (or means
of access),

4.5.5A.c

the person is directly involved in any of the activities mentioned in
paragraphs (a) or (b),

4.5.5A.d

the person is a digital settlement asset exchange provider,

4.5.5A.e

the person sets rules, standards, or conditions of access or participation in
relation to the payment system, or

4.5.5A.f

the person provides any service that facilitates, or supports, a transfer of
money or digital settlement assets to be made using the payment system,
including any infrastructure provider in relation to the system.

4.5.5B

In this Part “ digital settlement asset exchange provider ” means a person who
provides one or more of the following services, including as creator or issuer
of any of the digital settlement assets, by—

4.5.5B.a

exchanging, or arranging the exchange of—

4.5.5B.a.i

digital settlement assets for money,

4.5.5B.a.ii

money for digital settlement assets,

4.5.5B.a.iii

digital settlement assets and money for digital settlement assets, or

4.5.5B.a.iv

digital settlement assets and money for money,

4.5.5B.b

exchanging, or arranging the exchange of, one digital settlement asset for
another, or

4.5.5B.c

operating an automated process to carry out any of the activities mentioned in
paragraphs (a) and (b).

4.5.5C

The Treasury may by regulations amend—

4.5.5C.a

the definition of “digital settlement asset” in subsection (4A);

4.5.5C.b

the definition of “DSA service provider” in subsection (5A);

4.5.5C.c

the definition in section 206AA of a person who provides services connected
with a recognised payment system that uses digital settlement assets.

5.1

9

After section 184 insert—

######### Recognition order: DSA service provider

9.184A

9.184A.1

The Treasury may by order (“recognition order”) specify a DSA service provider
as a recognised DSA service provider for the purposes of this Part.

9.184A.2

A recognition order under this section must specify in as much detail as is
reasonably practicable the services provided.

9.184A.3

The Treasury may not specify a DSA service provider operated solely by the
Bank of England.

10

In the heading to section 185 (recognition criteria) after “criteria” insert
“: payment system” .

11

After section 185 insert—

######### Recognition criteria: DSA service provider

11.185A

11.185A.1

The Treasury may make a recognition order in respect of a DSA service provider
only if satisfied that any deficiencies in the services provided by the
service provider, or any disruption to the provision of those services, would
be likely—

11.185A.1.a

to threaten the stability of, or confidence in, the UK financial system, or

11.185A.1.b

to have serious consequences for business or other interests throughout the
United Kingdom.

11.185A.2

In considering whether to specify a DSA service provider the Treasury must
have regard to—

11.185A.2.a

the value of the services in relation to payment systems that the DSA service
provider presently provides or is likely to provide in the future,

11.185A.2.b

the nature of the services in relation to payment systems that the DSA service
provider provides,

11.185A.2.c

whether those services or their equivalent could be provided by others, and

11.185A.2.d

the relationship between the DSA service provider and—

11.185A.2.d.i

operators of payment systems that use digital settlement assets, and

11.185A.2.d.ii

other DSA service providers.
