After section 192 (role of FCA and PRA), insert—

######### Power of Bank to require FCA to refrain from specified action

20.192A

20.192A.1

Where the first, second and third conditions are met, the Bank of England may
give a direction under this section to the FCA.

20.192A.2

The first condition is that the FCA is proposing to exercise any of its powers
in relation to—

20.192A.2.a

a recognised payment system that includes arrangements using digital
settlement assets, or

20.192A.2.b

a recognised DSA service provider.

20.192A.3

The second condition is that the Bank of England is of the opinion that the
exercise of the power in the manner proposed may—

20.192A.3.a

threaten the stability of the UK financial system,

20.192A.3.b

have serious consequences for business or other interests in the United
Kingdom (including for the payment system or provider in relation to which the
powers are proposed to be exercised), or

20.192A.3.c

have an adverse effect on the Bank’s ability to act in its capacity as a
monetary authority.

20.192A.4

The third condition is that the Bank of England is of the opinion that the
giving of the direction is necessary in order to avoid an outcome mentioned in
subsection (3).

20.192A.5

A direction under this section is a direction requiring the FCA not to
exercise the power or not to exercise it in a specified manner.

20.192A.6

The direction may be expressed to have effect during a specified period or
until revoked.

20.192A.7

The FCA is not required to comply with a direction under this section if or to
the extent that in the opinion of the FCA compliance would be incompatible
with any international obligation of the United Kingdom.

After section 203B (annual report) insert—

######### Policy statement

33.203C

33.203C.1

The Bank of England must prepare a statement of the general policy it proposes
to follow in relation to its oversight under this Part of —

33.203C.1.a

recognised payment systems that include arrangements using digital settlement
assets,

33.203C.1.b

DSA service providers, and

33.203C.1.c

service providers as described in sections 206A and 206AA.

33.203C.2

Before issuing a statement of policy under this section, the Bank must consult
the FCA.

33.203C.3

The Bank must —

33.203C.3.a

publish the statement on its website,

33.203C.3.b

send a copy to the Treasury, and

33.203C.3.c

review the statement from time to time and revise it if necessary (and
paragraphs (a) and (b) apply to a revision).

33.203C.4

Nothing in this section is to be regarded as preventing the Bank of England
from exercising any of its powers under this Part where it considers it
necessary to do so by reason of urgency, before it has prepared a statement
under this section.

digital settlement assets, subsection (2)(a) includes a person providing
services connected with the system. See section 206AA.

37.6

In the opening words of subsection (4), after “(2)(b)” insert  “or (2A)(b) or
systems under subsection (2B)(b)” .

37.7

In subsection (4)(b) after “system” insert  “or DSA service provider” .

37.8

In subsection (5) after “(2)(b)” insert  “, (2A)(b) or (2B)(b)” .

38

After section 206A insert—

######### Service providers connected with a recognised payment system that uses digital settlement assets

38.206AA

For the purposes of section 206A(3A), a person provides services connected
with the system where—

38.206AA.a

the person creates or issues the digital settlement assets involved in the
payment system,

38.206AA.b

the person provides services to safeguard, or to safeguard and administer,
digital settlement assets including their private cryptographic keys (or means
of access),

38.206AA.c

the person is directly involved in any of the activities mentioned in
paragraphs (a) or (b),

38.206AA.d

the person is a digital settlement asset exchange provider,

38.206AA.e

the person sets rules, standards, or conditions of access or participation in
relation to the payment system, or

38.206AA.f

the person provides any service that facilitates, or supports, a transfer of
money or digital settlement assets to be made using the payment system,
including any infrastructure provider in relation to the system.

39

In section 259 (statutory instruments), in the Table in subsection (3), in
Part 5, at the appropriate place insert—

          182(5C) Meaning of “digital settlement asset” and “DSA service
provider” Draft affirmative resolution

##### Amendments to the Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013

41.2.2A

In this Part—

      “ funds ” includes digital settlement assets (except in section
41(2)(e));           “ digital settlement asset ” means a digital
representation of value or rights, whether or not cryptographically secured,
that—         can be used for the settlement of payment obligations,
can be transferred, stored or traded electronically, and           uses
technology supporting the recording or storage of data (which may include
distributed ledger technology).

41.2.2B

in, a digital settlement asset.

Section 51

1

The Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013 is amended as follows.

In section 39 (overview)—

2.a

after subsection (11) insert—

2.a.11A

Sections 102A and 102B contain provision about Treasury powers to make
recommendations in connection with the Payment Systems Regulator’s general
duties and to specify matters to which the Regulator must have regard when
exercising certain functions.

;

2.b

in subsection (12) for “107” substitute  “107A” .

3

by the Secretary of State with section 1 of the Climate Change Act 2008 (UK
net zero emissions target) and section 5 of the Environment Act 2021

4

After section 102 (power of PRA to require Regulator to refrain from specified
action), insert—

######## Recommendations

######### Recommendations by Treasury in connection with general duties

4.102A

4.102A.1

The Treasury may at any time by notice in writing to the Payment Systems
Regulator make recommendations to the Regulator about aspects of the economic
policy of His Majesty’s Government to which the Regulator should have regard
when considering—

4.102A.1.a

how to advance one or more of its payment systems objectives,

4.102A.1.b

the application of the regulatory principles in section 53, and

4.102A.1.c

its exercise of functions under—

4.102A.1.c.i

Regulation (EU) 2015/751  of the European Parliament and of the Council of 29
April 2015 on interchange fees for card-based payment transactions,

4.102A.1.c.ii

the Payment Card Interchange Fee Regulations 2015 ( S.I. 2015/1911 ), or

4.102A.1.c.iii

the Payment Services Regulations 2017 ( S.I. 2017/752 ).

4.102A.2

The Treasury must make recommendations under subsection (1) at least once in
each Parliament.

4.102A.3

The Payment Systems Regulator must respond to each recommendation made to it
under subsection (1) by notifying the Treasury in writing of—

4.102A.3.a

action that the Regulator has taken or intends to take in accordance with the
recommendation, or

4.102A.3.b

the reasons why the Regulator has not acted or does not intend to act in
accordance with the recommendation.

4.102A.4

The notice under subsection (3) must be given before the end of 12 months
beginning with the date the notice containing the recommendation was given
under subsection (1).

4.102A.5

Where the Payment Systems Regulator has given notice under subsection (3) in
relation to a recommendation, the Regulator must by notice in writing update
the Treasury on the matters mentioned in subsection (3)(a) and (b) before the
end of each subsequent period of 12 months.

4.102A.6

Subsection (5) does not apply if the Treasury have notified the Payment
Systems Regulator in writing that no update (or further update) is required.

4.102A.7

The Payment Systems Regulator is not required under subsection (3) or (5) to
provide any information whose publication would in the opinion of the
Regulator be against the public interest.

4.102A.8

The Treasury must—

4.102A.8.a

publish in such manner as they think fit any notice given under subsection
(1), (3) or (5), and

4.102A.8.b

lay a copy of it before Parliament.

5

Before section 103 (regulator’s general duty to consult) insert (under the
italic heading  “Consultation, accountability and oversight” )—

######## Matters to consider when imposing generally applicable requirements

5.102B

5.102B.1

This section applies where the Payment Systems Regulator proposes to impose a
generally applicable requirement (as defined by section 104(1)).

5.102B.2

The Regulator must have regard to any specified matters that are relevant to
the imposition of the requirement in question.

5.102B.3

“ Specified ” means specified in regulations made by the Treasury for the
purposes of this section.

5.102B.4

The specification of a matter for the purposes of this section may apply
generally to the exercise of a function or be limited in whatever way the
Treasury consider appropriate, including by reference to—

5.102B.4.a

the power under which the function is carried out;

5.102B.4.b

the persons to whom the carrying out of the function apply;

5.102B.4.c

the activities or subject-matter to which the function relates.

5.102B.5

The duty under subsection (2) is in addition to any other requirements to have
regard to matters when exercising relevant functions imposed by another
provision of this Act or by any other enactment.

6

In section 104 (consultation in relation to generally applicable
requirements)—

6.a

in subsection (1), in the words before paragraph (a) for “section” substitute
“Part” ;

6.b

in subsection (3) after paragraph (b) insert—

6.b.ba

an explanation of the ways in which having regard to specified matters under
section 102B(2) has affected the proposed requirement,

;

6.c

after subsection (12) insert—

6.c.12A

The duty to provide the explanation referred to in subsection (3)(ba) does not
apply in relation to any proposed requirement which changes an existing
requirement and the changes consist of, or include, changes which, in the
Payment Systems Regulator’s opinion, are not material.

6.c.12B

Where an explanation is not provided by virtue of subsection (12A), the draft
of the proposed requirement must be accompanied by a statement of the Payment
Systems Regulator’s opinion.

7

After section 104 insert—

######## Requirements in connection with public consultations

7.104A

7.104A.1

This section applies where the Payment Systems Regulator issues a public
consultation.

7.104A.2

The Payment Systems Regulator must include information in the consultation
about any engagement by the Payment Systems Regulator with the statutory
panels of the Payment Systems Regulator, the FCA and the PRA in relation to
the matters being consulted on.

7.104A.3

The Payment Systems Regulator is not required under subsection (2) to include
any information whose publication would in the opinion of the Payment Systems
Regulator be against the public interest.

7.104A.4

For the purposes of this section, the Payment Systems Regulator issues a
public consultation if it publishes any proposals for the purpose of bringing
them to the attention of the public (whether or not under a duty to do so
imposed by an enactment).

7.104A.5

In this section a “statutory panel”—

7.104A.5.a

in relation to the Payment Systems Regulator, means a panel established under
section 103(3),

7.104A.5.b

in relation to the FCA, has the meaning given by section 1RA(8) of FSMA 2000,
and

7.104A.5.c

in relation to the PRA, has the meaning given by section 2NA(8) of FSMA 2000.

######## Duty of Regulator to review generally applicable requirements

7.104B

The Payment Systems Regulator must keep under review generally any generally
applicable requirements.

######## Statement of policy relating to review of requirements

7.104C

7.104C.1

The Payment Systems Regulator must prepare and publish a statement of its
policy with respect to its review of requirements under section 104B.

7.104C.2

The statement must provide information about—

7.104C.2.a

how representations (including by a relevant panel) can be made to the
Regulator with respect to its review of requirements under section 104B, and

7.104C.2.b

the arrangements to ensure that those representations are considered.

7.104C.3

In this section “ relevant panel ” means—

7.104C.3.a

a panel of the Payment Systems Regulator established under section 103(3),

7.104C.3.b

a panel of the FCA mentioned in section 1RA(8) of FSMA 2000, and

7.104C.3.c

a panel of the PRA mentioned in section 2NA(8) of FSMA 2000.

7.104C.4

If a statement published under this section is altered or replaced by the
Payment Systems Regulator, the Regulator must publish the altered or replaced
statement.

7.104C.5

A statement prepared under this section must be published by the Payment
Systems Regulator in the way appearing to the Regulator to be best designed to
bring it to the attention of the public.

######## Requirement to review specified requirements

7.104D

7.104D.1

The Treasury may by direction require the Payment Systems Regulator to carry
out a review of any generally applicable requirement specified in the
direction if—

7.104D.1.a

the requirement has been in force for at least 12 months,

7.104D.1.b

the Treasury consider that it is in the public interest that the requirement
is reviewed, and

7.104D.1.c

it does not appear to the Treasury that—

7.104D.1.c.i

the regulator is carrying out, or proposes to carry out, a review of that
requirement, or

7.104D.1.c.ii

if the regulator proposes to carry out a review, the proposals are appropriate
for the purposes of carrying out an effective review.

7.104D.2

The Treasury must consult the Payment Systems Regulator before giving a
direction under subsection (1).

7.104D.3

In exercising the power under this section, the Treasury must have regard to
the desirability of minimising any adverse effect that the carrying out of the
review may have on the exercise by the Payment Systems Regulator of any of its
other functions.

7.104D.4

A direction under subsection (1) may—

7.104D.4.a

specify the period within which a review must be carried out;

7.104D.4.b

determine the scope and conduct of a review;

7.104D.4.c

require the provision of interim reports during the carrying out of a review.

7.104D.5

Provision made in a direction under subsection (4)(b) may include a
requirement—

7.104D.5.a

for a review to be carried out by a person appointed by the Payment Systems
Regulator who is independent of the Regulator;

7.104D.5.b

for any such appointment to be made only with the approval of the Treasury.

7.104D.6

As soon as practicable after giving the direction the Treasury must—

7.104D.6.a

lay before Parliament a copy of the direction, and

7.104D.6.b

publish the direction in such manner as the Treasury think fit.

7.104D.7

Subsection (6) does not apply where the Treasury consider that publication of
the direction would be against the public interest.

7.104D.8

A direction under this section may be varied or revoked by the giving of a
further direction.

######## Report on certain reviews

7.104E

7.104E.1

This section applies where the Treasury have given a direction to the Payment
Systems Regulator under section 104D(1) to carry out a review.

7.104E.2

The Payment Systems Regulator must provide a written report to the Treasury as
to the opinion of the Regulator in relation to the following matters—

7.104E.2.a

whether the requirements under review advance one or more of the payment
systems objectives;

7.104E.2.b

whether and to what extent the requirements are functioning effectively and
achieving their intended purpose;

7.104E.2.c

whether any amendments need to be made to the requirements and, if so, what
those amendments should be;

7.104E.2.d

whether any requirements should be withdrawn (with or without replacement);

7.104E.2.e

whether any other action should be taken and, if so, what that action should
be.

7.104E.3

As soon as practicable after receiving the report the Treasury must—

7.104E.3.a

lay before Parliament a copy of the report, and

7.104E.3.b

publish the report in such manner as the Treasury think fit.

7.104E.4

When complying with subsection (3) the Treasury may withhold material from the
report if the Treasury consider that publication of the material would be
against the public interest.

######## Power of Treasury to require the imposition of generally applicable requirements

7.104F

7.104F.1

The Treasury may by regulations require the Payment Systems Regulator to
exercise a power under this Part to impose a generally applicable requirement
in relation to a specified activity or a specified description of person.

7.104F.2

Regulations under this section may—

7.104F.2.a

specify matters that the requirement must cover;

7.104F.2.b

specify a period within which the requirement must be made.

7.104F.3

But except so far as permitted by subsection (2), regulations under this
section may not require the requirement to be imposed—

7.104F.3.a

in a specified form or with specified content, or

7.104F.3.b

to achieve or advance a specified outcome.

7.104F.4

If no period is specified under subsection (2)(b) the requirement must be
imposed as soon as reasonably practicable after the coming into force of the
regulations.

######## Consultation with the FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel

7.104G

7.104G.1

Except as provided by subsection (2), the Payment Systems Regulator must
consult the FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel, and that Panel must provide
advice, about the following matters—

7.104G.1.a

the preparation of a cost benefit analysis under section 104(3)(a) or (6);

7.104G.1.b

the preparation of its statement of policy under section 104H.

7.104G.2

The requirement to consult under subsection (1)(a) does not apply in such
cases as may be set out in the statement of policy maintained under section
104H.

7.104G.3

The FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel must—

7.104G.3.a

keep under review how the Payment Systems Regulator is performing generally in
carrying out its duties under section 104(3)(a) and (6), and

7.104G.3.b

provide to the Payment Systems Regulator whatever recommendations the Panel
thinks appropriate as a result of such review.

7.104G.4

The Payment Systems Regulator must consider representations that are made to
it by the FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel.

7.104G.5

The Payment Systems Regulator must from time to time publish in such manner as
it thinks fit responses to the representations.

7.104G.6

In this section references to the “ FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel ” are to
the panel established under section 138IA of FSMA 2000.

######## Statement of policy in relation to cost benefit analyses

7.104H

7.104H.1

The Payment Systems Regulator must prepare and publish a statement of policy
in relation to the preparation of cost benefit analyses for the purposes of
section 104.

7.104H.2

The statement must provide information about—

7.104H.2.a

the methodology adopted in preparing cost benefit analyses;

7.104H.2.b

matters to which the Payment Systems Regulator has regard in determining
whether section 104(8) applies;

7.104H.2.c

matters to which the Payment Systems Regulator has regard in determining
whether section 104(10) or (11) applies in relation to the preparation of a
cost benefit analysis;

7.104H.2.d

arrangements to ensure that representations in connection with a cost benefit
analysis that are made in accordance with section 104(3)(d) are considered;

7.104H.2.e

cases in which the requirement to consult the FCA Cost Benefit Analysis Panel
in relation to the preparation of a cost benefit analysis does not apply.

7.104H.3

The statement may include whatever other information in relation to cost
benefit analyses that the Payment Systems Regulator considers appropriate.

7.104H.4

The Payment Systems Regulator may alter or replace a statement published under
this section.

7.104H.5

The Payment Systems Regulator must publish a statement as altered or replaced
under subsection (4).

7.104H.6

Publication under this section is to be made in such manner as the Payment
Systems Regulator considers best designed to bring the statement to the
attention of the public.

######## Statement of policy on panel appointments

7.104I

7.104I.1

The Payment Systems Regulator must prepare and publish a statement of policy
in relation to the appointment of members to any panel established under
section 103(3).

7.104I.2

The statement must provide information about—

7.104I.2.a

the process adopted for making appointments;

7.104I.2.b

matters considered in determining who is appointed.

7.104I.3

The statement may provide whatever other information in relation to the making
of appointments that the Payment Systems Regulator considers appropriate.

7.104I.4

The Payment Systems Regulator may alter or replace a statement published under
this section.

7.104I.5

The Payment Systems Regulator must publish a statement as altered or replaced
under subsection (4).

7.104I.6

Before publishing a statement under this section the Payment Systems Regulator
must—

7.104I.6.a

consult the Treasury about the proposed statement, and

7.104I.6.b

have regard to any representations the Treasury make in response to the
consultation.

7.104I.7

Publication under this section is to be made in such manner as the Payment
Systems Regulator considers best designed to bring the statement to the
attention of the public.

8

After section 107 insert—

######## International trade obligations

8.107A

8.107A.1

This section applies where it appears to the Payment Systems Regulator that
there is a material risk that a relevant action it proposes to take would be
incompatible with an international trade obligation.

8.107A.2

The Payment Systems Regulator must give written notice to the Treasury of the
proposed action before proceeding to take it.

8.107A.3

Subsection (2) applies only if a duty to consult applies in respect of the
taking of the relevant action.

8.107A.4

For the purposes of subsection  (1)  the Payment Systems Regulator proposes to
take a “relevant action” if it—

8.107A.4.a

proposes to impose a generally applicable requirement, or

8.107A.4.b

proposes to make changes to its general policies and practices.

8.107A.5

For the purposes of subsection (3) a duty to consult applies in respect of a
relevant action if—

8.107A.5.a

the duty imposed by section 104 to publish a draft of a proposed requirement
applies in respect of the action, or

8.107A.5.b

any other duty (whether or not imposed by a provision of this Act) to publish
the proposal to take the action in question applies.

8.107A.6

The requirement imposed by subsection (2) must be carried out before the duty
to consult in respect of the relevant action is carried out.

8.107A.7

Subsection (8) applies in a case where a notice under subsection (2) is not
given because of subsection (3).

8.107A.8

The Payment Systems Regulator must give written notice to the Treasury of the
relevant action it has taken as soon as reasonably practicable after taking it
if it appears to the Regulator that there is a material risk that the action
is incompatible with an international trade obligation.

8.107A.9

In this section “ international trade obligation ” means an obligation of the
United Kingdom that relates to financial services or markets under—

8.107A.9.a

a free trade agreement, as defined by section 5(1) of the Trade Act 2021, or

8.107A.9.b

the agreement establishing the World Trade Organisation signed at Marrakesh on
15 April 1994.

9

In section 110(1) (interpretation), at the appropriate place insert—

      “ generally applicable requirement ” has the meaning given by section
104(1);

.

10

In section 143 (orders and regulations: Parliamentary control), in subsection
(2), after paragraph (b) insert—

10.ba

regulations under section 102B (matters to consider when imposing generally
applicable requirements);

10.bb

regulations under section 104F (power to require imposition of generally
applicable requirements);

.

11

In Schedule 4 (the Payment Systems Regulator), after paragraph 7(2)(b) insert—

11.ba

set out any engagement with a statutory panel established under section
103(3),

11.bb

set out how the Regulator has complied with the statement of policy on panel
appointments prepared under section 104I in relation to the process for making
appointments and the matters considered in determining who is appointed,

.

12

In Schedule 4, after paragraph 7 insert—

######## Other reports

12.7A

12.7A.1

The Treasury may (subject to this paragraph) at any time by direction require
the Regulator to publish a report containing information about such matters as
are specified in the direction.

12.7A.2

The Treasury may give a direction under this paragraph requiring information
to be published only if the Treasury consider that—

12.7A.2.a

the information is reasonably necessary for the purpose of reviewing and
scrutinising the discharge of the Regulator’s functions, and

12.7A.2.b

other available information is not sufficient to meet that purpose.

12.7A.3

Subject to sub-paragraph (4), the Regulator must publish a report prepared
under a direction given under this paragraph in such manner, and within such
period, as the direction may require.

12.7A.4

Nothing in this paragraph requires the inclusion in the report of any
information whose publication would be against the public interest.

12.7A.5

A direction under this paragraph may not—

12.7A.5.a

require a report to be published more than once in each quarter;

12.7A.5.b

require the publication of information that is confidential information as
defined by section 91(2).

12.7A.6

The Treasury must consult the Regulator before giving a direction under this
paragraph.

12.7A.7

In exercising the power under this paragraph, the Treasury must have regard to
the desirability of minimising any adverse effect that the preparation of the
report required in accordance with the direction may have on the exercise by
the Regulator of any of its other functions.

12.7A.8

The Treasury must—

12.7A.8.a

lay before Parliament a copy of a direction given under this paragraph, and

12.7A.8.b

publish the direction in such manner as the Treasury think fit.

12.7A.9

A direction under this paragraph may be varied or revoked by the giving of a
further direction.

13

In Schedule 4, after paragraph 14 insert—

######## Engagement with Parliamentary Committees

13.14A

13.14A.1

This paragraph applies where the Regulator issues a relevant consultation.

13.14A.2

For the purposes of this paragraph the Regulator issues a relevant
consultation if it—

13.14A.2.a

publishes proposed generally applicable requirements under section 104,

13.14A.2.b

publishes a proposal under a duty imposed by another provision of this Act or
by any other enactment, or

13.14A.2.c

publishes other proposals about the exercise of any of its general functions.

13.14A.3

The Regulator must, as soon as reasonably practicable after issuing the
consultation, notify in writing the chair of each relevant Parliamentary
Committee that the consultation has been issued.

13.14A.4

The notification must specify the parts of the consultation (if any) that
address the ways in which the proposals subject to consultation—

13.14A.4.a

advance the Regulator’s payment systems objectives,

13.14A.4.b

demonstrate that the Regulator has had regard to the regulatory principles in
section 53 when preparing the proposals, and

13.14A.4.c

engage with matters to which the Regulator must have regard under regulations
made under section 102B.

13.14A.5

The notification must also specify any other part of the consultation which
the Regulator considers should be drawn to the attention of the relevant
Parliamentary Committees.

13.14A.6

References in this paragraph to the relevant Parliamentary Committees are
references to—

13.14A.6.a

the Treasury Committee of the House of Commons,

13.14A.6.b

the Committee of the House of Lords which—

13.14A.6.b.i

is charged with responsibility by that House for the purposes of this
paragraph, and

13.14A.6.b.ii

has notified the Regulator that it is a relevant Parliamentary Committee for
those purposes, and

13.14A.6.c

the Joint Committee of both Houses which—

13.14A.6.c.i

is charged with responsibility by those Houses for the purposes of this
paragraph, and

13.14A.6.c.ii

has notified the Regulator that it is a relevant Parliamentary Committee for
those purposes.

13.14A.7

References in this paragraph to the Treasury Committee of the House of
Commons—

13.14A.7.a

if the name of that Committee is changed, are references to that Committee by
its new name, and

13.14A.7.b

if the functions of that Committee (or substantially corresponding functions)
become functions of a different Committee of the House of Commons, are to be
treated as reference to the Committee by which the functions are exercisable.

13.14A.8

Any question arising under sub-paragraph (7) is to be determined by the
Speaker of the House of Commons.

13.14B

13.14B.1

This paragraph applies where—

13.14B.1.a

the Regulator issues a public consultation, and

13.14B.1.b

a Committee of the House of Commons or the House of Lords, or a joint
Committee of both Houses, has provided to the Regulator representations in
response to the consultation.

13.14B.2

For the purposes of this paragraph, the Regulator issues a public consultation
if it publishes the draft of any proposals for the purpose of bringing them to
the attention of the public (whether or not under a duty to do so imposed by
an enactment).

13.14B.3

The Regulator must give to the chair of the Committee concerned a written
response to the representations.

13.14B.4

The duty to respond imposed by sub-paragraph (3) applies only so far as the
Regulator would not be under a corresponding duty to do so imposed by another
enactment.

13.14B.5

The Regulator is not required under sub-paragraph (3) to provide any
information whose publication would in the opinion of the Regulator be against
the public interest.

  Cash access services

Section 54

##### New Part 8B of FSMA 2000

1

After Part 8A of FSMA 2000 (short selling) insert—

######### Cash access services

########## Introductory

########### Overview

1.131M

This Part—

1.131M.a

requires the Treasury to publish a statement of policy concerning cash deposit
and withdrawal services,

1.131M.b

enables the Treasury to designate persons involved in the provision of such
services, and

1.131M.c

gives the FCA functions in relation to designated persons.

########### Cash access services and coordination arrangements

1.131N

1.131N.1

This section defines “cash”, “cash access service”, “free cash access service”
and “ cash access coordination arrangements ” for the purposes of this Part.

1.131N.2

“ Cash ” means—

1.131N.2.a

banknotes issued by the Bank of England, or an authorised bank in its capacity
as an issuer of banknotes in Scotland or Northern Ireland (see Part 6 of the
Banking Act 2009), or

1.131N.2.b

coins made by the Mint, within the meaning of the Coinage Act 1971 (see
section 11 of that Act).

1.131N.3

A “cash access service” is—

1.131N.3.a

a service which enables cash to be placed on a relevant current account (a
“cash deposit service”), or

1.131N.3.b

a service which enables cash to be withdrawn from a relevant current account
(a “cash withdrawal service”).

1.131N.4

A “free cash access service” is a cash access service that is—

1.131N.4.a

a free of charge service which enables cash to be placed on a relevant
personal current account, or

1.131N.4.b

a free of charge service which enables cash to be withdrawn from a relevant
personal current account.

1.131N.5

“Cash access coordination arrangements” are arrangements—

1.131N.5.a

which are designed to coordinate the provision of cash access services by two
or more providers of such services, but

1.131N.5.b

which do not directly provide cash access services to any person.

1.131N.6

In relation to cash access coordination arrangements—

1.131N.6.a

a reference to the “ operator ” of such arrangements is to any person with
responsibility under the arrangements for managing or operating them;

1.131N.6.b

a reference to the operation of such arrangements includes their management.

1.131N.7

In this section, “ relevant current account ” has the meaning given by section
131O .

########### Current accounts and relevant current account providers

1.131O

1.131O.1

This section defines “current account”, “relevant current account”, “relevant
personal current account” and “ relevant current account provider ” for the
purposes of this Part.

1.131O.2

“ Current account ” means an account by means of which one or more named
persons are able to—

1.131O.2.a

place cash,

1.131O.2.b

withdraw cash, and

1.131O.2.c

execute and receive payment transactions to and from third parties, including
the execution of credit transfers.

1.131O.3

For the purposes of subsection  (2) (c) , “ payment transaction ” means an act
initiated by the payer or payee, or on behalf of the payer, of placing,
transferring or withdrawing funds, irrespective of any underlying obligations
between the payer and payee.

1.131O.4

A “ relevant personal current account ” means a relevant current account held
by one or more individuals for purposes outside any business, trade, craft or
profession of that individual or those individuals.

1.131O.5

“ Relevant current account provider ” means a person—

1.131O.5.a

who has a Part 4A permission to accept deposits, and

1.131O.5.b

who provides current accounts in reliance on that permission (“relevant
current accounts”).

1.131O.6

But the following are not relevant current account providers—

1.131O.6.a

credit unions, within the meaning given by section 31(1) of the Credit Unions
Act 1979 or Article 2(2) of the Credit Unions (Northern Ireland) Order 1985 (
S.I. 1985/1205)(N.I.12) ;

1.131O.6.b

a society that is registered within the meaning of the Friendly Societies Act
1974 (see section 111(1) of that Act) or incorporated under the Friendly
Societies Act 1992.

1.131O.7

The Treasury may by regulations—

1.131O.7.a

amend a definition in this section;

1.131O.7.b

amend any other provision of this Part in consequence of provision made under
paragraph  (a) .

########## Cash access policy statement

########### Cash access policy statement

1.131P

1.131P.1

The Treasury must prepare a cash access policy statement.

1.131P.2

A “cash access policy statement” is a statement of the policies of His
Majesty’s Government concerning cash access services in the United Kingdom, or
a part of the United Kingdom.

1.131P.3

The reference to cash access services in subsection (2) includes free cash
access services.

1.131P.4

Policies may be stated in relation to, among other things—

1.131P.4.a

cash deposit services and cash withdrawal services;

1.131P.4.b

services provided in relation to current accounts of different descriptions;

1.131P.4.c

services provided in predominantly urban areas and services provided in
predominantly rural areas.

1.131P.5

In preparing a cash access policy statement, the Treasury must—

1.131P.5.a

consult the FCA, and

1.131P.5.b

have regard to any report provided under section  131Q .

1.131P.6

The Treasury must publish a cash access policy statement in such manner as
they consider appropriate.

1.131P.7

The Treasury—

1.131P.7.a

must keep the cash access policy statement under review;

1.131P.7.b

may prepare a revised statement (and subsections  (5)  and  (6)  apply in
relation to any revised statement).

########### Provision of reports to assist the Treasury

1.131Q

1.131Q.1

The FCA must, on a request from the Treasury, prepare and send to the Treasury
a report on a matter specified in the request.

1.131Q.2

The Treasury may only make a request under this section for a report that they
reasonably require in connection with—

1.131Q.2.a

the preparation of a cash access policy statement (see section  131P ), or

1.131Q.2.b

a decision whether or not to designate a person for the purposes of this Part
(see section  131R ).

1.131Q.3

A request for a report under this section—

1.131Q.3.a

must be made in writing, and

1.131Q.3.b

may require the FCA to send the report to the Treasury within such reasonable
period as may be specified in the request (or such other period as may be
agreed).

1.131Q.4

Nothing in section 348, or in regulations made under section 349, is to be
taken as preventing or restricting the ability of the FCA to disclose
information to the Treasury for the purposes of this section.

1.131Q.5

Subsection  (4)  does not apply in relation to information provided to the FCA
by a regulatory authority outside the United Kingdom.

########## Designation

########### Designation

1.131R

1.131R.1

The Treasury may designate a person for the purposes of this Part if the
person is—

1.131R.1.a

a relevant current account provider, or

1.131R.1.b

an operator of cash access coordination arrangements, and at least one of the
participants in the arrangements is a relevant current account provider
designated under this section.

1.131R.2

A person is designated by giving the person (the “designated person”) a notice
in accordance with this Part (a “designation notice”).

1.131R.3

A designation notice must specify whether the person is designated in relation
to—

1.131R.3.a

the United Kingdom,

1.131R.3.b

Great Britain only, or

1.131R.3.c

Northern Ireland only.

1.131R.4

A designation notice given to the operator of cash access coordination
arrangements must specify the arrangements in as much detail as is reasonably
practicable.

1.131R.5

Before giving a designation notice to a person the Treasury must—

1.131R.5.a

consult the FCA,

1.131R.5.b

notify the person, and

1.131R.5.c

consider any representations made.

1.131R.6

A designated person must—

1.131R.6.a

comply with rules made by the FCA under section  131V ;

1.131R.6.b

comply with directions given by the FCA to the designated person under section
131W .

########### Designation criteria

1.131S

1.131S.1

The Treasury may designate a person for the purposes of this Part, in relation
to the United Kingdom, Great Britain only, or Northern Ireland only (as the
case may be), only if satisfied that doing so is likely to further the purpose
mentioned in section  131U (1) .

1.131S.2

In considering whether to designate a relevant current account provider, the
Treasury must have regard to—

1.131S.2.a

the distribution of cash access services operated by the provider in the
United Kingdom, Great Britain or Northern Ireland (as the case may be);

1.131S.2.b

the distribution in the United Kingdom, Great Britain or Northern Ireland (as
the case may be) of persons holding current accounts provided by the provider;

1.131S.2.c

the provider’s share of the current account market in the United Kingdom,
Great Britain or Northern Ireland (as the case may be);

1.131S.2.d

the total value of the deposits held in current accounts provided by the
provider in the United Kingdom, Great Britain or Northern Ireland (as the case
may be).

1.131S.3

If a relevant current account provider is part of a group which includes one
or more other relevant current account providers, references in subsection
(2)  to the provider are to be read as references to—

1.131S.3.a

the provider, and

1.131S.3.b

each of those other relevant current account providers.

1.131S.4

For the purposes of subsection  (3) , section 421 (meaning of “ group ”)
applies with the omission of subsection (1)(g) of that section.

########### Cancellation or variation of a designation notice

1.131T

1.131T.1

If a designation notice has been given to a person the Treasury may, by
further notice, cancel the designation notice.

1.131T.2

If a designation notice has been given to a person (including a designation
notice as varied by a notice under this subsection), the Treasury may by
further notice, vary the earlier notice.

1.131T.3

If a further notice under subsection  (2)  would designate a person in
relation to a part of the United Kingdom in relation to which the person was
not designated by the earlier notice, sections  131R (3)  and  (5)  and  131S
apply in relation to the further notice.

########## Supervision of designated persons

########### Purpose for which FCA must exercise functions under this Part

1.131U

1.131U.1

The FCA must exercise its functions under this Part for the purpose of seeking
to ensure reasonable provision of cash access services in the United Kingdom,
or a part of the United Kingdom.

1.131U.2

In this section references to cash access services include references to free
cash access services.

1.131U.3

“Reasonable provision” of cash access services is provision of such nature and
extent as the FCA may determine, having regard to—

1.131U.3.a

the cash access policy statement currently in effect (see section  131P ), and

1.131U.3.b

such other matters as it considers appropriate.

1.131U.4

In making a determination for the purposes of subsection  (3)  the FCA must,
in particular, have regard to any local deficiencies in provision of cash
access services—

1.131U.4.a

which the FCA is aware of, and

1.131U.4.b

the impacts of which the FCA considers to be significant.

1.131U.5

A local deficiency in provision of cash access services is a circumstance
which limits the ability of persons in any locality in a part of the United
Kingdom to—

1.131U.5.a

withdraw cash from a relevant current account, or

1.131U.5.b

place cash on a relevant current account.

1.131U.6

In determining whether there are local deficiencies in the provision of cash
access services, and the significance of the impacts of such deficiencies, the
FCA must have regard to—

1.131U.6.a

the cash access policy statement currently in effect, and

1.131U.6.b

such other matters as it considers appropriate.

1.131U.7

Those other matters may include (but are not limited to)—

1.131U.7.a

the number of persons likely to be affected by the deficiency;

1.131U.7.b

the characteristics of the persons likely to be affected by the deficiency;

1.131U.7.c

the likely impact on the persons likely to be affected.

########### FCA rules

1.131V

1.131V.1

The FCA may make such rules applying to designated persons as appear to the
FCA to be necessary or expedient for the purpose mentioned in section  131U
(1) .

1.131V.2

Rules under this section must not require a designated person to do (or
refrain from doing) any thing in relation to a part of the United Kingdom in
relation to which the person is not designated.

1.131V.3

Section 137T (general supplementary powers for rules made by a regulator)
applies in relation to rules made by the FCA under this section as if, in
paragraph (a), the reference to descriptions of authorised persons, activity
or investment were to descriptions of designated persons and activities
carried on by such persons.

1.131V.4

Section 138A (modification or waiver of rules) applies in relation to rules
made by the FCA under this section as if subsection (4)(b) were omitted.

1.131V.5

Section 138I (consultation by FCA before making rules) applies to rules under
this section as if, in subsection (2)(d), the reference to the FCA’s duties
under section 1B(1) and (5)(a) were to the purpose for which the FCA must
exercise its functions under this Part.

########### Power to direct designated persons

1.131W

1.131W.1

The FCA may give a direction under this section to a designated person if it
considers that it is desirable to give the direction for the purpose mentioned
in section  131U (1) .

1.131W.2

A direction under this section must not require a designated person to do (or
refrain from doing) any thing in relation to a part of the United Kingdom in
relation to which the person is not designated.

1.131W.3

A direction under this section may require the person to—

1.131W.3.a

take specified action;

1.131W.3.b

refrain from taking specified action;

1.131W.3.c

review, or take remedial action in respect of, past conduct.

1.131W.4

A requirement imposed by a direction under this section may be expressed to
expire at the end of a specified period, but the imposition of a requirement
that expires at the end of a specified period does not affect the power to
give a further direction imposing a new requirement.

1.131W.5

A direction under this section—

1.131W.5.a

may be revoked by the FCA by written notice to the person to whom it is given,
and

1.131W.5.b

ceases to be in force if the person to whom it is given ceases to be a
designated person.

########### Procedure for directions

1.131X

1.131X.1

If the FCA proposes to give a direction under section  131W , or gives such a
direction with immediate effect, it must give written notice to the designated
person to whom the direction is given (or to be given).

1.131X.2

A direction under section  131W  takes effect—

1.131X.2.a

immediately, if the notice under subsection  (1)  states that is the case,

1.131X.2.b

on such other date as may be specified in the notice, or

1.131X.2.c

if no date is specified in the notice, when the matter to which the notice
relates is no longer open to review.

1.131X.3

A direction under section  131W  may be expressed to take effect immediately
(or on a specified date) only if the FCA reasonably considers that it is
necessary for the direction to take effect immediately (or on that date).

1.131X.4

The notice under subsection  (1)  must—

1.131X.4.a

give details of the direction;

1.131X.4.b

state the FCA’s reasons for the direction and for its determination as to when
the direction takes effect;

1.131X.4.c

inform the designated person that the person may make representations to the
FCA within such period as may be specified in the notice (whether or not the
person has referred the matter to the Tribunal);

1.131X.4.d

inform the designated person of the person’s right to refer the matter to the
Tribunal.

1.131X.5

The FCA may extend the period allowed under the notice for making
representations.

1.131X.6

The FCA must give the designated person written notice if, having considered
any representations made by the person, it decides—

1.131X.6.a

to give the direction proposed;

1.131X.6.b

if the direction has been given, not to revoke the direction.

1.131X.7

The FCA must give the designated person written notice if, having considered
any representations made by the person, it decides—

1.131X.7.a

not to give the direction proposed;

1.131X.7.b

to give a different direction;

1.131X.7.c

to revoke a direction.

1.131X.8

A notice given under subsection  (6)  must inform the notified person of the
person’s right to refer the matter to the Tribunal.

1.131X.9

A notice under subsection  (7)(b)  must comply with subsection  (4) .

1.131X.10

If a notice informs the designated person of the person’s right to refer a
matter to the Tribunal, it must give an indication of the procedure on such a
reference.

1.131X.11

For the purposes of subsection  (2)(c) , whether a matter is open to review is
to be determined in accordance with section 391(8).

########### Information gathering and investigations

1.131Y

1.131Y.1

For the purposes of this Part, Part 11 (information gathering and
investigations) applies in accordance with this section.

1.131Y.2

Sections 165A to 165C, 169 and 169A do not apply.

1.131Y.3

Any reference to an authorised person includes a person designated for the
purposes of this Part (whether or not the person is an authorised person).

1.131Y.4

In addition—

1.131Y.4.a

references to an authorised person in sections 165 and 176(3A)(a) include a
person mentioned in subsection  (5)  (whether or not the person is an
authorised person);

1.131Y.4.b

sections 175 to 177 apply in relation to section 165 as modified in accordance
with paragraph  (a) .

1.131Y.5

The persons are—

1.131Y.5.a

a relevant current account provider who is not a designated person for the
purposes of this Part;

1.131Y.5.b

an operator of cash access coordination arrangements who is not a designated
person for the purposes of this Part;

1.131Y.5.c

the operator of, or an infrastructure provider in relation to, a payment
system, who is not a designated person for the purposes of this Part;

1.131Y.5.d

a person (other than a person mentioned in paragraph  (a) ,  (b)  or  (c) )
who provides cash access services and is not a designated person for the
purposes of this Part;

1.131Y.5.e

a person who provides a relevant service to a person mentioned in paragraph
(a) ,  (b) ,  (c)  or  (d)  and is not a designated person for the purposes of
this Part.

1.131Y.6

In subsection  (5)(c) , “payment system”, and “operator” and “ infrastructure
provider ” in relation to a payment system, have the same meanings as in Part
5 of the Financial Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013 (see section 110 of that
Act).

1.131Y.7

For the purposes of subsection  (5)(e) , a “relevant service” is a service
provided in connection with the provision of cash access services.

1.131Y.8

In relation to a person who is not an authorised person but is treated as such
for the purposes of this Part (by virtue of subsection  (3)  or  (4) ), any
reference to “either regulator” is to the FCA only.

########### Disciplinary measures

1.131Z

For the purposes of enforcing a requirement imposed by or under this Part,
Part 14 (disciplinary measures) applies as if—

1.131Z.a

any reference to an authorised person includes a person designated for the
purposes of this Part (whether or not that person is an authorised person),
and

1.131Z.b

section 206A (suspending permission to carry on regulated activities etc) were
omitted.

########### Costs of supervision

1.131Z1

Rules made under paragraph 23 of Schedule 1ZA, in connection with the carrying
out of any of the FCA’s functions under this Part, must not provide for the
payment of fees to the FCA by any person other than a designated person who is
a relevant current account provider.

########### Exclusion and modification of other FCA duties

1.131Z2

1.131Z2.1

Where the FCA is discharging a function under this Part, section 1B (FCA’s
general duties) applies as if—

1.131Z2.1.a

in subsection (1)(b), the reference to one or more of the FCA’s operational
objectives were to the purpose mentioned in section  131U (1) ;

1.131Z2.1.b

subsections (4) and (4A) (promoting effective competition in the interests of
consumers and advancing competitiveness and growth) do not apply.

1.131Z2.2

In discharging its functions under this Part, the regulatory principles in
section 3B(1) have effect as if, in paragraph (g), the reference to the FCA’s
objectives included the purpose mentioned in section  131U (1) .

1.131Z2.3

Section 395 applies in relation to a decision of the FCA made in connection
with a function under this Part as if, in subsection (3)(a), the reference to
the FCA’s operational objectives included the purpose mentioned in section
131U (1) .
