inform the CCP of its right to refer the matter to the Tribunal.

12.3

A notice given under paragraph  11(4)  must—

12.3.a

give details of the requirement,

12.3.b

give the Bank’s reasons for imposing the requirement,

12.3.c

state when the requirement takes effect,

12.3.d

inform the director that the director may make representations to the Bank
within such period as may be specified in the notice (whether or not the
matter has been referred to the Tribunal), and

12.3.e

inform the director of the director’s right to refer the matter to the
Tribunal.

12.4

The Bank may extend the period allowed by the notice given under paragraph
11(2) ,  (3)  or  (4)  for making representations.

12.5

A notice under paragraph  11(7)(a)  about the imposition of a requirement
under paragraph  5  must comply with sub-paragraph  (1) .

12.6

A notice under paragraph  11(7)(a)  about the appointment of a person as a
temporary manager or the variation of the terms of the appointment of a person
as a temporary manager must comply with sub-paragraph  (2) .

12.7

A notice under paragraph  11(7)(a)  about the imposition of a requirement
under paragraph  6(7)  must comply with sub-paragraph  (3) .

12.8

In this paragraph, any reference to “ appointment ” includes re-appointment.

###### Temporary restriction on remuneration

13

13.1

The Bank may by direction restrict or prohibit for a specified period
discretionary payments to specified employees of a CCP or specified
shareholders of a CCP.

13.2

The power under sub-paragraph  (1)  may be exercised only if—

13.2.a

a stabilisation power is not being exercised in relation to the CCP,

13.2.b

at least one of the conditions in sub-paragraph  (3)  is met, and

13.2.c

the condition in sub-paragraph  (4)  is met.

13.3

The conditions in this sub-paragraph are—

13.3.a

there is or is likely soon to be a significant deterioration in the financial
situation of the CCP (within the meaning given by paragraph  7(6) );

13.3.b

there is a material risk of a threat to the ability of the CCP to maintain
critical clearing services;

13.3.c

there is a risk of a significant disruption to the operation of the CCP;

13.3.d

the operation of the CCP poses a risk to the financial stability of the United
Kingdom.

13.4

The condition in this sub-paragraph is that the exercise of the power is
necessary or desirable having regard to the public interest in—

13.4.a

the stability of the UK financial system, or

13.4.b

the continuity of critical clearing services.

13.5

The Bank must prepare and publish a statement of its policy with respect to
the giving of directions under this paragraph.

13.6

The Bank may alter or replace a statement of policy published under this
paragraph.

13.7

The Bank must publish a statement as altered or replaced under sub-paragraph
(6) .

13.8

No directions may be given under this paragraph before the statement of policy
under sub-paragraph  (5)  has been published.

13.9

The specified period for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1)  must not exceed 5
years.

13.10

Directions under this paragraph—

13.10.a

must be given in writing to the employees or shareholders that the directions
apply to;

13.10.b

may be varied or revoked.

13.11

In this paragraph “ discretionary payments ” means payments, made otherwise
than under a contractual obligation, of any of the following—

13.11.a

equity remuneration;

13.11.b

dividend payments;

13.11.c

share buy-backs;

13.11.d

variable remuneration including, where an employee is a senior manager,
bonuses, discretionary pension benefits and severance payments.

###### Restriction on remuneration: review and revocation

14

14.1

This paragraph applies where a direction has been given under paragraph  13(1)
in relation to a CCP.

14.2

The Bank must, at least once every 3 months after giving the direction, carry
out a review of whether the requirements for the exercise of the power
continue to be met.

14.3

If at any time the Bank becomes aware that the requirements for the exercise
of the power cease to be met, the Bank must revoke the direction with
immediate effect.

14.4

The direction ceases to have effect if a stabilisation power is exercised in
respect of the CCP.

##### Special resolution action

###### Special resolution objectives

15

15.1

This paragraph sets out the special resolution objectives.

15.2

The Bank must have regard to the special resolution objectives in using, or
considering the use of, the stabilisation powers.

15.3

Objective 1 is to protect and enhance the stability of the UK financial
system, including in particular by—

15.3.a

preventing contagion (including contagion to market infrastructures), and

15.3.b

maintaining market discipline.

15.4

Objective 2 is to protect and enhance public confidence in the stability of
the UK financial system.

15.5

Objective 3 is to maintain the continuity of central counterparty clearing
services.

15.6

Objective 4 is to protect public funds.

15.7

Objective 5 is to avoid interfering with property rights in contravention of a
Convention right (within the meaning of the Human Rights Act 1998).

15.8

The order in which the objectives are listed in this paragraph is not
significant; they are to be balanced as appropriate in each case.

15.9

In this paragraph, “market infrastructures” include recognised investment
exchanges, recognised clearing houses and recognised CSDs, within the meaning
of section 285 of FSMA 2000.

###### Code of Practice

16

16.1

The Treasury must issue a code of practice about the use of the stabilisation
powers.

16.2

The code may, in particular, provide guidance on—

16.2.a

how the special resolution objectives are to be understood and achieved,

16.2.b

the choice between different options,

16.2.c

the information to be provided in the course of a consultation under this
Schedule,

16.2.d

how to determine whether Condition 2 in paragraph  17  is met,

16.2.e

how to determine whether the test for the use of stabilisation powers under
paragraph  19  is satisfied,

16.2.f

paragraphs  89  and  92 , and

16.2.g

compensation, including how the Treasury intend to satisfy the requirement
under paragraph  87(3) .

16.3

See also paragraph  29  which requires the inclusion in the code of certain
matters about bridge central counterparties.

16.4

The Treasury may revise and re-issue the code of practice.

16.5

Before issuing or re-issuing the code of practice the Treasury must consult
the Bank, the FCA and the PRA.

16.6

The Bank must have regard to the code of practice.

16.7

As soon as is reasonably practicable after issuing or re-issuing the code of
practice the Treasury must lay a copy before Parliament.

###### General conditions

17

17.1

A stabilisation power may be exercised in respect of a CCP only if the Bank is
satisfied that each of the following conditions is met.

17.2

Condition 1 is that the CCP is failing or likely to fail.

17.3

Condition 2 is that—

17.3.a

having regard to timing and other relevant circumstances, it is not reasonably
likely that (ignoring the stabilisation powers) action will be taken by or in
respect of the CCP that will result in Condition 1 ceasing to be met, or

17.3.b

in the Bank’s assessment, the action that may be taken by or in respect of the
CCP for the purpose of ensuring that Condition 1 is no longer met might have
an adverse impact on the stability of the UK financial system.

17.4

Condition 3 is that the exercise of the power is necessary having regard to
the public interest in the advancement of one or more of the special
resolution objectives.

17.5

Condition 4 is that one or more of the special resolution objectives would not
be met to the same extent by the winding up of the CCP.

17.6

For the purposes of Condition 1, a CCP is failing or likely to fail if one or
more of the following apply—

17.6.a

the CCP is failing or is likely to fail to meet the recognition requirements
(within the meaning of section 286 of FSMA 2000);

17.6.b

the value of the assets of the CCP is less than the amount of its liabilities;

17.6.c

the CCP is unable to pay its debts or other liabilities as they fall due;

17.6.d

any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (c)  will, in the near future, apply to the CCP;

17.6.e

extraordinary public financial support is required in respect of the CCP and
sub-paragraph  (9)  does not apply to that support.

17.7

The Bank may treat Condition 1 as met if satisfied that it would be met but
for the withdrawal or possible withdrawal of critical clearing services by the
CCP.

17.8

The Bank must treat Conditions 1 and 2(a) as met if satisfied that those
conditions would be met but for financial assistance provided by—

17.8.a

the Treasury, or

17.8.b

the Bank (disregarding ordinary market assistance offered by the Bank on its
usual terms).

17.9

This sub-paragraph applies where, in order to remedy a serious disturbance in
the economy of the United Kingdom and preserve financial stability, the
extraordinary public financial support takes either of the following forms—

17.9.a

a State guarantee to back liquidity facilities provided by the Bank, or

17.9.b

a State guarantee of newly issued liabilities.

17.10

Before determining that Conditions 2, 3 and 4 are met the Bank must consult—

17.10.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

17.10.b

the FCA, and

17.10.c

the Treasury.

###### Effect on other group members

18

Where the Bank is considering the exercise of a stabilisation power in respect
of a CCP which is a member of a group, the Bank must have regard to—

18.a

the need to minimise the effect of the exercise of the power on other
undertakings in the same group, and

18.b

the potential effect of the exercise of the power on the financial stability
of countries other than the United Kingdom (particularly those countries in
which any member of that group is operating).

###### Specific conditions: financial assistance cases

19

19.1

In a financial assistance case, the Bank may exercise a stabilisation power in
respect of the CCP concerned in accordance with paragraph  27 ,  29  or  30
only if satisfied that the condition in sub-paragraph  (3)  is met.

19.2

“ Financial assistance case ” means a case where the Treasury notify the Bank
that they have provided financial assistance in respect of a CCP for the
purpose of resolving or reducing a serious threat to the stability of the UK
financial system.

19.3

The condition is that—

19.3.a

the Treasury have given a recommendation to the Bank to exercise the
stabilisation power on the grounds that it is necessary in order to protect
the public interest, and

19.3.b

the Bank considers that the exercise of the stabilisation power is an
appropriate way to provide that protection.

19.4

The condition in this paragraph is in addition to the conditions in paragraph
17 .

###### Resolution liaison panel

20

20.1

The Treasury must make arrangements for a panel to advise the Treasury about
the effect of the special resolution regime on—

20.1.a

CCPs,

20.1.b

persons with whom CCPs do business, and

20.1.c

the financial markets.

20.2

In particular, the panel may advise the Treasury about—

20.2.a

the exercise of powers to make statutory instruments under or by virtue of
this Schedule, (excluding the stabilisation powers and regulations under
paragraphs  87  and  153 ),

20.2.b

the code of practice under paragraph  16 , and

20.2.c

anything else referred to the panel by the Treasury.

20.3

The Treasury must ensure that the panel includes—

20.3.a

a member appointed by the Treasury,

20.3.b

a member appointed by the Bank,

20.3.c

a member appointed by the PRA,

20.3.d

a member appointed by the FCA,

20.3.e

one or more persons who in the Treasury’s opinion represent the interests of
CCPs,

20.3.f

one or more persons who in the Treasury’s opinion represent the interests of
clearing members of CCPs,

20.3.g

one or more persons who in the Treasury’s opinion have expertise in law
relating to the UK financial system, and

20.3.h

one or more persons who in the Treasury’s opinion have expertise in insolvency
law and practice.

###### Restrictions on use of certain resolution powers

21

21.1

Where the Bank has exercised the first stabilisation option (private sector
purchaser) in respect of a CCP it may only exercise the relevant resolution
powers in relation to the residual CCP.

21.2

Where the Bank has exercised the third stabilisation option (transfer of
ownership) in respect of a CCP it may only exercise the relevant resolution
powers in respect of the CCP where the transferee under paragraph  30  is—

21.2.a

the Bank,

21.2.b

a company wholly owned by the Bank or the Treasury, or

21.2.c

a nominee of the Treasury.

21.3

In this paragraph—

      “ relevant resolution powers ” means any of the resolution powers under
paragraphs  27  to  38 ;           the “ residual CCP ” means the CCP all or
part of whose business has been transferred in accordance with paragraph
27(2) .

###### Pre-resolution valuation

22

22.1

Before the Bank exercises a stabilisation power in respect of a CCP, it must
ensure that the assets and liabilities of the CCP are valued.

22.2

The purpose of a valuation carried out under sub-paragraph  (1)  is to—

22.2.a

inform the decision as to—

22.2.a.i

whether the conditions for the exercise of a stabilisation power are
satisfied,

22.2.a.ii

which stabilisation option should be employed,

22.2.a.iii

the extent to which any liabilities should be cancelled, modified, converted
or deferred through the use of a write-down instrument,

22.2.a.iv

the extent to which any securities should be cancelled, diluted, modified,
converted or deferred through the use of a write-down instrument,

22.2.a.v

what assets, liabilities or securities (if any) are to be transferred by a
property transfer instrument, share transfer instrument or write-down
instrument, and

22.2.a.vi

the value of any consideration to be paid to the CCP or the owners of the
securities for any assets, liabilities or securities so transferred, and

22.2.b

ensure that the full extent of any losses on the assets of that CCP are
appreciated at the time that the Bank exercises a stabilisation power.

22.3

Unless sub-paragraph  (4)  applies, the Bank must arrange for the appointment
of an independent valuer in accordance with paragraph  24  to carry out a
valuation for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1) .

22.4

Where the Bank considers that the urgency of the case makes it appropriate to
exercise the stabilisation power before a valuation can be carried out by a
person appointed in accordance with sub-paragraph  (3) , the Bank may carry
out a provisional valuation of the assets and liabilities of the CCP for the
purposes of sub-paragraph  (1) .

22.5

In carrying out a valuation required under sub-paragraph  (1) , the person
carrying out the valuation must—

22.5.a

make prudent assumptions as to possible rates of default and the severity of
losses suffered by the CCP,

22.5.b

disregard potential financial assistance which may be provided by the Bank or
the Treasury after the Bank has exercised the stabilisation power (except for
ordinary market assistance offered by the Bank on its usual terms),

22.5.c

take account of the fact that the Bank and the Treasury may charge interest or
fees in respect of any loans or guarantees provided to the CCP after the Bank
has exercised the stabilisation power,

22.5.d

apply any relevant methodology specified in regulations made under this
paragraph.

22.6

A provisional valuation carried out under sub-paragraph  (4)  must in
particular make provision in respect of additional losses by the CCP in
accordance with any regulations made under this paragraph.

22.7

A valuation under sub-paragraph  (1)  must be accompanied by—

22.7.a

a balance sheet of the CCP as at the date of the valuation,

22.7.b

a report on the financial position of the CCP,

22.7.c

an analysis and an estimate of the accounting value of the assets of the CCP,

22.7.d

a list of the outstanding liabilities of the CCP (including any off-balance
sheet liabilities), with the creditors subdivided into classes according to
the priority their claims would receive in insolvency proceedings, and

22.7.e

an estimate of the amount that each class of creditors and shareholders might
be expected to receive if the CCP went into insolvent liquidation.

22.8

Where appropriate, the information in sub-paragraph  (7)(c)  may be
supplemented by an analysis and estimate of the value of the assets and
liabilities of the CCP on a market value basis.

22.9

Where a provisional valuation is carried out under sub-paragraph  (4) , the
Bank need only comply with sub-paragraph  (7)  as far as it is reasonable to
do so in the circumstances.

22.10

The Treasury may by regulations make provision for the purposes of a valuation
under this paragraph specifying—

22.10.a

the methodology for assessing the value of the assets and liabilities of a
CCP;

22.10.b

the methodology for calculating and including a buffer for additional losses
in the provisional valuation.

22.11

Before making regulations under sub-paragraph  (10)  the Treasury must consult
the Bank.

22.12

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the negative procedure.

###### Replacement of Bank’s provisional valuation

23

23.1

Where the Bank has carried out a provisional valuation under paragraph  22
before exercising a stabilisation power, the Bank must arrange for the
appointment of an independent valuer in accordance with paragraph  24  to
carry out a full valuation in accordance with this paragraph as soon as
reasonably practicable.

23.2

The purpose of the valuation carried out under sub-paragraph  (1)  is to—

23.2.a

ensure the full extent of any losses on the assets of the CCP is recognised in
the accounting records of the CCP, and

23.2.b

inform a decision by the Bank as to whether—

23.2.b.i

additional consideration should be paid by a bridge central counterparty for
any property, rights or liabilities transferred by a property transfer
instrument, or securities transferred by a share transfer instrument, or

23.2.b.ii

the Bank should exercise the power under paragraph  26  to increase or
reinstate any liability which has been reduced, cancelled or deferred by a
write-down instrument.

23.3

A valuation carried out under sub-paragraph  (1)  must comply with sub-
paragraph  (5)  of paragraph  22  and be accompanied by the information
required in sub-paragraph  (7)  of that paragraph.

###### Independent valuer: valuation under paragraph 

24

24.1

The Bank must make arrangements for the appointment of a person to act as an
independent valuer for the purposes of a valuation to be conducted under
paragraph  22  or  23 .

24.2

The Bank may require the CCP to which the valuation relates to reimburse the
Bank for costs it incurs in relation to the independent valuer (including
remuneration and allowances paid to the valuer and the valuer’s staff).

24.3

A person may not be appointed as an independent valuer under sub-paragraph
(1)  unless the Bank is satisfied that the person is independent from the Bank
and the CCP to which the valuation relates.

24.4

An independent valuer is to hold and vacate office in accordance with the
terms of the appointment.

24.5

An independent valuer may be removed from office only on the grounds of
incapacity or serious misconduct.

24.6

In the event of the death of an independent valuer, or an independent valuer
being removed from office or resigning, a new independent valuer must be
appointed by the Bank in accordance with this paragraph.

###### Independent valuer: supplemental

25

25.1

An independent valuer may do anything necessary or desirable for the purposes
of or in connection with the performance of the functions of the office.

25.2

The Treasury may by regulations confer specific functions on independent
valuers; in particular, the regulations may—

25.2.a

enable an independent valuer to apply to a court or tribunal for an order
requiring the provision of information or the giving of oral or written
evidence;

25.2.b

enable or require independent valuers to publish, disclose or withhold
information.

25.3

Provision under sub-paragraph  (2)  may—

25.3.a

confer a discretion on independent valuers;

25.3.b

confer jurisdiction on a court or tribunal;

25.3.c

make provision about oaths, expenses and other procedural matters relating to
the giving of evidence or the provision of information;

25.3.d

make provision about enforcement.

25.4

An independent valuer may appoint staff.

25.5

The Treasury may by regulations make provision about the procedure to be
followed by independent valuers.

25.6

Independent valuers (and their staff) are neither servants nor agents of the
Crown (and, in particular, are not civil servants).

25.7

Records of an independent valuer are public records for the purposes of the
Public Records Act 1958.

25.8

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the negative procedure.

###### Consequences of a replacement valuation

26

26.1

Where the independent valuation carried out under paragraph  23(1)  produces a
higher valuation of the net asset value of the CCP than a provisional
valuation carried out under paragraph  22(4) , the Bank may—

26.1.a

modify any liability of the CCP which has been reduced, deferred or cancelled
by a write-down instrument so as to increase or reinstate that liability, or

26.1.b

instruct a bridge central counterparty to pay additional consideration—

26.1.b.i

to the CCP for any property, rights or liabilities transferred to the bridge
central counterparty by a property transfer instrument, or

26.1.b.ii

to the previous holders of securities issued by the CCP for any securities
transferred to the bridge central counterparty by a share transfer instrument.

26.2

The power in sub-paragraph  (1) (a)—

26.2.a

may not be exercised so as to increase the value of the liability beyond the
value it would have had if the write-down instrument which reduced, cancelled
or deferred it had not been made, and

26.2.b

must be exercised by a resolution instrument (whether or not that instrument
contains any other provision authorised by this Schedule).

###### Private sector purchaser

27

27.1

The first stabilisation option is to sell all or part of the business of the
CCP to a commercial purchaser.

27.2

For that purpose the Bank may make—

27.2.a

one or more share transfer instruments;

27.2.b

one or more property transfer instruments.

###### Private sector purchaser: marketing

28

28.1

Subject to sub-paragraph  (4)  and  (5) , the Bank must make arrangements for
marketing—

28.1.a

any securities issued by the CCP which the Bank intends to transfer by a share
transfer instrument under paragraph  27(2)(a) , or

28.1.b

any property, rights or liabilities of the CCP which the Bank intends to
transfer by a property transfer instrument under paragraph  27(2)(b) .

28.2

The arrangements under sub-paragraph  (1)  must—

28.2.a

be as transparent as possible having regard to the circumstances and the need
to maintain financial stability;

28.2.b

ensure there is no conflict of interest;

28.2.c

take account of the need for the Bank to act quickly to address the situation
where a CCP is failing or likely to fail;

28.2.d

aim at maximising, as far as possible, the sale price for the property, rights
or liabilities involved.

28.3

The arrangements under sub-paragraph  (1)  must not—

28.3.a

materially misrepresent the securities, property, rights or liabilities which
the Bank intends to transfer;

28.3.b

favour or discriminate between potential purchasers or grant an unfair
advantage to a potential purchaser.

28.4

Sub-paragraph  (1)  does not apply if the Bank considers that complying with
that sub-paragraph would undermine one or more of the special resolution
objectives.

28.5

In particular sub-paragraph  (1)  does not apply if the Bank considers that—

28.5.a

there is a material threat to financial stability in the United Kingdom
arising from or aggravated by the failure or likely failure of the CCP, and

28.5.b

complying with sub-paragraph  (1)  would undermine the effectiveness of the
first stabilisation option in addressing that threat or achieving the
objective in paragraph  15(4) .

###### Bridge central counterparty

29

29.1

The second stabilisation option is to transfer all or part of the business of
the CCP to a company which meets the requirements of sub-paragraph  (2)  (a
“bridge central counterparty”).

29.2

Those requirements are that the company—

29.2.a

is wholly or partially owned by the Bank,

29.2.b

is controlled by the Bank, and

29.2.c

is created for the purposes of receiving a transfer by virtue of this
paragraph with a view to maintaining access to critical clearing services and
(in due course) selling the CCP or its business.

29.3

For that purpose the Bank may make—

29.3.a

one or more property transfer instruments;

29.3.b

one or more share transfer instruments.

29.4

The code of practice under paragraph  16  must include provision about the
management and control of bridge central counterparties including, in
particular, provision about—

29.4.a

setting objectives,

29.4.b

the content of the articles of association,

29.4.c

the content of reports under paragraph  114 ,

29.4.d

different arrangements for management and control at different stages, and

29.4.e

eventual disposal.

29.5

The Bank must, without delay, take all necessary steps to wind up the bridge
central counterparty if—

29.5.a

all or substantially all of the bridge central counterparty’s assets, rights
and liabilities have been transferred to a third party, or

29.5.b

following a transfer to the bridge central counterparty under this paragraph,
no further transfer to the bridge central counterparty is made under this
paragraph during the relevant post-transfer period.

29.6

Sub-paragraph  (5)  does not apply if the bridge central counterparty—

29.6.a

has merged with another entity,

29.6.b

has ceased to meet the requirements of sub-paragraph  (2)(a)  or  (b) , or

29.6.c

has already been wound up.

29.7

“ The relevant post-transfer period ” means the period of two years beginning
with the day of the transfer mentioned in sub-paragraph  (5)(a) , subject to
any extension under sub-paragraph  (8) .

29.8

The Bank may extend (or further extend) the relevant post-transfer period by
one year if it is satisfied that the extension—

29.8.a

would support one or more of the outcomes mentioned in sub-paragraph  (5)(a)
or  (6)(a) ,  (b)  or  (c) , or

29.8.b

is necessary to ensure the continuity of critical clearing services.

29.9

Where property, rights or liabilities are first transferred by property
transfer instrument to a bridge central counterparty and later transferred
(whether or not by the exercise of a power under this Schedule) to another
company which is wholly owned by the Bank, that other company is an “onward
bridge central counterparty”.

29.10

An onward bridge central counterparty—

29.10.a

is a bridge central counterparty for the purposes of—

29.10.a.i

sub-paragraphs  (4)  to  (6) ,

29.10.a.ii

paragraph 34(6)(d),

29.10.a.iii

paragraph  110 ,

29.10.a.iv

paragraph  112 , and

29.10.a.v

paragraph  114(5) , but

29.10.b

is not a bridge central counterparty for the purposes of—

29.10.b.i

paragraph  52 ,

29.10.b.ii

paragraph  69 , and

29.10.b.iii

paragraph  114(1) .

###### Transfer of ownership

30

30.1

The third stabilisation option is to transfer ownership of the CCP to any
person other than a bridge central counterparty or a commercial purchaser.

30.2

For that purpose the Bank may make one or more share transfer instruments.

###### Tear-up power

31

31.1

The fourth stabilisation option is to make one or more tear-up instruments for
the purpose of ensuring that the CCP has a matched book.

31.2

A tear-up instrument is an instrument that makes provision terminating one or
more contracts held by the CCP with clearing members.

31.3

Where the Bank exercises the power under sub-paragraph  (1) , it must as soon
as reasonably practicable determine the value of the terminated contract.

31.4

On the basis of the determination under sub-paragraph  (3)  the Bank must as
soon as reasonably practicable either—

31.4.a

require the CCP to make a commercially reasonable payment, representing the
value of the terminated contract, to the clearing member who is a party to the
contract, or

31.4.b

require the clearing member who is a party to the contract to make a
commercially reasonable payment, representing the value of the terminated
contract, to the CCP.

31.5

The Bank must within 12 months of this paragraph coming into force publish a
statement of policy as to how it determines what a commercially reasonable
payment is for the purpose of complying with sub-paragraph  (4) .

31.6

The Bank may alter or replace a statement of policy published under this
paragraph.

31.7

The Bank must publish a statement as altered or replaced under sub-paragraph
(6) .

31.8

For the purposes of this paragraph, a CCP has a matched book when the sum of
the financial obligations owed by the CCP to its clearing members is equal to
the sum of the financial obligations owed to the CCP by its clearing members.

###### Cash call power

32

32.1

The fifth stabilisation option is to make one or more cash call instruments.

32.2

A cash call instrument is an instrument that makes provision requiring one or
more clearing members of the CCP to pay an amount in cash specified in the
instrument to the CCP.

32.3

The Treasury may by regulations—

32.3.a

make provision for calculating the maximum cash amount that may be specified
for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (2) ;

32.3.b

specify circumstances in which the Bank may require a CCP to use specified
funds of specified clearing members to satisfy all or part of that member’s
obligations under sub-paragraph  (2) .

32.4

The power under sub-paragraph  (1)  does not apply to a clearing member—

32.4.a

which is an interoperable CCP,

32.4.b

which falls within Article 1(4) or (5) of EMIR, or

32.4.c

in relation to which a direction under regulation 3(1)(f) of the Equivalence
Determinations for Financial Services and Miscellaneous Provisions (Amendment
etc) (EU Exit) Regulations 2019 ( S.I. 2019/541 ) is in force.

32.5

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the negative procedure.

###### Power to reduce variation margin payments

33

33.1

The sixth stabilisation option is to make one or more variation instruments.

33.2

A variation instrument is an instrument that makes provision to reduce or
cancel a variation margin payment that a CCP would have otherwise paid to a
clearing member of the CCP.

33.3

The power under this paragraph may be exercised only for the purpose of
recovering losses arising as a result of a clearing member defaulting on the
member’s obligations to the CCP.

33.4

The power under sub-paragraph  (1)  does not apply to a clearing member—

33.4.a

which falls within Article 1(4) or (5) of EMIR, or

33.4.b

in relation to which a direction under regulation 3(1)(f) of the Equivalence
Determinations for Financial Services and Miscellaneous Provisions (Amendment
etc) (EU Exit) Regulations 2019 ( S.I. 2019/541 ) is in force.

33.5

In this paragraph, a “ variation margin payment ” means a payment reflecting
an increase in the market value of a clearing member’s position in the market.

###### Write-down power

34

34.1

The seventh stabilisation option is for the Bank to make one or more write-
down instruments.

34.2

A write-down instrument is an instrument that makes any of the following
provision (or any combination of the following)—

34.2.a

provision cancelling an unsecured liability owed by the CCP;

34.2.b

provision modifying or changing the form of an unsecured liability owed by the
CCP;

34.2.c

provision that a contract under which the CCP has an unsecured liability is to
have effect as if a specified right had been exercised under it;

34.2.d

provision under paragraph  35(1) .

34.3

The power under this paragraph may be exercised only for the purpose of
recovering losses arising otherwise than as a result of a clearing member
defaulting on the member’s obligations to the CCP.

34.4

The power under sub-paragraph  (2)  may not be exercised so as to affect the
following liabilities—

34.4.a

liabilities to employees or workers, including liabilities owed to a pension
scheme in respect of those persons;

34.4.b

liabilities to commercial or trade creditors arising from the provision to the
CCP of goods or services that are critical to the continuity of the CCP’s
critical clearing services;

34.4.c

HMRC debts which are preferential debts within the meaning of section 386 of
the Insolvency Act 1986;

34.4.d

liabilities to designated systems, operators of designated systems, or
participants in such systems to the extent that the liabilities arise from
their participation in the system;

34.4.e

liabilities to interoperable CCPs;

34.4.f

liabilities to central banks;

34.4.g

liabilities to clearing members so far as these relate to initial margin
requirements;

34.4.h

liabilities to small enterprises.

34.5

The reference to modifying a liability owed by the CCP includes a reference to
modifying the terms (or the effect of the terms) of a contract under which the
CCP has a liability.

34.6

The reference to changing the form of a liability owed by the CCP includes,
for example—

34.6.a

converting an instrument under which a CCP owes a liability from one form or
class to another,

34.6.b

replacing such an instrument with another instrument of a different form or
class,

34.6.c

creating a new security (of any form or class) in connection with the
modification of such an instrument, or

34.6.d

converting those liabilities into securities issued by the CCP or a bridge
central counterparty or UK parent of the CCP.

34.7

The Treasury may by regulations amend sub-paragraph (4) by—

34.7.a

adding to the list of liabilities;

34.7.b

amending or omitting any liability listed.

34.8

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the affirmative procedure.

34.9

In this paragraph—

      “ designated system ” has the meaning given by regulation 2 of the
Financial Markets and Insolvency (Settlement Finality) Regulations 1999 ( S.I.
1999/2979 ) as amended from time to time;           “ initial margin
requirements ” means margins provided by clearing members to a CCP to cover
the CCP’s potential future exposure in the event of default by those members;
“ small enterprise ” means an enterprise which employs fewer than 50 people
and whose annual turnover or annual balance sheet total does not exceed £10
million.

###### Powers in relation to securities

35

35.1

A write-down instrument may—

35.a

cancel, transfer, dilute or modify any securities to which this sub-paragraph
applies;

35.b

convert any such securities from one form or class into another.

35.2

Sub-paragraph  (1)  applies to securities issued by the CCP that fall within
class 1 in paragraph  40 .

35.3

A write-down instrument may—

35.3.a

make provision with respect to rights attaching to securities issued by the
CCP;

35.3.b

provide for the listing of securities issued by the CCP to be discontinued or
suspended;

35.3.c

provide for the listing or admission to trading on a regulated market of
securities in class 1 (and related class 3 securities) created in accordance
with that or any other write-down instrument;

35.3.d

provide for the listing or admission to trading on a regulated market of
existing securities in class 2 modified by that or any other write-down
instrument  ....

35.4

The reference in sub-paragraph  (1)  to converting securities from one form or
class into another includes creating a new security in connection with the
modification of an existing security.

35.5

In sub-paragraph  (3)  any reference to a class of securities is to be
construed in accordance with paragraph  40 .

35.6

The provision that may be made under sub-paragraph  (3)(a)  includes, for
example—

35.6.a

provision that specified rights attaching to securities are to be treated as
having been exercised;

35.6.b

provision that the Bank is to be treated as authorised to exercise specified
rights attaching to securities;

35.6.c

provision that specified rights attaching to securities may not be exercised
for a period specified in the instrument.

35.7

In sub-paragraph  (3) —

35.7.a

the reference to “listing” is to listing under section 74 of FSMA 2000, and

35.7.b

“ regulated market ” has the meaning given in section 103(1) of FSMA 2000.

35.8

Where the listing of securities is suspended in accordance with a write-down
instrument, those securities are to be treated for the purposes of section 96
of, and paragraph 23(6) of Schedule 1ZA to, FSMA 2000 as still being listed.

35.9

The provision that may be made under this paragraph in relation to any
securities is in addition to any provision that the Bank may have power to
make in relation to them under paragraph  34 .

###### Report on provisions in write-down instrument

36

36.1

This paragraph applies to a relevant provision in a write-down instrument.

36.2

The Bank must report to the Chancellor of the Exchequer stating the reasons
why that provision has been made in the case of the securities or liabilities
concerned.

36.3

If the provision departs from the insolvency treatment principles, the report
must state the reasons why it does so.

36.4

The insolvency treatment principles are that where an instrument includes a
relevant provision—

36.4.a

the provision made by the instrument must be consistent with treating existing
claims in respect of the CCP’s shares and all the liabilities of the CCP in
accordance with the priority they would enjoy on a liquidation, and

36.4.b

any creditors who would have equal priority on a liquidation are to bear
losses on an equal footing with each other.

36.5

A report must comply with any other requirements as to content that may be
specified by the Treasury.

36.6

A report must be made as soon as reasonably practicable after the making of
the instrument to which it relates.

36.7

The Chancellor of the Exchequer must lay a copy of each report under sub-
paragraph  (2)  before Parliament.

36.8

In this paragraph a “ relevant provision ” means a provision falling within
paragraph  34(2) .

###### Priority between creditors

37

37.1

The Treasury may, for the purpose of ensuring that the treatment of any claims
in respect of a CCP’s shares or any liabilities in any write-down instrument
is aligned to an appropriate degree with the treatment of claims and
liabilities on an insolvency, by regulations specify matters or principles to
which the Bank is to be required to have regard in making any such instrument.

37.2

Regulations under this paragraph may for example—

37.2.a

specify the insolvency treatment principles (as defined in paragraph  36(4) )
or alternative principles;

37.2.b

specify the meaning of “insolvency” for one or more purposes of the
regulations.

37.3

Regulations under this paragraph may amend paragraph  36(4) .

37.4

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Power to take control

38

38.1

The eighth stabilisation option is for the Bank to make one or more
instruments of control.

38.2

An instrument of control is an instrument that makes any of the following
provision —

38.2.a

provision transferring any voting rights exercisable by shareholders of the
CCP or, if the CCP is an unincorporated association, members of the CCP to the
Bank for a specified period;

38.2.b

provision transferring specified powers, rights, duties or liabilities of the
directors or senior managers of the CCP to the Bank for a specified period.

38.3

Provision made under sub-paragraph  (2)  may for example include—

38.3.a

provision for exemptions or applying modifications in relation to any powers,
rights, duties or liabilities transferred;

38.3.b

provision for the Bank to exercise such powers, rights, duties or liabilities
under the CCP’s rules as may be specified in the instrument;

38.3.c

provision for the Bank to exercise such powers, rights, duties or liabilities
in relation to any contracts that the CCP is a party to as may be specified in
the instrument.

###### Shadow directors etc

39

39.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank uses one or more of the stabilisation
options mentioned in paragraph 1(3) in respect of a CCP unless the CCP has
ceased to be subject to the exercise of any stabilisation power mentioned in
paragraph 1(4).

39.2

A relevant person is not to be treated in relation to the CCP—

39.2.a

as a shadow director for the purposes of the relevant enactments,

39.2.b

as a person who discharges managerial responsibilities for the purposes of
those enactments (unless that person has been appointed as a director or a
senior manager), or

39.2.c

as a director within the meaning of section 417(1)(b) of FSMA 2000 (a person
in accordance with whose directions or instructions the directors of a body
corporate are accustomed to act).

39.3

In this paragraph—

      “ relevant enactment ” means—         the Companies Act 2006;
the Insolvency Act 1986;           the Company Directors Disqualification Act
1986;           FSMA 2000;           the Insolvency (Northern Ireland) Order
1989 ( S.I. 1989/2405 (N.I. 19) );           the Company Directors
Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002 ( S.I. 2002/3150 (N.I. 4) );
“ relevant person ” means—         the Bank,           persons who are
employed by, or act on behalf of, the Bank, and           a temporary manager
appointed under paragraph 6 of this Schedule.

###### Interpretation: “securities”

40

40.1

In this Schedule “ securities ” includes anything falling within any of the
following classes.

40.2

Class 1: shares and stock.

40.3

Class 2: debentures, including—

40.3.a

debenture stock,

40.3.b

loan stock,

40.3.c

bonds,

40.3.d

certificates of deposit, and

40.3.e

any other instrument creating or acknowledging a debt.

40.4

Class 3: warrants or other instruments that entitle the holder to acquire
anything in Class 1 or 2.

###### Share transfer instrument

41

41.1

A share transfer instrument is for purposes of this Schedule an instrument
which—

41.1.a

provides for securities issued by a specified CCP to be transferred;

41.1.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of securities issued by a specified CCP (whether or not the transfer has been
or is to be effected by that instrument, by another share transfer instrument
or otherwise).

41.2

A share transfer instrument may relate to—

41.2.a

specified securities, or

41.2.b

securities of a specified description.

###### Effect

42

42.1

In this paragraph “ transfer ” means a transfer provided for by a share
transfer instrument.

42.2

A transfer takes effect by virtue of the instrument (and in accordance with
its provisions as to timing or other ancillary matters).

42.3

A transfer takes effect despite any restriction arising by virtue of contract
or legislation or in any other way.

42.4

In sub-paragraph  (3)  “ restriction ” includes—

42.4.a

any restriction, inability or incapacity affecting what can or cannot be
assigned or transferred (whether generally or by a particular person), and

42.4.b

a requirement for consent (by any name).

42.5

A share transfer instrument may provide for a transfer to take effect free
from any trust, liability or other encumbrance (and may include provision
about their extinguishment).

42.6

A share transfer instrument may extinguish rights to acquire securities
falling within Class 1 or 2 in paragraph  40 .

###### Continuity

43

43.1

A share transfer instrument may provide for a transferee to be treated for any
purpose connected with the transfer as the same person as the transferor.

43.2

A share transfer instrument may provide for agreements made or other things
done by or in relation to a transferor to be treated as made or done by or in
relation to the transferee.

43.3

A share transfer instrument may provide for anything (including legal
proceedings) that relates to anything transferred and is in the process of
being done by or in relation to the transferor immediately before the transfer
date, to be continued by or in relation to the transferee.

43.4

A share transfer instrument may modify references (express or implied) in an
instrument or document to a transferor.

43.5

A share transfer instrument may require or permit—

43.5.a

a transferor to provide a transferee with information and assistance;

43.5.b

a transferee to provide a transferor with information and assistance.

###### Conversion and delisting

44

44.1

A share transfer instrument may provide for securities to be converted from
one form or class to another.

44.2

A share transfer instrument may provide for the listing of securities, under
section 74 of FSMA 2000, to be discontinued or suspended.

44.3

Where the listing of securities is suspended in accordance with a share
transfer instrument, those securities are to be treated for the purposes of
section 96 of, and paragraph 23(6) of Schedule 1ZA to, FSMA 2000 as still
being listed.

###### Directors and senior managers

45

45.1

A share transfer instrument may enable the Bank—

45.1.a

to remove a director or senior manager of a specified CCP;

45.1.b

to vary the service contract of a director or senior manager of a specified
CCP;

45.1.c

to terminate the service contract of a director or senior manager of a
specified CCP;

45.1.d

to appoint a director or a senior manager of a specified CCP.

45.2

Sub-paragraph  (1)  also applies to a director or senior manager of a relevant
CCP group company of the specified CCP.

45.3

A “ relevant CCP group company ” means a CCP group company that is
incorporated in, or formed under the law of any part of, the United Kingdom.

45.4

Appointments under sub-paragraph  (1)(d)  are to be on terms and conditions
agreed with the Bank.

###### Ancillary instruments: production, registration, etc

46

46.1

A share transfer instrument may permit or require the execution, issue or
delivery of an instrument.

46.2

A share transfer instrument may provide for a transfer to have effect
irrespective of —

46.2.a

whether an instrument has been produced, delivered, transferred or otherwise
dealt with;

46.2.b

registration.

46.3

A share transfer instrument may provide for the effect of an instrument
executed, issued or delivered, in accordance with the instrument.

46.4

A share transfer instrument may modify or annul the effect of an instrument.

46.5

A share transfer instrument may—

46.5.a

entitle a transferee to be registered in respect of transferred securities;

46.5.b

require a person to effect registration.

###### Incidental provision

47

47.1

A share transfer instrument may include incidental, consequential or
transitional provision.

47.2

In relying on sub-paragraph  (1)  a share transfer instrument—

47.2.a

may make provision generally or only for specified purposes, cases or
circumstances, and

47.2.b

may make different provision for different purposes, cases or circumstances.

###### Procedure: instruments

48

48.1

As soon as is reasonably practicable after making a share transfer instrument
in respect of a CCP, the Bank must send a copy to—

48.1.a

the CCP,

48.1.b

the Treasury,

48.1.c

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

48.1.d

the FCA, and

48.1.e

any other person specified in the code of practice under paragraph  16 .

48.2

As soon as is reasonably practicable after making share transfer instrument
the Bank must publish a copy—

48.2.a

on the Bank’s website,

48.2.b

in at least one other medium chosen by the Bank to maximise the likelihood of
the instrument coming to the attention of persons likely to be affected by it,
and

48.2.c

if securities of the CCP have been admitted to trading on a regulated market
(within the meaning of section 103(1) of FSMA 2000), by means of a regulatory
information service (within the meaning of section 313D of that Act),

and arrange for the publication of a copy on the website of the CCP in respect
of which the instrument was made.

48.3

Where the Treasury receive a copy of a share transfer instrument under sub-
paragraph  (1)  they must lay a copy before Parliament.

###### Supplemental instruments

49

49.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a share transfer instrument, in
respect of securities issued by a CCP, in accordance with paragraph  27(2) ,
29(3)  or  30(2)  (“the original instrument”).

49.2

The Bank may make one or more supplemental share transfer instruments.

49.3

A supplemental share transfer instrument is a share transfer instrument which—

49.3.a

provides for the transfer of securities which were issued by the CCP before
the original instrument and have not been transferred by the original
instrument or another supplemental share transfer instrument;

49.3.b

makes provision of a kind that a share transfer instrument may make under
paragraph  41(1)(b)  (whether or not in connection with a transfer under the
original instrument).

49.4

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a supplemental share transfer
instrument (but it is to be treated in the same way as any other share
transfer instrument for all other purposes, including for the purposes of the
application of a power under this Schedule).

49.5

Before making a supplemental share transfer instrument the Bank must consult—

49.5.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

49.5.b

the FCA, and

49.5.c

the Treasury.

49.6

The possibility of making a supplemental share transfer instrument in reliance
on sub-paragraph  (2)  is without prejudice to the possibility of making a new
instrument in accordance with paragraphs  27(2) ,  29(3)  and  30(2)  (and not
in reliance on sub-paragraph  (2)  above).

49.7

Paragraph  48  applies where the Bank has made a supplemental share transfer
instrument.

###### Onward transfer

50

50.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a share transfer instrument, in
respect of securities issued by a CCP, in accordance with paragraph  27(2) ,
29(3)  or  30(2)  (“the original instrument”).

50.2

The Bank may make one or more onward share transfer instruments.

50.3

An onward share transfer instrument is a share transfer instrument which—

50.3.a

provides for the transfer of—

50.3.a.i

securities which were issued by the CCP before the original instrument and
have been transferred by the original instrument or a supplemental share
transfer instrument, or

50.3.a.ii

securities which were issued by the CCP after the original instrument;

50.3.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of securities issued by the CCP (whether the transfer has been or is to be
effected by that instrument, by another share transfer instrument or
otherwise).

50.4

An onward share transfer instrument may not transfer securities to the
transferor under the original instrument.

50.5

The Bank may not make an onward share transfer instrument unless the
transferee under the original instrument is—

50.5.a

the Bank,

50.5.b

a nominee of the Treasury, or

50.5.c

a company wholly owned by the Bank or the Treasury.

50.6

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to an onward share transfer instrument
(but it is to be treated in the same way as any other share transfer
instrument for all other purposes, including for the purposes of the
application of a power under this Schedule).

50.7

Before making an onward share transfer instrument the Bank must consult—

50.7.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA, and

50.7.b

the FCA.

50.8

Paragraph  48  applies where the Bank has made an onward share transfer
instrument.

###### Reverse share transfer

51

51.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a share transfer instrument in
accordance with paragraph  27(2) ,  29(3)  or  30(2)  (“the original
instrument”) providing for the transfer of securities issued by a CCP to a
person (“the original transferee”).

51.2

The Bank may make one or more reverse share transfer instruments in respect of
securities issued by the CCP and held by the original transferee (whether or
not they were transferred by the original instrument).

51.3

If the Bank makes an onward share transfer instrument in respect of securities
transferred by the original instrument, the Bank may make one or more reverse
share transfer instruments in respect of securities issued by the CCP and held
by a transferee under the onward share transfer instrument (“the onward
transferee”).

51.4

A reverse share transfer instrument is a share transfer instrument which—

51.4.a

provides for transfer to the transferor under the original instrument (where
sub-paragraph  (2)  applies);

51.4.b

provides for transfer to the original transferee (where sub-paragraph  (3)
applies);

51.4.c

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of securities which are, could be or could have been transferred under
paragraph (a) or (b).

51.5

The Bank may not make a reverse share transfer instrument under sub-paragraph
(2)  unless—

51.5.a

the original transferee is—

51.5.a.i

the Bank,

51.5.a.ii

a company wholly owned by the Bank or the Treasury, or

51.5.a.iii

a nominee of the Treasury, or

51.5.b

the reverse share transfer instrument is made with the written consent of the
original transferee.

51.6

The Bank may not make a reverse share transfer instrument under sub-paragraph
(3)  unless—

51.6.a

the onward transferee is—

51.6.a.i

the Bank,

51.6.a.ii

a company wholly owned by the Bank or the Treasury, or

51.6.a.iii

a nominee of the Treasury, or

51.6.b

the reverse share transfer instrument is made with the written consent of the
onward transferee.

51.7

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a reverse share transfer instrument
(but it is to be treated in the same way as any other share transfer
instrument for all other purposes including for the purposes of the
application of a power under this Schedule).

51.8

Before making a reverse share transfer instrument the Bank must consult—

51.8.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA, and

51.8.b

the FCA.

51.9

Paragraph  48  applies where the Bank has made a reverse share transfer
instrument.

###### Bridge central counterparties: share transfers

52

52.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a property transfer instrument
or share transfer instrument in respect of a bridge central counterparty in
accordance with paragraph  29(3)  (“the original instrument”).

52.2

The Bank may make one or more bridge central counterparty share transfer
instruments.

52.3

A bridge central counterparty share transfer instrument is a share transfer
instrument which—

52.3.a

provides for securities issued by the bridge central counterparty to be
transferred;

52.3.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of securities issued by the bridge central counterparty (whether the transfer
has been or is to be effected by that instrument, by another share transfer
instrument or otherwise).

52.4

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a bridge central counterparty share
transfer instrument (but it is to be treated in the same way as any other
share transfer instrument for all other purposes, including for the purposes
of the application of a power under this Schedule).

52.5

Before making a bridge central counterparty share transfer instrument the Bank
must consult—

52.5.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

52.5.b

the FCA, and

52.5.c

the Treasury.

52.6

Paragraph  48  applies where the Bank has made a bridge central counterparty
share transfer instrument.

###### Bridge central counterparties: reverse share transfer

53

53.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a bridge central counterparty
share transfer instrument in accordance with paragraph  52(2)  (“the original
instrument”).

53.2

The Bank may make one or more bridge central counterparty reverse share
transfer instruments in respect of securities issued by the bridge central
counterparty and held by a transferee under the original instrument.

53.3

A bridge central counterparty reverse share transfer instrument is a share
transfer instrument which—

53.3.a

provides for transfer to the transferor under the original instrument;

53.3.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of securities which are, could be or could have been transferred under
paragraph  (a) .

53.4

The Bank must not make a bridge central counterparty reverse share transfer
instrument unless—

53.4.a

the transferee under the original instrument is—

53.4.a.i

a company wholly owned by the Bank,

53.4.a.ii

a company wholly owned by the Treasury, or

53.4.a.iii

a nominee of the Treasury, or

53.4.b

the bridge central counterparty reverse share transfer instrument is made with
the written consent of the transferee under the original instrument.

53.5

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a bridge central counterparty reverse
share transfer instrument (but it is to be treated in the same way as any
other share transfer instrument for all other purposes including for the
purposes of the application of a power under this Schedule).

53.6

Before making a bridge central counterparty reverse share transfer instrument
the Bank must consult—

53.6.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

53.6.b

the FCA, and

53.6.c

the Treasury.

53.7

Paragraph  48  applies where the Bank has made a bridge central counterparty
reverse share transfer instrument.

###### Property transfer instrument

54

54.1

A property transfer instrument is an instrument which—

54.1.a

provides for property, rights or liabilities of a specified CCP to be
transferred;

54.1.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of property, rights or liabilities of a specified CCP (whether the transfer
has been or is to be effected by that instrument, by another property transfer
instrument or otherwise).

54.2

A property transfer instrument may relate to—

54.2.a

all property, rights and liabilities of the specified CCP,

54.2.b

all its property, rights and liabilities subject to specified exceptions,

54.2.c

specified property, rights or liabilities, or

54.2.d

property, rights or liabilities of a specified description.

###### Effect

55

55.1

In this paragraph “ transfer ” means a transfer provided for by a property
transfer instrument.

55.2

A transfer takes effect by virtue of the instrument (and in accordance with
its provisions as to timing or other ancillary matters).

55.3

A transfer takes effect despite any restriction arising by virtue of contract
or legislation or in any other way.

55.4

In sub-paragraph  (3)  “ restriction ” includes—

55.4.a

any restriction, inability or incapacity affecting what can and cannot be
assigned or transferred (whether generally or by a particular person), and

55.4.b

a requirement for consent (by any name).

55.5

A property transfer instrument may provide for a transfer to be conditional
upon a specified event or situation—

55.5.a

occurring or arising, or

55.5.b

not occurring or arising.

55.6

A property transfer instrument may include provision dealing with the
consequences of breach of a condition imposed under sub-paragraph  (5) ; and
the consequences may include—

55.6.a

automatic vesting in the original transferor;

55.6.b

an obligation to effect a transfer back to the original transferor, with
specified consequences for failure to comply (which may include provision
conferring a discretion on a court or tribunal);

55.6.c

provision making a transfer or anything done in connection with a transfer
void or voidable.

55.7

Where a property transfer instrument makes provision in respect of property
held on trust (however arising) it may also make provision about—

55.7.a

the terms on which the property is to be held after the instrument takes
effect, and

55.7.b

how any powers, rights or obligations in respect of the property are to be
exercisable or have effect after the instrument takes effect.

55.8

Provision under sub-paragraph  (7)(a)  may remove or alter the terms of the
trust on which the property is held only to the extent that the Bank thinks it
necessary or expedient for the purpose of transferring—

55.8.a

the legal or beneficial interest of the transferor in the property;

55.8.b

any powers, rights or obligations of the transferor in respect of the
property.

55.9

In sub-paragraph  (8)  references to the transferor are references to the
transferor under the property transfer instrument.

###### Transferable property

56

A property transfer instrument may transfer any property, rights or
liabilities including, in particular—

56.a

property, rights and liabilities acquired or arising between the making of the
instrument and the transfer date,

56.b

rights and liabilities arising on or after the transfer date in respect of
matters occurring before that date,

56.c

property outside the United Kingdom,

56.d

rights and liabilities under the law of a country or territory outside the
United Kingdom, and

56.e

rights and liabilities under an enactment.

###### Continuity

57

57.1

A property transfer instrument may provide—

57.1.a

for a transfer to be, or to be treated as, a succession;

57.1.b

for a transferee to be treated for any purpose connected with the transfer as
the same person as the transferor.

57.2

A property transfer instrument may provide for agreements made or other things
done by or in relation to a transferor to be treated as made or done by or in
relation to the transferee.

57.3

A property transfer instrument may provide for anything (including legal
proceedings) that relates to anything transferred and is in the process of
being done by or in relation to the transferor immediately before the transfer
date, to be continued by or in relation to the transferee.

57.4

A property transfer instrument which transfers or enables the transfer of a
contract of employment may include provision about continuity of employment.

57.5

A property transfer instrument may modify references (express or implied) in
an instrument or document to a transferor.

57.6

In so far as rights and liabilities in respect of anything transferred are
enforceable after transfer, a property transfer instrument may provide for
apportionment between transferor and transferee to a specified extent and in
specified ways.

57.7

A property transfer instrument may enable the transferor and transferee by
agreement to modify a provision of the instrument; but a modification—

57.7.a

must achieve a result that could have been achieved by the instrument, and

57.7.b

may not transfer (or arrange for the transfer of) property, rights or
liabilities.

57.8

A property transfer instrument may require or permit—

57.8.a

a transferor to provide a transferee with information and assistance;

57.8.b

a transferee to provide a transferor with information and assistance.

###### Directors and senior managers

58

58.1

A property transfer instrument may enable the Bank—

58.1.a

to remove a director or senior manager of a specified CCP;

58.1.b

to vary the service contract of a director or senior manager of a specified
CCP;

58.1.c

to terminate the service contract of a director or senior manager of a
specified CCP;

58.1.d

to appoint a director or senior manager of a specified CCP.

58.2

Sub-paragraph  (1)  also applies to a director or senior manager of a relevant
CCP group company of the specified CCP.

58.3

A “ relevant CCP group company ” means a CCP group company incorporated in, or
formed under the law of any part of, the United Kingdom.

58.4

Appointments under sub-paragraph  (1)(d)  are to be on terms and conditions
agreed with the Bank.

###### Recognised central counterparty rules

59

59.1

A property transfer instrument made in respect of a CCP may make provision
about the consequences of a transfer for the rules of the CCP.

59.2

In particular, an instrument may—

59.2.a

modify or amend the rules of a CCP;

59.2.b

in a case where some, but not all, of the business of a CCP is transferred,
make provision as to the application of the rules in relation to the parts of
the business that are, and are not, transferred.

59.3

Provision by virtue of this paragraph may (but need not) be limited so as to
have effect—

59.3.a

for a specified period, or

59.3.b

until a specified event occurs or does not occur.

###### Recognised central counterparty membership

60

60.1

A property transfer instrument made in respect of a CCP may make provision
about the consequences of a transfer for membership of the CCP.

60.2

In particular, an instrument may—

60.2.a

make provision modifying the terms on which a person is a clearing member of a
CCP;

60.2.b

in a case where some, but not all, of the business of a CCP is transferred,
provide for a person who was a clearing member of the transferor to remain a
clearing member of the transferor while also becoming a clearing member of the
transferee.

###### Licences

61

61.1

A licence in respect of anything transferred by a property transfer instrument
continues to have effect despite the transfer.

61.2

A property transfer instrument may disapply sub-paragraph  (1)  to a specified
extent.

61.3

Where a licence imposes rights or obligations, a property transfer instrument
may apportion responsibility for exercise or compliance between transferor and
transferee.

61.4

In this paragraph “ licence ” includes permission and approval and any other
permissive document in respect of anything transferred.

###### Foreign property

62

62.1

This paragraph applies where a property transfer instrument transfers foreign
property.

62.2

In sub-paragraph  (1)  “ foreign property ” means—

62.2.a

property outside the United Kingdom, or

62.2.b

rights and liabilities under foreign law.

62.3

The transferor and the transferee must each take any necessary steps to ensure
that the transfer is effective as a matter of foreign law (if it is not wholly
effective by virtue of the property transfer instrument).

62.4

Until the transfer is effective as a matter of foreign law, the transferor
must—

62.4.a

hold the property or right for the benefit of the transferee (together with
any additional property or right accruing by virtue of the original property
or right), or

62.4.b

discharge the liability on behalf of the transferee.

62.5

If the Bank determines that, in spite of any action taken by the transferee or
the transferor, it is not possible for the transfer of certain property to be
effective under the law of the jurisdiction where the property is located or
(where the property consists of rights or liabilities) the law under which it
arises—

62.5.a

sub-paragraph  (4)  ceases to apply, and

62.5.b

the provisions of the property transfer instrument relating to that property
are void.

62.6

The Bank must give notice of any determination under sub-paragraph  (5)  to
the transferor and the transferee.

62.7

The transferor must meet any expenses of the transferee in complying with this
paragraph.

62.8

An obligation imposed by this paragraph is enforceable as if created by
contract between the transferor and transferee.

62.9

The transferor must comply with any directions of the Bank in respect of the
obligations under sub-paragraphs  (3)  and  (4) ; and—

62.9.a

a direction may disapply sub-paragraphs  (3)  and  (4)  to a specified extent,
and

62.9.b

obligations imposed by direction are enforceable as if created by contract
between the transferor and the Bank.

62.10

In this paragraph “ foreign law ” means the law of a country or territory
outside the United Kingdom.

###### Incidental provision

63

63.1

A property transfer instrument may include incidental, consequential or
transitional provision.

63.2

In relying on sub-paragraph  (1)  an instrument—

63.2.a

may make provision generally or only for specified purposes, cases or
circumstances, and

63.2.b

may make different provision for different purposes, cases or circumstances.

###### Procedure

64

64.1

As soon as is reasonably practicable after making a property transfer
instrument in respect of a CCP, the Bank must send a copy to—

64.1.a

the CCP,

64.1.b

the Treasury,

64.1.c

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

64.1.d

the FCA, and

64.1.e

any other person specified in the code of practice under paragraph  16 .

64.2

As soon as is reasonably practicable after making a property transfer
instrument the Bank must publish a copy—

64.2.a

on the Bank’s website,

64.2.b

in at least one other medium chosen by the Bank to maximise the likelihood of
the instrument coming to the attention of persons likely to be affected, and

64.2.c

if securities of the CCP have been admitted to trading on a regulated market
(within the meaning of section 103(1) of FSMA 2000), by means of a regulatory
information service (within the meaning of section 313D of that Act),

and arrange for the publication of a copy on the website of the CCP in respect
of which the instrument was made.

64.3

Where the Treasury receive a copy of a property transfer instrument under sub-
paragraph  (1)  they must lay a copy before Parliament.

###### Property transfer instrument: delisting

65

65.1

A property transfer instrument may provide for the listing of securities,
under section 74 of FSMA 2000, to be discontinued or suspended.

65.2

Where the listing of securities is suspended in accordance with a property
transfer instrument, those securities are to be treated for the purposes of
section 96 of, and paragraph 23(6) of Schedule 1ZA to, FSMA 2000 as still
being listed.

###### Transfer of property subsequent to resolution instrument

66

66.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a resolution instrument.

66.2

The Bank may make one or more property transfer instruments in respect of
property, rights or liabilities of the CCP.

66.3

Paragraph  17  does not apply to a property transfer instrument under sub-
paragraph  (2) .

66.4

Before making a property transfer instrument under sub-paragraph  (2)  the
Bank must consult—

66.4.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

66.4.b

the FCA, and

66.4.c

the Treasury.

###### Supplemental instruments

67

67.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a property transfer instrument
in accordance with paragraph  27(2)  or  29(3)  (“the original instrument”).

67.2

The Bank may make one or more supplemental property transfer instruments.

67.3

A supplemental property transfer instrument is a property transfer instrument
which—

67.3.a

provides for property, rights or liabilities to be transferred from the
transferor under the original instrument (whether accruing or arising before
or after the original instrument);

67.3.b

makes other provision of a kind that an original property transfer instrument
may make under paragraph  54(1)(b)  (whether in connection with a transfer
under the original instrument or in connection with a transfer under that or
another supplemental instrument).

67.4

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a supplemental property transfer
instrument (but it is to be treated in the same way as any other property
transfer instrument for all other purposes, including for the purposes of the
application of a power under this Schedule).

67.5

Before making a supplemental property transfer instrument the Bank must
consult—

67.5.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

67.5.b

the FCA, and

67.5.c

the Treasury.

67.6

The possibility of making a supplemental property transfer instrument in
reliance on sub-paragraph  (2)  is without prejudice to the possibility of
making a new instrument in accordance with paragraph  27(2)  or  29(3)  (and
not in reliance on sub-paragraph  (2)  above).

67.7

Paragraph  64  applies where the Bank has made a supplemental property
transfer instrument.

###### Private sector purchaser: reverse property transfer

68

68.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a property transfer instrument
in accordance with paragraph  27(2)  (“the original instrument”) providing for
the transfer of property, rights or liabilities of a CCP to a person (“the
original transferee”).

68.2

The Bank may make one or more private sector reverse property transfer
instruments in respect of property, rights or liabilities of the original
transferee.

68.3

A private sector reverse property transfer instrument is a property transfer
instrument which—

68.3.a

provides for transfer to the transferor under the original instrument;

68.3.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of property, rights or liabilities that are, could be or could have been
transferred under paragraph  (a)  (whether the transfer has been or is to be
effected by that instrument or otherwise).

68.4

The Bank must not make a private sector reverse property transfer instrument
without the written consent of the original transferee.

68.5

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a private sector reverse property
transfer instrument (but it is to be treated in the same way as any other
property transfer instrument for all other purposes including for the purposes
of the application of a power under this Schedule).

68.6

Before making a private sector reverse property transfer instrument the Bank
must consult—

68.6.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

68.6.b

the FCA, and

68.6.c

the Treasury.

68.7

Paragraph  64  applies where the Bank has made a private sector reverse
property transfer instrument.

###### Onward transfer

69

69.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a property transfer instrument
in respect of a bridge central counterparty in accordance with paragraph
29(3)  (“the original instrument”).

69.2

The Bank may make one or more onward property transfer instruments.

69.3

An onward property transfer instrument is a property transfer instrument
which—

69.3.a

provides for property, rights or liabilities of the bridge central
counterparty to be transferred (whether accruing or arising before or after
the original instrument);

69.3.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of property, rights or liabilities of the bridge central counterparty (whether
the transfer has been or is to be effected by that instrument, by another
property transfer instrument or otherwise).

69.4

An onward property transfer instrument may relate to property, rights or
liabilities of the bridge central counterparty whether or not they were
transferred under the original instrument.

69.5

An onward property transfer instrument may not transfer property, rights or
liabilities to the transferor under the original instrument.

69.6

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to an onward property transfer
instrument (but for other purposes it is to be treated in the same way as any
other property transfer instrument, including for the purposes of the
application of a power under this Schedule).

69.7

Before making an onward property transfer instrument the Bank must consult—

69.7.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA

69.7.b

the FCA, and

69.7.c

the Treasury.

69.8

Paragraph  64  applies where the Bank of England has made an onward property
transfer instrument.

###### Bridge central counterparties: reverse property transfer

70

70.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a property transfer instrument
in accordance with paragraph  29(3)  (“the original instrument”) providing for
the transfer of property, rights or liabilities to a bridge central
counterparty.

70.2

The Bank may make one or more bridge central counterparty reverse property
transfer instruments in respect of property, rights or liabilities of the
bridge central counterparty.

70.3

If the Bank makes an onward property transfer instrument under paragraph  69
the Bank may make one or more reverse property transfer instruments in respect
of property, rights or liabilities of a transferee under the onward property
transfer instrument (“the onward transferee”).

70.4

A bridge central counterparty reverse property transfer instrument is a
property transfer instrument which—

70.4.a

provides for transfer to the transferor under the original instrument (where
sub-paragraph  (2)  applies);

70.4.b

provides for transfer to the bridge central counterparty (where sub-paragraph
(3)  applies);

70.4.c

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of property, rights or liabilities that are, could be or could have been
transferred under paragraph  (a)  or  (b)  (whether the transfer has been or
is to be effected by that instrument or otherwise).

70.5

The Bank must not make a bridge central counterparty reverse property transfer
instrument unless—

70.5.a

the onward transferee is—

70.5.a.i

a company wholly owned by the Bank,

70.5.a.ii

a company wholly owned by the Treasury, or

70.5.a.iii

a company wholly owned by a nominee of the Treasury, or

70.5.b

the bridge central counterparty reverse property transfer is made with the
written consent of the onward transferee.

70.6

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a bridge central counterparty reverse
property transfer instrument (but it is to be treated in the same way as any
other property transfer instrument for all other purposes including for the
purposes of the application of a power under this Schedule).

70.7

Before making a bridge central counterparty reverse property transfer
instrument the Bank must consult—

70.7.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

70.7.b

the FCA, and

70.7.c

the Treasury.

70.8

Paragraph  64  applies where the Bank has made a bridge central counterparty
reverse property transfer instrument.

###### Transfer of ownership and private sector purchaser: property transfer

71

71.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a share transfer instrument, in
respect of securities issued by a CCP, in accordance with paragraph  27(2)  or
30(2)  (“the original instrument”).

71.2

The Bank may make one or more property transfer instruments.

71.3

A property transfer instrument is an instrument which—

71.3.a

provides for property, rights or liabilities of the CCP to be transferred
(whether accruing or arising before or after the original instrument);

71.3.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of property, rights or liabilities of the CCP (whether the transfer has been
or is to be effected by the instrument or otherwise).

71.4

The Bank may not make a property transfer instrument in accordance with this
paragraph unless the original instrument transferred securities to—

71.4.a

the Bank,

71.4.b

a company wholly owned by the Bank or the Treasury, or

71.4.c

a nominee of the Treasury.

71.5

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a property transfer instrument made
in accordance with this paragraph.

71.6

Before making a property transfer instrument in accordance with this
paragraph, the Bank must consult—

71.6.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA, and

71.6.b

the FCA.

71.7

Paragraph  64  applies where the Bank has made a property transfer instrument
