in accordance with this paragraph.

###### Transfer of ownership: reverse property transfer

72

72.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a property transfer instrument
in accordance with paragraph  71(2)  (“the original instrument”).

72.2

The Bank may make one or more reverse property transfer instruments in respect
of property, rights and liabilities of the transferee under the original
instrument.

72.3

A reverse property transfer instrument is a property transfer instrument
which—

72.3.a

provides for transfer to the transferor under the original instrument;

72.3.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of property, rights or liabilities which are, could be or could have been
transferred.

72.4

The Bank must not make a reverse property transfer instrument unless—

72.4.a

the transferee under the original instrument is—

72.4.a.i

the Bank,

72.4.a.ii

a company wholly owned by the Bank or the Treasury, or

72.4.a.iii

a nominee of the Treasury, or

72.4.b

the reverse property transfer instrument is made with the written consent of
the transferee under the original instrument.

72.5

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a reverse property transfer
instrument made in accordance with this paragraph.

72.6

Before making a reverse property transfer instrument in accordance with this
paragraph, the Bank must consult—

72.6.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA, and

72.6.b

the FCA.

72.7

Paragraph  64  applies where the Bank has made a reverse property transfer
instrument in accordance with this paragraph.

###### Bridge central counterparty: supplemental property transfer powers

73

73.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a share transfer instrument in
accordance with paragraph  29(3)  (“the original instrument”) providing for
the transfer of securities issued by a CCP (“the CCP”) to a bridge central
counterparty.

73.2

The Bank may make one or more property transfer instruments in relation to the
CCP (“bridge central counterparty supplemental property transfer
instruments”).

73.3

A bridge central counterparty supplemental property transfer instrument is an
instrument which—

73.3.a

provides for property, rights or liabilities of the CCP to be transferred
(whether accruing or arising before or after the original instrument);

73.3.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of property, rights or liabilities of the CCP (whether the transfer has been
or is to be effected by the instrument or otherwise).

73.4

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a bridge central counterparty
supplemental property transfer instrument (but it is to be treated in the same
way as any other property transfer instrument for all other purposes including
for the purposes of the application of a power under this Schedule).

73.5

Before making a bridge central counterparty supplemental property transfer
instrument the Bank must consult—

73.5.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

73.5.b

the FCA, and

73.5.c

the Treasury.

73.6

The possibility of making a bridge central counterparty supplemental property
transfer instrument in reliance on sub-paragraph  (2)  is without prejudice to
the possibility of making a property transfer instrument in accordance with
paragraph  29(3)  (and not in reliance on sub-paragraph  (2)  above).

73.7

Paragraph  64  applies where the Bank has made a bridge central counterparty
supplemental property transfer instrument.

###### Bridge central counterparty: supplemental reverse property transfer powers

74

74.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a bridge central counterparty
supplemental property transfer instrument in accordance with paragraph  73
(“the original instrument”).

74.2

The Bank may make one or more reverse property transfer instruments (“bridge
central counterparty supplemental reverse property transfer instruments”) in
respect of property, rights or liabilities of the transferee under the
original instrument.

74.3

A bridge central counterparty supplemental reverse property transfer
instrument is an instrument which—

74.3.a

provides for transfer to the transferor under the original instrument;

74.3.b

makes other provision for the purposes of, or in connection with, the transfer
of property, rights or liabilities which are, could be or could have been
transferred under paragraph (a) (whether the transfer has been or is to be
effected by that instrument or otherwise).

74.4

Paragraphs  17  and  19  do not apply to a bridge central counterparty
supplemental reverse property transfer instrument (but it is to be treated in
the same way as any other property transfer instrument for all other purposes
including for the purposes of the application of a power under this Schedule).

74.5

The Bank must not make a bridge central counterparty supplemental reverse
property transfer instrument unless—

74.5.a

the transferee under the original instrument is—

74.5.a.i

a company wholly owned by the Bank of England,

74.5.a.ii

a company wholly owned by the Treasury, or

74.5.a.iii

a nominee of the Treasury, or

74.5.b

it is made with the written consent of the transferee under the original
instrument.

74.6

Before making a bridge central counterparty supplemental reverse property
transfer instrument the Bank must consult—

74.6.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

74.6.b

the FCA, and

74.6.c

the Treasury.

74.7

Paragraph  64  applies where the Bank has made a bridge central counterparty
supplemental property transfer instrument.

###### Restriction of partial transfers

75

75.1

In this Schedule, “ partial property transfer ” means a property transfer
instrument which provides for the transfer of some, but not all of the
property, rights and liabilities of a CCP.

75.2

The Treasury may by regulations—

75.2.a

restrict the making of partial property transfers;

75.2.b

impose conditions on the making of partial property transfers;

75.2.c

require partial property transfers to include specified provision or provision
to a specified effect;

75.2.d

provide for a partial property transfer to be void or voidable, or for other
consequences (including automatic transfer of other property, rights or
liabilities) to arise, if or in so far as the partial property transfer is
made or purported to be made in contravention of a provision of the
regulations.

75.3

Regulations under this paragraph may apply to partial property transfers
generally or only to partial property transfers—

75.3.a

of a specified kind, or

75.3.b

made or applying in specified circumstances.

75.4

Provision under sub-paragraph  (2)  may, in particular, refer to particular
classes of liabilities.

75.5

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Power to protect certain interests

76

76.1

In this paragraph—

76.1.a

“ security interests ” means arrangements under which one person acquires, by
way of security, an actual or contingent interest in the property of another,

76.1.b

“title transfer collateral arrangements” are arrangements under which Person 1
transfers assets to Person 2 on terms providing for Person 2 to transfer
assets if specified obligations are discharged,

76.1.c

“set-off arrangements” are arrangements under which two or more debts, claims
or obligations can be set off against each other,

76.1.d

“netting arrangements” are arrangements under which a number of claims or
obligations can be converted into a net claim or obligation and include, in
particular, “close-out” netting arrangements, under which actual or
theoretical debts are calculated during the course of a contract for the
purpose of enabling them to be set off against each other or to be converted
into a net debt, and

76.1.e

“ protected arrangements ” means security interests, title transfer collateral
arrangements, set-off arrangements and netting arrangements.

76.2

The Treasury may by regulations —

76.2.a

restrict the making of partial property transfers in cases that involve, or
where they might affect, protected arrangements;

76.2.b

impose conditions on the making of partial property transfers in cases that
involve, or where they might affect, protected arrangements;

76.2.c

require partial property transfers to include specified provision, or
provision to a specified effect, in respect of or for purposes connected with
protected arrangements;

76.2.d

provide for a partial property transfer to be void or voidable, or for other
consequences (including automatic transfer of other property, rights or
liabilities) to arise, if or in so far as the partial property transfer is
made or purported to be made in contravention of a provision of the
regulations.

76.3

Regulations under this paragraph may apply to protected arrangements generally
or only to arrangements—

76.3.a

of a specified kind, or

76.3.b

made or applying in specified circumstances.

76.4

Regulations under this paragraph may include provision for determining which
arrangements are to be, or not to be, treated as protected arrangements; in
particular, regulations may provide for arrangements to be classified not
according to their description by the parties but according to one or more
indications of how they are treated, or are intended to be treated, in
commercial practice.

76.5

In this paragraph “ arrangements ” includes arrangements which—

76.5.a

are formed wholly or partly by one or more contracts or trusts;

76.5.b

arise under or are wholly or partly governed by the law of a country or
territory outside the United Kingdom;

76.5.c

wholly or partly arise automatically as a matter of law;

76.5.d

involve any number of parties;

76.5.e

operate partly by reference to other arrangements between other parties.

76.6

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Creation of liabilities

77

77.1

The provision that may be made by a property transfer instrument in reliance
on paragraph  54(1)(b) ,  67(3)(b) ,  68(3)(b) ,  69(3)(b) ,  70(4)(c) ,
71(3)(b) ,  72(3)(b) ,  73(3)(b) , or  74(3)(b)  includes provision for the
creation of liabilities.

77.2

The provision may be framed by reference to an agreement which has been or is
to be entered into, or anything else which has been or is to be done, by any
person (including a person other than the person making the instrument).

###### Regulations for safeguarding certain financial arrangements: write-down instruments

78

78.1

In this paragraph “ protected arrangements ” means security interests, title
transfer collateral arrangements, set-off arrangements and netting
arrangements.

78.2

In sub-paragraph  (1) —

78.2.a

“ security interests ” means arrangements under which one person acquires, by
way of security, an actual or contingent interest in the property of another,

78.2.b

“title transfer collateral arrangements” are arrangements under which Person 1
transfers assets to Person 2 on terms providing for Person 2 to transfer
assets if specified obligations are discharged,

78.2.c

“set-off arrangements” are arrangements under which two or more debts, claims
or obligations can be set off against each other, and

78.2.d

“netting arrangements” are arrangements under which a number of claims or
obligations can be converted into a net claim or obligation and include, in
particular, “close-out” netting arrangements, under which actual or
theoretical debts are calculated during the course of a contract for the
purpose of enabling them to be set off against each other or to be converted
into a net debt.

78.3

The Treasury may by regulations —

78.3.a

restrict the making of a write-down instrument in cases that involve, or where
they might affect, protected arrangements;

78.3.b

impose conditions on the making of write-down instruments in cases that
involve, or where they might affect, protected arrangements;

78.3.c

require write-down instruments to include specified provision, or provision to
a specified effect, in respect of or for purposes connected with protected
arrangements;

78.3.d

provide for a write-down instrument to be void or voidable, or for other
consequences to arise, if or in so far as the write-down instrument is made or
purported to be made in contravention of a provision of the regulations;

78.3.e

specify principles to which the Bank is to be required to have regard in
making a write-down instrument—

78.3.e.i

that involves protected arrangements, or

78.3.e.ii

where the making of the instrument might affect protected arrangements.

78.4

Regulations under this paragraph may apply to protected arrangements generally
or only to arrangements—

78.4.a

of a specified kind, or

78.4.b

made or applying in specified circumstances.

78.5

Regulations under this paragraph may include provision for determining which
arrangements are to be, or not to be, treated as protected arrangements; in
particular, regulations may provide for arrangements to be classified not
according to their description by the parties but according to one or more
indications of how they are treated, or are intended to be treated, in
commercial practice.

78.6

In this paragraph “ arrangements ” includes arrangements which—

78.6.a

are formed wholly or partly by one or more contracts or trusts;

78.6.b

arise under or are wholly or partly governed by the law of a country or
territory outside the United Kingdom;

78.6.c

wholly or partly arise automatically as a matter of law;

78.6.d

involve any number of parties;

78.6.e

operate partly by reference to other arrangements between other parties.

78.7

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Resolution instruments: effect and supplementary matters

79

79.1

In this Schedule “ resolution instrument ” means—

79.1.a

a cash call instrument;

79.1.b

a tear-up instrument;

79.1.c

a variation instrument;

79.1.d

a write-down instrument;

79.1.e

an instrument of control.

79.2

A resolution instrument must be made in writing.

79.3

A resolution instrument in respect of a CCP ceases to have effect on whichever
of the following occurs first—

79.3.a

such date as may be specified in the instrument,

79.3.b

the making of a share transfer instrument or a property transfer instrument in
relation to the CCP, or

79.3.c

any of the conditions under paragraph  17  ceasing to be met in relation to
the CCP.

79.4

The Bank may at any time amend a resolution instrument to specify or amend a
date for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (3)(a) .

79.5

Before amending a resolution instrument in accordance with sub-paragraph  (4)
the Bank must consult the Treasury.

79.6

Provision made in a resolution instrument takes effect despite any restriction
arising by virtue of contract or legislation or in any other way.

79.7

A resolution instrument may provide for anything (including legal proceedings)
that relates to anything affected by the instrument and is in the process of
being done immediately before the instrument takes effect to be continued from
the time the instrument takes effect.

79.8

A resolution instrument may modify references (express or implied) in an
instrument or document.

79.9

A resolution instrument may require or permit any person to provide
information and assistance to the Bank or another person, for the purposes of
or in connection with provision made or to be made in that or another
resolution instrument.

79.10

A resolution instrument—

79.10.a

may include supplemental, incidental, consequential or transitional provision,

79.10.b

may make provision generally or only for specified purposes, cases or
circumstances,

79.10.c

may make different provision for different purposes, cases or circumstances,
and

79.10.d

may make provision for exemptions.

79.11

A resolution instrument ceasing to have effect does not affect the validity of
anything previously done in accordance with it.

###### Write-down instruments: supplementary

80

80.1

A write-down instrument may permit or require the execution, issue or delivery
of an instrument.

80.2

A write-down instrument may provide for any provision in the instrument to
have effect irrespective of—

80.2.a

whether an instrument has been produced, delivered, transferred or otherwise
dealt with;

80.2.b

registration.

80.3

A write-down instrument may provide for the effect of an instrument executed,
issued or delivered in accordance with the instrument.

80.4

A write-down instrument may—

80.4.a

entitle a person to be registered in respect of a security;

80.4.b

require a person to effect registration.

###### Resolution instruments: procedure

81

81.1

As soon as is reasonably practicable after making a resolution instrument in
respect of a CCP, the Bank must send a copy of the instrument to—

81.1.a

the CCP,

81.1.b

the Treasury,

81.1.c

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

81.1.d

the FCA, and

81.1.e

any other person specified in the code of practice under paragraph  16 .

81.2

As soon as is reasonably practicable after making a resolution instrument the
Bank must publish a copy—

81.2.a

on the Bank’s website,

81.2.b

in at least one other medium chosen by the Bank to maximise the likelihood of
the instrument coming to the attention of persons likely to be affected, and

81.2.c

if securities of the CCP have been admitted to trading on a regulated market
(within the meaning of section 103(1) of FSMA 2000), by means of a regulatory
information service (within the meaning of section 313D of that Act),

and arrange for the publication of a copy on the website of the CCP in respect
of which the instrument was made.

81.3

Where the Treasury receive a copy of a resolution instrument under sub-
paragraph  (1)  they must lay a copy before Parliament.

###### Supplemental resolution instruments

82

82.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a resolution instrument (“the
original instrument”) with respect to a CCP.

82.2

The Bank may make, with respect to the CCP, one or more resolution instruments
designated by the Bank as supplemental resolution instruments.

82.3

Paragraphs  17 ,  22  and  79(3)(c)  do not apply to a supplemental resolution
instrument (but it is to be treated in the same way as a resolution instrument
for all other purposes, including for the purposes of the application of a
power under this Schedule).

82.4

Before making a supplemental resolution instrument, the Bank must consult—

82.4.a

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA,

82.4.b

the FCA, and

82.4.c

the Treasury.

82.5

The possibility of making a supplemental resolution instrument in reliance on
sub-paragraph  (2)  is without prejudice to the possibility of making a new
resolution instrument in accordance with paragraphs  31(1) ,  32(1) , 33(1),
34(1) and  38(1)  (and not in reliance on sub-paragraph  (2)  above).

###### Directors and senior managers

83

83.1

A resolution instrument may enable the Bank—

83.1.a

to remove a director or senior manager of a specified CCP;

83.1.b

to vary the service contract of a director or senior manager of a specified
CCP;

83.1.c

to terminate the service contract of a director or senior manager of a
specified CCP;

83.1.d

to appoint a director or a senior manager of a specified CCP.

83.2

Sub-paragraph  (1)  also applies to a director or senior manager of a relevant
CCP group company of the specified CCP.

83.3

A “relevant CCP group company” is a CCP group company incorporated in, or
formed under the law of any part of, the United Kingdom.

83.4

Appointments under sub-paragraph  (1)(d)  are to be on terms and conditions
agreed with the Bank.

###### Termination rights etc

84

84.1

In this paragraph—

      “ resolution measure ” means—         the making by the Bank of a
stabilisation instrument in relation to a CCP,           where an instrument
of control under paragraph  38  is in place in relation to a CCP, the exercise
by the Bank of any relevant rules of the CCP,           a measure taken by a
CCP as a result of directions given under paragraph  2 ,           the removal
by a CCP of a director or senior manager as a result of a requirement imposed
under paragraph  5 ,           the appointment of a temporary manager in
relation to a CCP under paragraph  6 ,           a restriction or prohibition
on payments under paragraph  13  or  102 ,           the recognition by the
Bank of third-country resolution action (or part of such action) in accordance
with Part 7 of this Schedule, or           the exercise by the Bank of a
stabilisation power by virtue of paragraph  146(3) ;                 “ default
event provision ” means a Type 1 or Type 2 default event provision (see sub-
paragraphs  (2)  and  (3) );           “ relevant rules ”, in relation to a
CCP, mean rules ensuring that the requirements under paragraph 29A or 36 of
the Schedule to the Financial Services and Markets Act 2000 (Recognition
Requirements for Investment Exchanges, Clearing Houses and Central Securities
Depositories) Regulations 2001 ( S.I. 2001/995 ) are met;           “
stabilisation instrument ” means—         a share transfer instrument,
a property transfer instrument, or           a resolution instrument.

84.2

A Type 1 default event provision is a provision of a contract or other
agreement that has the effect that if a specified event occurs or situation
arises—

84.2.a

the agreement is terminated, modified or replaced,

84.2.b

rights or duties under the agreement are terminated, modified or replaced,

84.2.c

a right accrues to terminate, modify or replace the agreement,

84.2.d

a right accrues to terminate, modify or replace rights or duties under the
agreement,

84.2.e

a sum becomes payable or ceases to be payable,

84.2.f

delivery of anything becomes due or ceases to be due,

84.2.g

a right to claim a payment or delivery accrues, changes or lapses,

84.2.h

any other right accrues, changes or lapses,

84.2.i

a right to accelerate, close out, set-off or net obligations accrues, changes
or lapses, or

84.2.j

an interest is created, changes or lapses.

84.3

A Type 2 default event provision is a provision of a contract or other
agreement that has the effect that a provision of the contract or agreement—

84.3.a

takes effect only if a specified event occurs or does not occur,

84.3.b

takes effect only if a specified situation arises or does not arise,

84.3.c

has effect only for so long as a specified event does not occur,

84.3.d

has effect only while a specified situation lasts,

84.3.e

applies differently if a specified event occurs,

84.3.f

applies differently if a specified situation arises, or

84.3.g

applies differently while a specified situation lasts.

84.4

For the purposes of sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (3)  it is the effect of a
provision that matters, not how it is described (nor, for example, whether it
is presented in a positive or a negative form).

84.5

Subject to sub-paragraph  (7) , sub-paragraph  (6)  applies where—

84.5.a

a contract or agreement is entered into by a CCP, and

84.5.b

the substantive obligations provided for in the contract or agreement
(including payment and delivery obligations and provision of collateral)
continue to be performed.

84.6

The following are to be disregarded in determining whether a default event
provision applies—

84.6.a

a resolution measure, and

84.6.b

the occurrence of any event directly linked to the application of such a
measure.

84.7

A stabilisation instrument may provide for sub-paragraph  (6) —

84.7.a

not to apply in relation to a contract or other agreement, or

84.7.b

to apply in relation to a contract or other agreement only to the extent
specified by the Bank in the instrument.

84.8

Provision may be made under sub-paragraph  (7)  only if the Bank considers
that such provision would advance one or more of the special resolution
objectives.

84.9

A stabilisation instrument may provide for sub-paragraph  (10)  or  (11)  to
apply (but need not apply either) in circumstances where sub-paragraph  (6)
would not apply.

84.10

If this sub-paragraph applies, the stabilisation instrument is to be
disregarded in determining whether a default event provision applies.

84.11

If this sub-paragraph applies, the stabilisation instrument is to be
disregarded in determining whether a default event provision applies except so
far as the instrument provides otherwise.

84.12

In sub-paragraphs  (9) ,  (10)  and  (11)  a reference to a stabilisation
instrument is a reference to—

84.12.a

the making of the instrument,

84.12.b

anything that is done by the instrument or is to be, or may be, done under or
by virtue of the instrument, and

84.12.c

any action or decision taken or made under this or another enactment in so far
as it resulted in, or was connected to, the making of the instrument.

84.13

Provision under sub-paragraph  (9)  may apply sub-paragraph  (10)  or  (11) —

84.13.a

generally or only for specified purposes, cases or circumstances, or

84.13.b

differently for different purposes, cases or circumstances.

84.14

A thing is not done by virtue of a stabilisation instrument for the purposes
of sub-paragraph  (12)(b)  merely by virtue of being done under a contract or
other agreement rights or obligations under which have been affected by the
instrument.

###### Deferment

85

85.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision for and in connection with the
suspension or waiver of provisions made under a resolution instrument.

85.2

The following are examples of provision that may be made by regulations under
this paragraph—

85.2.a

provision specifying matters to which the Bank must have regard before
suspending or waiving provisions under a resolution instrument;

85.2.b

provision specifying the procedure for suspending or waiving such provisions;

85.2.c

provision specifying the maximum time period for which a suspension under the
regulations may take effect;

85.2.d

provision for review of any suspension or waiver of provisions under a
resolution instrument.

85.3

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the negative procedure.

###### Recovery of expenses

86

86.1

The Bank may, in making a resolution instrument, share transfer instrument or
property transfer instrument in relation to a CCP, direct that CCP to pay the
Bank a specified fee to cover expenses reasonably incurred by the Bank in
connection with exercising that option.

86.2

The Treasury may direct a CCP in relation to which the Bank has made a
resolution instrument, share transfer instrument or property transfer
instrument to pay the Treasury a specified fee to cover expenses reasonably
incurred by the Treasury in connection with the exercise by the Bank of that
power in relation to the CCP.

###### Compensation scheme

87

87.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision for protecting the financial
interests of relevant persons in connection with the making of a stabilisation
instrument in respect of a CCP.

87.2

For the purposes of sub-paragraph (1) regulations may make provision
establishing a scheme, which may for example include provision—

87.2.a

for determining whether relevant persons should be paid compensation or
providing for relevant persons to be paid compensation;

87.2.b

for paying any compensation (including payments in instalment or subject to
terms and conditions);

87.2.c

under which specified relevant persons become entitled to the proceeds of
disposal of things transferred under a share transfer instrument or property
transfer instrument.

87.3

In making regulations under this paragraph the Treasury must have regard
(among other matters) to the desirability of ensuring that any person who is a
relevant person before the making of a stabilisation instrument does not
receive less favourable treatment than they would have received had—

87.3.a

the CCP entered insolvency immediately before the stabilisation instrument was
made, and

87.3.b

all the relevant rules of the CCP been applied in the period leading up to the
insolvency.

87.4

The regulations may provide for the amount of compensation payable to relevant
persons to be determined by a person appointed in accordance with the
regulations (an “independent valuer”).

87.5

The regulations may make such further provision about independent valuers as
the Treasury consider to be appropriate, including (among other things)—

87.5.a

provision about appointment and tenure,

87.5.b

provision for remuneration of independent valuers and their staff,

87.5.c

provision conferring functions on independent valuers (including conferring a
discretion),

87.5.d

provision specifying principles to be applied by independent valuers to
determine the amount of compensation,

87.5.e

provision about the procedure to be followed by independent valuers,

87.5.f

provision about the liability of independent valuers, and

87.5.g

provision about appeals against decisions by independent valuers (including
conferring jurisdiction on a court or tribunal).

87.6

The regulations may provide for compensation or other payments to be made by—

87.6.a

the Treasury, or

87.6.b

any other specified persons.

87.7

In this paragraph—

      references to “insolvency” include a reference to—         liquidation,
administration,           receivership,           a composition with
creditors, and           a scheme of arrangement;                 “ relevant
person ”, in relation to a CCP, means—         clearing members of the CCP;
creditors of the CCP;           shareholders of the CCP;           clients
within the meaning of Article 2 of EMIR where they have a contractual
relationship as principal with the CCP.

87.8

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Instruments: notification of members and creditors

88

88.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has applied one or more of the
stabilisation options in respect of a CCP.

88.2

Except where securities issued by the CCP have been admitted to trading on a
regulated market (within the meaning given in section 103(1) of FSMA 2000),
the Bank must send a copy of any property transfer instrument, share transfer
instrument or resolution instrument made in respect of the CCP to each of the
following persons who are known to the Bank—

88.2.a

the CCP’s shareholders or, if the CCP is an unincorporated association, its
members, and

88.2.b

creditors of the CCP.

###### General continuity obligation: property transfers

89

89.1

In this paragraph—

89.1.a

“ residual CCP ” means a CCP all or part of whose business has been
transferred under a property transfer instrument in accordance with paragraph
27(2) , 29(3), 66(2) or 73(2),

89.1.b

“ group company ” means anything which is, or was immediately before the
transfer, a group undertaking in relation to a residual CCP,

89.1.c

“ group undertaking ” has the meaning given by section 1161(5) of the
Companies Act 2006,

89.1.d

“ the transferred business ” means the part of the CCP’s business that has
been transferred, and

89.1.e

“ transferee ” means a commercial purchaser or bridge central counterparty to
whom all or part of the transferred business has been transferred.

89.2

In this paragraph a reference to insolvency includes a reference to
liquidation, administration, receivership, composition with creditors and a
scheme of arrangement.

89.3

The residual CCP and each group company must provide such services and
facilities as are required to enable a transferee to operate the transferred
business, or part of it, effectively.

89.4

The duty under sub-paragraph  (3)  (the “continuity obligation”) may be
enforced as if created by contract between the residual CCP or group company
and the transferee.

89.5

The continuity obligation continues to apply despite the residual CCP or group
company entering insolvency, and may not be disclaimed by a liquidator under
section 178(2) of the Insolvency Act 1986 or Article 152(1) of the Insolvency
(Northern Ireland) Order 1989.

89.6

The duty to provide services and facilities in pursuance of the continuity
obligation is subject to a right to receive reasonable consideration.

89.7

But if the services and facilities provided in pursuance of the continuity
obligation were provided to the CCP whose business has been transferred, under
an agreement with that CCP, before the property transfer instrument providing
for the transfer was made, they are to continue for the duration of that
agreement to be provided on the terms set out in that agreement (and sub-
paragraph  (6)  does not apply).

89.8

The continuity obligation is not limited to the provision of services or
facilities directly to a transferee.

89.9

The Bank may, with the consent of the Treasury, by notice to the residual CCP
or a group company state that in the Bank’s opinion—

89.9.a

specified activities are required to be undertaken in accordance with the
continuity obligation;

89.9.b

activities are required to be undertaken in accordance with the continuity
obligation on specified terms.

89.10

A notice under sub-paragraph  (9)  is to be determinative of the nature and
extent of the continuity obligation as from the time when the notice is given.

###### Special continuity obligations: property transfers

90

90.1

Expressions in this paragraph have the same meaning as in paragraph  89 .

90.2

The Bank may—

90.2.a

cancel a contract or other arrangement between the residual CCP and a group
company or a third party (whether or not rights or obligations under it have
been transferred to a transferee);

90.2.b

modify the terms of a contract or other arrangement between the residual CCP
and a group company or a third party (whether or not rights or obligations
under it have been transferred to a transferee);

90.2.c

add or substitute a transferee as a party to a contract or other arrangement
between the residual CCP and a group company or a third party;

90.2.d

confer and impose rights and obligations on a group company or third party and
a transferee, which must have effect as if created by contract between them;

90.2.e

confer and impose rights and obligations on the residual CCP and a transferee
which must have effect as if created by contract between them.

90.3

In modifying or setting terms under sub-paragraph  (2)  the Bank must aim, so
far as is reasonably practicable, to preserve or include—

90.3.a

provision for reasonable consideration, and

90.3.b

any other provision that would be expected in arrangements concluded between
parties dealing at arm’s length.

90.4

The power under sub-paragraph  (2) —

90.4.a

may be exercised only in so far as the Bank thinks it necessary to ensure the
provision of such services and facilities as are required to enable the
transferee to operate the transferred business, or part of it, effectively,

90.4.b

may be exercised only with the consent of the Treasury, and

90.4.c

must be exercised by way of provision in a property transfer instrument.

90.5

An obligation imposed on the residual CCP or a group company under sub-
paragraph (2)(d) or (e) continues to apply despite the residual CCP or group
company entering insolvency, and may not be disclaimed by a liquidator under
section 178(2) of the Insolvency Act 1986 or Article 152(1) of the Insolvency
(Northern Ireland) Order 1989.

###### Continuity obligations: onward property transfers

91

91.1

In this paragraph—

91.1.a

“ onward transfer ” means a transfer of property, rights or liabilities
(whether or not under a power in this Schedule) from—

91.1.a.i

a person who is a transferee under a property transfer instrument under
paragraph  29(3)  (an “original transferee”), or

91.1.a.ii

a CCP, securities issued by which were earlier transferred by a share transfer
instrument under paragraph  29(3)  or  30(2) , and

91.1.b

the person to whom the onward transfer is made is referred to as an “ onward
transferee ”.

91.2

The Bank may—

91.2.a

provide for an obligation under paragraph  89  to apply in respect of an
onward transferee;

91.2.b

extend paragraph  90  so as to permit action to be taken under paragraph
90(2)  for the purpose of enabling an onward transferee to operate the
transferred business, or part of it, effectively.

91.3

Sub-paragraph  (2)  may be relied on to impose obligations on—

91.3.a

an original transferee (where the original transfer was a property transfer),

91.3.b

a residual CCP within the meaning of paragraph  89  (where the original
transfer was a property transfer),

91.3.c

the CCP (where the original transfer was a share transfer),

91.3.d

anything which is or was a group undertaking (within the meaning of section
1161(5) of the Companies Act 2006) of anything within paragraphs  (a)  to  (c)
, or

91.3.e

any combination of the above.

91.4

Sub-paragraph  (2)  may be used to impose obligations—

91.4.a

in addition to obligations under or by virtue of paragraph  89  or  90 , or

91.4.b

replacing obligations under or by virtue of either of those paragraphs to a
specified extent.

91.5

A power under sub-paragraph  (2)  is exercisable by giving a notice to each
person—

91.5.a

on whom a continuity obligation is to be imposed under the power, or

91.5.b

who is expected to benefit from a continuity obligation under the power.

91.6

Paragraphs  89(3)  to  (10)  and  90(3)  and  (4)  apply to an obligation as
applied under sub-paragraph  (2) —

91.6.a

construing “transferred business” as the business transferred by means of the
onward transfer, and

91.6.b

with any other necessary modification.

91.7

The Bank may act under or by virtue of sub-paragraph  (2)  only with the
consent of the Treasury.

###### General continuity obligation: share transfers

92

92.1

In this paragraph and paragraph  93 —

92.1.a

“ transferred CCP ” means a CCP all or part of the ownership of which has been
transferred in accordance with paragraph  27(2) ,  29(3) , or  30(2) ,

92.1.b

“ former group company ” means anything which was a group undertaking in
relation to the transferred CCP immediately before the transfer (whether or
not it is also a group undertaking in relation to the transferred CCP
immediately after the transfer),

92.1.c

“ group undertaking ” has the meaning given by section 1161(5) of the
Companies Act 2006.

92.2

In this paragraph a reference to insolvency includes a reference to
liquidation, administration, receivership, composition with creditors and a
scheme of arrangement.

92.3

Each former group company must provide such services and facilities as are
required to enable the transferred CCP to operate effectively.

92.4

The duty under sub-paragraph  (3)  (the “continuity obligation”) may be
enforced as if created by contract between the transferred CCP and the former
group company.

92.5

The continuity obligation continues to apply despite the former group company
entering insolvency, and may not be disclaimed by a liquidator under section
178(2) of the Insolvency Act 1986 or Article 152(1) of the Insolvency
(Northern Ireland) Order 1989.

92.6

The duty to provide services and facilities in pursuance of the continuity
obligation is subject to a right to receive reasonable consideration.

92.7

But if the services and facilities provided in pursuance of the continuity
obligation were provided to the transferred CCP, under an agreement with that
CCP, before the share transfer instrument providing for the transfer was made,
they are to continue for the duration of that agreement to be provided on the
terms set out in that agreement (and sub-paragraph  (6)  does not apply).

92.8

The continuity obligation is not limited to the provision of services or
facilities directly to the transferred CCP.

92.9

The Bank may by notice to a former group company state that in the Bank’s
opinion—

92.9.a

specified activities are required to be undertaken in accordance with the
continuity obligation;

92.9.b

activities are required to be undertaken in accordance with the continuity
obligation on specified terms.

92.10

A notice under sub-paragraph  (9)  is to be determinative of the nature and
extent of the continuity obligation as from the time when the notice is given.

92.11

The Bank may act under or by virtue of sub-paragraph  (9)  only with the
consent of the Treasury.

###### Special continuity obligations: share transfers

93

93.1

Expressions in this paragraph have the same meaning as in paragraph  92 .

93.2

The Bank may—

93.2.a

cancel a contract or other arrangement between the transferred CCP and a
former group company or a third party;

93.2.b

modify the terms of a contract or other arrangement between the transferred
CCP and a former group company or a third party;

93.2.c

confer and impose rights and obligations on a former group company or a third
party and the transferred CCP, which has effect as if created by contract
between them.

93.3

In modifying or setting terms under sub-paragraph  (2)  the Bank must aim, so
far as is reasonably practicable, to preserve or include—

93.3.a

a provision for reasonable consideration, and

93.3.b

any other provision that would be expected in arrangements concluded between
parties dealing at arm’s length.

93.4

The power under sub-paragraph  (2) —

93.4.a

may be exercised only in so far as the Bank thinks it necessary to ensure the
provision of such services and facilities as are required to enable the
transferred CCP to operate effectively,

93.4.b

may be exercised by the Bank only with the consent of the Treasury, and

93.4.c

must be exercised by way of provision in a share transfer instrument.

93.5

An obligation imposed on the transferred CCP or a former group company under
sub-paragraph (2)(b) or (c) continues to apply despite the transferred CCP or
former group company entering insolvency, and may not be disclaimed by a
liquidator under section 178(2) of the Insolvency Act 1986 or Article 152(1)
of the Insolvency (Northern Ireland) Order 1989.

###### Continuity obligations: onward share transfers

94

94.1

In this paragraph “ onward transfer ” means a transfer (whether or not under a
power in this Schedule) of securities issued by a CCP where—

94.1.a

securities issued by the CCP were earlier transferred by a share transfer
instrument under paragraph  29(3)  or  30(2) , or

94.1.b

the CCP was the transferee under a property transfer instrument under
paragraph  29(3) .

94.2

The Bank may—

94.2.a

provide for an obligation under paragraph  92  to apply in respect of the CCP
after the onward transfer;

94.2.b

extend paragraph  93  so as to permit action to be taken under paragraph
93(2)  to enable the CCP to operate effectively after the onward transfer.

94.3

Sub-paragraph  (2)  may be relied on to impose obligations on—

94.3.a

the CCP,

94.3.b

anything which is or was a group undertaking (within the meaning of section
1161(5) of the Companies Act 2006) of the CCP,

94.3.c

anything which is or was a group undertaking of the residual CCP (in a case to
which sub-paragraph  (1)(b)  applies), or

94.3.d

any combination of the above.

94.4

Sub-paragraph  (2)  may be used to impose obligations—

94.4.a

in addition to obligations under or by virtue of paragraph  92  or  93 , or

94.4.b

replacing obligations under or by virtue of either of those paragraphs to a
specified extent.

94.5

A power under sub-paragraph  (2)  is exercisable by giving a notice to each
person—

94.5.a

on whom a continuity obligation is to be imposed under the power, or

94.5.b

who is expected to benefit from a continuity obligation under the power.

94.6

Paragraphs  92(4)  to  (10)  and 94(3) and (4) apply to an obligation as
applied under sub-paragraph  (2)  with any necessary modification.

94.7

The Bank may act under or by virtue of sub-paragraph  (2)  only with the
consent of the Treasury.

###### Continuity obligations: consideration and terms

95

95.1

The Treasury may by regulations specify matters which are to be or not to be
considered in determining—

95.1.a

what amounts to reasonable consideration for the purpose of paragraphs  89  to
94 ;

95.1.b

what provisions to include in accordance with paragraph  90(3)(b)  or
93(3)(b) .

95.2

The Bank may give guarantees or indemnities in respect of consideration for
services or facilities provided or to be provided in pursuance of a continuity
obligation.

95.3

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the negative procedure.

###### Continuity obligations: termination

96

96.1

The Bank may by notice terminate an obligation arising under paragraph  89  or
92 .

96.2

The power under sub-paragraph  (1)  is exercisable by giving a notice to each
person—

96.2.a

on whom the obligation is imposed, or

96.2.b

who has benefited or might have expected to benefit from the obligation.

96.3

A reference in sub-paragraph  (1)  to obligations under a paragraph includes a
reference to obligations under that paragraph as applied under paragraph  91
or  94 .

###### Suspension of obligations

97

97.1

Where the Bank is exercising a stabilisation power in respect of a CCP (a “CCP
under resolution”) the Bank may suspend obligations to make a payment, or
delivery, under a contract where one of the parties to the contract is the CCP
under resolution.

97.2

A suspension imposed under sub-paragraph  (1)  does not apply to—

97.2.a

payments of eligible claims, or

97.2.b

payments or deliveries to excluded persons (see paragraph  100 ).

97.3

A suspension imposed under sub-paragraph  (1) —

97.3.a

begins when the instrument providing for the suspension is first published,

97.3.b

must end no later than midnight at the end of the first business day following
the day on which the instrument providing for the suspension is published, and

97.3.c

subject to sub-paragraph  (2) , suspends all obligations to make a payment or
delivery under the contract in question, whether the obligation concerned is
that of the CCP under resolution or of any other party to the contract.

97.4

Where a payment or delivery under the contract concerned first fell due within
the period of the suspension, that payment or delivery is treated as being due
immediately on the expiry of the suspension.

97.5

The power under sub-paragraph  (1)  must be exercised by way of provision in a
share transfer instrument, property transfer instrument, resolution instrument
or third-country instrument.

97.6

The Bank must have regard to the impact a suspension might have on the orderly
functioning of the financial markets before exercising the power in sub-
paragraph  (1) .

97.7

In this paragraph, “ eligible claim ” means a claim in respect of which
compensation is payable under the Financial Services Compensation Scheme.

###### Restriction of security interests

98

98.1

Where the Bank is exercising a stabilisation power in respect of a CCP (a “CCP
under resolution”) the Bank may suspend the rights of a secured creditor of
the CCP to enforce any security interest the creditor has in relation to any
assets of the CCP.

98.2

A suspension under sub-paragraph  (1) —

98.2.a

begins when the instrument providing for the suspension is first published,
and

98.2.b

must end no later than midnight at the end of the first business day following
the day on which that instrument is published.

98.3

But the Bank may not suspend the rights of an excluded person to enforce any
security interest that person may have in relation to any asset of the CCP
under resolution which has been pledged or provided to the excluded person in
question as collateral or as cover for margin.

98.4

The power under sub-paragraph  (1)  must be exercised by way of provision in a
share transfer instrument, property transfer instrument, resolution instrument
or third-country instrument.

98.5

Where the power in sub-paragraph  (1)  is being exercised in a partial
property transfer, the Bank must ensure that any restrictions on the
enforcement of security interests which it imposes under that sub-paragraph
are applied consistently for all CCP group companies in respect of which the
Bank is exercising a stabilisation power.

98.6

The Bank must have regard to the impact a suspension might have on the orderly
functioning of the financial markets before exercising the power in sub-
paragraph  (1) .

98.7

For the purposes of this paragraph, a “ security interest ” means an interest
or right held for the purpose of securing the payment of money or the
performance of any other obligation.

###### Suspension of termination rights

99

99.1

The Bank may suspend the termination right of any party to a qualifying
contract (other than a party who is an excluded person).

99.2

A contract is a “qualifying contract” for the purpose of this paragraph if—

99.2.a

one of the parties to the contract is a CCP in respect of which the Bank is
exercising a stabilisation power (a “CCP under resolution”) and all the
obligations under the contract to make a payment, make delivery or provide
collateral continue to be performed, or

99.2.b

one of the parties to the contract is a subsidiary of a CCP under resolution
and the condition in sub-paragraph  (3)  is met.

99.3

The condition is that—

99.3.a

the obligations of the subsidiary are guaranteed or otherwise supported by the
CCP under resolution,

99.3.b

the termination rights under the contract are triggered by the insolvency or
the financial condition of the CCP under resolution, and

99.3.c

if a property transfer instrument has been made in relation to the CCP under
resolution—

99.3.c.i

all the assets and liabilities relating to the contract have been or are being
transferred to, or assumed by, a single transferee, or

99.3.c.ii

the Bank is providing adequate protection for the performance of the
obligations of the subsidiary under the contract in any other way.

99.4

The Bank must have regard to the impact a suspension might have on the orderly
functioning of the financial markets before exercising the power in sub-
paragraph  (1) .

99.5

The power under sub-paragraph  (1)  must be exercised by way of provision in a
share transfer instrument, property transfer instrument, resolution instrument
or third-country instrument.

99.6

A suspension imposed under sub-paragraph  (1) —

99.6.a

begins when the instrument providing for the suspension is first published,
and

99.6.b

must end no later than midnight at the end of the first business day following
the day on which that instrument is published.

99.7

A person may exercise a termination right under a contract before the expiry
of the suspension if that person is given notice by the Bank that the rights
and liabilities of the CCP under resolution covered by the contract are not—

99.7.a

to be transferred to another undertaking through the exercise of a
stabilisation power, or

99.7.b

to be made subject to a share transfer instrument, property transfer
instrument, resolution instrument or third-country instrument.

99.8

If—

99.8.a

no notice has been given by the Bank under sub-paragraph  (7) , and

99.8.b

a termination right has been triggered otherwise than through the exercise of
a stabilisation power or the imposition of a suspension under sub-paragraph
(1) (or the occurrence of an event directly linked to the exercise of a
stabilisation power),

a person may, on the expiry of the suspension, exercise the termination right
in accordance with the terms of the contract.

99.9

But, where the rights and liabilities of the CCP under resolution or the
subsidiary under the contract have been transferred to another undertaking,
sub-paragraph  (8)  applies only if the event giving rise to the termination
right has been triggered by that undertaking.

99.10

For the purposes of this paragraph, “ termination right ” means—

99.10.a

a right to terminate a contract,

99.10.b

a right to accelerate, close out, set-off or net obligations, or any similar
provision that suspends, modifies or extinguishes an obligation of a party to
the contract, or

99.10.c

a provision that prevents an obligation from arising under the contract.

###### Suspension: general provision

100

For the purposes of paragraphs  97  to  99 —

      “ business day ” means any day other than a Saturday, a Sunday, or a day
which is a bank holiday under the Banking and Financial Dealings Act 1971 in
any part of the United Kingdom;           “ excluded person ” means—         a
person who has been declared to be, or who is an operator of, a designated
system under regulation 4 of the Financial Markets and Insolvency (Settlement
Finality) Regulations 1999 ( S.I. 1999/2979 ),           a CCP,           a
third-country central counterparty (within the meaning given by section 285 of
FSMA 2000), or           a central bank.

###### Stay on terminating membership

101

101.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has made a resolution instrument, share
transfer instrument or a property transfer instrument in relation to a CCP.

101.2

A clearing member of the CCP may not at any time during the relevant period
terminate their membership of the CCP.

101.3

The “ relevant period ” for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (2)  is the period
of 48 hours beginning with the time the instrument in question comes into
force.

101.4

A resolution instrument, share transfer instrument or property transfer
instrument in relation to a CCP may provide for sub-paragraph  (2) —

101.4.a

not to apply in relation to clearing members of the CCP, or

101.4.b

to apply in relation to clearing members of the CCP only to the extent
specified by the Bank in the instrument.

101.5

Provision may be made under sub-paragraph  (4)  only if the Bank considers
that such provision would advance one or more of the special resolution
objectives.

###### Restriction on remuneration

102

102.1

The Bank may restrict or prohibit for a specified period discretionary
payments to specified employees or specified shareholders of a CCP.

102.2

The power under sub-paragraph  (1)  must be exercised by way of provision in a
share transfer instrument, property transfer instrument or resolution
instrument.

102.3

The specified period for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1)  must not exceed 5
years (but this is subject to sub-paragraph  (4) ).

102.4

A provision under sub-paragraph  (1)  restricting or prohibiting discretionary
payments in relation to a CCP ceases to have effect if—

102.4.a

any of the conditions under paragraph  17  cease to be met in relation to the
CCP, and

102.4.b

the Bank is satisfied that following the exercise of any of the stabilisation
powers in relation to the CCP, the CCP has sufficient resources to pay
compensation and repay any public funds in connection with the exercise of
those powers.

102.5

In this paragraph—

      “ discretionary payments ” has the meaning given in paragraph  13 ;
“ specified ” means specified in the instrument under sub-paragraph  (2) .

###### Pensions

103

103.1

This paragraph applies to—

103.1.a

share transfer instruments, and

103.1.b

property transfer instruments.

103.2

An instrument may make provision—

103.2.a

about the consequences of a transfer for a pension scheme;

103.2.b

about property, rights and liabilities of any pension scheme of the CCP.

103.3

In particular, an instrument may—

103.3.a

modify any rights and liabilities,

103.3.b

apportion rights and liabilities, or

103.3.c

transfer property of, or accrued rights in, one pension scheme to another
(with or without consent).

103.4

Provision by virtue of this paragraph may (but need not) amend the terms of a
pension scheme.

103.5

A share or property transfer instrument may make provision in reliance on this
paragraph only with the consent of the Treasury.

103.6

In this paragraph—

103.6.a

“ pension scheme ” includes any arrangement for the payment of pension,
allowances and gratuities, and

103.6.b

a reference to a pension scheme of a CCP is a reference to a scheme in respect
of which the CCP, or a CCP group company, is or was an employer.

###### Disputes

104

104.1

This paragraph applies to—

104.1.a

share transfer instruments,

104.1.b

property transfer instruments,

104.1.c

resolution instruments, and

104.1.d

third-country instruments.

104.2

An instrument may include provision for disputes to be determined in a
specified manner.

104.3

Provision by virtue of sub-paragraph  (2)  may, in particular—

104.3.a

confer jurisdiction on a court or tribunal;

104.3.b

confer discretion on a specified person.

###### Tax

105

105.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision about the fiscal consequences
of the exercise of a stabilisation power.

105.2

Regulations may relate to—

105.2.a

capital gains tax,

105.2.b

corporation tax,

105.2.c

income tax,

105.2.d

inheritance tax,

105.2.e

stamp duty,

105.2.f

stamp duty land tax, or

105.2.g

stamp duty reserve tax.

105.3

Regulations may apply to—

105.3.a

anything done in connection with an instrument,

105.3.b

things transferred or otherwise affected by virtue of an instrument,

105.3.c

a transferor or transferee under an instrument, and

105.3.d

persons otherwise affected by an instrument.

105.4

Regulations may—

105.4.a

modify or disapply an enactment;

105.4.b

provide for an action to have or not have specified consequences;

105.4.c

provide for specified classes of property (including securities), rights or
liabilities to be treated, or not treated, in a specified way;

105.4.d

withdraw or restrict a relief;

105.4.e

extend, restrict or otherwise modify a charge to tax;

105.4.f

provide for matters to be determined by the Treasury in accordance with
provision made by or in accordance with the regulations.

105.5

Regulations may make provision for the fiscal consequences of the exercise of
a stabilisation power in respect of things done—

105.5.a

during the period of three months before the date on which the stabilisation
power is exercised, or

105.5.b

on or after that date.

105.6

In relation to the exercise of a supplemental, onward, bridge or subsequent
instrument under paragraph  49 ,  50 , 52, 66,  67 ,  69 ,  71 ,  73  or  82 ,
in sub-paragraph  (5)(a)  above “ the stabilisation power ” is a reference to
the first stabilisation power in connection with which the supplemental,
onward, bridge or subsequent instrument is made.

105.7

The Treasury may by regulations amend sub-paragraph  (2)  so as to—

105.7.a

add an entry, or

105.7.b

remove an entry.

105.8

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Stay or sist of legal proceedings

106

106.1

This paragraph applies where—

106.1.a

the Bank has exercised a stabilisation power in relation to a CCP or a CCP
group company, and

106.1.b

the CCP or CCP group company is a party to legal proceedings before a court in
the United Kingdom.

106.2

The Bank may apply to that court for a stay or sist of proceedings where the
Bank reasonably considers that a stay or sist of those proceedings is
necessary for an effective application of the stabilisation options or the
stabilisation powers.

###### Insolvency proceedings

107

107.1

This paragraph applies to a CCP if—

107.1.a

a stabilisation power has been exercised in respect of the CCP, or

107.1.b

the conditions in paragraph  17  are met in relation to the CCP.

107.2

Insolvency proceedings may not be commenced in relation to the CCP except by,
or with the consent of, the Bank.

107.3

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (2) , the commencement of insolvency
proceedings means—

107.3.a

making an application for an administration order,

107.3.b

presenting a petition for winding up,

107.3.c

proposing a resolution for voluntary winding up, or

107.3.d

appointing an administrator.

###### Recognition of transferee company

108

108.1

The Bank may provide for a company to which the business of a CCP is
transferred in accordance with paragraph  29(3)  to be treated as a CCP for
the purposes of FSMA 2000—

108.1.a

for a specified period, or

108.1.b

until a specified event occurs.

108.2

The provision may have effect—

108.2.a

for a period specified in the instrument, or

108.2.b

until the occurrence of an event specified or described in the instrument.

108.3

The power under this paragraph—

108.3.a

may be exercised only with the consent of the Treasury, and

108.3.b

must be exercised by way of provision in a property transfer instrument.

###### International obligation notice: general

109

109.1

The Bank may not exercise a stabilisation power in respect of a CCP if the
Treasury notify the Bank that the exercise would be likely to contravene an
international obligation of the United Kingdom.

109.2

A notice under sub-paragraph  (1) —

109.2.a

must be in writing, and

109.2.b

may be withdrawn (generally, partially or conditionally).

109.3

If the Treasury give a notice under sub-paragraph  (1)  the Bank must consider
other exercises of the stabilisation powers with a view to—

109.3.a

pursuing the special resolution objectives, and

109.3.b

avoiding the objections on which the Treasury’s notice was based.

109.4

The Treasury may by notice to the Bank disapply sub-paragraph  (3)  in respect
of a CCP and a notice may be revoked by further notice.

###### International obligation notice: bridge central counterparty

110

110.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has transferred all or part of a CCP’s
business to a bridge central counterparty.

110.2

The Bank must comply with any notice of the Treasury requiring the Bank, for
the purpose of ensuring compliance by the United Kingdom with its
international obligations—

110.2.a

to take specified action under this Schedule in respect of the bridge central
counterparty, or

110.2.b

not to take specified action under this Schedule in respect of the bridge
central counterparty.

110.3

A notice under sub-paragraph  (2) —

110.3.a

must be in writing, and

110.3.b

may be withdrawn (generally, partially or conditionally).

110.4

A notice may include requirements about timing.

###### Public funds: general

111

111.1

The Bank may not exercise a stabilisation power in respect of a CCP without
the Treasury’s consent if the exercise of that power would be likely to have
implications for public funds.

111.2

In sub-paragraph  (1) —

111.2.a

“ public funds ” means the Consolidated Fund and any other account or source
of money which cannot be drawn or spent other than by, or with the authority
of, the Treasury, and

111.2.b

action has implications for public funds if it would or might involve or lead
to a need for the application of public funds.

111.3

The Treasury may by regulations specify considerations which are to be, or not
to be, taken into account in determining whether action has implications for
public funds for the purpose of sub-paragraph  (1) .

111.4

If the Treasury refuse consent under sub-paragraph  (1) , the Bank must
consider other exercises of the stabilisation powers with a view to—

111.4.a

pursuing the special resolution objectives, and

111.4.b

avoiding the objections on which the Treasury’s refusal was based.

111.5

The Treasury may by notice to the Bank disapply sub-paragraph  (4)  in respect
of a CCP; and a notice may be revoked by further notice.

111.6

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the negative procedure.

###### Public funds: bridge central counterparty

112

112.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has transferred all or part of a CCP’s
business to a bridge central counterparty.

112.2

The Bank may not take action in respect of the bridge central counterparty
without the Treasury’s consent if the action would be likely to have
implications for public funds.

112.3

Paragraph  111 (2)  and  (3)  have effect for the purposes of this paragraph.

###### Private sector purchaser: report

113

113.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank sells all or part of a CCP’s business to
a commercial purchaser.

113.2

The Bank must report to the Chancellor of the Exchequer about the exercise of
the power to make share transfer instruments and property transfer instruments
under paragraph  27(2) .

113.3

The report must comply with any requirements as to content specified by the
Treasury.

113.4

The report must be made as soon as is reasonably practicable after the end of
one year beginning with the date of the first transfer instrument made under
paragraph  27(2) .

###### Bridge central counterparty: report

114

114.1

Where the Bank transfers all or part of a CCP’s business to a bridge central
counterparty, the Bank must report to the Chancellor of the Exchequer about
the activities of the bridge central counterparty.

114.2

The first report must be made as soon as is reasonably practicable after the
end of one year beginning with the date of the first transfer to the bridge
central counterparty.

114.3

A report must be made as soon as is reasonably practicable after the end of
each subsequent year.

114.4

The Chancellor of the Exchequer must lay a copy of each report under sub-
paragraph  (2)  or  (3)  before Parliament.

114.5

The Bank must comply with any request of the Treasury for a report dealing
with specified matters in relation to a bridge central counterparty.

114.6

A request under sub-paragraph  (5)  may include provision about—

114.6.a

the content of the report;

114.6.b

timing.

###### Resolution instruments: report

115

115.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank makes one or more resolution instruments
in respect of a CCP.

115.2

The Bank must, on request by the Treasury, report to the Chancellor of the
Exchequer about—

115.2.a

the exercise of the power to make the resolution instrument, and

115.2.b

any other matters in relation to the CCP that the Treasury may specify.

115.3

In relation to the matter specified in sub-paragraph  (2)(a) , the report must
comply with any requirements that the Treasury may specify.

115.4

The Chancellor of the Exchequer must lay a copy of each report under sub-
paragraph  (2)  before Parliament.

###### Transfer of ownership: report

116

116.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank makes one or more share transfer
instruments in respect of a CCP under paragraph  30(2) .

116.2

The Bank must report to the Chancellor of the Exchequer about the exercise of
the power to make share transfer instruments under that paragraph.

116.3

The report must comply with any requirements as to content specified by the
Treasury.

116.4

The report must be made as soon as is reasonably practicable after the end of
one year beginning with the date of the first transfer instrument made under
paragraph  30(2) .

###### Sale to commercial purchaser, transfer to bridge central counterparty and transfer of ownership: conditions for group companies

117

117.1

The Bank may exercise a stabilisation power in respect of a CCP group company
in accordance with paragraph  27(2) ,  29(3)  or  30(2)  if each of the
following conditions is met.

117.2

Condition 1 is that the Bank is satisfied that the general conditions for the
exercise of a stabilisation power set out in paragraph  17  are met in respect
of a CCP in the same group.

117.3

Condition 2 (which does not apply in a financial assistance case) is that the
Bank is satisfied that the exercise of the power in respect of the CCP group
company is necessary, having regard to the public interest in—

117.3.a

the stability of the UK financial system, and

117.3.b

the maintenance of public confidence in the stability of that system.

117.4

Condition 3 (which applies only in a financial assistance case) is that—

117.4.a

the Treasury have recommended the Bank to exercise a stabilisation power on
the grounds that it is necessary to protect the public interest, and

117.4.b

in the Bank’s opinion, exercise of the power in respect of the CCP group
company is an appropriate way to provide that protection.

117.5

Condition 4 is that the CCP group company is an undertaking incorporated in,
or formed under the law of any part of, the United Kingdom.

117.6

Before determining whether Condition 2 or 3 (as appropriate) is met, the Bank
must consult—

117.6.a

the Treasury,

117.6.b

if the CCP is a PRA-authorised person, the PRA, and

117.6.c

the FCA.

117.7

In exercising a stabilisation power in reliance on this paragraph the Bank
must have regard to the need to minimise the effect of the exercise of the
power on other undertakings in the same group.

117.8

In this paragraph “ financial assistance case ” means a case in which the
Treasury notify the Bank that they have provided financial assistance in
respect of a CCP in the same group for the purpose of resolving or reducing a
serious threat to the stability of the UK financial system.

###### Paragraph 

118

118.1

In paragraph  117  references to CCPs includes references to CCP group
companies.

118.2

Where the Bank exercises a stabilisation power in respect of a CCP group
company in reliance on paragraph  117 , the provisions relating to the
stabilisation powers contained in this Schedule (except paragraphs  17  and
19 ) and any other enactment apply (with any necessary modifications) as if
the CCP group company were a CCP.

##### Information, investigation and enforcement

###### Information

119

119.1

This paragraph applies only to information and documents reasonably required
in connection with the exercise by the Bank of functions conferred by or under
this Schedule.

119.2

The Bank may, by notice in writing given to a CCP or CCP group company,
require the CCP or CCP group company—

119.2.a

to provide specified information or information of a specified description, or

119.2.b

to produce specified documents or documents of a specified description.

119.3

The information or documents must be provided or produced—

119.3.a

before the end of such reasonable period as may be specified, and

119.3.b

at such place as may be specified.

119.4

An officer who has written authorisation from the Bank to do so may require a
CCP or CCP group company without delay—

119.4.a

to provide the officer with specified information or information of a
specified description, or

119.4.b

to produce to the officer specified documents or documents of a specified
description.

119.5

The Bank may require any information provided under this paragraph to be
provided in such form as it may reasonably require.

119.6

The Bank may require—

119.6.a

any information provided, whether in a document or otherwise, to be verified
in such manner, or

119.6.b

any document produced to be authenticated in such manner,

as it may reasonably require.

119.7

The powers conferred by sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (4)  may also be exercised
by the Bank to impose requirements on a person who is connected with a CCP.

119.8

“ Officer ” means an officer of the Bank, and includes a member of the Bank’s
staff or an agent of the Bank.

119.9

“ Specified ” means—

119.9.a

in sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (3) , specified in the notice, and

119.9.b

in sub-paragraph  (4) , specified in the authorisation.

119.10

For the purposes of this paragraph, a person is connected with a CCP if that
person is or has at any relevant time been—

119.10.a

a member of that CCP’s group,

119.10.b

a controller of that CCP (within the meaning of section 422 of FSMA 2000), or

119.10.c

in relation to that CCP, a person mentioned in Part 1 of Schedule 15 to FSMA
2000 (reading references in that Part to the authorised person as references
to the CCP).

###### Reports by skilled persons

120

120.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank has required or could require a person
to whom sub-paragraph  (2)  applies (“ the person concerned ”) to provide
information or produce documents with respect to any matter (“the matter
concerned”) under paragraph  119 .

120.2

This sub-paragraph applies to—

120.2.a

a CCP,

120.2.b

a member of a CCP’s group, or

120.2.c

a person who has at any relevant time been a person falling within paragraph
(a)  or  (b) ,

who is, or was at the relevant time, carrying on a business.

120.3

The Bank may either—

120.3.a

by notice in writing given to the person concerned, require that person to
provide the Bank with a report on the matter concerned, or

120.3.b

itself appoint a person to provide the Bank with a report on the matter
concerned.

120.4

When acting under sub-paragraph  (3)(a) , the Bank may require the report to
be in such form as may be specified in the notice.

120.5

The Bank must give notice of an appointment under sub-paragraph  (3)(b)  to
the person concerned.

120.6

The person appointed to make a report—

120.6.a

must be a person appearing to the Bank to have the skills necessary to make a
report on the matter concerned, and

120.6.b

where the appointment is to be made by the person concerned, must be a person
nominated or approved by the Bank.

120.7

It is the duty of—

120.7.a

the person concerned, and

120.7.b

any person who is providing (or who has at any time provided) services to the
person concerned in relation to the matter concerned,

to give the person appointed to prepare a report all such assistance as the
appointed person may reasonably require.

120.8

The obligation imposed by sub-paragraph  (7)  is enforceable, on the
application of the Bank, by an injunction or, in Scotland, by an order for
specific performance under section 45 of the Court of Session Act 1988.

120.9

The Bank may, in relation to an appointment under sub-paragraph  (3)(b) ,
require a CCP to pay to the Bank a fee to cover the expenses incurred by the
Bank in relation to the appointment.

###### Appointment of persons to carry out general investigations

121

121.1

This paragraph applies only for the purposes of the functions of the Bank
conferred by or under this Schedule.

121.2

If it appears to the Bank that there is a good reason for doing so, the Bank
may appoint one or more competent persons to conduct an investigation on its
behalf into—

121.2.a

the nature, conduct or state of the business of a CCP,

121.2.b

a particular aspect of that business, or

121.2.c

the ownership or control of a CCP.

121.3

If a person appointed under sub-paragraph  (2)  thinks it necessary for the
purposes of the investigation, that person may also investigate the business
of a person who is or has at any relevant time been a member of a group of
which the CCP under investigation is part.

121.4

A person appointed under sub-paragraph  (2)  who decides to investigate the
business of any person under sub-paragraph  (3)  must give that person written
notice of that decision.

121.5

In this paragraph, “ business ” includes any part of a business.

###### Appointment of person to carry out investigations in particular cases

122

122.1

This paragraph applies if it appears to the Bank that there are circumstances
suggesting that a person may have failed to comply with any relevant
requirement.

122.2

The Bank may appoint one or more competent persons to conduct an investigation
on its behalf.

122.3

In this paragraph “ relevant requirement ” means a requirement imposed by or
under this Schedule.

###### Investigations etc in support of foreign resolution authorities

123

123.1

On receiving a request to which sub-paragraph  (3)  applies from a foreign
resolution authority, the Bank may—

123.1.a

exercise the power conferred by paragraph  119 , or

123.1.b

appoint one or more competent persons to investigate any matter.

123.2

Accordingly, for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1)(a) , paragraph  119  has
effect as if it also referred to information and documents reasonably required
by the Bank to meet such a request.

123.3

This sub-paragraph applies to a request if the request is made by a foreign
resolution authority in connection with the exercise by that authority of
functions in relation to third-country resolution action (within the meaning
of paragraph  145 ) corresponding to the stabilisation powers of the Bank
under this Schedule.

123.4

An investigator appointed under sub-paragraph  (1)(b)  has the same powers as
an investigator appointed under paragraph  122 .

123.5

In deciding whether or not to exercise its investigative power, the Bank may
take into account in particular—

123.5.a

whether, in the territory of the foreign resolution authority concerned,
corresponding assistance would be given to the Bank,

123.5.b

whether the case concerns the breach of a law, or other requirement, which has
no close parallel in the United Kingdom or involves the assertion of a
jurisdiction not recognised by the United Kingdom,

123.5.c

the seriousness of the case and its importance to persons in the United
Kingdom, and

123.5.d

whether it is otherwise appropriate in the public interest to give the
assistance sought.

123.6

The Bank may decide that it will not exercise its investigative power unless
the foreign resolution authority undertakes to make such contribution towards
the cost of its exercise as the Bank considers appropriate.

123.7

“ Foreign resolution authority ” means an authority, in a country or territory
outside the United Kingdom, which exercises functions referred to in sub-
paragraph  (3) .

123.8

“ Investigative power ” means one of the powers mentioned in sub-paragraph
(1) .

###### Investigations: general

124

124.1

This paragraph applies if the Bank appoints one or more competent persons
(“investigators”) under paragraph  121  or  122  to conduct an investigation
on its behalf.

124.2

The Bank must give written notice of the appointment of an investigator to the
person who is the subject of the investigation (“the person under
investigation”).

124.3

A notice under sub-paragraph  (2)  must—

124.3.a

specify the provisions under which, and as a result of which, the investigator
was appointed, and

124.3.b

state the reason for the investigator’s appointment.

124.4

Nothing prevents the Bank from appointing a person who is a member of its
staff as an investigator.

124.5

An investigator must make a report of the investigation to the Bank.

124.6

The Bank may, by a direction to an investigator, control—

124.6.a

the scope of the investigation,

124.6.b

the period during which the investigation is to be conducted,

124.6.c

the conduct of the investigation, and

124.6.d

the reporting of the investigation.

124.7

A direction may, in particular—

124.7.a

confine the investigation to particular matters;

124.7.b

extend the investigation to additional matters;

124.7.c

require the investigator to discontinue the investigation or to take only such
steps as are specified in the direction;

124.7.d

require the investigator to make such interim reports as are so specified.

124.8

If there is a change in the scope or conduct of the investigation and, in the
opinion of the Bank, the person under investigation is likely to be
significantly prejudiced by not being made aware of it, that person must be
given written notice of the change.

124.9

If the appointment is under paragraph  122 , sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (8)  do
not apply if the Bank believes that the notice required by the sub-paragraph
in question would be likely to result in the investigation being frustrated.

###### Powers of persons appointed under paragraph 

125

125.1

This paragraph applies to an investigator appointed under paragraph  121  to
conduct an investigation on behalf of the Bank.

125.2

The investigator may require the person who is the subject of the
investigation (“the person under investigation”) or any person connected with
the person under investigation—

125.2.a

to attend before the investigator at a specified time and place and answer
