questions, or

125.2.b

otherwise to provide such information as the investigator may require for the
purposes of the investigation.

125.3

The investigator may also require any person to produce at a specified time
and place any specified documents or documents of a specified description.

125.4

A requirement under sub-paragraph  (2)  or  (3)  may be imposed only so far as
the investigator reasonably considers the question, provision of information
or production of the document to be relevant to the purposes of the
investigation.

125.5

For the purposes of this paragraph, a person (“ B ”) is connected with the
person under investigation (“ A ”) if B is or has at any relevant time been—

125.5.a

a member of A’s group;

125.5.b

a controller of A;

125.5.c

in relation to A, a person mentioned in Part 1 or 2 of Schedule 15 to FSMA
2000 (reading references in those Parts to the authorised person or the person
under investigation as references to A).

125.6

In this paragraph—

      “ controller ” has the meaning given in section 422 of FSMA 2000;
“ specified ” means specified in a notice in writing.

###### Powers of persons appointed as a result of paragraph 

126

126.1

This paragraph applies to an investigator appointed under paragraph  122  to
conduct an investigation on behalf of the Bank.

126.2

The investigator has—

126.2.a

the powers conferred by paragraph  125  on an investigator appointed under
paragraph  121 , and

126.2.b

the powers conferred by sub-paragraphs  (3)  and  (4) .

126.3

The investigator may require the person who is the subject of the
investigation (“the person under investigation”) to give the investigator all
assistance in connection with the investigation which that person is
reasonably able to give.

126.4

The investigator may require a person who is neither the person under
investigation nor a person connected with the person under investigation—

126.4.a

to attend before the investigator at a specified time and place and answer
questions, or

126.4.b

otherwise to provide such information as the investigator may require for the
purposes of the investigation.

126.5

A requirement may only be imposed under sub-paragraph  (4)  if the
investigator is satisfied that the requirement is necessary or expedient for
the purposes of the investigation.

126.6

Paragraph  125 (5)  and  (6)  applies for the purposes of this paragraph.

###### Admissibility of statements made to investigators

127

127.1

A statement made to an investigator appointed under paragraph  121  or  122
by a person in compliance with an information requirement is admissible in
evidence in any proceedings, so long as it also complies with any requirement
governing the admissibility of evidence in the circumstances in question.

127.2

But in criminal proceedings in which that person is charged with an offence to
which this sub-paragraph applies—

127.2.a

no evidence relating to the statement may be adduced, and

127.2.b

no question relating to it may be asked—

by or on behalf of the prosecution, or the Bank (as the case may be), unless
evidence relating to it is adduced, or a question relating to it is asked, in
the proceedings by or on behalf of that person.

127.3

Sub-paragraph  (2)  applies to any offence other than one under—

127.3.a

paragraph  132 ,

127.3.b

section 398 of FSMA 2000 (misleading FCA or PRA: residual cases),

127.3.c

section 5 of the Perjury Act 1911 (false statements made otherwise than on
oath),

127.3.d

section 44(2) of the Criminal Law (Consolidation) (Scotland) Act 1995 (false
statements made otherwise than on oath), or

127.3.e

Article 10 of the Perjury (Northern Ireland) Order 1979 (false declarations
etc).

127.4

“ Information requirement ” means a requirement imposed by an investigator
under paragraph  125 ,  126  or  128 .

###### Information and documents: supplemental provision

128

128.1

If the Bank has power under this Schedule to require a person to produce a
document but if it appears that the document is in the possession of a third
person, that power may be exercised in relation to the third person.

128.2

If a document is produced in response to a requirement imposed under this
Schedule, the person to whom it is produced may—

128.2.a

take copies or extracts from the document, or

128.2.b

require the person producing the document, or any relevant person to provide
an explanation of the document.

128.3

A document so produced may be retained for so long as the person to whom it is
produced considers that it is necessary to retain it (rather than copies of
it) for the purposes for which the document was requested.

128.4

If the person to whom a document is so produced has reasonable grounds for
believing—

128.4.a

that the document may have to be produced for the purposes of any legal
proceedings, and

128.4.b

that it might otherwise be unavailable for those purposes,

it may be retained until the proceedings are concluded.

128.5

If a person who is required under this Schedule to produce a document fails to
do so, the Bank or an investigator may require that person to state, to the
best of that person’s knowledge and belief, where the document is.

128.6

A lawyer may be required under this Schedule to furnish the name and address
of the lawyer’s client.

128.7

No person may be required under this Schedule to disclose information or
produce a document in respect of which the person (“ A ”) owes an obligation
of confidence unless—

128.7.a

A is the person under investigation or a member of that person’s group,

128.7.b

the person to whom the obligation of confidence is owed is the person under
investigation or a member of that person’s group,

128.7.c

the person to whom the obligation of confidence is owed consents to the
disclosure or production, or

128.7.d

the imposing on A of a requirement with respect to such information or
document has been specifically authorised by the Bank.

128.8

If a person claims a lien on a document, its production under this Schedule
does not affect the lien.

128.9

In this paragraph—

      “ controller ” has the meaning given by section 422 of FSMA 2000;
“ investigator ” means a person appointed under paragraph  121  or  122 ;
“ relevant person ”, in relation to a person who is required to produce a
document, means a person who—         has been or is or is proposed to be a
director or controller of that person,           has been or is an auditor of
that person,           has been or is an actuary, accountant or lawyer
appointed or instructed by that person, or           has been or is an
employee of that person.

###### Protected items

129

129.1

A person may not be required under this Schedule to produce, disclose or
permit the inspection of protected items.

129.2

“ Protected items ” means—

129.2.a

communications between a professional legal adviser and that adviser’s client
or any person representing such a client which fall within sub-paragraph  (3)
,

129.2.b

communications between a professional legal adviser, that adviser’s client or
any person representing such a client and any other person which fall within
sub-paragraph  (3)  (as a result of paragraph  (b)  of that sub-paragraph),
and

129.2.c

items which—

129.2.c.i

are enclosed with, or referred to in, such communications,

129.2.c.ii

fall within sub-paragraph  (3) , and

129.2.c.iii

are in the possession of a person entitled to be in possession of them.

129.3

A communication or item falls within this sub-paragraph if it is made—

129.3.a

in connection with the giving of legal advice to the client, or

129.3.b

in connection with, or in contemplation of, legal proceedings and for the
purposes of those proceedings.

129.4

A communication or item is not a protected item if it is held with the
intention of furthering a criminal purpose.

###### Entry of premises under warrant

130

130.1

A justice of the peace may issue a warrant under this paragraph if satisfied
on information on oath given by or on behalf of the Secretary of State, the
Bank or an investigator that there are reasonable grounds for believing that
the first, second or third set of conditions is satisfied.

130.2

The first set of conditions is—

130.2.a

that a person on whom an information requirement has been imposed has failed
(wholly or in part) to comply with it, and

130.2.b

that on the premises specified in the warrant—

130.2.b.i

there are documents which have been required, or

130.2.b.ii

there is information which has been required.

130.3

The second set of conditions is—

130.3.a

that the premises specified in the warrant are premises of a CCP or a member
of the same group as a CCP,

130.3.b

that there are on the premises documents or information in relation to which
an information requirement could be imposed, and

130.3.c

that if such a requirement were to be imposed—

130.3.c.i

it would not be complied with, or

130.3.c.ii

the documents or information to which it related would be removed, tampered
with or destroyed.

130.4

The third set of conditions is—

130.4.a

that an offence mentioned in paragraph  132  has been (or is being) committed
by any person,

130.4.b

that there are on the premises specified in the warrant documents or
information relevant to whether that offence has been (or is being) committed,

130.4.c

that an information requirement could be imposed in relation to those
documents or that information, and

130.4.d

that if such a requirement were to be imposed—

130.4.d.i

it would not be complied with, or

130.4.d.ii

the documents or information to which it related would be removed, tampered
with or destroyed.

130.5

A warrant under this paragraph authorises a constable—

130.5.a

to enter the premises specified in the warrant,

130.5.b

to search the premises and take possession of any documents or information
appearing to be documents or information of a kind in respect of which a
warrant under this paragraph was issued (“ the relevant kind ”) or to take, in
relation to any such documents or information, any such steps which may appear
to be necessary for preserving them or preventing interference with them,

130.5.c

to take copies of, or extracts from, any documents or information appearing to
be of the relevant kind,

130.5.d

to require any person on the premises to provide an explanation of any
document or information appearing to be of the relevant kind or to state where
it may be found, and

130.5.e

to use such force as may be reasonably necessary.

130.6

A warrant under this paragraph may be executed by any constable.

130.7

The warrant may authorise persons to accompany any constable who is executing
it.

130.8

The powers in sub-paragraph  (5)  may be exercised by a person authorised by
the warrant to accompany a constable; but that person may exercise those
powers only in the company of, and under the supervision of, a constable.

130.9

In England and Wales, sections 15(5) to (8) and 16(3) to (12) of the Police
and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 (execution of search warrants and safeguards)
apply to warrants issued under this paragraph.

130.10

In Northern Ireland, Articles 17(5) to (8) and 18(3) to (12) of the Police and
Criminal Evidence (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 apply to warrants issued under
this paragraph.

130.11

In the application of this paragraph to Northern Ireland the reference to a
justice of the peace is a reference to a lay magistrate.

130.12

In the application of this paragraph to Scotland—

130.12.a

for the reference to a justice of the peace substitute references to a justice
of the peace or a sheriff, and

130.12.b

for the references to information on oath substitute references to evidence on
oath.

130.13

“ Investigator ” means an investigator appointed under paragraph  121  or  122
.

130.14

“ Information requirement ” means a requirement imposed—

130.14.a

by the Bank under paragraph  119  or  128 , or

130.14.b

by an investigator under paragraph  125 ,  126  or  128 .

###### Retention of documents obtained under paragraph 

131

131.1

Any document of which possession is taken under paragraph  130  (“a seized
document”) may be retained for so long as it is necessary to retain it (rather
than copies of it) in the circumstances.

131.2

A person claiming to be the owner of a seized document may apply to a
magistrates’ court, or in Scotland the sheriff, for an order for the delivery
of the document to the person appearing to the court or sheriff to be the
owner.

131.3

If on an application under sub-paragraph  (2)  the court, or in Scotland the
sheriff, cannot ascertain who is the owner of the seized document the court or
sheriff (as the case may be) may make such order as the court or sheriff
thinks fit.

131.4

An order under sub-paragraph  (2)  or  (3)  does not affect the right of any
person to take legal proceedings against any person in possession of a seized
document for the recovery of the document.

131.5

Any right to bring proceedings (as described in sub-paragraph  (4) ) may only
be exercised within 6 months of the date of the order made under sub-paragraph
(2)  or  (3) .

###### Offences etc

132

132.1

If a person other than the investigator (“ the defaulter ”) fails to comply
with a requirement imposed on the defaulter under paragraph  125 ,  126  or
128 , the person imposing the requirement may certify that fact in writing to
the court.

132.2

If the court is satisfied that the defaulter has failed without reasonable
excuse to comply with the requirement, it may deal with the defaulter (and, in
the case of a body corporate, any director or other officer) as if that person
were in contempt.

132.3

“ Officer ”, in relation to a limited liability partnership, means a member of
the limited liability partnership.

132.4

A person who knows or suspects that an investigation is being or is likely to
be conducted under paragraph  121 ,  122  or  123  is guilty of an offence if—

132.4.a

that person falsifies, conceals, destroys or otherwise disposes of a document
which that person knows or suspects is or would be relevant to such an
investigation, or

132.4.b

that person causes or permits the falsification, concealment, destruction or
disposal of such a document,

unless that person shows that that person had no intention of concealing facts
disclosed by the document from the investigator.

132.5

A person who, in purported compliance with a requirement imposed on that
person by any relevant requirement—

132.5.a

provides information which that person knows to be false or misleading in a
material particular, or

132.5.b

recklessly provides information which is false or misleading in a material
particular,

is guilty of an offence.

132.6

Any person who intentionally obstructs the exercise of any rights conferred by
a warrant under paragraph  130  is guilty of an offence.

132.7

A person guilty of an offence under sub-paragraph  (4) ,  (5)  or  (6)  is
liable, on summary conviction—

132.7.a

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 3 months or a
fine, or both;

132.7.b

In Scotland and Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 3
months or a fine not exceeding level 5 on the standard scale, or both.

132.8

In this paragraph—

      “ court ” means—         the High Court,           in Scotland, the
Court of Session;                 “ relevant requirement ” has the meaning
given in paragraph  122 .

###### Prosecution of offences under paragraph 

133

133.1

Proceedings for an offence under paragraph  132  may be instituted—

133.1.a

in England and Wales, only by the Bank or by or with the consent of the
Director of Public Prosecutions, and

133.1.b

in Northern Ireland, only by the Bank or by or with the consent of the
Director of Public Prosecutions for Northern Ireland.

133.2

In exercising its power to institute proceedings for an offence under
paragraph  132 , the Bank must comply with any conditions or restrictions
imposed in writing by the Treasury.

133.3

Conditions or restrictions may be imposed under sub-paragraph  (2)  in
relation to proceedings generally, or such proceedings or categories of
proceedings as the Treasury may direct.

###### Offences under paragraph 

134

134.1

If an offence under paragraph  132  committed by a body corporate is shown—

134.1.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of an officer, or

134.1.b

to be attributable to any neglect on the part of an officer,

the officer as well as the body corporate is guilty of the offence and liable
to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

134.2

If the affairs of a body corporate are managed by its members, sub-paragraph
(1)  applies in relation to the acts and defaults of a member in connection
with that member’s functions of management as if that member were a director
of the body.

134.3

If an offence under paragraph  132  committed by a partnership is shown—

134.3.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of a partner, or

134.3.b

to be attributable to any neglect on the part of a partner,

the partner as well as the body corporate is guilty of the offence and liable
to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

134.4

In sub-paragraph  (3)  “ partner ” includes a person purporting to act as
partner.

134.5

“ Officer ” in relation to a body corporate means—

134.5.a

a director, member of the committee of management, chief executive, manager,
secretary or other similar officer of the body, or a person purporting to act
in any such capacity, and

134.5.b

an individual who is a controller of the body (and for these purposes, “
controller ” has the meaning given in section 422 of FSMA 2000).

134.6

If an offence under paragraph  132  committed by an unincorporated association
(other than a partnership) is shown—

134.6.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of an officer of the
association or a member of its governing body, or

134.6.b

to be attributable to any neglect on the part of such an officer or member,

the officer or member as well as the association is guilty of the offence and
liable to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

###### Injunctions to prevent failure to comply with relevant requirement

135

135.1

If, on the application of the Bank, the court is satisfied that there is a
reasonable likelihood that any person will contravene a relevant requirement,
the court may make an order restraining, or in Scotland an interdict
prohibiting, the contravention.

135.2

The jurisdiction conferred by this paragraph is exercisable—

135.2.a

in England and Wales, and Northern Ireland, by the High Court, and

135.2.b

in Scotland, by the Court of Session.

135.3

In this paragraph “ relevant requirement ” has the meaning given in paragraph
122 .

###### Regulatory sanctions

136

136.1

If the Bank considers that a person has failed to comply with a relevant
requirement imposed on the person, it may do one or more of the following—

136.1.a

publish a statement to that effect;

136.1.b

impose on that person a penalty, in respect of the failure, of such amount as
it considers appropriate;

136.1.c

with a view to ensuring that the failure ceases or is not repeated or the
consequences of the failure are mitigated, direct that person to refrain from
any conduct;

136.1.d

prohibit that person from holding an office or position involving
responsibility for taking decisions about the management of—

136.1.d.i

a named CCP,

136.1.d.ii

a CCP of a specified description, or

136.1.d.iii

any CCP.

136.2

A prohibition under sub-paragraph  (1)(d) may apply—

136.2.a

for a specified period,

136.2.b

until further notice, or

136.2.c

permanently.

136.3

If the Bank considers that a failure by a person to comply with a relevant
requirement occurred with the consent or connivance of, or was attributable to
any neglect on the part of, an officer of that person, it may do one or more
of the following—

136.3.a

publish a statement to that effect;

136.3.b

impose on that officer a penalty, in respect of the failure, of such amount as
it considers appropriate;

136.3.c

with a view to ensuring that the failure ceases or is not repeated or the
consequences of the failure are mitigated, direct that person to refrain from
any conduct specified in the direction.

136.4

A penalty under this paragraph—

136.4.a

must be paid to the Bank, and

136.4.b

may be enforced by the Bank as a debt.

136.5

In this paragraph “ relevant requirement ” has the meaning given in paragraph
122 .

###### Determination of sanctions

137

When determining the type of sanction, and level of any penalty, to be imposed
on a person under paragraph  136 , the Bank must take into account all
relevant circumstances, including where appropriate—

137.a

the gravity and the duration of the failure,

137.b

the degree of responsibility of the person,

137.c

the financial strength of the person,

137.d

the amount of profits gained or losses avoided by the person,

137.e

the losses for third parties caused by the failure,

137.f

the level of co-operation of the person with the Bank,

137.g

previous failures by the person, and

137.h

any potential systemic consequences of the failure.

###### Procedure: warning notice

138

138.1

If the Bank proposes to impose a sanction on a person under paragraph  136(1)
or  (3)  it must give that person a warning notice.

138.2

Section 387 of FSMA 2000 applies in relation to a warning notice given under
sub-paragraph  (1)  and to the Bank as it applies in relation to a warning
notice given under that Act and to the regulator which gave that notice,
subject to sub-paragraphs  (3)  and  (4) .

138.3

In complying with section 387(1)(a) of that Act, a warning notice must in
particular—

138.3.a

if it is about a proposal to publish a statement, set out the terms of the
statement,

138.3.b

if it is about a proposal to impose a penalty, specify the amount of the
penalty,

138.3.c

if it is about a proposal to direct a person to refrain from certain conduct,
specify the conduct, and

138.3.d

if it is about a proposal to impose a prohibition on holding an office or
other position, specify the extent of the prohibition.

138.4

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (2) , section 387 of that Act has effect as
if subsections (1A) and (3A) were omitted.

###### Procedure: decision notice

139

139.1

If the Bank decides to impose a sanction on a person under paragraph  136(1)
or  (3)  it must without delay give that person a decision notice.

139.2

If the decision is to publish a statement, the decision notice must set out
the terms of the statement.

139.3

If the decision is to impose a penalty, the decision notice must specify the
amount of the penalty.

139.4

If the decision is to refrain from certain conduct, the decision notice must
specify the conduct.

139.5

If the decision is to impose a prohibition on holding an office or other
position, the decision notice must specify the extent of the prohibition.

139.6

Section 388 of FSMA 2000 applies in relation to a decision notice given under
sub-paragraph  (1)  and the Bank as it applies in relation to a decision
notice given under that Act and the regulator which gave that notice, subject
to sub-paragraph  (7) .

139.7

Section 388 of that Act has effect for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (6)  as
if—

139.7.a

in subsection (1)(e)(i) for “this Act” there were substituted  “paragraph  141
of Schedule 11 to the Financial Services and Markets Act 2023” , and

139.7.b

subsections (1A) and (2) were omitted.

###### Procedure: general

140

140.1

Sections 389, 390 and 392 to 394 of FSMA 2000 apply in relation to a warning
notice given under paragraph  138 , a decision notice given under paragraph
139  and the Bank as they apply in relation to a warning notice or decision
notice given under that Act and the regulator which gave that notice, subject
to sub-paragraphs  (2)  to  (4) .

140.2

Section 389 of that Act has effect as if subsection (2) were omitted.

140.3

Section 390 has effect as if—

140.3.a

in subsection (2A), in paragraph (a), for “133(6)(b)” there were substituted
“133(5)(b)” ,

140.3.b

in that paragraph, for “133(6)” there were substituted  “133(5)” ,

140.3.c

for subsection (4) there were substituted—

140.3.c.4

A final notice about a direction under paragraph  136(1)(c)  or  (3)(c)  of
Schedule 11 to the Financial Services and Markets Act 2023 or a prohibition
under paragraph  136(1)(d)  of that Schedule must—

140.3.c.4.a

specify the conduct to which the direction relates or the extent of the
prohibition, and

140.3.c.4.b

give details of the date on which the direction or prohibition has effect.

140.4

Section 392 has effect as if for paragraphs (a) and (b) there were
substituted—

140.4.a

a warning notice given under paragraph  138  of Schedule 11 to the Financial
Services and Markets Act 2023;

140.4.b

a decision notice given under paragraph  139  of Schedule 11 to the Financial
Services and Markets Act 2023.

###### Appeals

141

141.1

If the Bank decides to impose a sanction on a person under paragraph  136 ,
the person may appeal to the Upper Tribunal.

141.2

The Bank may not impose a sanction while an appeal under this paragraph could
be brought or is pending.

###### Injunctions: failure to comply with certain paragraph 

142

142.1

If, on the application of the Bank, the court is satisfied—

142.1.a

that there is a reasonable likelihood that there will be a compliance failure,
or

142.1.b

that there has been a compliance failure and there is a reasonable likelihood
that it will continue or be repeated,

the court may make an order restraining the conduct constituting the failure.

142.2

If, on the application of the Bank, the court is satisfied—

142.2.a

that there has been a compliance failure, and

142.2.b

that there are steps which could be taken for remedying the failure,

the court may make an order requiring anyone who appears to have been
knowingly concerned in the failure to take such steps as the court may direct
to remedy it.

142.3

If, on the application of the Bank, the court is satisfied—

142.3.a

that there may have been a compliance failure by any person, or

142.3.b

that a person may have been knowingly concerned in a compliance failure,

the court may make an order restraining that person from dealing with any
assets which it is satisfied the person is reasonably likely to deal with.

142.4

“ Compliance failure ” means—

142.4.a

a failure to comply with a direction under paragraph  136(1)(c)  or  (3)(c) ,
or

142.4.b

a breach of a prohibition imposed under paragraph  136(1)(d) .

142.5

The jurisdiction conferred by this paragraph is exercisable—

142.5.a

in England and Wales and Northern Ireland, by the High Court, and

142.5.b

in Scotland, by the Court of Session.

142.6

In this paragraph—

142.6.a

references to an order restraining anything are, in Scotland, to be read as
references to an interdict prohibiting that thing,

142.6.b

references to an order requiring steps to be taken are, in Scotland, to be
read as references to an order for specific performance under section 45 of
the Court of Session Act 1988,

142.6.c

references to remedying a failure include mitigating its effect, and

142.6.d

references to dealing with assets include disposing of them.

###### Publication

143

143.1

In the case of a warning notice under paragraph  138 —

143.1.a

neither the Bank nor a person to whom it is given or copied may publish the
notice,

143.1.b

a person to whom the notice is given or copied may not publish any details
concerning the notice unless the Bank has published those details, and

143.1.c

after consulting the persons to whom the notice is given or copied, the Bank
may publish such information about the matter to which the notice relates as
it considers appropriate.

143.2

A person to whom a decision notice under paragraph  139  is given or copied
may not publish the notice or any details concerning it unless the Bank has
published the notice or those details.

143.3

A notice of discontinuance must state that, if the person to whom the notice
is given consents, the Bank may publish such information as it considers
appropriate about the matter to which the discontinued proceedings related.

143.4

A copy of a notice of discontinuance must be accompanied by a statement that,
if the person to whom the notice is copied consents, the Bank may publish such
information as it considers appropriate about the matter to which the
discontinued proceedings related, so far as relevant to that person.

143.5

Subject to sub-paragraph  (8) , where the Bank gives a decision notice it may
publish such information about the matter to which the notice relates as it
considers appropriate.

143.6

Where the Bank publishes information under sub-paragraph  (5)  and the person
to whom the decision notice is given refers the matter to the Upper Tribunal,
the Bank must, without undue delay, publish on its website information about
the status of the appeal and its outcome.

143.7

Subject to sub-paragraph  (8) , where the Bank gives a final notice—

143.7.a

it must, without undue delay, publish details of any sanction to which the
notice relates on its website, and

143.7.b

it may publish such other information about the matter to which the notice
relates as it considers appropriate.

143.8

Information about a matter to which a decision notice or a final notice
relates must be published anonymously where—

143.8.a

the sanction is imposed (or proposed to be imposed) on an individual and
following an obligatory prior assessment publication of personal data is found
to be disproportionate, or

143.8.b

were it not published anonymously, publication would—

143.8.b.i

jeopardise the stability of financial markets or an ongoing criminal
investigation, or

143.8.b.ii

cause, in so far as it can be determined, disproportionate damage to the
persons involved.

143.9

Where sub-paragraph  (8)  applies, the person publishing the information may
make such arrangements as to the publication of information (including as to
the timing of publication) as are necessary to preserve the anonymity of the
person on whom the sanction is imposed.

143.10

Where the Bank publishes information in accordance with sub-paragraphs  (6)
to  (9) , it must ensure the information remains on its website for at least
five years, unless the information is personal data and the data protection
legislation requires the information to be retained for a different period.

143.11

In this paragraph—

      “ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act);           “ notice of
discontinuance ” and “ final notice ” have the same meaning as in sections 389
and 390 of FSMA 2000 (which are applied (with modifications) by paragraph  140
).

###### Co-operation

144

In connection with the exercise of its powers to impose sanctions under
paragraph  136 , the Bank must take such steps as it considers appropriate to
co-operate with—

144.a

the FCA, and

144.b

any person who exercises functions outside the United Kingdom equivalent to
those exercisable by the Bank under this Schedule.

##### Third-country resolution actions

###### Third-country resolution actions

145

145.1

This paragraph applies where the Bank is notified of third-country resolution
action in respect of a third-country central counterparty.

145.2

The Bank must make an instrument which—

145.2.a

recognises the action,

145.2.b

refuses to recognise the action, or

145.2.c

recognises part of the action and refuses to recognise the remainder.

An instrument within paragraph  (a) ,  (b)  or  (c)  is a “ third-country
instrument ” (as is an instrument under paragraph  146 ).

145.3

The Bank may only make a decision under sub-paragraph  (2)  with the approval
of the Treasury.

145.4

Recognition of the action (or a part of it) may be refused only if the Bank
and the Treasury are satisfied that one or more of the following conditions
are satisfied—

145.4.a

recognition would have an adverse effect on financial stability in the United
Kingdom;

145.4.b

under the third-country resolution action creditors (including in particular
clearing members) located or payable in the United Kingdom would not, by
reason of being located or payable in the United Kingdom, receive the same
treatment as creditors who are located or payable in the country concerned and
have similar legal rights;

145.4.c

recognition of, and taking action in support of, the third-country resolution
action (or the part) would have material fiscal implications for the United
Kingdom;

145.4.d

recognition would be unlawful under section 6 of the Human Rights Act 1998
(public authority not to act contrary to Human Rights Convention).

145.5

The recognition of a third-country resolution action (or any part of it) is
without prejudice to any normal insolvency proceedings.

145.6

In this paragraph—

      “ third-country central counterparty ” has the meaning given by section
285 of FSMA 2000;           “ third-country resolution action ” means action
under the law of a country or territory outside the United Kingdom to manage
the failure or likely failure of a third-country central counterparty—
the anticipated results of which are, in relation to a third-country central
counterparty, broadly comparable to results which could have been anticipated
from the exercise of a stabilisation option in relation to an entity in the
United Kingdom corresponding to the third-country central counterparty, and
the objectives of which are broadly comparable, in relation to the country or
territory concerned, to the special resolution objectives in paragraph  15  as
they apply in relation to the United Kingdom.

###### Effects of recognition on third-country resolution action

146

146.1

This paragraph applies where an instrument under paragraph  145  recognises
any third-country resolution action (or a part of it).

146.2

The third-country resolution action (or part) produces the same legal effects
in any part of the United Kingdom as it would have produced had it been made
(with due authority) under the law of that part of the United Kingdom.

146.3

For the purposes of supporting, or giving full effect to, the third-county
resolution action (or the part), the Bank may exercise, in relation to a
third-country central counterparty, one or more of the stabilisation options,
or one or more of the stabilisation powers, available to the Bank in relation
to a similar entity in the United Kingdom.

146.4

But, for the purposes of exercising a power by virtue of sub-paragraph  (3) ,
provision which could otherwise be made under this Schedule in a share
transfer instrument, property transfer instrument or resolution instrument may
instead be made in—

146.4.a

the instrument made under paragraph  145  recognising the third-country
resolution action (or part), or

146.4.b

a further instrument made by the Bank under this paragraph.

An instrument under paragraph  (b)  is a “ third-country instrument ” (as is
an instrument under paragraph  145(2)(a) ,  (b)  or  (c) ).

146.5

This Schedule (other than this paragraph) applies in relation to the exercise
of any power by virtue of sub-paragraph  (3) , subject to sub-paragraphs  (6)
and  (7)  and any other necessary modifications.

146.6

Paragraph  15  (special resolution objectives) has effect as if after sub-
paragraph (7) there were inserted—

146.6.7A

Objective 6 is to support third-country resolution action with a view to
promoting objectives which, in relation to the country or territory concerned,
correspond to Objectives 1 to 5 in relation to the United Kingdom.

146.7

Paragraphs  17  to  19  do not apply.

146.8

Paragraph  145(6)  applies for the purposes of this paragraph.

###### Third-country instruments: supplementary provision

147

147.1

Paragraph  47  (incidental provision) applies to a third-country instrument as
it applies to a share transfer instrument.

147.2

Paragraph  48  (procedure: instruments) applies to a third-country instrument
as it applies to a share transfer instrument, except that references in that
paragraph to the CCP are to be read as references to the third-country central
counterparty to which the third-country instrument relates.

147.3

Paragraph  109  (international obligation notice: general) applies in relation
to the making of a third-country instrument under paragraph  145  or  146  as
it applies in relation to the exercise of a stabilisation power, except that—

147.3.a

for the purposes of paragraph  109(3) , paragraph 15 is to be read subject to
the modification in paragraph  146(6) , and

147.3.b

in sub-paragraph (4), the reference to a CCP is to be read as a reference to a
third-country central counterparty in respect of which a third-country
instrument is made.

147.4

Paragraph  110  (international obligation notice: bridge central counterparty)
applies where the Bank has, by virtue of paragraph  146 , transferred all or
part of the business of a third-country central counterparty to a bridge
central counterparty as it applies where the Bank has transferred all or part
of the business of a CCP to a bridge central counterparty.

147.5

Paragraph  145(6)  applies for the purposes of this paragraph.

##### General

###### Information

148

148.1

The Bank may disclose information that it thinks relevant to the financial
stability of—

148.1.a

individual CCPs, or

148.1.b

one or more aspects of the UK financial system.

148.2

Information about the business or other affairs of a specified or identifiable
person may be disclosed under sub-paragraph  (1)  only to—

148.2.a

the Treasury;

148.2.b

the FCA;

148.2.c

the scheme manager of the Financial Services Compensation Scheme (established
under Part 15 of FSMA 2000);

148.2.d

the Payment Systems Regulator (established under section 40 of the Financial
Services (Banking Reform) Act 2013);

148.2.e

an authority in a country or territory outside the United Kingdom which
exercises functions similar to those of the Treasury, the Bank, the PRA or the
FCA in relation to financial stability.

148.3

Except as provided by sub-paragraph  (4) , the disclosure of information under
this paragraph does not breach—

148.3.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

148.3.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

148.4

This paragraph does not authorise a disclosure of information if the
disclosure would contravene the data protection legislation (but in
determining whether a disclosure would do so, take into account the duties
imposed by this paragraph).

148.5

In this paragraph “ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as
in the Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act).

Sections 348, 349, 352 and 353 of FSMA 2000 (disclosure of information) apply

in subsection (5)—

the Financial Services and Markets Act 2023 (reports by skilled persons);

149.2.c.i.cb

a person appointed to act as a temporary manager under paragraph  6  of
Schedule 11 to the Financial Services and Markets Act 2023,

149.2.c.ii

in paragraph (e) for “to (c)” there were substituted  “to (cb)” , and

149.2.d

after subsection (6)(b) there were inserted—

149.2.d.c

a competent person appointed by the Bank of England under Part 6 of Schedule
11 to the Financial Services and Markets Act 2023.

149.3

PRA” there were substituted  “the PRA or the Bank of England” .

###### Remedies on judicial review

150

150.1

Where an application is made for judicial review of a decision of the Bank to
exercise the stabilisation powers in relation to a CCP or CCP group company
(“relevant proceedings”)—

150.1.a

a ruling by the court that the decision is unlawful does not affect a relevant
transfer or a relevant provision in a stabilisation instrument made by the
Bank pursuant to that decision, and

150.1.b

the court may not quash any provision in a stabilisation instrument made by
the Bank if that provision makes a relevant transfer or a relevant provision.

150.2

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1) —

150.2.a

“ stabilisation instrument ” means—

150.2.a.i

a share transfer instrument,

150.2.a.ii

a property transfer instrument, or

150.2.a.iii

a resolution instrument;

150.2.b

a “relevant provision” in a stabilisation instrument means—

150.2.b.i

in relation to a tear-up instrument, provision under paragraph  31(2) ,

150.2.b.ii

in relation to a cash call instrument, provision under paragraph  32(2) ,

150.2.b.iii

in relation to a variation instrument, provision under paragraph  33(2) ,

150.2.b.iv

in relation to a write-down instrument, provision under paragraph  34(2)  or
35 , and

150.2.b.v

in relation to an instrument of control, provision under paragraph  38(2) ;

150.2.c

a transfer is a “relevant transfer” if it transfers to any person—

150.2.c.i

property, rights or liabilities of the CCP or CCP group company, or of a
bridge central counterparty, or

150.2.c.ii

securities issued by the CCP, or CCP group company, or of a bridge central
counterparty.

150.3

Sub-paragraph  (1)  does not affect the power of the court, subject to section
244 of the Banking Act 2009 (immunity), to award damages as a remedy in
relevant proceedings.

###### Giving of notices, documents etc under this Schedule

151

Regulations under section 414 of FSMA 2000 (service of notices), and
subsection (4) of that section, apply in relation to any notice, direction or
document of any kind required to be given under any provision of this Schedule
(however that requirement is expressed) as if those provisions were provisions
of that Act.

###### “Financial assistance”

152

152.1

In this Schedule “ financial assistance ” includes giving guarantees or
indemnities and any other kind of financial assistance (actual or contingent).

152.2

The Treasury may by regulations provide that a specified activity or
transaction, or class of activity or transaction, is to be or not to be
treated as financial assistance for a specified purpose of this Schedule; and
sub-paragraph  (1)  is subject to this sub-paragraph.

152.3

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the negative procedure.

###### Modifications to the law

153

153.1

The Treasury may by regulations modify the law for the purpose of enabling the
powers under this Schedule to be used effectively, having regard to the
special resolution objectives.

153.2

Regulations may be made—

153.2.a

for the general purpose of the exercise of powers under this Schedule,

153.2.b

to facilitate a particular proposed or possible use of a power, or

153.2.c

in connection with a particular exercise of a power.

153.3

Regulations under sub-paragraph  (2)(c)  may make provision which has
retrospective effect in so far as the Treasury consider it necessary or
desirable for giving effect to the particular exercise of a power under this
Schedule in connection with which the regulations are made (but in relying on
this sub-paragraph the Treasury must have regard to the fact that it is in the
public interest to avoid retrospective legislation).

153.4

In sub-paragraph  (1)  “ modify the law ” means—

153.4.a

disapply or modify the effect of a provision of an enactment (other than a
provision made by or under this Act),

153.4.b

disapply or modify the effect of a rule of law not set out in legislation, or

153.4.c

amend any provision of an instrument or regulations made in the exercise of a
stabilisation power.

153.5

Specific powers under this Schedule are without prejudice to the generality of
this paragraph.

153.6

Regulations under this paragraph are—

153.6.a

subject to the affirmative procedure, or

153.6.b

if the Treasury consider it necessary for the regulations to come into force
without delay, subject to the made affirmative procedure.

153.7

Where regulations under this paragraph are subject to the made affirmative
procedure the statutory instrument containing the regulations must be laid
before Parliament after being made.

153.8

Regulations contained in a statutory instrument laid before Parliament under
sub-paragraph  (7)  cease to have effect at the end of the period of 28 days
beginning with the day on which the instrument is made unless, during that
period, the instrument is approved by a resolution of each House of
Parliament.

153.9

In calculating the period of 28 days, no account is to be taken of any whole
days that fall within a period during which—

153.9.a

Parliament is dissolved or prorogued, or

153.9.b

either House of Parliament is adjourned for more than four days.

153.10

If regulations cease to have effect as a result of sub-paragraph  (8) , that
does not—

153.10.a

affect the validity of anything previously done under the regulations, or

153.10.b

prevent the making of new regulations.

###### Interpretation

154

In this Schedule—

      “ Bank ” means the Bank of England;           “ bridge central
counterparty ” has the meaning given by paragraph  29(1) ;           “ cash
call instrument ” has the meaning given by paragraph  32 ;           “ CCP ”
means a recognised central counterparty (see paragraph  155 );           “ CCP
group company ” has the meaning given by paragraph  156 ;           “ central
counterparty ” means a body corporate or an unincorporated association which
interposes itself between the counterparties to the contracts traded on one or
more financial markets, becoming the buyer to every seller and the seller to
every buyer;           “ clearing member ” has the meaning given in Article 2
of EMIR and, unless otherwise provided, includes an interoperable CCP;
“clearing” and “ clearing services ”, in relation to a CCP, have the meaning
given by section 313 of FSMA 2000;           “ critical clearing services ”
means clearing services the withdrawal of which the Bank considers may
threaten the stability of the UK financial system;           “ director ”
includes, in relation to a CCP which has no board of directors, a member of
the equivalent management body responsible for the management of the CCP
concerned;           “ EMIR ” means  Regulation (EU) No 648/2012  of the
European Parliament and of the Council of 4 July 2012 on OTC derivatives,
central counterparties and trade repositories;           “ employee ” includes
the holder of an office;           “ extraordinary public financial support ”
means financial assistance that is provided by the Treasury or the Bank in
order to preserve or restore the viability, liquidity or solvency of a CCP, a
CCP group company or a group which includes a CCP, other than—
ordinary market assistance offered by the Bank on its usual terms, or
a liquidity facility which is provided—         to a CCP that is facing
temporary liquidity problems but is solvent, and           by the Bank on its
own initiative and on its own terms;                       “ financial
assistance ” has the meaning given by paragraph  152 ;           “ group ” has
the meaning given by section 474 of the Companies Act 2006;           “
instrument of control ” has the meaning given by paragraph  38 ;           “
interoperable CCP ” means a CCP with which an interoperability arrangement
(within the meaning of Article 2 of EMIR) has been established;           “
parent ” means a parent undertaking within the meaning given by section 1162
of the Companies Act 2006;           “ partial property transfer ” has the
meaning given by paragraph  75(1) ;           “ PRA-authorised person ” has
the meaning given by section 2B(5) of FSMA 2000;           “ recognition
requirements ” means the requirements resulting from section 286 of FSMA 2000;
“ resolution instrument ” has the meaning given by paragraph  79 ;           “
securities ” has the meaning given by paragraph  40 ;           “ service
contract ” has the meaning given by section 227 of the Companies Act 2006;
“ senior manager ”, in relation to a CCP, means a person who—
exercises executive functions within that CCP, and           is responsible,
and directly accountable to the directors, for the day to day management of
that CCP;                 “ special resolution objectives ” means the
objectives set out in paragraph  15 ;           “ stabilisation instrument ”
has the meaning given by paragraph  84 ;           “ stabilisation options ”
means the options described in paragraph  1(3) ;           “ stabilisation
powers ” means the powers described in paragraph  1(4) ;           “
subsidiary ” means a subsidiary undertaking within the meaning given by
section 1162 of the Companies Act 2006.           “ tear-up instrument ” has
the meaning given by paragraph  31 ;           “ third-country instrument ”
has the meaning given by paragraph  145 ;           “ third-country resolution
action ” has the meaning given by paragraph  145 ;           “transfer date”—
in relation to a share transfer instrument, means the date on or at which a
share transfer instrument (or the relevant part of it) takes effect, or
in relation to a property transfer instrument, means the date on or at which a
property transfer instrument (or the relevant part of it) takes effect;
“ UK financial system ” has the meaning given by section 1I of FSMA 2000;
“ variation instrument ” has the meaning given by paragraph  33 ;           “
write-down instrument ” has the meaning given by paragraph  34 .

###### Recognised central counterparty

155

155.1

In this Schedule “ recognised central counterparty ” has the meaning given by
section 285 of FSMA 2000.

155.2

But “ recognised central counterparty ” does not include a recognised clearing
house (within the meaning of section 285 of FSMA 2000) which is also—

155.2.a

a bank,

155.2.b

a building society (within the meaning of section 119 of the Building
Societies Act 1986),

155.2.c

a credit union (within the meaning of section 31 of the Credit Unions Act 1979
or Article 2(2) of the Credit Unions (Northern Ireland) Order 1985), or

155.2.d

an investment firm.

155.3

Where a stabilisation power is exercised in respect of a recognised central
counterparty, the body does not cease to be a recognised central counterparty
for the purposes of this Schedule if the recognition order under Part 18 of
FSMA 2000 is later revoked.

###### Interpretation: “CCP group company”, etc

156

156.1

In this Schedule “ CCP group company ” means an undertaking—

156.1.a

which is (or, but for the exercise of a stabilisation power, would be) in the
same group as a CCP, and

156.1.b

in respect of which any conditions specified in regulations made by the
Treasury are met.

156.2

Regulations under this paragraph may require the Bank to consult specified
persons before determining whether the conditions are met.

156.3

Regulations under this paragraph are subject to the affirmative procedure.

156.4

Undertakings are in the same group for the purposes of paragraph  117  and
this paragraph if they are group undertakings in respect of each other.

156.5

Expressions defined in the Companies Act 2006 have the same meaning in
paragraph  117  and this paragraph as in that Act.

##### Treasury support for CCPs

###### Consolidated Fund

157

157.1

There is to be paid out of money provided by Parliament expenditure incurred—

157.1.a

by the Treasury, or by the Secretary of State with the consent of the
Treasury, in respect of, or in connection with giving, financial assistance to
or in respect of a CCP (other than in respect of loans made in accordance with
paragraph  158 ), or

157.1.b

by the Treasury in respect of financial assistance to the Bank in connection
with this Schedule.

157.2

For the purpose of sub-paragraph  (1)(a)  expenditure is incurred in respect
of financial assistance in respect of CCPs if it is incurred in respect of an
activity, transaction or arrangement, or class of activity, transaction or
arrangement, which is expected to facilitate any part of the business of one
or more CCPs; and for that purpose it does not matter—

157.2.a

whether or not that is the sole or principal expected effect of the activity,
transaction or arrangement, or

157.2.b

whether the sole or principal motive for the activity, transaction or
arrangement is—

157.2.b.i

its effect on CCPs,

157.2.b.ii

its effect on the economy as a whole,

157.2.b.iii

its effect on a particular industry or sector of the economy, or

157.2.b.iv

its effect on clearing members of CCPs.

157.3

In this paragraph “ financial assistance ” has the meaning given by paragraph
152  (and regulations under that paragraph may restrict or expand the effect
of sub-paragraph  (2) )

157.4

Expenditure which could be paid out of money provided by Parliament under sub-
paragraph  (1)  may be charged on and paid out of the Consolidated Fund if the
Treasury are satisfied that the need for the expenditure is too urgent to
permit arrangements to be made for the provision of money by Parliament.

157.5

Where money is paid in reliance on sub-paragraph  (4)  the Treasury must as
soon as is reasonably practicable lay a report before Parliament specifying
the amount paid (but not the identity of the CCP or other institution to or in
respect of which it is paid).

157.6

If the Treasury think it necessary on public interest grounds, they may delay
or dispense with a report under sub-paragraph (5).

###### National Loans Fund

158

158.1

Where the Treasury propose to make a loan to or in respect of a CCP, they may
arrange for money to be paid out of the National Loans Fund.

158.2

The Treasury may make arrangements under sub-paragraph  (1)  only where they
think it necessary to make the loan urgently in order to protect the stability
of the UK financial system

158.3

The Treasury may determine—

158.3.a

the rate of interest on a loan, and

158.3.b

other terms and conditions.

158.4

Sums received by the Treasury in respect of loans by virtue of this paragraph
must be paid into the National Loans Fund.

158.5

Neither section 16 of the Banking (Special Provisions) Act 2008 (finance) nor
any other enactment restricts the breadth of application of this paragraph.

158.6

Where money is paid in reliance on sub-paragraph  (1)  the Treasury must as
soon as is reasonably practicable lay a report before Parliament specifying
the amount paid (but not the identity of the CCP or other institution to or in
respect of which it is paid).

158.7

If the Treasury think it necessary on public interest grounds, they may delay
or dispense with a report under sub-paragraph (6).
