Write-down orders

Section 58

##### Write-down orders: main provisions

1

1.1

Part 24 of FSMA 2000 (insolvency) is amended as follows.

1.2

In section 360 (application of Part 2 of 1986 Act or Part 3 of 1989 Order
(administration) to insurers), at the end insert—

1.2.4

Subsection  (5)  applies where, by virtue of an order under this section, a
person may be appointed as administrator of an insurer.

1.2.5

While a write-down order under section  377A  has effect in relation to an
insurer, a person may not be appointed as administrator of the insurer without
the consent of the PRA.

1.3

Omit section 377 (reducing the value of contracts instead of winding up).

1.4

Before section 378 (treatment of assets on winding up) insert—

########### Write-down orders

1.4.377A

1.4.377A.1

A “write-down order” is an order of the court directing that the value of one
or more of an insurer’s liabilities is reduced on such terms as may be
specified in the order.

1.4.377A.2

The court may make a write-down order in relation to an insurer if it is
satisfied that—

1.4.377A.2.a

the insurer is, or is likely to become, unable to pay its debts (within the
meaning given to that expression by section 123 of the 1986 Act or Article 103
of the 1989 Order), and

1.4.377A.2.b

making the order is reasonably likely to lead to a better outcome for the
insurer’s policyholders and other creditors (taken as a whole) than not making
the order.

1.4.377A.3

A write-down order—

1.4.377A.3.a

takes effect on the later of—

1.4.377A.3.a.i

the date specified in the order, and

1.4.377A.3.a.ii

the date on which the appointment of a person to act as the manager of the
order first takes effect (see section  377G (7) );

1.4.377A.3.b

ceases to have effect in accordance with section  377H ;

1.4.377A.3.c

may be revoked or varied in accordance with section  377I .

1.4.377A.4

A write-down order may not be made in relation to an insurer—

1.4.377A.4.a

which is in administration (within the meaning of Schedule B1 to the 1986 Act
or Schedule B1 to the 1989 Order), or

1.4.377A.4.b

which is in liquidation by virtue of—

1.4.377A.4.b.i

a resolution for voluntary winding up, or

1.4.377A.4.b.ii

a winding-up order under section 125 of the 1986 Act or Article 105 of the
1989 Order.

1.4.377A.5

A write-down order may not reduce the value of an excluded liability (within
the meaning given by section  377B ).

1.4.377A.6

A liability, to the extent of its reduction by a write-down order under this
section, is to be treated as extinguished unless and until revived by section
377H or 377I.

1.4.377A.7

In this section, “ creditor ” includes a contingent or prospective creditor.

########### Excluded liabilities

1.4.377B

1.4.377B.1

Each of the following is an “excluded liability”—

1.4.377B.1.a

a liability with an original maturity of less than 7 days;

1.4.377B.1.b

an amount payable in respect of goods delivered, or a service provided, on or
after the date on which the write-down order is made;

1.4.377B.1.c

an amount in respect of remuneration or expenses of a person appointed under
section  377G  to act as the manager of the write-down order (including
amounts incurred before, as well as after, the person’s appointment in
connection with the order or the application for the order);

1.4.377B.1.d

an amount secured on property of any kind, other than an amount secured by a
charge which, as created, was a floating charge;

1.4.377B.1.e

an amount payable in respect of wages or salary arising under a contract of
employment;

1.4.377B.1.f

a contribution or other sum payable in respect of an occupational pension
scheme;

1.4.377B.1.g

an amount payable in respect of redundancy payments;

1.4.377B.1.h

an amount payable under a contract or other instrument involving financial
services.

1.4.377B.2

In this section—

“ contract or other instrument involving financial services ” has the meaning
given by Schedule ZA2 to the 1986 Act, but does not include an agreement which
is, or forms part of, an arrangement involving the issue of a capital market
investment (see paragraph 6 of that Schedule); “ floating charge ” has the
meaning given by section 251 of the 1986 Act or paragraph (1) of Article 5 of
the 1989 Order; “ redundancy payment ” means— a redundancy payment under Part
11 of the Employment Rights Act 1996 or Part 12 of the Employment Rights
(Northern Ireland) Order 1996 ( S.I. 1996/1919 (N.I. 16) ), or a payment made
to a person who agrees to the termination of their employment in circumstances
where they would have been entitled to a redundancy payment under that Part if
dismissed; “ wages or salary ” includes— a sum payable in respect of a period
of holiday; a sum payable in respect of a period of absence through illness or
other good cause; a sum payable in lieu of holiday.

########### Application for a write-down order

1.4.377C

1.4.377C.1

An application to the court for a write-down order in relation to an insurer
may be made only by—

1.4.377C.1.a

the Treasury;

1.4.377C.1.b

the PRA;

1.4.377C.1.c

the insurer;

1.4.377C.1.d

a shareholder of the insurer;

1.4.377C.1.e

a policyholder or other creditor (including a contingent or prospective
creditor) of the insurer.

1.4.377C.2

An application for a write-down order may not be withdrawn without the
permission of the court.

1.4.377C.3

A person other than the PRA or the Treasury—

1.4.377C.3.a

must obtain the consent of the PRA before making an application for a write-
down order;

1.4.377C.3.b

must notify the PRA before seeking the court’s permission to withdraw an
application for a write-down order.

1.4.377C.4

Consent under subsection  (3) —

1.4.377C.4.a

must be in writing, and

1.4.377C.4.b

must be filed with the court with the relevant application.

1.4.377C.5

The PRA must consult the FCA before—

1.4.377C.5.a

making an application for a write-down order, or

1.4.377C.5.b

giving or refusing consent for a person to make an application for a write-
down order.

########### Powers of the FCA and PRA to participate in proceedings

1.4.377D

1.4.377D.1

This section applies if an application is made to the court for a write-down
order.

1.4.377D.2

The FCA and the PRA are entitled to be heard—

1.4.377D.2.a

at any hearing relating to the application, and

1.4.377D.2.b

if an order is made, at any hearing relating to the order.

1.4.377D.3

Any notice or other document required to be sent to a creditor of the insurer—

1.4.377D.3.a

in relation to the application, or

1.4.377D.3.b

if an order is made, in relation to the order,

must also be sent to the FCA and the PRA.

########### Powers of the court

1.4.377E

On an application for a write-down order, the court may—

1.4.377E.a

if, on hearing the application, it is satisfied of the matters in section
377A (2) , make a write-down order in the terms sought, or in such other terms
as the court thinks appropriate;

1.4.377E.b

dismiss the application;

1.4.377E.c

adjourn the hearing conditionally or unconditionally;

1.4.377E.d

make any other order which the court thinks appropriate.

########### Duty to notify creditors

1.4.377F

1.4.377F.1

This section applies where a write-down order is made in relation to an
insurer.

1.4.377F.2

As soon as reasonably practicable after the order is made, the insurer must
notify the FCA, the PRA and each affected person that the order has been made.

1.4.377F.3

An “affected person” is a person of a description specified in rules made by
the PRA for the purposes of this section.

1.4.377F.4

Notification under this section—

1.4.377F.4.a

must include such other information as may be specified in rules made by the
PRA for the purposes of this section, and

1.4.377F.4.b

must be given in such form and manner as may be specified in rules made by the
PRA for the purposes of this section.

1.4.377F.5

Failure to notify an affected person in accordance with this section, or rules
made by the PRA for the purposes of this section, does not affect the validity
of the write-down order in relation to that person or any other person.

########### The manager

1.4.377G

1.4.377G.1

The court may by order appoint one or more eligible persons to act as the
manager of a write-down order (“the manager”).

1.4.377G.2

An order under subsection  (1)  may—

1.4.377G.2.a

be made at the same time as the write-down order or at a later date (but see
section  377A (3)(a) );

1.4.377G.2.b

appoint a person in addition to or instead of a person who is for the time
being appointed;

1.4.377G.2.c

give such directions about the carrying out of the person’s functions as the
manager as the court thinks appropriate.

1.4.377G.3

The court may by order terminate the appointment of a person who is for the
time being appointed to act as the manager of a write-down order.

1.4.377G.4

Sections  377C  and 377D apply to an application to the court for an order
under subsection  (1)  or  (3)  as they apply to an application for a write-
down order but—

1.4.377G.4.a

if the application is for the appointment of a person in addition to, or
instead of, a person for the time being appointed, section  377C (1)  applies
as if the persons mentioned included a person for the time being appointed;

1.4.377G.4.b

section  377C (2)  does not apply.

1.4.377G.5

The court may appoint a person to act as the manager of a write-down order
only if—

1.4.377G.5.a

the PRA has provided the court with a statement that the person is suitably
qualified, and

1.4.377G.5.b

the person has provided the court with a statement that the person consents so
to act.

1.4.377G.6

Where it is proposed that more than one person should act as the manager, the
statement under subsection  (5)(b)  must specify—

1.4.377G.6.a

which of the functions of the manager (if any) are to be exercised by the
persons acting jointly, and

1.4.377G.6.b

which of the functions of the manager (if any) are to be exercised by any or
all of the persons.

1.4.377G.7

The appointment of a person to act as the manager—

1.4.377G.7.a

takes effect at the time specified in the order by which the person is
appointed, and

1.4.377G.7.b

ceases to have effect at the time specified in the order by which the person’s
appointment is terminated (whether by being replaced by another person or
otherwise).

1.4.377G.8

Schedule 19A makes further provision about the manager of a write-down order.

########### Write-down order ceasing to have effect

1.4.377H

1.4.377H.1

A reduction in the value of a liability of an insurer under a write-down order
ceases to have effect—

1.4.377H.1.a

on such date as may be specified in the order (and different dates may be
specified in relation to different liabilities or liabilities of different
types), or

1.4.377H.1.b

if earlier, or if no such date is specified, the date on which a termination
event happens (or, if more than one termination event happens, the earliest of
those dates).

1.4.377H.2

In the following table—

1.4.377H.2.a

the first column specifies each event which is a termination event for the
purposes of this section, and

1.4.377H.2.b

the second column specifies, in relation to each termination event, the date
on which the event happens for the purposes of this section.

Event Date event happens The write-down order being— revoked, or varied so as
to remove the liability in question from its scope, by an order under section
377I The date specified in the order under section  377I  as the date on which
the revocation or variation is to take effect, or if no date is specified, the
date on which the order under section  377I  is made The insurer ceasing to
have permission under Part 4A to carry out contracts of insurance The date on
which the withdrawal of permission takes effect The transfer of the liability
in question pursuant to an insurance business transfer scheme which has effect
in accordance with an order under section 111(1) The date on which the
transfer takes effect The making of a winding-up order against the insurer The
date on which the order is made The voluntary winding up of the insurer The
date on which the liquidator is appointed The coming into force of a voluntary
arrangement (under Part 1 of the 1986 Act or Part 2 of the 1989 Order) in
relation to the insurer The date on which the voluntary arrangement comes into
force The insurer entering administration The date on which the appointment of
an administrator takes effect.

1.4.377H.3

Where a write-down order is varied, this section applies as if references to
the write-down order were to the order as varied.

########### Variation or revocation of a write-down order

1.4.377I

1.4.377I.1

The court may, by order—

1.4.377I.1.a

revoke a write-down order, or

1.4.377I.1.b

vary (or further vary) a write-down order.

1.4.377I.2

Section  377A (2)(b)  applies to the making of an order under this section as
it applies to the making of the write-down order.

1.4.377I.3

In varying (or further varying) a write-down order the court may, in
particular—

1.4.377I.3.a

remove one or more of the insurer’s liabilities from the scope of the order
(but removing all such liabilities from the scope of the order takes effect as
a termination of the order);

1.4.377I.3.b

bring one or more of the insurer’s liabilities within the scope of the order
(on such terms as the court may specify);

1.4.377I.3.c

further reduce the value of one or more of the insurer’s liabilities;

1.4.377I.3.d

increase the value of one or more of the insurer’s liabilities to any amount
less than the value the liability had before the write-down order took effect;

1.4.377I.3.e

vary any term specified in the order, including the period for which a
reduction in the value of a liability has effect;

1.4.377I.3.f

make any other order that the court thinks appropriate.

1.4.377I.4

Sections  377C  to  377F  apply to an application for an order under this
section as they apply to an application for a write-down order but with the
following modifications—

1.4.377I.4.a

section  377C (1)  applies as if the list of persons entitled to make an
application included—

1.4.377I.4.a.i

the FCA;

1.4.377I.4.a.ii

the scheme manager of the Financial Services Compensation Scheme (see section
212(1));

1.4.377I.4.a.iii

a person appointed under section  377G  to act as the manager of the write-
down order;

1.4.377I.4.b

if the person making the application is the scheme manager of the Financial
Services Compensation Scheme, section  377C (3)  does not apply.

1.4.377I.5

The scheme manager of the Financial Services Compensation Scheme must consult
the FCA and the PRA before making an application to vary or revoke a write-
down order.

1.4.377I.6

Where a provisional liquidator of the insurer has been appointed under section
135 of the 1986 Act or Article 115 of the 1989 Order, a person appointed to
act as the manager of a write-down order must obtain the consent of the
provisional liquidator before making an application for an order under this
section.

########### Further provision about write-down orders

1.4.377J

In Schedule  19B—

1.4.377J.a

Part  1  makes provision about the enforcement of a liability of an insurer
while a write-down order has effect;

1.4.377J.b

Part  2  makes provision about the disposal of an insurer’s assets and the
making of certain payments by an insurer while a write-down order has effect;

1.4.377J.c

Part 3 makes provision about the treatment of an insurer’s liabilities for the
purposes of certain provisions relating to insolvency while a write-down order
has effect;

1.4.377J.d

Part 4 makes provision about interest payable in respect of liabilities
reduced under a write-down order or prevented from being enforced while a
write-down order has effect.

##### The manager of a write-down order

2

After Schedule 19 to FSMA 2000 (competition information), insert—

The manager of a write-down order

Section 377G

########### Application of Schedule

2.1

2.1.1

This Schedule applies where—

2.1.1.a

a write-down order has been made under section  377A  in relation to an
insurer, and

2.1.1.b

one or more persons have been appointed under section  377G  to act as the
manager of the order.

2.1.2

Where only one person acts as the manager, a reference in this Schedule to
“the manager” is to that person.

2.1.3

Where two or more persons act jointly as the manager—

2.1.3.a

a reference in this Schedule to the manager is a reference to those persons
acting jointly;

2.1.3.b

where an offence of omission is committed by the manager, each of the persons
appointed to act jointly—

2.1.3.b.i

commits the offence, and

2.1.3.b.ii

may be proceeded against and punished individually.

2.1.4

Where persons act jointly in respect of only some of the functions of the
manager, sub-paragraph  (3)  applies only in relation to those functions.

2.1.5

Where two or more persons act concurrently as the manager, a reference in this
Schedule to the manager is a reference to any of the persons appointed (or any
combination of them).

2.1.6

In this Schedule, “ creditor ” includes a contingent or prospective creditor.

########### Status of the manager

2.2

The manager is an officer of the court.

########### Monitoring the insurer’s affairs

2.3

2.3.1

The manager must monitor the insurer’s affairs for the purpose of forming a
view as to whether—

2.3.1.a

it remains the case that the write-down order is reasonably likely to lead to
a better outcome for the insurer’s policyholders and other creditors (taken as
a whole) than if the write-down order were not in effect, or

2.3.1.b

that will remain the case, or once again be the case, if the directors of the
insurer were to take certain action or refrain from taking certain action.

2.3.2

If the manager forms the view mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1)(b) , the manager
may make such recommendations to the directors of the insurer as the manager
thinks appropriate.

2.3.3

In forming a view mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1) , the manager is entitled to
rely on information provided by the insurer, unless the manager has reason to
doubt its accuracy.

2.3.4

If directed to do so by the FCA or the PRA, the manager must provide a report
to that regulator on such matters relating to the insurer’s affairs, and at
such intervals, as that regulator may specify.

########### Application by manager to revoke or vary a write-down order

2.4

2.4.1

This paragraph applies if the manager forms the view that it is in the
interests of the insurer’s policyholders and other creditors (taken as a
whole) for the write-down order to be—

2.4.1.a

revoked, or

2.4.1.b

varied in one or more respects.

2.4.2

The manager must apply to the court for such orders (whether under section
377I  or otherwise) as the manager thinks likely to achieve the best outcome
for the insurer’s policyholders and other creditors (taken as a whole).

2.4.3

In forming the view mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1) , the manager may have
regard, among other things—

2.4.3.a

to whether recommendations under paragraph  3(2)  have been made (and if so,
whether they have been acted upon);

2.4.3.b

to whether recommendations, or further recommendations, under paragraph  3(2)
could be made (and if so, the likelihood that they will be acted upon).

########### Provision of information and assistance to the manager

2.5

2.5.1

The manager may require a relevant person to provide such information or
assistance as the manager may reasonably require for the purpose of carrying
out the manager’s functions.

2.5.2

Each of the following is a “relevant person” for these purposes—

2.5.2.a

a director of the insurer, or of a body corporate in the same group as the
insurer;

2.5.2.b

an employee of the insurer, or of a body corporate in the same group as the
insurer;

2.5.2.c

a person providing a service to the insurer, or to a body corporate in the
same group as the insurer;

2.5.2.d

a person who has at any relevant time been a person falling within paragraph
(a) ,  (b)  or  (c) .

2.5.3

A relevant person must comply with a requirement under this paragraph to
provide information as soon as is practicable.

2.5.4

The obligation imposed by sub-paragraph  (3)  is enforceable, on the
application of the manager—

2.5.4.a

by an injunction, or

2.5.4.b

in Scotland, by an order for specific performance under section 45 of the
Court of Session Act 1988.

########### Application by manager for directions

2.6

The manager may apply to the court for directions about the carrying out of
the manager’s functions.

########### Challenges to the manager’s actions

2.7

2.7.1

Any of the following persons may apply to the court on the ground that an act,
omission or decision of the manager has unfairly harmed the interests of the
applicant—

2.7.1.a

a director of the insurer;

2.7.1.b

a shareholder of the insurer;

2.7.1.c

a policyholder or other creditor of the insurer;

2.7.1.d

any other person affected by the write-down order.

2.7.2

Any of the following persons may apply to the court on the ground that an act,
omission or decision of the manager is not in the interests of the insurer’s
policyholders and other creditors (taken as a whole)—

2.7.2.a

the FCA;

2.7.2.b

the PRA;

2.7.2.c

the scheme manager of the Financial Services Compensation Scheme (see section
212(1));

2.7.2.d

a provisional liquidator of the insurer.

2.7.3

Before making an application under sub-paragraph  (2) —

2.7.3.a

the FCA must consult the PRA;

2.7.3.b

the PRA must consult the FCA;

2.7.3.c

the scheme manager of the Financial Services Compensation Scheme must notify
the FCA and the PRA.

2.7.4

On an application under this paragraph the court may—

2.7.4.a

confirm, reverse or modify any act or decision of the manager,

2.7.4.b

give the manager directions, or

2.7.4.c

make such other order as the court thinks appropriate (but may not, under this
paragraph, order the manager to pay any compensation).

2.7.5

Where an application under this paragraph relates to a failure by the manager
to apply to the court for the variation or termination of the write-down
order, the court may treat the application as an application for an order
under section  377I  made by a person entitled to apply for an order under
that section.

##### Further provision about write-down orders

3

After Schedule 19A to FSMA 2000 (the manager of a write-down order), inserted
by Part 2 of this Schedule, insert—

Further provision about write-down orders

Section 377J

########### Restrictions on enforcement

############ Application of this Part of this Schedule

3.1

3.1.1

This Part of this Schedule applies in relation to an insurer—

3.1.1.a

during the period—

3.1.1.a.i

beginning with the date on which an application is made for a write-down order
in relation to the insurer, and

3.1.1.a.ii

ending with the date on which the order is made or the application is
withdrawn or dismissed;

3.1.1.b

during the period—

3.1.1.b.i

beginning with the date on which a write-down order is made in relation to the
insurer, and

3.1.1.b.ii

ending with the last day of the period of six months beginning with the day on
which the write-down order takes effect (see section  377A (3)(a) );

3.1.1.c

during such further period as the court may order.

3.1.2

This Part of this Schedule ceases to apply—

3.1.2.a

where the court orders that it should cease to apply (and in accordance with
the terms of the order), or

3.1.2.b

where the write-down order ceases to have effect (because, in accordance with
section  377H , each reduction in the value of a liability of the insurer
ceases to have effect).

3.1.3

The court—

3.1.3.a

may make an order under sub-paragraph (1)(c) or  (2)(a)  only on an
application by a person mentioned in sub-paragraph  (4) ;

3.1.3.b

may not specify in an order under sub-paragraph (1)(c) a period longer than
six months (but may make one or more further such orders).

3.1.4

The persons are—

3.1.4.a

a person entitled to make an application for a write-down order in relation to
the insurer (see section  377C (1) );

3.1.4.b

a person appointed under section  377G  to act as the manager of the write-
down order;

3.1.4.c

a provisional liquidator of the insurer;

3.1.4.d

the FCA.

3.1.5

Before making an application for an order under this Part of this Schedule—

3.1.5.a

a person other than the PRA or the Treasury must consult the PRA;

3.1.5.b

the PRA must consult the FCA.

############ Moratorium on proceedings

3.2

3.2.1

Where this Part of this Schedule applies in relation to an insurer, except
with the permission of the court—

3.2.1.a

no step may be taken to enforce security over the insurer’s property;

3.2.1.b

no step may be taken to repossess goods in the insurer’s possession under a
hire-purchase agreement;

3.2.1.c

a landlord may not exercise a right of forfeiture by peaceable re-entry in
relation to premises let to the insurer;

3.2.1.d

in Scotland, a landlord may not exercise a right of irritancy in relation to
premises let to the insurer;

3.2.1.e

no legal process (including legal proceedings, execution, distress or
diligence) may be instituted, carried out or continued against the insurer or
its property.

3.2.2

Where the court gives permission for something to be done that would otherwise
be prevented by this paragraph, it may impose a condition on, or a requirement
in connection with, the permission.

3.2.3

In this paragraph, “ landlord ” includes a person to whom rent is payable.

############ Exceptions

3.3

3.3.1

This Part of this Schedule does not apply in relation to—

3.3.1.a

arrangements entered into after the date on which this Part of this Schedule
first applied in relation to the insurer;

3.3.1.b

employment tribunal proceedings or any legal process arising out of such
proceedings;

3.3.1.c

proceedings, not within paragraph  (b) , involving a claim between an employer
and a worker.

3.3.2

Nothing in this Part of this Schedule—

3.3.2.a

prevents the FCA or the PRA from exercising a function it has in relation to
the insurer or any other person;

3.3.2.b

prevents a consumer from taking steps to enforce a money award or direction
under section 229 or 404B.

3.3.3

Nothing in this Part of this Schedule affects the operation of—

3.3.3.a

Part 7 of the Companies Act 1989 (financial markets and insolvency);

3.3.3.b

the Financial Markets and Insolvency Regulations 1996 ( S.I. 1996/1469 );

3.3.3.c

the Financial Markets and Insolvency (Settlement Finality) Regulations 1999 (
S.I. 1999/2979 );

3.3.3.d

the Financial Collateral Arrangements (No.2) Regulations 2003 ( S.I. 2003/3226
).

3.3.4

The Treasury may by regulations amend sub-paragraph (3).

3.3.5

In this paragraph—

“ agency worker ” has the meaning given by section 13(2) of the Employment
Relations Act 1999; “ arrangements ” includes any agreement, understanding,
scheme, transaction or series of transactions; “employer”— in relation to an
agency worker, has the meaning given by section 13(2) of the Employment
Relations Act 1999; otherwise, has the meaning given by section 230(4) of the
Employment Rights Act 1996; “ worker ” means an individual who is— a worker
within the meaning of section 230(3) of the Employment Rights Act 1996, or an
agency worker.

########### Dealing with assets etc

############ Application of this Part of this Schedule

3.4

This Part of this Schedule applies while a write-down order has effect in
relation to one or more liabilities of an insurer.

############ Dealing with assets

3.5

The insurer may not dispose of, or otherwise deal with, any of its assets
(whether in the United Kingdom or elsewhere) except—

3.5.a

in the ordinary way of the insurer’s business, or

3.5.b

with the consent of the PRA.

############ Paying variable remuneration

3.6

The insurer may not pay variable remuneration that is not regulated by a
collective bargaining agreement, except with the consent of the PRA.

############ Distributions

3.7

The insurer may not make a distribution, within the meaning of Part 23 of the
Companies Act 2006, except with the consent of the PRA.

########### Treatment of written-down liabilities for certain purposes

############ Application of this Part of this Schedule

3.8

3.8.1

This Part of this Schedule applies in relation to a liability of an insurer
while the value of the liability is reduced under a write-down order.

3.8.2

Where the write-down order is varied, this Part of this Schedule applies as if
references to the write-down order were to the order as varied.

############ Relevant insolvency provisions

3.9

3.9.1

In determining the value of the liability for the purposes of a relevant
insolvency provision, no account is to be taken of the contingent or
prospective value of the liability, or interest on the liability, arising from
any expectation that the write-down order will be varied, further varied or
cease to have effect (whether in relation to the liability or generally).

3.9.2

The relevant insolvency provisions are—

3.9.2.a

section 123 of the 1986 Act or Article 103 of the 1989 Order, or any statutory
provision which applies that section or that Article;

3.9.2.b

Article 11 of  Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2015/35  of 10 October
2014 supplementing  Directive 2009/138/EC  of the European Parliament and of
the Council on the taking-up and pursuit of the business of Insurance and
Reinsurance (Solvency 2);

3.9.2.c

PRA rules applicable to non-directive insurers, within the meaning given by
the Rulebook made by the PRA under this Act (as that Rulebook has effect from
time to time).

3.9.3

The Treasury may by regulations amend sub-paragraph  (2) .

############ Reinsurance contracts

3.10

3.10.1

This paragraph applies where—

3.10.1.a

the liability is a liability under a contract of insurance the insurer carries
out as principal (“contract A”), and

3.10.1.b

the insurer enters into a reinsurance contract under which contract A, or any
liability under contract A, is reinsured (“contract B”).

3.10.2

In determining the value of the liability for the purposes of contract B, no
account is to be taken of the reduction in value of the liability under the
write-down order.

########### Interest

3.11

3.11.1

This Part of this Schedule applies where—

3.11.1.a

the value of a liability of an insurer is reduced under a write-down order,

3.11.1.b

while the write-down order has effect in relation to the liability, an amount
of the liability is due and payable (or would be due and payable but for the
write-down order), and

3.11.1.c

the amount remains due and payable after the reduction ceases to have effect.

3.11.2

The amount carries statutory interest, within the meaning of the Late Payment
of Commercial Debts (Interest) Act 1998, for the period—

3.11.2.a

beginning with the date on which the write-down order took effect or, if
later, the date on which the amount became due and payable (or would have
become due and payable but for the write-down order), and

3.11.2.b

ending with the day on which the amount is paid.

3.11.3

Where a write-down order is varied, this section applies as if references to
the write-down order were to the order as varied.

##### Write-down orders: financial services compensation scheme

4

Part 15 of FSMA 2000 (the Financial Services Compensation Scheme) is amended
as follows.

5

After section 217 (insurers in financial difficulties) insert—

######### Insurers subject to write-down orders

5.217ZA

5.217ZA.1

The compensation scheme must include provision requiring the scheme manager to
take specified measures for safeguarding policyholders affected by write-down
orders.

5.217ZA.2

A person (“ P ”) is a policyholder affected by a write-down order if—

5.217ZA.2.a

P is a policyholder of an insurer in respect of whom a write-down order has
effect, and

5.217ZA.2.b

the value of any thing to which P is (or may become) entitled, in P’s capacity
as a policyholder of the insurer, is reduced under the write-down order.

5.217ZA.3

Measures specified by virtue of subsection  (1)  must, in particular, require
financial assistance to be given to insurers subject to write-down orders for
the purpose mentioned in subsection  (4) .

5.217ZA.4

The purpose is to enable payments to be made to affected policyholders in
respect of the reduction in value of their entitlements (or contingent
entitlements), as mentioned in subsection  (2)(b) .

5.217ZA.5

Financial assistance given under this section—

5.217ZA.5.a

must not be used for any purpose other than the purpose mentioned in
subsection  (4) ;

5.217ZA.5.b

is not to be taken into account, to any extent, in valuing the assets of the
insurer for any purpose.

5.217ZA.6

Measures taken by the scheme manager by virtue of this section are in addition
to any measures the scheme manager may take under powers provided by virtue of
section 217(1).

5.217ZA.7

In this section and section  217ZB —

“ insurer ” means a relevant person who has permission to carry out contracts
of insurance; “ write-down order ” means an order under section 377A (as it
has effect in accordance with section 377H).

######### Recovery of financial assistance under section 

5.217ZB

5.217ZB.1

The compensation scheme may make provision giving the scheme manager a right
of recovery in respect of financial assistance given to an insurer by virtue
of section  217ZA .

5.217ZB.2

Any right of recovery the scheme manager has in respect of financial
assistance given to an insurer by virtue of subsection  (1)  must not be
exercised against a policyholder of the insurer.

5.217ZB.3

Subsection  (4)  applies where, by virtue of subsection  (1) , the scheme
manager has a right of recovery in respect of financial assistance given to an
insurer.

5.217ZB.4

In valuing the insurer’s liabilities for the purposes of a relevant insolvency
provision, no account is to be taken of any expectation that the right will be
exercised.

5.217ZB.5

In subsection  (4) , “ relevant insolvency provision ” has the same meaning as
in paragraph  9  of Schedule 19B (treatment of written-down liabilities for
purposes of relevant insolvency provisions).

6

In section 219 (scheme manager’s power to require information), in subsection
(1A), after paragraph (b) insert—

6.ba

on a person (P) who is an insurer who has been given financial assistance
under section  217ZA ,

.

7

After section 220 (scheme manager’s power to inspect information held by
liquidator etc), insert—

######### Power to inspect information held by write-down manager

7.220A

7.220A.1

For the purpose of assisting the scheme manager to discharge its functions
under section  217ZA  or  217ZB  in relation to an insurer, a person to whom
this section applies must permit a person authorised by the scheme manager to
inspect relevant documents.

7.220A.2

This section applies to a person appointed under section  377G  to act as the
manager of a write-down order which has effect in relation to the insurer.

7.220A.3

A person inspecting a document under this section may take copies of, or
extracts from, the document.

  Insurers in financial difficulties: enforcement of contracts

Section 58

##### New Schedule 19C to FSMA 2000

1

1.1

Part 24 of FSMA 2000 (insolvency) is amended as follows.

1.2

After section 377J (further provision about write-down orders), inserted by
Part 1 of Schedule 12 to this Act, insert—

########### Insurers in financial difficulties: enforcement of contracts

1.2.377K

Schedule 19C makes provision about the enforcement of certain contracts to
which an insurer is a party while the insurer is in financial difficulties
(within the meaning given by the Schedule).

1.3

After Schedule 19B (further provision about write-down orders), inserted by
Part 3 of Schedule 12 to this Act, insert—

  Insurers in financial difficulties: enforcement of contracts

Section 377K

############# Introductory

############## Application of this Schedule

1.3.1

This Schedule applies in relation to an insurer while the insurer is in
financial difficulties.

############## “Financial difficulties”

1.3.2

1.3.2.1

An insurer is in “ financial difficulties ” for the purposes of this Schedule
if—

1.3.2.1.a

Part 1 of Schedule 19B (write-down orders: restrictions on enforcement) has
effect in relation to the insurer (see paragraph 1(1) and  (2)  of that
Schedule);

1.3.2.1.b

the insurer is in administration, within the meaning of Schedule B1 to the
1986 Act or Schedule B1 to the 1989 Order, or awaiting administration;

1.3.2.1.c

a petition for the winding up of the insurer has been presented and has not
been withdrawn or determined.

1.3.2.2

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1)(b) , an insurer is awaiting
administration while an application for an administration order in respect of
the insurer has been made to the court and—

1.3.2.2.a

the application has not yet been granted or dismissed, or

1.3.2.2.b

the application has been granted but the administration order has not yet
taken effect.

1.3.2.3

For the purposes of this Schedule, an insurer “enters into financial
difficulties”—

1.3.2.3.a

in a case to which sub-paragraph  (1)(a)  applies, on the date on which Part 1
of Schedule 19B first has effect in relation to the insurer;

1.3.2.3.b

in a case to which sub-paragraph  (1)(b)  applies, on the date on which the
application for the administration order is made to the court;

1.3.2.3.c

in a case to which sub-paragraph  (1)(c)  applies, on the date on which the
winding-up petition is presented.

############# Policyholder surrender rights

############## Restriction on policyholder surrender rights

1.3.3

1.3.3.1

Where this Schedule applies in relation to an insurer, the total value of a
policyholder’s rights under a relevant contract of insurance which the
policyholder may surrender in a relevant period must not exceed the surrender
limit for that period.

1.3.3.2

For these purposes—

      “ relevant contract of insurance ” means a contract of long-term
insurance which is not a contract in respect of which the following conditions
are met—         the benefits under the contract are payable only on death or
in respect of incapacity due to injury, sickness or infirmity;           the
contract has no surrender value, or the consideration consists of a single
premium and the surrender value does not exceed that premium;           the
contract makes no provision for its conversion or extension in a manner which
would result in it ceasing to comply with either of the above conditions;
“ relevant period ” means—         the period of 12 months beginning with the
date on which the insurer entered into financial difficulties, and
each subsequent period of 12 months;                 “ surrender limit ”, in
relation to a relevant contract of insurance and relevant period, is an amount
equal to 5% of the total surrender value of the contract on the day on which
the relevant period began.

############## Switching rights

1.3.4

1.3.4.1

This paragraph applies where the value of a right under a relevant contract of
insurance is wholly or partly determined by reference to property of any
description.

1.3.4.2

The reference in paragraph  3 (1)  to the surrender of rights by a
policyholder includes the exercise by the policyholder of a contractual right
to change the property by reference to which the value of a right is (wholly
or partly) determined.

############## Consent to exceed surrender limit

1.3.5

1.3.5.1

Paragraph  3 (1)  does not apply if, or to the extent that, consent for the
surrender of an amount that would exceed the surrender limit for the relevant
period has been given by—

1.3.5.1.a

the court,

1.3.5.1.b

a relevant office-holder, or

1.3.5.1.c

where there is no relevant office-holder, the insurer.

1.3.5.2

For these purposes, “ relevant office-holder ” means—

1.3.5.2.a

a provisional liquidator of the insurer;

1.3.5.2.b

an administrator of the insurer;

1.3.5.2.c

a person appointed to act as the manager of a write-down order that has effect
in relation to the insurer.

1.3.5.3

The court, a relevant office-holder or the insurer (as the case may be) may
give consent under sub-paragraph  (1)  only if satisfied that not doing so
would cause the policyholder hardship.

1.3.5.4

Where a provisional liquidator of an insurer has been appointed, the manager
of a write-down order that has effect in relation to the insurer must obtain
the consent of the provisional liquidator before giving consent under sub-
paragraph  (1) .

1.3.5.5

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving consent under sub-paragraph
(1) , a relevant office-holder or the insurer must notify the PRA.

############# Termination etc of relevant contracts

############## Relevant contracts

1.3.6

1.3.6.1

For the purposes of this Part of this Schedule, a contract to which an insurer
is a party is a “relevant contract” if it is—

1.3.6.1.a

a contract for the supply of goods or services to the insurer,

1.3.6.1.b

a financial contract, or

1.3.6.1.c

a reinsurance contract under which contracts of insurance the insurer carries
out as principal are reinsured.

1.3.6.2

“ Financial contract ” means—

1.3.6.2.a

a contract for the provision of financial services consisting of—

1.3.6.2.a.i

lending (including the factoring and financing of commercial transactions),

1.3.6.2.a.ii

financial leasing, or

1.3.6.2.a.iii

providing guarantees or commitments;

1.3.6.2.b

a securities contract, including—

1.3.6.2.b.i

a contract for the purchase, sale or loan of a security or group or index of
securities;

1.3.6.2.b.ii

an option on a security or group or index of securities;

1.3.6.2.b.iii

a repurchase or reverse repurchase transaction on any such security, group or
index;

1.3.6.2.c

a commodities contract, including—

1.3.6.2.c.i

a contract for the purchase, sale or loan of a commodity or group or index of
commodities for future delivery;

1.3.6.2.c.ii

an option on a commodity or group or index of commodities;

1.3.6.2.c.iii

a repurchase or reverse repurchase transaction on any such commodity, group or
index;

1.3.6.2.d

a futures or forwards contract, including a contract (other than a commodities
contract) for the purchase, sale or transfer of a commodity or property of any
other description, service, right or interest for a specified price at a
future date;

1.3.6.2.e

a swap agreement, including—

1.3.6.2.e.i

a swap or option relating to interest rates, spot or other foreign exchange
agreements, currency, an equity index or equity, a debt index or debt,
commodity indexes or commodities, weather, emissions or inflation;

1.3.6.2.e.ii

a total return, credit spread or credit swap;

1.3.6.2.e.iii

any agreement or transaction similar to an agreement that is referred to in
sub-paragraph (i) or (ii) and is the subject of recurrent dealing in the swaps
or derivatives markets.

1.3.6.3

But a master agreement for any contract or agreement referred to in sub-
paragraph  (2)  is not a relevant contract for the purposes of this Part of
this Schedule.

1.3.6.4

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (2) , “ commodities ” includes—

1.3.6.4.a

units recognised for compliance with the requirements of  EU Directive
2003/87/EC  establishing a scheme for greenhouse gas emission allowance
trading,

1.3.6.4.b

allowances under paragraph 5 of Schedule 2 to the Climate Change Act 2008
relating to a trading scheme dealt with under Part 1 of that Schedule (schemes
limiting activities relating to emissions of greenhouse gas), and

1.3.6.4.c

renewables obligation certificates issued—

1.3.6.4.c.i

by the Gas and Electricity Markets Authority under an order made under section
32B of the Electricity Act 1989, or

1.3.6.4.c.ii

by the Northern Ireland Authority for Utility Regulation under the Energy
(Northern Ireland) Order 2003 ( S.I. 2003/419 (N.I. 6) ) and pursuant to an
order made under Articles 52 to 55F of that Order.

############## Restriction on termination etc

1.3.7

1.3.7.1

Where this Schedule applies in relation to an insurer, a provision of a
relevant contract, entered into by the insurer before the insurer first enters
into financial difficulties, ceases to have effect if, and to the extent that,
under the provision—

1.3.7.1.a

the contract would terminate, a supply would cease, or any other thing would
occur, because the insurer is in financial difficulties, or

1.3.7.1.b

another party to the contract would be entitled to terminate the contract,
cease a supply, or do any other thing, because the insurer is in financial
difficulties.

1.3.7.2

Where—

1.3.7.2.a

under a provision of a relevant contract, another party to the contract is
entitled to terminate the contract, cease a supply, or do any other thing
because of an event occurring before the insurer was in financial
difficulties, and

1.3.7.2.b

the entitlement arises before the insurer was in financial difficulties,

the entitlement may not be exercised while the insurer is in financial
difficulties.

1.3.7.3

A supplier of goods or services to an insurer must not—

1.3.7.3.a

make it a condition of a supply of goods or services, while the insurer is in
financial difficulties, that any outstanding charges in respect of a supply
made to the insurer before the insurer is in financial difficulties are paid,
or

1.3.7.3.b

do anything which has that effect.

############## Consent to terminate relevant contracts

1.3.8

1.3.8.1

Sub-paragraph  (2)  applies where—

1.3.8.1.a

a provision of a relevant contract ceases to have effect under paragraph  7
(1) , or

1.3.8.1.b

an entitlement under a provision of a relevant contract is not exercisable
under paragraph  7 (2) .

1.3.8.2

A party to the contract (other than the insurer) may terminate the contract,
or do another thing in relation to the contract, if consent to terminate the
contract or do that other thing (as the case may be) has been given by—

1.3.8.2.a

the court,

1.3.8.2.b

a relevant office holder, or

1.3.8.2.c

where there is no relevant office-holder, the insurer.

1.3.8.3

For these purposes, “ relevant office-holder ” means an administrator or
provisional liquidator of the insurer (but does not include a person appointed
to act as the manager of a write-down order that has effect in relation to the
insurer).

1.3.8.4

The court, a relevant office-holder or the insurer (as the case may be) may
give consent under sub-paragraph  (2)  only if satisfied that not doing so
would cause hardship to any person.

1.3.8.5

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving consent under sub-paragraph
(2) , a relevant office-holder or the insurer must notify the PRA.

############# Exclusions and disapplication of this Schedule

############## Exclusions

1.3.9

1.3.9.1

Nothing in this Schedule affects the operation of—

1.3.9.1.a

Part 7 of the Companies Act 1989 (financial markets and insolvency);

1.3.9.1.b

the Financial Markets and Insolvency Regulations 1996 ( S.I. 1996/1469 );

1.3.9.1.c

the Financial Markets and Insolvency (Settlement Finality) Regulations 1999 (
S.I. 1999/2979 );

1.3.9.1.d

the Financial Collateral Arrangements (No.2) Regulations 2003 ( S.I. 2003/3226
).

1.3.9.2

Nothing in this Schedule affects any protected arrangements within the meaning
of section 48P of the Banking Act 2009.

############## Disapplication of this Schedule by the court

1.3.10

1.3.10.1

The court may order that this Schedule, or a specified provision of this
Schedule—

1.3.10.a

does not apply (insofar as it would otherwise) in relation to one or more
contracts to which the insurer is a party, or

1.3.10.b

applies with specified modifications in relation to one or more such
contracts.

1.3.10.2

An order under this paragraph—

1.3.10.2.a

must specify the contracts to which it applies;

1.3.10.2.b

may specify all of the contracts to which the insurer is a party (and to which
one or more provisions of this Schedule would otherwise apply).

1.3.10.3

For the purposes of an order under this paragraph—

      “ contract ” includes a contract of insurance;           “ specified ”
means specified or described in the order.

1.3.10.4

The court may make an order under this paragraph only if satisfied that one or
more of the following grounds is made out—

1.3.10.4.a

not making the order would be likely to cause hardship to any person (other
than the insurer);

1.3.10.4.b

where the insurer is in financial difficulties by virtue of paragraph  2(1)(a)
(write-down order), making the order is reasonably likely to lead to a better
outcome for the insurer’s policyholders and other creditors (taken as a whole)
than not making the order;

1.3.10.4.c

where the insurer is in financial difficulties by virtue of paragraph  2(1)(b)
(administration), making the order is reasonably likely to promote the purpose
of administration.

1.3.10.5

The “ purpose of administration ” means—

1.3.10.5.a

where the insurer is in, or is awaiting, administration under Part 2 of the
1986 Act (as modified, in relation to insurers, by the Financial Services and
Markets Act 2000 (Administration Orders Relating to Insurers) Order 2010 (
S.I. 2010/3023 )), an objective specified in paragraph 3 or 3A of Schedule B1
to the 1986 Act;

1.3.10.5.b

where the insurer is in, or is awaiting, administration under Part 3 of the
1989 Order (as modified, in relation to insurers, by the Financial Services
and Markets Act 2000 (Administration Orders Relating to Insurers) (Northern
Ireland) Order 2007 ( S.I. 2007/846 )), an objective specified in paragraph 4
of Schedule B1 to the 1989 Order.

############## Procedure

1.3.11

1.3.11.1

An order under paragraph  10  may be made on the court’s own motion or on an
application by—

1.3.11.1.a

where the insurer is in financial difficulties by virtue of paragraph  2(1)(a)
(write-down order), a person mentioned in paragraph  1(4)  of Schedule 19B;

1.3.11.1.b

where the insurer is in financial difficulties by virtue of paragraph  2(1)(b)
(administration), a person mentioned in sub-paragraph  (2) ;

1.3.11.1.c

where the insurer is in financial difficulties by virtue of paragraph  2(1)(c)
(winding up), a person entitled to petition for the winding up of the insurer;

1.3.11.1.d

a provisional liquidator of the insurer;

1.3.11.1.e

the FCA.

1.3.11.2

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1)(b) , the persons are—

1.3.11.2.a

where an administrator has been appointed, the administrator;

1.3.11.2.b

where the insurer is in, or is awaiting, administration under Part 2 of the
1986 Act, a person mentioned in paragraph 12(1) of Schedule B1 to that Act;

1.3.11.2.c

where the insurer is in, or is awaiting, administration under Part 3 of the
1989 Order, a person mentioned in paragraph 13(1) of Schedule B1 to that
Order.

1.3.11.3

Before making an application for an order under paragraph  10 —

1.3.11.3.a

a person other than a person mentioned in sub-paragraph  (4)  must obtain the
consent of the PRA;

1.3.11.3.b

a person mentioned in sub-paragraph  (4)  must consult the PRA.

1.3.11.4

The persons mentioned in this sub-paragraph are—

1.3.11.4.a

the FCA;

1.3.11.4.b

an administrator of the insurer;

1.3.11.4.c

a provisional liquidator of the insurer;

1.3.11.4.d

a person appointed to act as the manager of the write-down order by virtue of
which the insurer is in financial difficulties for the purposes of this
Schedule.

1.3.11.5

Consent under sub-paragraph  (3)(a) —

1.3.11.5.a

must be in writing, and

1.3.11.5.b

must be filed with the court with the relevant application.

1.3.11.6

The PRA must consult the FCA before giving or refusing consent under sub-
paragraph  (3)(a) .

############# Powers to amend this Schedule

1.3.12

The Treasury may by regulations amend this Schedule so as to—

1.3.12.a

vary or omit any of paragraphs  (a) ,  (b)  and  (c)  of paragraph  2(1) ;

1.3.12.b

change the percentage figure specified in the definition of “surrender limit”
in paragraph  3(2) ;

1.3.12.c

amend paragraph  6  (meaning of “ relevant contract ”);

1.3.12.d

amend paragraph  9  (exclusions from the operation of this Schedule).

##### Consequential amendments

2

In section 429 of FSMA 2000 (Parliamentary control of statutory instruments),
in subsection (2B), at the end insert—

2.e

provision made under paragraph  12  of Schedule 19C.

Credit unions

Section 73

##### Introductory

1

The Credit Unions Act 1979 is amended as follows.

##### Specified financial activities

2

2.1

Section 1 (registration) is amended as follows.

2.2

After subsection (2) insert—

2.2.2A

The objects of a credit union are—

2.2.2A.a

each of the mandatory objects specified in subsection (3), or

2.2.2A.b

each of those mandatory objects together with the optional object specified in
subsection  (3ZZA) .

2.3

In subsection (3), in the words before paragraph (a), before “objects” insert
“mandatory” .

2.4

After subsection (3) insert—

2.4.3ZZA

The optional object of a credit union is to carry on one or more of the
financial activities specified in section  1ZA (1)  for the benefit of the
members of the society.

2.5

In subsection (3ZA), for “subsection (3)” substitute  “subsections (3) and
(3ZZA) ” .

3

After section 1 insert—

######### Specified financial activities

3.1ZA

3.1ZA.1

The financial activities specified for the purposes of the optional object of
a credit union (see section 1 (3ZZA) ) are—

3.1ZA.1.a

entering into conditional sale agreements, as the seller;

3.1ZA.1.b

entering into hire purchase agreements, as the person from whom goods are
bailed or (in Scotland) hired;

3.1ZA.1.c

insurance distribution activities.

3.1ZA.2

The Treasury may by regulations specify requirements or restrictions in
relation to the carrying on by a credit union of a financial activity
specified in subsection  (1) .

######### Power to specify further financial activities

3.1ZB

3.1ZB.1

The Treasury may by regulations—

3.1ZB.1.a

amend section  1ZA  so as to specify further financial activities for the
purposes of the optional object of a credit union;

3.1ZB.1.b

make such amendments of this Act, or any other enactment, as appear to them to
be appropriate in consequence of any provision made under paragraph  (a) .

3.1ZB.2

Amendments made by regulations under subsection  (1)  may, in particular,
provide that a credit union may carry on a financial activity specified in the
regulations if the credit union has the optional object specified in section 1
(3ZZA) .

3.1ZB.3

Regulations under section  1ZA (2)  made in relation to a financial activity
specified in regulations under subsection  (1)  may, in particular, make
provision about fees or other charges payable in respect of the activity or
activities that are ancillary to the activity.

3.1ZB.4

Before making regulations under this section, the Treasury must consult such
persons as appear to them to be appropriate.

3.1ZB.5

A statutory instrument containing (whether alone or with other provision)
regulations under this section may not be made unless a draft of the
instrument has been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, each House
of Parliament.

4

In section 2 (supplementary and transitional provisions as to registration),
in subsection (3)—

4.a

for “those” substitute  “the mandatory objects” ;

4.b

after “section 1(3) above” insert  “(whether or not the society also has the
optional object specified in section 1 (3ZZA)  above)” .

##### Ancillary services

6

6.1

Section 9A (power to charge for ancillary services) is amended as follows.

6.2

In subsection (2), in the words before paragraph (a), for “the activity of
accepting a deposit or making a loan” substitute  “an activity mentioned in
subsection (3)” .

6.3

After subsection (2) insert—

6.3.3

The activities mentioned in this subsection are—

6.3.3.a

accepting a deposit;

6.3.3.b

making a loan;

6.3.3.c

entering into a conditional sale agreement, as the seller;

6.3.3.d

entering into a hire purchase agreement, as the person from whom goods are
bailed or (in Scotland) hired.

##### Loans

7

7.1

Section 11 (loans) is amended as follows.

7.2

In subsection (1)—

7.2.a

omit “to a member”;

7.2.b

at the end insert

, to—

7.2.b.a

a member, or

7.2.b.b

another credit union (whether or not a member).

7.3

After subsection (1) insert—

7.3.1ZA

Where a loan is made under subsection (1)(b) to a credit union that is not a
member of the lending credit union, the maximum period within which the loan
must be repaid is six months.

7.4

After subsection (7) insert—

7.4.8

An order under subsection (5) may make different provision in relation to—

7.4.8.a

loans made to a member;

7.4.8.b

loans made to a credit union that is not a member of the lending credit union.

##### Conditional sale and hire purchase agreements

8

Before section 12 (power to hold land for limited purposes) insert—

######### Conditional sale and hire purchase agreements

8.11E

8.11E.1

If the objects of a credit union include the optional object specified in
section 1 (3ZZA)  it may (subject to such terms, including as to security, as
its rules may provide)—

8.11E.1.a

enter into a conditional sale agreement, as the seller, with a member of the
credit union, or

8.11E.1.b

enter into a hire purchase agreement, as the person from whom goods are bailed
or (in Scotland) hired, with a member of the credit union.

8.11E.2

A credit union may only enter into an agreement mentioned in subsection  (1)
with a corporate member if—

8.11E.2.a

the credit union’s rules provide that it may do so, and

8.11E.2.b

entering into the agreement would not result in the aggregate of the
outstanding balances under all such agreements made by the credit union with
corporate members exceeding 10% of the aggregate of the outstanding balances
under all such agreements made by the credit union with members, or such
higher percentage as may be specified in regulations made by the Treasury.

8.11E.3

Subsection  (4)  applies where—

8.11E.3.a

an agreement mentioned in subsection  (1)  is entered into by a credit union
with a member, and

8.11E.3.b

the agreement is not a secured agreement within the meaning of section  11F .

8.11E.4

The terms of the agreement must include provision as to whether, for the
duration of the agreement, the member is permitted to withdraw shares where
the member’s paid-up shareholding in the credit union is, or following the
withdrawal would be, less than the member’s total liability (including
contingent liability) to the credit union.

8.11E.5

Any interest charged under an agreement mentioned in subsection  (1) —

8.11E.5.a

must not exceed the rate specified in subsection  (7) , and

8.11E.5.b

must be inclusive of all administrative and other expenses incurred in
connection with the making of the agreement.

8.11E.6

The rate specified in this subsection is 3% per month on the sum outstanding
under the agreement.

8.11E.7

The Treasury may by regulations amend subsection  (7)  to substitute a
different rate for the rate that is for the time being specified.

######### Agreements to be treated as secured

8.11F

8.11F.1

This section applies where—

8.11F.1.a

a credit union enters into an agreement mentioned in section  11E (1)  with a
member of the credit union, and

8.11F.1.b

at the time the agreement is entered into, the member’s paid-up shareholding
in the credit union is equal to or greater than the member’s total liability
(including contingent liability) to the credit union.

8.11F.2

On the application of the member to the credit union, the agreement is to be
treated for the purposes of this Act as a secured agreement.

##### Insurance distribution activities

9

After section  11F  (inserted by paragraph  8 ) insert—

######### Insurance distribution activities

9.11G

If the objects of a credit union include the optional object specified in
section 1 (3ZZA) , it may (subject to such terms as the rules of the credit
union may provide)—

9.11G.a

carry on an insurance distribution activity which constitutes or involves the
provision of a service to a member, and

9.11G.b

charge such fee as it considers appropriate for providing the service.

10.b

, or

10.b.b

11

In section 23A (power to make provision corresponding to provision applying to
building societies), omit subsection (5).

12

In section 29 (orders and regulations), in subsection (2) for “section”
substitute  “sections  1ZB (5)  and” .

13

13.1

Section 31 (interpretation, etc.) is amended as follows.

13.2

In subsection (1), at the appropriate places insert—

“ conditional sale agreement ” means an agreement for the sale of goods under
which— the purchase price or part of it is payable by instalments, and the
property in the goods is to remain with the seller (notwithstanding that the
buyer is to be in possession of the goods) until such conditions as to the
payment of instalments or otherwise as may be specified in the agreement are
fulfilled;

;

“ enactment ” includes— an enactment contained in subordinate legislation
within the meaning of the Interpretation Act 1978; an enactment contained in,
or in an instrument made under, an Act of the Scottish Parliament; an
enactment contained in, or in an instrument made under, Northern Ireland
legislation within the meaning of the Interpretation Act 1978; an enactment
contained in, or in an instrument made under, a Measure or Act of the National
Assembly for Wales;

;

“ hire purchase agreement ” means an agreement— which is not a conditional
sale agreement, under which goods are bailed or (in Scotland) hired to a
person (“ P ”) in return for periodical payments by P, and the property in the
goods will pass to P if the terms of the agreement are complied with and one
or more of the following occurs— the exercise by P of an option to purchase
the goods; the doing by any party to the agreement of any other act specified
in the agreement; the happening of any event specified in the agreement;

.

13.3

After subsection (1A) insert—

13.3.1B

In this Act, “ insurance distribution activity ” means any of the following
activities—

13.3.1B.a

dealing in rights under a contract of insurance as agent;

13.3.1B.b

arranging deals in rights under a contract of insurance;

13.3.1B.c

assisting in the administration and performance of a contract of insurance;

13.3.1B.d

advising on buying or selling rights under a contract of insurance;

13.3.1B.e

agreeing to do any of the activities specified in paragraphs  (a)  to  (d) .

13.3.1C

Subsection  (1B)  must be read with—

13.3.1C.a

section 22 of the 2000 Act;

13.3.1C.b

any relevant order under that section; and

13.3.1C.c

Schedule 2 to that Act.

13.4

In subsection (4)—

13.4.a

in the words before paragraph (a), omit “(which are replaced by, or are
inconsistent with, provisions of the 2000 Act)”;

13.4.b

omit paragraph (b);

13.4.c

omit paragraph (d).

14

In Schedule 1 (matters to be provided for in rules of credit union), in
paragraph 9, after “members”, in both places, insert  “or other credit unions”
.

##### Transitional provision

15

The amendments made by paragraphs  7(3)  and  14  do not apply in relation to
a loan made by a credit union to another credit union before the earliest date
on which either of those amendments comes into force (whether or not any
amount of the loan remains outstanding on or after that date).

16

The amendment made by paragraph  13(4)(b)  does not apply in relation to a
year of account of a credit union beginning before the date on which that
amendment comes in force (and accordingly, sections 77 and 78 of the Co-
operative and Community Benefit Societies Act 2014 do not apply in relation to
any such year of account).
